We performed a preliminary study in order to determine any difference between a non selective beta - blocker ( <mark>timolol</mark> ) and a selective beta - blocker ( <mark>betaxolol</mark> ) regarding CNS side effects . 
Eight glaucomatous patients chronically treated with <mark>timolol</mark> 0 . 5 % / 12h , suffering from depression diagnosed through DMS - III - R criteria , were included in the study . 
During the six - month follow up , depression was quantified through the Beck and Zung - Conde scales every two months . 
In a double blind cross - over study with control group , the patients under <mark>timolol</mark> treatment presented higher depression values measured through the Beck and the Zung - Conde scales ( p < 0 . 001 vs control ) . 
These results suggest that <mark>betaxolol</mark> could be less of a depression - inducer than <mark>timolol</mark> in predisposed patients . 
Protection against <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced neurotoxicity toward striatal <mark>dopamine</mark> neurons in rodents by <mark>LY274614</mark> , an excitatory <mark>amino acid</mark> antagonist . 
<mark>LY274614</mark> , <mark>3SR , 4aRS , 6SR , 8aRS - 6 - [ phosphonomethyl ] decahydr oisoquinoline - 3 - carboxylic acid</mark> , has been described as a potent antagonist of the <mark>N - methyl - D - aspartate</mark> ( <mark>NMDA</mark> ) subtype of <mark>glutamate</mark> receptor . 
Here its ability to antagonize the prolonged depletion of <mark>dopamine</mark> in the striatum by <mark>amphetamine</mark> in <mark>iprindole</mark> - treated rats is reported . 
A single 18 . 4 mg / kg ( i . p . ) dose of ( + / - ) - <mark>amphetamine</mark> hemisulfate , given to rats pretreated with <mark>iprindole</mark> , resulted in persistent depletion of <mark>dopamine</mark> in the striatum 1 week later . 
This prolonged depletion of <mark>dopamine</mark> in the striatum was antagonized by <mark>dizocilpine</mark> ( <mark>MK - 801</mark> , a non - competitive antagonist of <mark>NMDA</mark> receptors ) or by <mark>LY274614</mark> ( a competitive antagonist of <mark>NMDA</mark> receptors ) . 
The protective effect of <mark>LY274614</mark> was dose - dependent , being maximum at 10 - 40 mgkg ( i . p . ) . 
A 10 mg / kg dose of <mark>LY274614</mark> was effective in antagonizing the depletion of <mark>dopamine</mark> in the striatum , when given as long as 8 hr prior to <mark>amphetamine</mark> but not when given 24 hr prior to <mark>amphetamine</mark> . 
Depletion of <mark>dopamine</mark> in the striatum was also antagonized when <mark>LY274614</mark> was given after the injection of <mark>amphetamine</mark> ; <mark>LY274614</mark> protected when given up to 4 hr after but not when given 8 or 24 hr after <mark>amphetamine</mark> . 
The prolonged depletion of <mark>dopamine</mark> in the striatum in mice , given multiple injections of <mark>methamphetamine</mark> , was also antagonized dose - dependently and completely by <mark>LY274614</mark> . 
The data strengthen the evidence that the neurotoxic effect of <mark>amphetamine</mark> and related compounds toward nigrostriatal <mark>dopamine</mark> neurons involves <mark>NMDA</mark> receptors and that <mark>LY274614</mark> is an <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor antagonist with long - lasting in vivo effects in rats . 
<mark>Ketoconazole</mark> - induced neurologic sequelae . 
A 77 - y - old patient developed weakness of extremities , legs paralysis , dysarthria and tremor 1 h after ingestion of 200 mg <mark>ketoconazole</mark> for the first time in his life . 
All complaints faded away within 24 h . 
Few days later , the patient used another 200 mg <mark>ketoconazole</mark> tablet , and within an hour experienced a similar clinical picture , which resolved again spontaneously within hours . 
Laboratory evaluations , including head CT scan , were normal . 
This case illustrates the need for close vigilance in adverse drug reactions , particularly in the elderly . 
Development of <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesias in parkinsonian monkeys may depend upon rate of symptom onset and / or duration of symptoms . 
<mark>Levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesias ( LIDs ) present a major problem for the long - term management of Parkinson ' s disease ( PD ) patients . 
Due to the interdependence of risk factors in clinical populations , it is difficult to independently examine factors that may influence the development of LIDs . 
Using macaque monkeys with different types of <mark>MPTP</mark> - induced parkinsonism , the current study evaluated the degree to which rate of symptom progression , symptom severity , and response to and duration of <mark>levodopa</mark> therapy may be involved in the development of LIDs . 
Monkeys with acute ( short - term ) <mark>MPTP</mark> exposure , rapid symptom onset and short symptom duration prior to initiation of <mark>levodopa</mark> therapy developed dyskinesia between 11 and 24 days of daily <mark>levodopa</mark> administration . 
In contrast , monkeys with long - term <mark>MPTP</mark> exposure , slow symptom progression and / or long symptom duration prior to initiation of <mark>levodopa</mark> therapy were more resistant to developing LIDs ( e . g . , dyskinesia developed no sooner than 146 days of chronic <mark>levodopa</mark> administration ) . 
All animals were similarly symptomatic at the start of <mark>levodopa</mark> treatment and had similar therapeutic responses to the drug . 
These data suggest distinct differences in the propensity to develop LIDs in monkeys with different rates of symptom progression or symptom durations prior to <mark>levodopa</mark> and demonstrate the value of these models for further studying the pathophysiology of LIDs . 
A diet promoting sugar dependency causes behavioral cross - sensitization to a low dose of <mark>amphetamine</mark> . 
Previous research in this laboratory has shown that a diet of intermittent excessive sugar consumption produces a state with neurochemical and behavioral similarities to drug dependency . 
The present study examined whether female rats on various regimens of sugar access would show behavioral cross - sensitization to a low dose of <mark>amphetamine</mark> . 
After a 30 - min baseline measure of locomotor activity ( day 0 ) , animals were maintained on a cyclic diet of 12 - h deprivation followed by 12 - h access to 10 % <mark>sucrose</mark> solution and chow pellets ( 12 h access starting 4 h after onset of the dark period ) for 21 days . 
Locomotor activity was measured again for 30 min at the beginning of days 1 and 21 of sugar access . 
Beginning on day 22 , all rats were maintained on ad libitum chow . 
Nine days later locomotor activity was measured in response to a single low dose of <mark>amphetamine</mark> ( 0 . 5 mg / kg ) . 
The animals that had experienced cyclic <mark>sucrose</mark> and chow were hyperactive in response to <mark>amphetamine</mark> compared with four control groups ( ad libitum 10 % <mark>sucrose</mark> and chow followed by <mark>amphetamine</mark> injection , cyclic chow followed by <mark>amphetamine</mark> injection , ad libitum chow with <mark>amphetamine</mark> , or cyclic 10 % <mark>sucrose</mark> and chow with a saline injection ) . 
These results suggest that a diet comprised of alternating deprivation and access to a sugar solution and chow produces bingeing on sugar that leads to a long lasting state of increased sensitivity to <mark>amphetamine</mark> , possibly due to a lasting alteration in the <mark>dopamine</mark> system . 
Reversible dilated cardiomyopathy related to <mark>amphotericin B</mark> therapy . 
We describe a patient who developed dilated cardiomyopathy and clinical congestive heart failure after 2 months of therapy with <mark>amphotericin B</mark> ( <mark>AmB</mark> ) for disseminated coccidioidomycosis . 
His echocardiographic abnormalities and heart failure resolved after <mark>posaconazole</mark> was substituted for <mark>AmB</mark> . 
It is important to recognize the rare and potentially reversible toxicity of <mark>AmB</mark> . 
<mark>NO</mark> - induced migraine attack : strong increase in plasma <mark>calcitonin gene - related peptide</mark> ( <mark>CGRP</mark> ) concentration and negative correlation with platelet <mark>serotonin</mark> release . 
The aim of the present study was to investigate changes in the plasma <mark>calcitonin gene - related peptide</mark> ( <mark>CGRP</mark> ) concentration and platelet <mark>serotonin</mark> ( <mark>5 - hydroxytriptamine</mark> , <mark>5 - HT</mark> ) content during the immediate headache and the delayed genuine migraine attack provoked by <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> . 
Fifteen female migraineurs ( without aura ) and eight controls participated in the study . 
Sublingual <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> ( 0 . 5 mg ) was administered . 
Blood was collected from the antecubital vein four times : 60 min before and after the <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> application , and 60 and 120 min after the beginning of the migraine attack ( mean 344 and 404 min ; 12 subjects ) . 
In those subjects who had no migraine attack ( 11 subjects ) a similar time schedule was used . 
Plasma <mark>CGRP</mark> concentration increased significantly ( P < 0 . 01 ) during the migraine attack and returned to baseline after the cessation of the migraine . 
In addition , both change and peak , showed significant positive correlations with migraine headache intensity ( P < 0 . 001 ) . 
However , plasma <mark>CGRP</mark> concentrations failed to change during immediate headache and in the subjects with no migraine attack . 
Basal <mark>CGRP</mark> concentration was significantly higher and platelet <mark>5 - HT</mark> content tended to be lower in subjects who experienced a migraine attack . 
Platelet <mark>serotonin</mark> content decreased significantly ( P < 0 . 01 ) after <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> in subjects with no migraine attack but no consistent change was observed in patients with migraine attack . 
In conclusion , the fact that plasma <mark>CGRP</mark> concentration correlates with the timing and severity of a migraine headache suggests a direct relationship between <mark>CGRP</mark> and migraine . 
In contrast , <mark>serotonin</mark> release from platelets does not provoke migraine , it may even counteract the headache and the concomitant <mark>CGRP</mark> release in this model . 
Hyperbaric <mark>oxygen</mark> therapy for control of intractable <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - induced hemorrhagic cystitis . 
We report a case of intractable hemorrhagic cystitis due to <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> therapy for Wegener ' s granulomatosis . 
Conservative treatment , including bladder irrigation with physiological saline and instillation of <mark>prostaglandin F2 alpha</mark> , failed to totally control hemorrhage . 
We then used hyperbaric <mark>oxygen</mark> at an absolute pressure of 2 atm , 5 days a week for 8 consecutive weeks . 
The bleeding ceased completely by the end of treatment and the patient remained free of hematuria thereafter . 
No side effect was noted during the course of therapy . 
In future , this form of therapy can offer a safe alternative in the treatment of <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - induced hemorrhagic cystitis . 
Acute psychosis due to treatment with <mark>phenytoin</mark> in a nonepileptic patient . 
The development of psychosis related to antiepileptic drug treatment is usually attributed to the interaction between the epileptic brain substratum and the antiepileptic drugs . 
The case of a nonepileptic patient who developed psychosis following <mark>phenytoin</mark> treatment for trigeminal neuralgia is described . 
This case suggests that the psychotic symptoms that occur following <mark>phenytoin</mark> treatment in some epileptic patients may be the direct result of medication , unrelated to seizures . 
Risks of the consumption of beverages containing <mark>quinine</mark> . 
Although the United States Food and Drug Administration banned its use for nocturnal leg cramps due to lack of safety and efficacy , <mark>quinine</mark> is widely available in beverages including tonic water and bitter lemon . 
Numerous anecdotal reports suggest that products containing <mark>quinine</mark> may produce neurological complications , including confusion , altered mental status , seizures , and coma , particularly in older women . 
Psychologists need to inquire about consumption of <mark>quinine</mark> - containing beverages as part of an evaluation process . 
Transient platypnea - orthodeoxia - like syndrome induced by <mark>propafenone</mark> overdose in a young woman with Ebstein ' s anomaly . 
In this report we describe the case of a 37 - year - old white woman with Ebstein ' s anomaly , who developed a rare syndrome called platypnea - orthodeoxia , characterized by massive right - to - left interatrial shunting with transient profound hypoxia and cyanosis . 
This shunt of blood via a patent foramen ovale occurred in the presence of a normal pulmonary artery pressure , and was probably precipitated by a <mark>propafenone</mark> overdose . 
This drug caused biventricular dysfunction , due to its negative inotropic effect , and hypotension , due to its peripheral vasodilatory effect . 
These effects gave rise to an increase in the right atrial pressure and a decrease in the left one with a consequent stretching of the foramen ovale and the creation of massive right - to - left shunting . 
In our case this interatrial shunt was very accurately detected at bubble contrast echocardiography . 
Noxious chemical stimulation of rat facial mucosa increases intracranial blood flow through a trigemino - parasympathetic reflex - - an experimental model for vascular dysfunctions in cluster headache . 
Cluster headache is characterized by typical autonomic dysfunctions including facial and intracranial vascular disturbances . 
Both the trigeminal and the cranial parasympathetic systems may be involved in mediating these dysfunctions . 
An experimental model was developed in the rat to measure changes in lacrimation and intracranial blood flow following noxious chemical stimulation of facial mucosa . 
Blood flow was monitored in arteries of the exposed cranial dura mater and the parietal cortex using laser Doppler flowmetry . 
<mark>Capsaicin</mark> ( 0 . 01 - 1 mm ) applied to oral or nasal mucosa induced increases in dural and cortical blood flow and provoked lacrimation . 
These responses were blocked by systemic pre - administration of <mark>hexamethonium chloride</mark> ( 20 mg / kg ) . 
The evoked increases in dural blood flow were also abolished by topical pre - administration of <mark>atropine</mark> ( 1 mm ) and [ Lys1 , Pro2 , 5 , Arg3 , 4 , Tyr6 ] - VIP ( 0 . 1 mm ) , a vasoactive intestinal polypeptide ( VIP ) antagonist , onto the exposed dura mater . 
We conclude that noxious stimulation of facial mucosa increases intracranial blood flow and lacrimation via a trigemino - parasympathetic reflex . 
The blood flow responses seem to be mediated by the release of <mark>acetylcholine</mark> and VIP within the meninges . 
Similar mechanisms may be involved in the pathogenesis of cluster headache . 
<mark>Organophosphate</mark> - induced convulsions and prevention of neuropathological damages . 
Such <mark>organophosphorus</mark> ( <mark>OP</mark> ) compounds as <mark>diisopropylfluorophosphate</mark> ( <mark>DFP</mark> ) , <mark>sarin</mark> and <mark>soman</mark> are potent inhibitors of acetylcholinesterases ( AChEs ) and butyrylcholinesterases ( BChEs ) . 
The acute toxicity of <mark>OPs</mark> is the result of their irreversible binding with AChEs in the central nervous system ( CNS ) , which elevates <mark>acetylcholine</mark> ( <mark>ACh</mark> ) levels . 
The protective action of subcutaneously ( SC ) administered antidotes or their combinations in <mark>DFP</mark> ( 2 . 0 mg / kg BW ) intoxication was studied in 9 - 10 - weeks - old Han - Wistar male rats . 
The rats received AChE reactivator <mark>pralidoxime - 2 - chloride</mark> ( <mark>2PAM</mark> ) ( 30 . 0 mg / kg BW ) , anticonvulsant <mark>diazepam</mark> ( 2 . 0 mg / kg BW ) , A ( 1 ) - <mark>adenosine</mark> receptor agonist <mark>N ( 6 ) - cyclopentyl adenosine</mark> ( <mark>CPA</mark> ) ( 2 . 0 mg / kg BW ) , <mark>NMDA</mark> - receptor antagonist <mark>dizocilpine maleate</mark> ( + - MK801 hydrogen maleate ) ( 2 . 0 mg / kg BW ) or their combinations with cholinolytic drug <mark>atropine sulfate</mark> ( 50 . 0 mg / kg BW ) immediately or 30 min after the single SC injection of <mark>DFP</mark> . 
The control rats received <mark>atropine sulfate</mark> , but also saline and olive oil instead of other antidotes and <mark>DFP</mark> , respectively . 
All rats were terminated either 24 h or 3 weeks after the <mark>DFP</mark> injection . 
The rats treated with <mark>DFP</mark> - <mark>atropine</mark> showed severe typical <mark>OP</mark> - induced toxicity signs . 
When <mark>CPA</mark> , <mark>diazepam</mark> or <mark>2PAM</mark> was given immediately after <mark>DFP</mark> - <mark>atropine</mark> , these treatments prevented , delayed or shortened the occurrence of serious signs of poisoning . 
<mark>Atropine</mark> - <mark>MK801</mark> did not offer any additional protection against <mark>DFP</mark> toxicity . 
In conclusion , <mark>CPA</mark> , <mark>diazepam</mark> and <mark>2PAM</mark> in combination with <mark>atropine</mark> prevented the occurrence of serious signs of poisoning and thus reduced the toxicity of <mark>DFP</mark> in rat . 
A <mark>pyridoxine</mark> - dependent behavioral disorder unmasked by <mark>isoniazid</mark> . 
A 3 - year - old girl had behavioral deterioration , with hyperkinesis , irritability , and sleeping difficulties after the therapeutic administration of <mark>isoniazid</mark> . 
The administration of pharmacologic doses of <mark>pyridoxine hydrochloride</mark> led to a disappearance of symptoms . 
After discontinuing <mark>isoniazid</mark> therapy a similar pattern of behavior was noted that was controlled by <mark>pyridoxine</mark> . 
A placebo had no effect , but <mark>niacinamide</mark> was as effective as <mark>pyridoxine</mark> . 
Periodic withdrawal of <mark>pyridoxine</mark> was associated with return of the hyperkinesis . 
The level of <mark>pyridoxal</mark> in the blood was normal during the periods of relapse . 
Metabolic studies suggested a block in the <mark>kynurenine</mark> pathway of <mark>tryptophan</mark> metabolism . 
The patient has been followed for six years and has required pharmacologic doses of <mark>pyridoxine</mark> to control her behavior . 
Recurrent excitation in the dentate gyrus of a murine model of temporal lobe epilepsy . 
Similar to rats , systemic <mark>pilocarpine</mark> injection causes status epilepticus ( SE ) and the eventual development of spontaneous seizures and mossy fiber sprouting in C57BL / 6 and CD1 mice , but the physiological correlates of these events have not been identified in mice . 
Population responses in granule cells of the dentate gyrus were examined in transverse slices of the ventral hippocampus from <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - treated and untreated mice . 
In <mark>Mg</mark> ( 2 + ) - free bathing medium containing <mark>bicuculline</mark> , conditions designed to increase excitability in the slices , electrical stimulation of the hilus resulted in a single population spike in granule cells from control mice and <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - treated mice that did not experience SE . 
In SE survivors , similar stimulation resulted in a population spike followed , at a variable latency , by negative DC shifts and repetitive afterdischarges of 3 - 60 s duration , which were blocked by ionotropic <mark>glutamate</mark> receptor antagonists . 
Focal <mark>glutamate</mark> photostimulation of the granule cell layer at sites distant from the recording pipette resulted in population responses of 1 - 30 s duration in slices from SE survivors but not other groups . 
These data support the hypothesis that SE - induced mossy fiber sprouting and synaptic reorganization are relevant characteristics of seizure development in these murine strains , resembling rat models of human temporal lobe epilepsy . 
Urinary bladder cancer in Wegener ' s granulomatosis : risks and relation to <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : To assess and characterise the risk of bladder cancer , and its relation to <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> , in patients with Wegener ' s granulomatosis . 
METHODS : In the population based , nationwide Swedish Inpatient Register a cohort of 1065 patients with Wegener ' s granulomatosis , 1969 - 95 , was identified . 
Through linkage with the Swedish Cancer Register , all subjects in this cohort diagnosed with bladder cancer were identified . 
Nested within the cohort , a matched case - control study was performed to estimate the association between <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> and bladder cancer using odds ratios ( ORs ) as relative risk . 
In the cohort the cumulative risk of bladder cancer after Wegener ' s granulomatosis , and the relative prevalence of a history of bladder cancer at the time of diagnosis of Wegener ' s granulomatosis , were also estimated . 
RESULTS : The median cumulative doses of <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> among cases ( n = 11 ) and controls ( n = 25 ) were 113 g and 25 g , respectively . 
The risk of bladder cancer doubled for every 10 g increment in <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> ( OR = 2 . 0 , 95 % confidence interval ( CI ) 0 . 8 to 4 . 9 ) . 
Treatment duration longer than 1 year was associated with an eightfold increased risk ( OR = 7 . 7 , 95 % CI 0 . 9 to 69 ) . 
The absolute risk for bladder cancer in the cohort reached 10 % 16 years after diagnosis of Wegener ' s granulomatosis , and a history of bladder cancer was ( non - significantly ) twice as common as expected at the time of diagnosis of Wegener ' s granulomatosis . 
CONCLUSION : The results indicate a dose - response relationship between <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> and the risk of bladder cancer , high cumulative risks in the entire cohort , and also the possibility of risk factors operating even before Wegener ' s granulomatosis . 
Differential modulation by <mark>estrogen</mark> of alpha2 - adrenergic and I1 - <mark>imidazoline</mark> receptor - mediated hypotension in female rats . 
We have recently shown that <mark>estrogen</mark> negatively modulates the hypotensive effect of <mark>clonidine</mark> ( mixed alpha2 - / I1 - receptor agonist ) in female rats and implicates the cardiovascular autonomic control in this interaction . 
The present study investigated whether this effect of <mark>estrogen</mark> involves interaction with alpha2 - and / or I1 - receptors . 
Changes evoked by a single intraperitoneal injection of <mark>rilmenidine</mark> ( 600 microg / kg ) or <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> ( 100 mg / kg ) , selective I1 - and alpha2 - receptor agonists , respectively , in blood pressure , hemodynamic variability , and locomotor activity were assessed in radiotelemetered sham - operated and ovariectomized ( Ovx ) Sprague - Dawley female rats with or without 12 - wk <mark>estrogen</mark> replacement . 
Three time domain indexes of hemodynamic variability were employed : the standard deviation of mean arterial pressure as a measure of blood pressure variability and the standard deviation of beat - to - beat intervals ( SDRR ) and the root mean square of successive differences in R - wave - to - R - wave intervals as measures of heart rate variability . 
In sham - operated rats , <mark>rilmenidine</mark> or <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> elicited similar hypotension that lasted at least 5 h and was associated with reductions in standard deviation of mean arterial pressure . 
SDRR was reduced only by <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> . 
Ovx significantly enhanced the hypotensive response to <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> , in contrast to no effect on <mark>rilmenidine</mark> hypotension . 
The enhanced <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> hypotension in Ovx rats was paralleled with further reduction in SDRR and a reduced locomotor activity . 
Estrogen replacement ( <mark>17beta - estradiol</mark> subcutaneous pellet , 14 . 2 microg / day , 12 wk ) of Ovx rats restored the hemodynamic and locomotor effects of <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> to sham - operated levels . 
These findings suggest that <mark>estrogen</mark> downregulates alpha2 - but not I1 - receptor - mediated hypotension and highlight a role for the cardiac autonomic control in <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> - <mark>estrogen</mark> interaction . 
Severe reversible left ventricular systolic and diastolic dysfunction due to accidental iatrogenic <mark>epinephrine</mark> overdose . 
<mark>Catecholamine</mark> - induced cardiomyopathy due to chronic excess of endogenous <mark>catecholamines</mark> has been recognized for decades as a clinical phenomenon . 
In contrast , reports of myocardial dysfunction due to acute iatrogenic overdose are rare . 
A 35 - year - old woman whose cervix uteri was inadvertently injected with 8 mg of <mark>epinephrine</mark> developed myocardial stunning that was characterized by severe hemodynamic compromise , profound , albeit transient , left ventricular systolic and diastolic dysfunction , and only modestly elevated biochemical markers of myocardial necrosis . 
Our case illustrates the serious consequences of medical errors that can be avoided through improved medication labeling and staff supervision . 
Cardioprotective effect of <mark>tincture of Crataegus</mark> on <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
<mark>Tincture of Crataegus</mark> ( <mark>TCR</mark> ) , an <mark>alcoholic extract of the berries of hawthorn</mark> ( <mark>Crataegus oxycantha</mark> ) , is used in herbal and homeopathic medicine . 
The present study was done to investigate the protective effect of <mark>TCR</mark> on experimentally induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
Pretreatment of <mark>TCR</mark> , at a dose of 0 . 5 mL / 100 g bodyweight per day , orally for 30 days , prevented the increase in lipid peroxidation and activity of marker enzymes observed in <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced rats ( 85 mg kg ( - 1 ) s . c . for 2 days at an interval of 24 h ) . 
<mark>TCR</mark> prevented the <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced decrease in antioxidant enzymes in the heart and increased the rate of <mark>ADP</mark> - stimulated <mark>oxygen</mark> uptake and respiratory coupling ratio . 
<mark>TCR</mark> protected against pathological changes induced by <mark>isoproterenol</mark> in rat heart . 
The results show that pretreatment with <mark>TCR</mark> may be useful in preventing the damage induced by <mark>isoproterenol</mark> in rat heart . 
Treatment of tinnitus by intratympanic instillation of <mark>lignocaine</mark> ( <mark>lidocaine</mark> ) 2 per cent through ventilation tubes . 
Idiopathic subjective tinnitus ( IST ) is one of the most obscure otological pathologies . 
This paper presents the results of treating IST by intratympanic instillation of <mark>lignocaine</mark> ( <mark>lidocaine</mark> ) 2 per cent through a grommet , for five weekly courses . 
Fifty - two patients suffering from intractable tinnitus entered this therapeutic trial , but only nine finished all five courses . 
In one patient , the tinnitus was almost completely abolished , but in all the nine patients the decompensated tinnitus changed to a compensated one . 
We suggest this mode of treatment for patients that were previously treated by drugs , acupuncture and biofeedback , with disappointing results . 
Patients should be warned about the side effects of vertigo and vomiting , which subsides gradually with every new instillation , and that the tinnitus may not disappear but will be alleviated , enabling them to cope more easily with the disease and lead a more normal life . 
The alpha3 and beta4 nicotinic <mark>acetylcholine</mark> receptor subunits are necessary for <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced seizures and hypolocomotion in mice . 
Binding of <mark>nicotine</mark> to nicotinic <mark>acetylcholine</mark> receptors ( nAChRs ) elicits a series of dose - dependent behaviors that go from altered exploration , sedation , and tremors , to seizures and death . 
nAChRs are pentameric ion channels usually composed of alpha and beta subunits . 
A gene cluster comprises the alpha3 , alpha5 and beta4 subunits , which coassemble to form functional receptors . 
We examined the role of the beta4 subunits in <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced seizures and hypolocomotion in beta4 homozygous null ( beta4 - / - ) and alpha3 heterozygous ( + / - ) mice . 
beta4 - / - mice were less sensitive to the effects of <mark>nicotine</mark> both at low doses , measured as decreased exploration in an open field , and at high doses , measured as sensitivity to <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced seizures . 
Using in situ hybridization probes for the alpha3 and alpha5 subunits , we showed that alpha5 mRNA levels are unchanged , whereas alpha3 mRNA levels are selectively decreased in the mitral cell layer of the olfactory bulb , and the inferior and the superior colliculus of beta4 - / - brains . 
alpha3 + / - mice were partially resistant to <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced seizures when compared to wild - type littermates . 
mRNA levels for the alpha5 and the beta4 subunits were unchanged in alpha3 + / - brains . 
Together , these results suggest that the beta4 and the alpha3 subunits are mediators of <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced seizures and hypolocomotion . 
The effects of <mark>sevoflurane</mark> on <mark>lidocaine</mark> - induced convulsions . 
The influence of <mark>sevoflurane</mark> on <mark>lidocaine</mark> - induced convulsions was studied in cats . 
The convulsive threshold ( mean + / - SD ) was 41 . 4 + / - 6 . 5 mg . 
l ( - 1 ) with <mark>lidocaine</mark> infusion ( 6 mg . kg ( - 1 ) . min ( - 1 ) ) , increasing significantly to 66 . 6 + / - 10 . 9 mg . 
l ( - 1 ) when the end - tidal concentration of <mark>sevoflurane</mark> was 0 . 8 % . 
However , the threshold ( 61 . 6 + / - 8 . 7 mg . l ( - 1 ) ) during 1 . 6 % <mark>sevoflurane</mark> was not significant from that during 0 . 8 % <mark>sevoflurane</mark> , indicating a celling effect . 
There was no significant difference in the convulsive threshold between <mark>sevoflurane</mark> and <mark>enflurane</mark> . 
The rise in blood pressure became less marked when higher concentrations of <mark>sevoflurane</mark> or <mark>enflurane</mark> were administered and the blood pressure at convulsions decreased significantly in 1 . 6 % <mark>sevoflurane</mark> , and in 0 . 8 % and 1 . 6 % <mark>enflurane</mark> . 
However , there was no significant difference in the <mark>lidocaine</mark> concentrations measured when the systolic blood pressure became 70 mmHg . 
<mark>Apamin</mark> , a selective blocker of <mark>calcium</mark> - dependent <mark>potassium</mark> channels , was administered intracerebroventricularly in rats anesthetized with 0 . 8 % <mark>sevoflurane</mark> to investigate the mechanism of the anticonvulsive effects . 
<mark>Apamin</mark> ( 10 ng ) had a tendency to decrease the convulsive threshold ( 21 . 6 + / - 2 . 2 to 19 . 9 + / - 2 . 5 mg . l ( - 1 ) ) but this was not statistically significant . 
It is suggested that <mark>sevoflurane</mark> reduces the convulsive effect of <mark>lidocaine</mark> toxicity but carries some risk due to circulatory depression . 
Cardiac toxicity observed in association with high - dose <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - based chemotherapy for metastatic breast cancer . 
INTRODUCTION : <mark>Cyclophosphamide</mark> is an alkylating agent given frequently as a component of many conditioning regimens . 
In high doses , its nonhematological dose - limiting toxicity is cardiomyopathy . 
STUDY DESIGN : We combined <mark>paclitaxel</mark> , <mark>melphalan</mark> and high - dose <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> , <mark>thiotepa</mark> , and <mark>carboplatin</mark> in a triple sequential high - dose regimen for patients with metastatic breast cancer . 
Analysis was performed on 61 women with chemotherapy - responsive metastatic breast cancer receiving 96 - h infusional <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> as part of a triple sequential high - dose regimen to assess association between presence of peritransplant congestive heart failure ( CHF ) and the following pretreatment characteristics : presence of electrocardiogram ( EKG ) abnormalities , age , hypertension , prior cardiac history , smoking , diabetes mellitus , prior use of <mark>anthracyclines</mark> , and left - sided chest irradiation . 
RESULTS : Six of 61 women ( 10 % ) developed clinically reversible grade 3 CHF following infusional <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> with a median percent decline in ejection fraction of 31 % . 
Incidence of transient <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - related cardiac toxicity ( 10 % ) is comparable to previous recorded literature . 
Older age was significantly correlated with the CHF development ; with median ages for the entire group and for patients developing CHF of 45 and 59 , respectively . 
No association was found with other pretreatment characteristics . 
CONCLUSIONS : As a result of these findings , oncologists should carefully monitor fluid balance in older patients . 
Routine EKG monitoring during infusional <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> did not predict CHF development . 
Tremor side effects of <mark>salbutamol</mark> , quantified by a laser pointer technique . 
OBJECTIVE : To study tremor side effects of <mark>salbutamol</mark> an easily applicable , quick and low - priced method is needed . 
A new method using a commercially available , pen - shaped laser pointer was developed . 
Aim of the study was to determine sensitivity , reproducibility , reference values and the agreement with a questionnaire . 
METHODS : Tremor was measured using a laser pointer technique . 
To determine sensitivity we assessed tremor in 44 patients with obstructive lung disease after administration of cumulative doses of <mark>salbutamol</mark> . 
Subjects were asked to aim at the centre of a target , subdivided in concentric circles , from 5 m distance . 
The circle in which the participant succeeded to aim was recorded in millimetres radius . 
In another series of measurements , reproducibility and reference values of the tremor was assessed in 65 healthy subjects in three sessions , at 9 a . m . , 4 p . m . and 9 a . m . , respectively , 1 week later . 
Postural tremor was measured with the arm horizontally outstretched rest tremor with the arm supported by an armrest and finally tremor was measured after holding a 2 - kg weight until exhaustion . 
Inter - observer variability was measured in a series of 10 healthy subjects . 
Tremor was measured simultaneously by two independent observers . 
RESULTS : <mark>Salbutamol</mark> significantly increased tremor severity in patients in a dose - dependent way . 
Within healthy adults no age - dependency could be found ( b = 0 . 262 mm / year ; P = 0 . 72 ) . 
There was no agreement between the questionnaire and tremor severity ( r = 0 . 093 ; P = 0 . 53 ) . 
Postural tremor showed no significant difference between the first and third session ( P = 0 . 07 ) . 
Support of the arm decreased tremor severity , exhaustion increased tremor severity significantly . 
A good agreement was found between two independent observers ( interclass correlation coefficient 0 . 72 ) . 
DISCUSSION : Quantifying tremor by using an inexpensive laser pointer is , with the exception of children ( < 12 years ) a sensitive and reproducible method . 
Safety and adverse effects associated with <mark>raloxifene</mark> : multiple outcomes of <mark>raloxifene</mark> evaluation . 
OBJECTIVE : To examine the effect of <mark>raloxifene</mark> on major adverse events that occur with postmenopausal <mark>estrogen</mark> therapy or <mark>tamoxifen</mark> . 
METHODS : The Multiple Outcomes of <mark>Raloxifene</mark> Evaluation , a multicenter , randomized , double - blind trial , enrolled 7 , 705 postmenopausal women with osteoporosis . 
Women were randomly assigned to <mark>raloxifene</mark> 60 mg / d or 120 mg / d or placebo . 
Outcomes included venous thromboembolism , cataracts , gallbladder disease , and endometrial hyperplasia or cancer . 
RESULTS : During a mean follow - up of 3 . 3 years , <mark>raloxifene</mark> was associated with an increased risk for venous thromboembolism ( relative risk [ RR ] 2 . 1 ; 95 % confidence interval [ CI ] 1 . 2 - 3 . 8 ) . 
The excess event rate was 1 . 8 per 1 , 000 woman - years ( 95 % CI - 0 . 5 - 4 . 1 ) , and the number needed to treat to cause 1 event was 170 ( 95 % CI 100 - 582 ) over 3 . 3 years . 
Risk in the <mark>raloxifene</mark> group was higher than in the placebo group for the first 2 years , but decreased to about the same rate as in the placebo group thereafter . 
<mark>Raloxifene</mark> did not increase risk for cataracts ( RR 0 . 9 ; 95 % CI 0 . 8 - 1 . 1 ) , gallbladder disease ( RR 1 . 0 ; 95 % CI 0 . 7 - 1 . 3 ) , endometrial hyperplasia ( RR 1 . 3 ; 95 % CI 0 . 4 - 5 . 1 ) , or endometrial cancer ( RR 0 . 9 ; 95 % CI 0 . 3 - 2 . 7 ) . 
CONCLUSION : <mark>Raloxifene</mark> was associated with an increased risk for venous thromboembolism , but there was no increased risk for cataracts , gallbladder disease , endometrial hyperplasia , or endometrial cancer . 
LEVEL OF EVIDENCE : I 
Optimization of <mark>levodopa</mark> therapy . 
While there is no single correct starting dose for <mark>levodopa</mark> therapy , many individuals can be started on either the 25 / 100 or controlled - release formula , following the general rule not to attempt to titrate <mark>carbidopa</mark> - <mark>levodopa</mark> to the point of " normality , " which can lead to toxicity . 
The physician should also determine the proper use of any adjunctive medications ; such combined therapy has become the standard approach to treatment . 
Following the initial period of therapy , emerging difficulties require a reassessment of therapeutic approaches , such as dosage adjustment or introduction of a <mark>dopamine</mark> agonist . 
Other possible adverse effects - - such as gastrointestinal disorders , orthostatic hypotension , <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced psychosis , sleep disturbances or parasomnias , or drug interactions - - also require carefully monitored individual treatment . 
Nonpharmacologic concerns can help the Parkinson ' s disease patient achieve and maintain optimal functioning , including daily exercise , physical therapy , and involvement with support groups . 
Long term audiological evaluation of beta - thalassemic patients . 
OBJECTIVE : The objective of this study was to identify the incidence and to monitor the progression of hearing loss in children and young adults with beta - thalassemia major . 
METHODS : One hundred and four ( 104 ) patients aged 6 - 35 years ( mean 17 , 2 years ) participated in the study . 
All patients were on a regular transfusion - chelation program maintaining a mean hemoglobin level of 9 . 5 gr / dl . 
Subjects were receiving <mark>desferrioxamine</mark> ( <mark>DFO</mark> ) chelation treatment with a mean daily dose of 50 - 60 mg / kg , 5 - 6 days a week during the first six years of the study , which was then reduced to 40 - 50 mg / kg for the following eight years . 
Patients were followed for 8 - 14 years . 
RESULTS : Overall , 21 out of 104 patients ( 20 . 2 % ) presented with high frequency sensorineural hearing loss ( SNHL ) , either unilateral or bilateral . 
No ototoxic factor , other than <mark>DFO</mark> , was present in any of the patients . 
Patients with SNHL presented with relatively lower serum ferritin levels than those with normal hearing , however , no statistically significant difference was observed . 
Subjects with SNHL were submitted to <mark>DFO</mark> reduction or temporary withdrawal . 
Following intervention , 7 out of 21 affected patients recovered , 10 remained stable and 4 demonstrated aggravation . 
CONCLUSION : The findings are indicative of <mark>DFO</mark> ' s contributing role in the development of hearing impairment . 
Regular audiologic evaluation is imperative in all thalassemic patients so that early changes may be recognized and treatment may be judiciously adjusted in order to prevent or reverse hearing impairment . 
Individual differences in renal ACE activity in healthy rats predict susceptibility to <mark>adriamycin</mark> - induced renal damage . 
BACKGROUND : In man , differences in <mark>angiotensin</mark> - converting enzyme ( ACE ) levels , related to ACE ( I / D ) genotype , are associated with renal prognosis . 
This raises the hypothesis that individual differences in renal ACE activity are involved in renal susceptibility to inflicted damage . 
Therefore , we studied the predictive effect of renal ACE activity for the severity of renal damage induced by a single injection of <mark>adriamycin</mark> in rats . 
METHODS : Renal ACE activity ( <mark>Hip - His - Leu</mark> cleavage by cortical homogenates ) was determined by renal biopsy in 27 adult male Wistar rats . 
After 1 week of recovery , proteinuria was induced by <mark>adriamycin</mark> [ 1 . 5 mg / kg intravenously ( i . v . ) n = 18 ; controls , saline i . v . n = 9 ] . 
Proteinuria was measured every 2 weeks . 
After 12 weeks , rats were sacrificed and their kidneys harvested . 
RESULTS : As anticipated , <mark>adriamycin</mark> elicited nephrotic range proteinuria , renal interstitial damage and mild focal glomerulosclerosis . 
Baseline renal ACE positively correlated with the relative rise in proteinuria after <mark>adriamycin</mark> ( r = 0 . 62 , P < 0 . 01 ) , renal interstitial alpha - smooth muscle actin ( r = 0 . 49 , P < 0 . 05 ) , interstitial macrophage influx ( r = 0 . 56 , P < 0 . 05 ) , interstitial collagen III ( r = 0 . 53 , P < 0 . 05 ) , glomerular alpha - smooth muscle actin ( r = 0 . 74 , P < 0 . 01 ) and glomerular desmin ( r = 0 . 48 , P < 0 . 05 ) . 
Baseline renal ACE did not correlate with focal glomerulosclerosis ( r = 0 . 22 , NS ) . 
In controls , no predictive values for renal parameters were observed . 
CONCLUSION : Individual differences in renal ACE activity predict the severity of <mark>adriamycin</mark> - induced renal damage in this outbred rat strain . 
This supports the assumption that differences in renal ACE activity predispose to a less favourable course of renal damage . 
Recurrent acute interstitial nephritis induced by <mark>azithromycin</mark> . 
A 14 - year - old girl is reported with recurrent , <mark>azithromycin</mark> - induced , acute interstitial nephritis . 
The second episode was more severe than the first ; and although both were treated with intensive corticosteroid therapy , renal function remained impaired . 
Although most cases of antibiotic induced acute interstitial nephritis are benign and self - limited , some patients are at risk for permanent renal injury . 
<mark>Spironolactone</mark> - induced renal insufficiency and hyperkalemia in patients with heart failure . 
BACKGROUND : A previous randomized controlled trial evaluating the use of <mark>spironolactone</mark> in heart failure patients reported a low risk of hyperkalemia ( 2 % ) and renal insufficiency ( 0 % ) . 
Because treatments for heart failure have changed since the benefits of <mark>spironolactone</mark> were reported , the prevalence of these complications may differ in current clinical practice . 
We therefore sought to determine the prevalence and clinical associations of hyperkalemia and renal insufficiency in heart failure patients treated with <mark>spironolactone</mark> . 
METHODS : We performed a case control study of heart failure patients treated with <mark>spironolactone</mark> in our clinical practice . 
Cases were patients who developed hyperkalemia ( <mark>K</mark> ( + ) > 5 . 0 mEq / L ) or renal insufficiency ( <mark>Cr</mark> > or = 2 . 5 mg / dL ) , and they were compared to 2 randomly selected controls per case . 
Clinical characteristics , medications , and serum chemistries at baseline and follow - up time periods were compared . 
RESULTS : Sixty - seven of 926 patients ( 7 . 2 % ) required discontinuation of <mark>spironolactone</mark> due to hyperkalemia ( n = 33 ) or renal failure ( n = 34 ) . 
Patients who developed hyperkalemia were older and more likely to have diabetes , had higher baseline serum <mark>potassium</mark> levels and lower baseline <mark>potassium</mark> supplement doses , and were more likely to be treated with beta - blockers than controls ( n = 134 ) . 
Patients who developed renal insufficiency had lower baseline body weight and higher baseline serum <mark>creatinine</mark> , required higher doses of loop diuretics , and were more likely to be treated with <mark>thiazide</mark> diuretics than controls . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Spironolactone</mark> - induced hyperkalemia and renal insufficiency are more common in our clinical experience than reported previously . 
This difference is explained by patient comorbidities and more frequent use of beta - blockers . 
Acute <mark>reserpine</mark> and subchronic <mark>haloperidol</mark> treatments change synaptosomal brain <mark>glutamate</mark> uptake and elicit orofacial dyskinesia in rats . 
<mark>Reserpine</mark> - and <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced orofacial dyskinesia are putative animal models of tardive dyskinesia ( TD ) whose pathophysiology has been related to free radical generation and oxidative stress . 
In the present study , the authors induced orofacial dyskinesia by acute <mark>reserpine</mark> and subchronic <mark>haloperidol</mark> administration to rats . 
<mark>Reserpine</mark> injection ( one dose of 1 mg / kg s . c . ) every other day for 3 days caused a significant increase in vacuous chewing , tongue protrusion and duration of facial twitching , compared to the control . 
<mark>Haloperidol</mark> administration ( one dose of 12 mg / kg once a week s . c . ) for 4 weeks caused an increase in vacuous chewing , tongue protrusion and duration of facial twitching observed in four weekly evaluations . 
After the treatments and behavioral observation , <mark>glutamate</mark> uptake by segments of the brain was analyzed . 
A decreased <mark>glutamate</mark> uptake was observed in the subcortical parts of animals treated with <mark>reserpine</mark> and <mark>haloperidol</mark> , compared to the control . 
Importantly , a decrease in <mark>glutamate</mark> uptake correlates negatively with an increase in the incidence of orofacial diskinesia . 
These results indicate that early changes in <mark>glutamate</mark> transport may be related to the development of vacuous chewing movements in rats . 
<mark>Ceftriaxone</mark> - associated biliary pseudolithiasis in paediatric surgical patients . 
It is well known that <mark>ceftriaxone</mark> leads to pseudolithiasis in some patients . 
Clinical and experimental studies also suggest that situations causing gallbladder dysfunction , such as fasting , may have a role for the development of pseudolithiasis . 
In this study , we prospectively evaluated the incidence and clinical importance of pseudolithiasis in paediatric surgical patients receiving <mark>ceftriaxone</mark> treatment , who often had to fast in the post - operative period . 
Fifty children who were given <mark>ceftriaxone</mark> were evaluated by serial abdominal sonograms . 
Of those , 13 ( 26 % ) developed biliary pathology . 
Comparison of the patients with or without pseudolithiasis revealed no significant difference with respect to age , sex , duration of the treatment and starvation variables . 
After cessation of the treatment , pseudolithiasis resolved spontaneously within a short period . 
The incidence of pseudolithiasis is not affected by fasting . 
Coronary aneurysm after implantation of a <mark>paclitaxel</mark> - eluting stent . 
Formation of coronary aneurysm is a rare complication of stenting with bare metal stents , but based on experimental studies drug - eluting stents may induce toxic effects on the vessel wall with incomplete stent apposition , aneurysm formation and with the potential of stent thrombosis or vessel rupture . 
We present a 43 - year - old man who developed a coronary aneurysm in the right coronary artery 6 months after receiving a <mark>paclitaxel</mark> - eluting stent . 
The patient was asymptomatic and the aneurysm was detected in a routine control . 
Angiography and intracoronary ultrasound demonstrated lack of contact between stent and vessel wall in a 15 - mm long segment with maximal aneurysm diameter of 6 . 0 mm . 
The patient was successfully treated with a graft stent . 
Causes of acute thrombotic microangiopathy in patients receiving kidney transplantation . 
OBJECTIVES : Thrombotic microangiopathy is a well - known problem in patients following renal transplantation . 
In postrenal transplantation , thrombotic microangiopathy is often a reflection of hemolytic uremic syndrome . 
We aimed to determine the causes of thrombotic microangiopathy in a population of renal transplantation recipients and discuss the literature . 
MATERIALS AND METHODS : We investigated the causes of thrombotic microangiopathy during a 1 - year period , from June 2003 to June 2004 , at the King Fahad National Guard Hospital in Riyadh , Saudi Arabia , by reviewing the slides of all transplant biopsies ( n = 25 ) performed during this interval . 
Pre - and posttransplant crossmatching was done when possible . 
RESULTS : Five cases of thrombotic microangiopathy were found . 
Three of these cases were from the 25 transplantations performed at King Fahad National Guard Hospital , while the other 2 transplantations had been performed abroad and were referred to us for follow - up . 
Three cases were related to <mark>cyclosporine</mark> , and 1 case was secondary to both <mark>cyclosporine</mark> and <mark>tacrolimus</mark> . 
The fifth case had features of thrombotic microangiopathy related to an antiphospholipid syndrome in a patient with systemic lupus erythematosus . 
CONCLUSIONS : In the literature , the most - frequent cause of hemolytic uremic syndrome in patients following renal transplantation is recurrence of the hemolytic uremic syndrome . 
Other causes include drug - related ( <mark>cyclosporine</mark> , <mark>tacrolimus</mark> ) toxicity , procoagulant status , and antibody - mediated rejection . 
We found that the most - frequent cause of thrombotic microangiopathy was drug related , secondary mainly to <mark>cyclosporine</mark> . 
In the current study , the frequency of thrombotic microangiopathy was similar to the percentage reported in the literature ( 20 % ) . 
Comparison of developmental toxicity of selective and non - selective cyclooxygenase - 2 inhibitors in CRL : ( WI ) WUBR Wistar rats - - <mark>DFU</mark> and <mark>piroxicam</mark> study . 
BACKGROUND : Cyclooxygenase ( COX ) inhibitors are one of the most often ingested drugs during pregnancy . 
Unlike general toxicity data , their prenatal toxic effects were not extensively studied before . 
The aim of the experiment was to evaluate the developmental toxicity of the non - selective ( <mark>piroxicam</mark> ) and selective ( <mark>DFU</mark> ; <mark>5 , 5 - dimethyl - 3 - ( 3 - fluorophenyl ) - 4 - ( 4 - methylsulphonyl ) phenyl - 2 ( 5H ) - furanon</mark> ) COX - 2 inhibitors . 
METHODS : Drugs were separately , orally once daily dosed to pregnant rats from day 8 to 21 ( GD1 = plug day ) . 
Doses were set at 0 . 3 , 3 . 0 and 30 . 0mg / kg for <mark>piroxicam</mark> and 0 . 2 , 2 . 0 and 20 . 0mg / kg for <mark>DFU</mark> . 
Fetuses were delivered on GD 21 and routinely examined . 
Comprehensive clinical and developmental measurements were done . 
The pooled statistical analysis for ventricular septal ( VSD ) and midline ( MD ) defects was performed for rat fetuses exposed to <mark>piroxicam</mark> , selective and non - selective COX - 2 inhibitor based on present and historic data . 
RESULTS : Maternal toxicity , intrauterine growth retardation , and increase of external and skeletal variations were found in rats treated with the highest dose of <mark>piroxicam</mark> . 
Decrease of fetal length was the only signs of the <mark>DFU</mark> developmental toxicity observed in pups exposed to the highest compound dose . 
Lack of teratogenicity was found in <mark>piroxicam</mark> and <mark>DFU</mark> - exposed groups . 
Prenatal exposure to non - selective COX inhibitors increases the risk of VSD and MD when compared to historic control but not with selective COX - 2 inhibitors . 
CONCLUSION : Both selective and non - selective COX - 2 inhibitors were toxic for rats fetuses when administered in the highest dose . 
Unlike <mark>DFU</mark> , <mark>piroxicam</mark> was also highly toxic to the dams . 
Prenatal exposure to selective COX - 2 inhibitors does not increase the risk of ventricular septal and midline defects in rat when compared to non - selective drugs and historic control . 
Lone atrial fibrillation associated with <mark>creatine</mark> monohydrate supplementation . 
Atrial fibrillation in young patients without structural heart disease is rare . 
Therefore , when the arrhythmia is present in this population , reversible causes must be identified and resolved . 
Thyroid disorders , illicit drug or stimulant use , and acute alcohol intoxication are among these causes . 
We report the case of a 30 - year - old Caucasian man who came to the emergency department in atrial fibrillation with rapid ventricular response . 
His medical history was unremarkable , except for minor fractures of the fingers and foot . 
Thyroid - stimulating hormone , <mark>magnesium</mark> , and <mark>potassium</mark> levels were within normal limits , urine drug screen was negative , and <mark>alcohol</mark> use was denied . 
However , when the patient was questioned about use of herbal products and supplements , the use of <mark>creatine</mark> monohydrate was revealed . 
The patient was admitted to the hospital , anticoagulated with unfractionated <mark>heparin</mark> , and given intravenous <mark>diltiazem</mark> for rate control and intravenous <mark>amiodarone</mark> for rate and rhythm control . 
When discharged less than 24 hours later , he was receiving <mark>metoprolol</mark> and <mark>aspirin</mark> , with follow - up plans for echocardiography and nuclear imaging to assess perfusion . 
Exogenous <mark>creatine</mark> is used by athletes to theoretically improve exercise performance . 
Vegetarians may also take <mark>creatine</mark> to replace what they are not consuming from meat , fish , and other animal products . 
Previous anecdotal reports have linked <mark>creatine</mark> to the development of arrhythmia . 
Clinicians must be diligent when interviewing patients about their drug therapy histories and include questions about their use of herbal products and dietary supplements . 
In addition , it is important to report adverse effects associated with frequently consumed supplements and herbal products to the Food and Drug Administration and in the literature . 
Seizures induced by the <mark>cocaine</mark> metabolite <mark>benzoylecgonine</mark> in rats . 
The half - life ( t1 / 2 ) of <mark>cocaine</mark> is relatively short , but some of the consequences of its use , such as seizures and strokes , can occur hours after exposure . 
This led us to hypothesize that a metabolite of <mark>cocaine</mark> may be responsible for some of those delayed sequelae . 
We evaluated the potential of the major metabolite of <mark>cocaine</mark> , <mark>benzoylecgonine</mark> ( <mark>BE</mark> ) , to cause seizures . 
Two separate equimolar doses ( 0 . 2 and 0 . 4 mumol ) of either <mark>cocaine</mark> or <mark>BE</mark> were injected ventricularly in unanesthetized juvenile rats . 
Treated rats were then evaluated for incidence , latency , and seizure pattern or for locomotor activity in animals without seizures . 
<mark>BE</mark> - Induced seizures occurred more frequently and had significantly longer latencies than those induced by equimolar amounts of <mark>cocaine</mark> . 
Whereas <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced seizures were best characterized as brief , generalized , and tonic and resulted in death , those induced by <mark>BE</mark> were prolonged , often multiple and mixed in type , and rarely resulted in death . 
Electrical recordings from the hippocampus showed a rhythmic progression in EEG frequency and voltage with clinical seizure expression . 
<mark>BE</mark> - Injected rats that did not have seizures had significantly more locomotor activity than <mark>cocaine</mark> - injected animals without seizures . 
The finding that <mark>cocaine</mark> - and <mark>BE</mark> - induced seizures differ in several respects suggests more than one mechanism for <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced seizures and emphasizes the importance of a <mark>cocaine</mark> metabolite , <mark>BE</mark> . 
The selective 5 - HT6 receptor antagonist <mark>Ro4368554</mark> restores memory performance in cholinergic and serotonergic models of memory deficiency in the rat . 
Antagonists at <mark>serotonin</mark> type 6 ( <mark>5 - HT</mark> ( 6 ) ) receptors show activity in models of learning and memory . 
Although the underlying mechanism ( s ) are not well understood , these effects may involve an increase in <mark>acetylcholine</mark> ( <mark>ACh</mark> ) levels . 
The present study sought to characterize the cognitive - enhancing effects of the <mark>5 - HT</mark> ( 6 ) antagonist <mark>Ro4368554</mark> ( <mark>3 - benzenesulfonyl - 7 - ( 4 - methyl - piperazin - 1 - yl ) 1H - indole</mark> ) in a rat object recognition task employing a cholinergic ( <mark>scopolamine</mark> pretreatment ) and a serotonergic - ( <mark>tryptophan</mark> ( <mark>TRP</mark> ) depletion ) deficient model , and compared its pattern of action with that of the acetylcholinesterase inhibitor <mark>metrifonate</mark> . 
Initial testing in a time - dependent forgetting task employing a 24 - h delay between training and testing showed that <mark>metrifonate</mark> improved object recognition ( at 10 and 30 mg / kg , p . o . ) , whereas <mark>Ro4368554</mark> was inactive . 
Both , <mark>Ro4368554</mark> ( 3 and 10 mg / kg , intraperitoneally ( i . p . ) ) and <mark>metrifonate</mark> ( 10 mg / kg , p . o . , respectively ) reversed memory deficits induced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> and <mark>TRP</mark> depletion ( 10 mg / kg , i . p . , and 3 mg / kg , p . o . , respectively ) . 
In conclusion , although <mark>Ro4368554</mark> did not improve a time - related retention deficit , it reversed a cholinergic and a serotonergic memory deficit , suggesting that both mechanisms may be involved in the facilitation of object memory by <mark>Ro4368554</mark> and , possibly , other <mark>5 - HT</mark> ( 6 ) receptor antagonists . 
Evaluation of the anticocaine monoclonal antibody <mark>GNC92H2</mark> as an immunotherapy for cocaine overdose . 
The illicit use of <mark>cocaine</mark> continues in epidemic proportions and treatment for cocaine overdose remains elusive . 
Current protein - based technology offers a new therapeutic venue by which antibodies bind the drug in the blood stream , inactivating its toxic effects . 
The therapeutic potential of the anticocaine antibody <mark>GNC92H2</mark> was examined using a model of cocaine overdose . 
Swiss albino mice prepared with intrajugular catheters were tested in photocell cages after administration of 93 mg / kg ( LD50 ) of <mark>cocaine</mark> and <mark>GNC92H2</mark> infusions ranging from 30 to 190 mg / kg . 
<mark>GNC92H2</mark> was delivered 30 min before , concomitantly or 3 min after <mark>cocaine</mark> treatment . 
Significant blockade of <mark>cocaine</mark> toxicity was observed with the higher dose of <mark>GNC92H2</mark> ( 190 mg / kg ) , where premorbid behaviors were reduced up to 40 % , seizures up to 77 % and death by 72 % . 
Importantly , <mark>GNC92H2</mark> prevented death even post - <mark>cocaine</mark> injection . 
The results support the important potential of <mark>GNC92H2</mark> as a therapeutic tool against cocaine overdose . 
Electrocardiographic evidence of myocardial injury in psychiatrically hospitalized <mark>cocaine</mark> abusers . 
The electrocardiograms ( ECG ) of 99 <mark>cocaine</mark> - abusing patients were compared with the ECGs of 50 schizophrenic controls . 
Eleven of the <mark>cocaine</mark> abusers and none of the controls had ECG evidence of significant myocardial injury defined as myocardial infarction , ischemia , and bundle branch block . 
Behavioral effects of <mark>urotensin - II</mark> centrally administered in mice . 
<mark>Urotensin - II</mark> ( <mark>U - II</mark> ) receptors are widely distributed in the central nervous system . 
Intracerebroventricular ( i . c . v . ) injection of <mark>U - II</mark> causes hypertension and bradycardia and stimulates prolactin and thyrotropin secretion . 
However , the behavioral effects of centrally administered <mark>U - II</mark> have received little attention . 
In the present study , we tested the effects of i . c . v . injections of <mark>U - II</mark> on behavioral , metabolic , and endocrine responses in mice . 
Administration of graded doses of <mark>U - II</mark> ( 1 - 10 , 000 ng / mouse ) provoked : ( 1 ) a dose - dependent reduction in the number of head dips in the hole - board test ; ( 2 ) a dose - dependent reduction in the number of entries in the white chamber in the black - and - white compartment test , and in the number of entries in the central platform and open arms in the plus - maze test ; and ( 3 ) a dose - dependent increase in the duration of immobility in the forced - swimming test and tail suspension test . 
Intracerebroventricular injection of <mark>U - II</mark> also caused an increase in : food intake at doses of 100 and 1 , 000 ng / mouse , water intake at doses of 100 - 10 , 000 ng / mouse , and horizontal locomotion activity at a dose of 10 , 000 ng / mouse . 
Whatever was the dose , the central administration of <mark>U - II</mark> had no effect on body temperature , nociception , <mark>apomorphine</mark> - induced penile erection and climbing behavior , and stress - induced plasma <mark>corticosterone</mark> level . 
Taken together , the present study demonstrates that the central injection of <mark>U - II</mark> at doses of 1 - 10 , 000 ng / mouse induces anxiogenic - and depressant - like effects in mouse . 
These data suggest that <mark>U - II</mark> may be involved in some aspects of psychiatric disorders . 
Learning of rats under amnesia caused by <mark>pentobarbital</mark> . 
Dissociated learning of rats in the normal state and the state of amnesia produced by <mark>pentobarbital</mark> ( 15 mg / kg , ip ) was carried out . 
Rats were trained to approach a shelf where they received food reinforcement . 
In Group 1 the rats were trained under the influence of <mark>pentobarbital</mark> to run to the same shelf as in the normal state . 
In Group 2 the rats were trained to approach different shelves in different drug states . 
It was shown that memory dissociation occurred in both groups . 
Differences in the parameters of training under the influence of <mark>pentobarbital</mark> between Groups 1 and 2 were revealed . 
These findings show that the brain - dissociated state induced by <mark>pentobarbital</mark> is formed with the participation of the mechanisms of information perception . 
The effects of short - term <mark>raloxifene</mark> therapy on fibrinolysis markers : TAFI , tPA , and PAI - 1 . 
BACKGROUND : Markers of fibrinolysis , thrombin - activatable fibrinolysis inhibitor ( TAFI ) , tissue - type plasminogen activator ( tPA ) , and plasminogen activator inhibitor - 1 ( PAI - 1 ) levels were studied for the evaluation of short - term effects of <mark>raloxifene</mark> administration in postmenopausal women . 
METHODS : Thirty - nine postmenopausal women with osteopenia or osteoporosis were included in this prospective , controlled clinical study . 
Twenty - five women were given <mark>raloxifene hydrochloride</mark> ( 60 mg / day ) plus <mark>calcium</mark> ( 500 mg / day ) . 
Age - matched controls ( n = 14 ) were given only <mark>calcium</mark> . 
Plasma TAFI , tPA , and PAI - 1 antigen levels were measured at baseline and after 3 months of treatment by commercially available ELISA kits . 
Variations of individuals were assessed by Wilcoxon ' s test . 
Relationship between those markers and demographic characteristics were investigated . 
RESULTS : Three months of <mark>raloxifene</mark> treatment was associated with a significant decrease in the plasma TAFI antigen concentrations ( 16 % change , P < 0 . 01 ) , and a significant increase in tPA antigen concentrations ( 25 % change , P < 0 . 05 ) . 
A significant correlation was found between baseline TAFI antigen concentrations and the duration of amenorrhea ( P < 0 . 05 ; r = 0 . 33 ) . 
CONCLUSION : We suggest that the increased risk of venous thromboembolism due to <mark>raloxifene</mark> treatment may be related to increased tPA levels , but not TAFI levels . 
<mark>Valproate</mark> - induced encephalopathy . 
<mark>Valproate</mark> - induced encephalopathy is a rare syndrome that may manifest in otherwise normal epileptic individuals . 
It may even present in patients who have tolerated this medicine well in the past . 
It is usually but not necessarily associated with hyperammonemia . 
The EEG shows characteristic triphasic waves in most patients with this complication . 
A case of <mark>valproate</mark> - induced encephalopathy is presented . 
The problems in diagnosing this condition are subsequently discussed . 
Recurrent dysphonia and <mark>acitretin</mark> . 
We report the case of a woman complaining of dysphonia while she was treated by <mark>acitretin</mark> . 
Her symptoms totally regressed after drug withdrawal and reappeared when <mark>acitretin</mark> was reintroduced . 
To our knowledge , this is the first case of <mark>acitretin</mark> - induced dysphonia . 
This effect may be related to the pharmacological effect of this drug on mucous membranes . 
<mark>Nitro - L - arginine methyl ester</mark> : a potential protector against <mark>gentamicin</mark> ototoxicity . 
The <mark>nitric oxide</mark> ( <mark>NO</mark> ) inhibitor <mark>nitro - L - arginine methyl ester</mark> ( <mark>L - NAME</mark> ) may act as an otoprotectant against high - frequency hearing loss caused by <mark>gentamicin</mark> , but further studies are needed to confirm this . <mark>Aminoglycoside</mark> antibiotics are still widely used by virtue of their efficacy and low cost . 
Their ototoxicity is a serious health problem and , as their ototoxic mechanism involves the production of <mark>NO</mark> , we need to assess the use of <mark>NO</mark> inhibitors for the prevention of <mark>aminoglycoside</mark> - induced sensorineural hearing loss . 
In this experimental study we used 30 Sprague - Dawley rats , 27 of which had <mark>gentamicin</mark> instilled into the middle ear . 
The otoprotectant <mark>L - NAME</mark> was administered topically to 12 / 27 animals . 
Its effect was determined in terms of attenuation of hearing loss , measured by shifts in the auditory brainstem response threshold . 
<mark>L - NAME</mark> reduced <mark>gentamicin</mark> - induced hearing loss in the high - frequency range , but gave no protection in the middle or low frequencies . 
Safety profile of a <mark>nicotine</mark> lozenge compared with that of <mark>nicotine</mark> gum in adult smokers with underlying medical conditions : a 12 - week , randomized , open - label study . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Nicotine</mark> polacrilex lozenges deliver 25 % to 27 % more <mark>nicotine</mark> compared with equivalent doses of <mark>nicotine</mark> polacrilex gum . 
The increased <mark>nicotine</mark> exposure from the lozenge has raised questions about the relative safety of the lozenge and gum . 
OBJECTIVE : The objective of this study was to compare the safety profiles of the 4 - mg <mark>nicotine</mark> lozenge and 4 - mg <mark>nicotine</mark> gum in smokers with selected label - restricted diseases . 
METHODS : This was a multicenter , randomized , open - label study in adult smokers with heart disease , hypertension not controlled by medication , and / or diabetes mellitus . 
Patients were randomized in a 1 : 1 ratio to receive the 4 - mg <mark>nicotine</mark> lozenge or 4 - mg <mark>nicotine</mark> gum . 
Safety assessments were made at baseline and at 2 , 4 , 6 , and 12 weeks after the start of product use . 
RESULTS : Nine hundred one patients were randomized to treatment , 447 who received the lozenge and 454 who received the gum ( safety population ) . 
The majority were women ( 52 . 7 % ) . 
Patients ' mean age was 53 . 9 years , their mean weight was 193 . 9 pounds , and they smoked a mean of 25 . 2 cigarettes per day at baseline . 
Five hundred fifty - three patients , 264 taking the lozenge and 289 taking the gum , used the study product for > or = 4 days per week during the first 2 weeks ( evaluable population ) . 
The <mark>nicotine</mark> lozenge and <mark>nicotine</mark> gum were equally well tolerated , despite increased <mark>nicotine</mark> exposure from the lozenge . 
The incidence of adverse events in the 2 groups was similar during the first 2 weeks of product use ( evaluation population : 55 . 3 % lozenge , 54 . 7 % gum ) , as well as during the entire study ( safety population : 63 . 8 % and 58 . 6 % , respectively ) . 
Stratification of patients by sex , age , extent of concurrent smoking , extent of product use , and severity of adverse events revealed no clinically significant differences between the lozenge and gum . 
The most common adverse events were nausea ( 17 . 2 % and 16 . 1 % ; 95 % CI , - 3 . 7 to 6 . 0 ) , hiccups ( 10 . 7 % and 6 . 6 % ; 95 % CI , 0 . 5 to 7 . 8 ) , and headache ( 8 . 7 % and 9 . 9 % ; 95 % Cl , - 5 . 0 to 2 . 6 ) . 
Serious adverse events were reported in 11 and 13 patients in the respective groups . 
Fewer than 6 % of patients in either group were considered by the investigator to have a worsening of their overall disease condition during the study . 
The majority of patients ( > 60 % ) experienced no change in their disease status from baseline . 
CONCLUSION : The 4 - mg <mark>nicotine</mark> lozenge and 4 - mg <mark>nicotine</mark> gum had comparable safety profiles in these patients with label - restricted medical conditions . 
Pharmacological modulation of pain - related brain activity during normal and central sensitization states in humans . 
Abnormal processing of somatosensory inputs in the central nervous system ( central sensitization ) is the mechanism accounting for the enhanced pain sensitivity in the skin surrounding tissue injury ( secondary hyperalgesia ) . 
Secondary hyperalgesia shares clinical characteristics with neurogenic hyperalgesia in patients with neuropathic pain . 
Abnormal brain responses to somatosensory stimuli have been found in patients with hyperalgesia as well as in normal subjects during experimental central sensitization . 
The aim of this study was to assess the effects of <mark>gabapentin</mark> , a drug effective in neuropathic pain patients , on brain processing of nociceptive information in normal and central sensitization states . 
Using functional magnetic resonance imaging ( fMRI ) in normal volunteers , we studied the <mark>gabapentin</mark> - induced modulation of brain activity in response to nociceptive mechanical stimulation of normal skin and <mark>capsaicin</mark> - induced secondary hyperalgesia . 
The dose of <mark>gabapentin</mark> was 1 , 800 mg per os , in a single administration . 
We found that ( i ) <mark>gabapentin</mark> reduced the activations in the bilateral operculoinsular cortex , independently of the presence of central sensitization ; ( ii ) <mark>gabapentin</mark> reduced the activation in the brainstem , only during central sensitization ; ( iii ) <mark>gabapentin</mark> suppressed stimulus - induced deactivations , only during central sensitization ; this effect was more robust than the effect on brain activation . 
The observed drug - induced effects were not due to changes in the baseline fMRI signal . 
These findings indicate that <mark>gabapentin</mark> has a measurable antinociceptive effect and a stronger antihyperalgesic effect most evident in the brain areas undergoing deactivation , thus supporting the concept that <mark>gabapentin</mark> is more effective in modulating nociceptive transmission when central sensitization is present . 
Investigation of mitochondrial involvement in the experimental model of epilepsy induced by <mark>pilocarpine</mark> . 
Mitochondrial abnormalities have been associated with several aspects of epileptogenesis , such as energy generation , control of cell death , neurotransmitter synthesis , and free radical ( FR ) production . 
Increased production of FRs may cause mtDNA damage leading to decreased activities of oxidative phosphorylation complexes containing mtDNA - encoded subunits . 
In this study , we investigated whether increased generation of FR during status epilepticus would be sufficient to provoke abnormalities in mtDNA and in the expression and activity of cytochrome c oxidase ( CCO ) , complex IV of the respiratory chain , in the chronic phase of the <mark>pilocarpine</mark> model of temporal lobe epilepsy . 
DNA analysis revealed low amounts of a 4 . 8 kb mtDNA deletion but with no differences in frequency or quantity in the control and experimental groups . 
We did not find abnormalities in the expression and distribution of an mtDNA - encoded subunit of CCO ( CCO - I ) or a relative decrease in CCO - I when compared with nuclear - encoded subunits ( CCO - IV and SDH - fp ) . 
No abnormality in CCO activity was observed through histochemistry . 
Although evidences of mitochondrial abnormalities were found in previously published studies , our results do not suggest that the FRs , generated during the acute phase , determined important abnormalities in mtDNA , in expression of CCO - I , and in CCO activity .

<mark>Enalapril</mark> but not <mark>nitrendipine</mark> reduced blood pressure significantly .
