<mark>Ketoconazole</mark> induced torsades de pointes without concomitant use of QT interval - prolonging drug . 
<mark>Ketoconazole</mark> is not known to be proarrhythmic without concomitant use of QT interval - prolonging drugs . 
We report a woman with coronary artery disease who developed a markedly prolonged QT interval and torsades de pointes ( TdP ) after taking <mark>ketoconazole</mark> for treatment of fungal infection . 
Her QT interval returned to normal upon withdrawal of <mark>ketoconazole</mark> . 
Genetic study did not find any mutation in her genes that encode cardiac IKr channel proteins . 
We postulate that by virtue of its direct blocking action on IKr , <mark>ketoconazole</mark> alone may prolong QT interval and induce TdP . 
This calls for attention when <mark>ketoconazole</mark> is administered to patients with risk factors for acquired long QT syndrome . 
Cerebral vasculitis following oral <mark>methylphenidate</mark> intake in an adult : a case report . 
<mark>Methylphenidate</mark> is structurally and functionally similar to <mark>amphetamine</mark> . 
Cerebral vasculitis associated with amphetamine abuse is well documented , and in rare cases ischaemic stroke has been reported after <mark>methylphenidate</mark> intake in children . 
We report the case of a 63 - year - old female who was treated with <mark>methylphenidate</mark> due to hyperactivity and suffered from multiple ischaemic strokes . 
We consider drug - induced cerebral vasculitis as the most likely cause of recurrent ischaemic strokes in the absence of any pathological findings during the diagnostic work - up . 
We conclude that <mark>methylphenidate</mark> mediated vasculitis should be considered in patients with neurological symptoms and a history of <mark>methylphenidate</mark> therapy . 
This potential side - effect , though very rare , represents one more reason to be very restrictive in the use of <mark>methylphenidate</mark> . 
<mark>MDMA</mark> polydrug users show process - specific central executive impairments coupled with impaired social and emotional judgement processes . 
In recent years working memory deficits have been reported in users of <mark>MDMA</mark> ( <mark>3 , 4 - methylenedioxymethamphetamine</mark> , <mark>ecstasy</mark> ) . 
The current study aimed to assess the impact of <mark>MDMA</mark> use on three separate central executive processes ( set shifting , inhibition and memory updating ) and also on " prefrontal " mediated social and emotional judgement processes . 
Fifteen polydrug <mark>ecstasy</mark> users and 15 polydrug non - <mark>ecstasy</mark> user controls completed a general drug use questionnaire , the Brixton Spatial Anticipation task ( set shifting ) , Backward Digit Span procedure ( memory updating ) , Inhibition of Return ( inhibition ) , an emotional intelligence scale , the Tromso Social Intelligence Scale and the Dysexecutive Questionnaire ( DEX ) . 
Compared with <mark>MDMA</mark> - free polydrug controls , <mark>MDMA</mark> polydrug users showed impairments in set shifting and memory updating , and also in social and emotional judgement processes . 
The latter two deficits remained significant after controlling for other drug use . 
These data lend further support to the proposal that cognitive processes mediated by the prefrontal cortex may be impaired by recreational <mark>ecstasy</mark> use . 
Phase II study of the <mark>amsacrine</mark> analogue <mark>CI - 921</mark> ( <mark>NSC 343499</mark> ) in non - small cell lung cancer . 
<mark>CI - 921</mark> ( <mark>NSC 343499</mark> ; <mark>9 - [ [ 2 - methoxy - 4 - [ ( methylsulphonyl ) amino ] phenyl ] amino ] - N , 5 - dimethyl - 4 - acridinecarboxamide</mark> ) is a topoisomerase II poison with high experimental antitumour activity . 
It was administered by 15 min infusion to 16 evaluable patients with non - small cell lung cancer ( NSCLC ) ( 7 with no prior treatment , 9 patients in relapse following surgery / radiotherapy ) at a dose ( 648 mg / m2 divided over 3 days , repeated every 3 weeks ) determined by phase I trial . 
Patients had a median performance status of 1 ( WHO ) , and median age of 61 years . 
The histology comprised squamous carcinoma ( 11 ) , adenocarcinoma ( 1 ) , mixed histology ( 2 ) , bronchio - alveolar carcinoma ( 1 ) and large cell undifferentiated carcinoma ( 1 ) . 
Neutropenia grade greater than or equal to 3 was seen in 15 patients , infections with recovery in 3 , and grand mal seizures in 1 patient . 
Grade less than or equal to 2 nausea and vomiting occurred in 66 % courses and phlebitis in the infusion arm in 37 % . 
1 patient with squamous cell carcinoma achieved a partial response lasting 5 months . 
Further testing in this and other tumour types using multiple daily schedules is warranted . 
Pharmacokinetics of <mark>desipramine HCl</mark> when administered with <mark>cinacalcet HCl</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : In vitro work has demonstrated that <mark>cinacalcet</mark> is a strong inhibitor of cytochrome P450 isoenzyme ( CYP ) 2D6 . 
The purpose of this study was to evaluate the effect of <mark>cinacalcet</mark> on CYP2D6 activity , using <mark>desipramine</mark> as a probe substrate , in healthy subjects . 
METHODS : Seventeen subjects who were genotyped as CYP2D6 extensive metabolizers were enrolled in this randomized , open - label , crossover study to receive a single oral dose of <mark>desipramine</mark> ( 50 mg ) on two separate occasions , once alone and once after multiple doses of <mark>cinacalcet</mark> ( 90 mg for 7 days ) . 
Blood samples were obtained predose and up to 72 h postdose . 
RESULTS : Fourteen subjects completed both treatment arms . 
Relative to <mark>desipramine</mark> alone , mean AUC and C ( max ) of <mark>desipramine</mark> increased 3 . 6 - and 1 . 8 - fold when coadministered with <mark>cinacalcet</mark> . 
The t ( 1 / 2 , z ) of <mark>desipramine</mark> was longer when <mark>desipramine</mark> was coadministered with <mark>cinacalcet</mark> ( 21 . 0 versus 43 . 3 hs ) . 
The t ( max ) was similar between the regimens . 
Fewer subjects reported adverse events following treatment with <mark>desipramine</mark> alone than when receiving <mark>desipramine</mark> with <mark>cinacalcet</mark> ( 33 versus 86 % ) , the most frequent of which ( nausea and headache ) have been reported for patients treated with either <mark>desipramine</mark> or <mark>cinacalcet</mark> . 
CONCLUSION : This study demonstrates that <mark>cinacalcet</mark> is a strong inhibitor of CYP2D6 . 
These data suggest that during concomitant treatment with <mark>cinacalcet</mark> , dose adjustment may be necessary for drugs that demonstrate a narrow therapeutic index and are metabolized by CYP2D6 . 
Case report : acute unintentional <mark>carbachol</mark> intoxication . 
INTRODUCTION : Intoxications with <mark>carbachol</mark> , a muscarinic cholinergic receptor agonist are rare . 
We report an interesting case investigating a ( near ) fatal poisoning . 
METHODS : The son of an 84 - year - old male discovered a newspaper report stating clinical success with plant extracts in Alzheimer ' s disease . 
The mode of action was said to be comparable to that of the synthetic compound ' <mark>carbamylcholin</mark> ' ; that is , <mark>carbachol</mark> . 
He bought 25 g of <mark>carbachol</mark> as pure substance in a pharmacy , and the father was administered 400 to 500 mg . 
<mark>Carbachol</mark> concentrations in serum and urine on day 1 and 2 of hospital admission were analysed by HPLC - mass spectrometry . 
RESULTS : Minutes after oral administration , the patient developed nausea , sweating and hypotension , and finally collapsed . 
Bradycardia , cholinergic symptoms and asystole occurred . 
Initial cardiopulmonary resuscitation and immediate treatment with <mark>adrenaline</mark> ( <mark>epinephrine</mark> ) , <mark>atropine</mark> and <mark>furosemide</mark> was successful . 
On hospital admission , blood pressure of the intubated , bradyarrhythmic patient was 100 / 65 mmHg . 
Further signs were hyperhidrosis , hypersalivation , bronchorrhoea , and severe miosis ; the electrocardiographic finding was atrio - ventricular dissociation . 
High doses of <mark>atropine</mark> ( up to 50 mg per 24 hours ) , <mark>adrenaline</mark> and <mark>dopamine</mark> were necessary . 
The patient was extubated 1 week later . 
However , increased dyspnoea and bronchospasm necessitated reintubation . 
Respiratory insufficiency was further worsened by Proteus mirabilis infection and severe bronchoconstriction . 
One week later , the patient was again extubated and 3 days later was transferred to a peripheral ward . 
On the next day he died , probably as a result of heart failure . 
Serum samples from the first and second days contained 3 . 6 and 1 . 9 mg / l <mark>carbachol</mark> , respectively . 
The corresponding urine concentrations amounted to 374 and 554 mg / l . 
CONCLUSION : This case started with a media report in a popular newspaper , initiated by published , peer - reviewed research on herbals , and involved human failure in a case history , medical examination and clinical treatment . 
For the first time , an analytical method for the determination of <mark>carbachol</mark> in plasma and urine has been developed . 
The analysed <mark>carbachol</mark> concentration exceeded the supposed serum level resulting from a therapeutic dose by a factor of 130 to 260 . 
Especially in old patients , intensivists should consider intoxications ( with cholinergics ) as a cause of acute cardiovascular failure . 
Pharmacological evidence for the potential of Daucus carota in the management of cognitive dysfunctions . 
The present study was aimed at investigating the effects of Daucus carota seeds on cognitive functions , total serum <mark>cholesterol</mark> levels and brain cholinesterase activity in mice . 
The ethanolic <mark>extract of Daucus carota seeds</mark> ( <mark>DCE</mark> ) was administered orally in three doses ( 100 , 200 , 400 mg / kg ) for seven successive days to different groups of young and aged mice . 
Elevated plus maze and passive avoidance apparatus served as the exteroceptive behavioral models for testing memory . 
<mark>Diazepam</mark> - , <mark>scopolamine</mark> - and ageing - induced amnesia served as the interoceptive behavioral models . 
<mark>DCE</mark> ( 200 , 400 mg / kg , p . o . ) showed significant improvement in memory scores of young and aged mice . 
The extent of memory improvement evoked by <mark>DCE</mark> was 23 % at the dose of 200 mg / kg and 35 % at the dose of 400 mg / kg in young mice using elevated plus maze . 
Similarly , significant improvements in memory scores were observed using passive avoidance apparatus and aged mice . 
Furthermore , <mark>DCE</mark> reversed the amnesia induced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> ( 0 . 4 mg / kg , i . p . ) and <mark>diazepam</mark> ( 1 mg / kg , i . p . ) . 
<mark>Daucus carota extract</mark> ( 200 , 400 mg / kg , p . o . ) reduced significantly the brain acetylcholinesterase activity and <mark>cholesterol</mark> levels in young and aged mice . 
The extent of inhibition of brain cholinesterase activity evoked by <mark>DCE</mark> at the dose of 400 mg / kg was 22 % in young and 19 % in aged mice . 
There was a remarkable reduction in total <mark>cholesterol</mark> level as well , to the extent of 23 % in young and 21 % in aged animals with this dose of <mark>DCE</mark> . 
Therefore , <mark>DCE</mark> may prove to be a useful remedy for the management of cognitive dysfunctions on account of its multifarious beneficial effects such as , memory improving property , <mark>cholesterol</mark> lowering property and anticholinesterase activity . 
<mark>Valproic acid</mark> induced encephalopathy - - 19 new cases in Germany from 1994 to 2003 - - a side effect associated to <mark>VPA</mark> - therapy not only in young children . 
<mark>Valproic acid</mark> ( <mark>VPA</mark> ) is a broad - spectrum antiepileptic drug and is usually well - tolerated . 
Rare serious complications may occur in some patients , including haemorrhagic pancreatitis , bone marrow suppression , <mark>VPA</mark> - induced hepatotoxicity and <mark>VPA</mark> - induced encephalopathy . 
The typical signs of <mark>VPA</mark> - induced encephalopathy are impaired consciousness , sometimes marked EEG background slowing , increased seizure frequency , with or without hyperammonemia . 
There is still no proof of causative effect of <mark>VPA</mark> in patients with encephalopathy , but only of an association with an assumed causal relation . 
We report 19 patients with <mark>VPA</mark> - associated encephalopathy in Germany from the years 1994 to 2003 , none of whom had been published previously . 
Cerebral haemorrhage induced by <mark>warfarin</mark> - the influence of drug - drug interactions . 
PURPOSE : To evaluate the frequency , severity and preventability of <mark>warfarin</mark> - induced cerebral haemorrhages due to <mark>warfarin</mark> and <mark>warfarin</mark> - drug interactions in patients living in the county of Osterg tland , Sweden . 
METHODS : All patients with a diagnosed cerebral haemorrhage at three hospitals during the period 2000 - 2002 were identified . 
Medical records were studied retrospectively to evaluate whether <mark>warfarin</mark> and <mark>warfarin</mark> - drug interactions could have caused the cerebral haemorrhage . 
The proportion of possibly avoidable cases due to drug interactions was estimated . 
RESULTS : Among 593 patients with cerebral haemorrhage , 59 ( 10 % ) were assessed as related to <mark>warfarin</mark> treatment . 
This imply an incidence of 1 . 7 / 100 , 000 treatment years . 
Of the 59 cases , 26 ( 44 % ) had a fatal outcome , compared to 136 ( 25 % ) among the non - <mark>warfarin</mark> patients ( p < 0 . 01 ) . 
A <mark>warfarin</mark> - drug interaction could have contributed to the haemorrhage in 24 ( 41 % ) of the <mark>warfarin</mark> patients and in 7 of these ( 12 % ) the bleeding complication was considered being possible to avoid . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Warfarin</mark> - induced cerebral haemorrhages are a major clinical problem with a high fatality rate . 
Almost half of the cases was related to a <mark>warfarin</mark> - drug interaction . 
A significant proportion of <mark>warfarin</mark> - related cerebral haemorrhages might have been prevented if greater caution had been taken when prescribing drugs known to interact with <mark>warfarin</mark> . 
Antipsychotic - like profile of <mark>thioperamide</mark> , a selective H3 - receptor antagonist in mice . 
Experimental and clinical evidence points to a role of central histaminergic system in the pathogenesis of schizophrenia . 
The present study was designed to study the effect of <mark>histamine</mark> H ( 3 ) - receptor ligands on neuroleptic - induced catalepsy , <mark>apomorphine</mark> - induced climbing behavior and <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced locomotor activities in mice . 
Catalepsy was induced by <mark>haloperidol</mark> ( 2 mg / kg p . o . ) , while <mark>apomorphine</mark> ( 1 . 5 mg / kg s . c . ) and <mark>amphetamine</mark> ( 2 mg / kg s . c . ) were used for studying climbing behavior and locomotor activities , respectively . 
<mark>( R ) - alpha - methylhistamine</mark> ( <mark>RAMH</mark> ) ( 5 microg i . c . v . ) and <mark>thioperamide</mark> ( <mark>THP</mark> ) ( 15 mg / kg i . p . ) , per se did not cause catalepsy . 
Administration of <mark>THP</mark> ( 3 . 75 , 7 . 5 and 15 mg / kg i . p . ) 1 h prior to <mark>haloperidol</mark> resulted in a dose - dependent increase in the catalepsy times ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 
However , pretreatment with <mark>RAMH</mark> significantly reversed such an effect of <mark>THP</mark> ( 15 mg / kg i . p . ) . 
<mark>RAMH</mark> per se showed significant reduction in locomotor time , distance traveled and average speed but <mark>THP</mark> ( 15 mg / kg i . p . ) per se had no effect on these parameters . 
On <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced hyperactivity , <mark>THP</mark> ( 3 . 75 and 7 . 5 mg / kg i . p . ) reduced locomotor time , distance traveled and average speed ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 
Pretreatment with <mark>RAMH</mark> ( 5 microg i . c . v . ) could partially reverse such effects of <mark>THP</mark> ( 3 . 75 mg / kg i . p . ) . 
Climbing behavior induced by <mark>apomorphine</mark> was reduced in animals treated with <mark>THP</mark> . 
Such an effect was , however , reversed in presence of <mark>RAMH</mark> . 
<mark>THP</mark> exhibited an antipsychotic - like profile by potentiating <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced catalepsy , reducing <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced hyperactivity and reducing <mark>apomorphine</mark> - induced climbing in mice . 
Such effects of <mark>THP</mark> were reversed by <mark>RAMH</mark> indicating the involvement of <mark>histamine</mark> H ( 3 ) - receptors . 
Findings suggest a potential for H ( 3 ) - receptor antagonists in improving the refractory cases of schizophrenia . 
Cauda equina syndrome after epidural <mark>steroid</mark> injection : a case report . 
OBJECTIVE : Conventional treatment methods of lumbusacral radiculopathy are physical therapy , epidural <mark>steroid</mark> injections , oral medications , and spinal manipulative therapy . 
Cauda equina syndrome is a rare complication of epidural anesthesia . 
The following case is a report of cauda equina syndrome possibly caused by epidural injection of <mark>triamcinolone</mark> and <mark>bupivacaine</mark> . 
CLINICAL FEATURES : A 50 - year - old woman with low back and right leg pain was scheduled for epidural <mark>steroid</mark> injection . 
INTERVENTION AND OUTCOME : An 18 - gauge Touhy needle was inserted until loss of resistance occurred at the L4 - 5 level . 
Spread of the contrast medium within the epidural space was determined by radiographic imaging . 
After verifying the epidural space , <mark>bupivacaine</mark> and <mark>triamcinolone diacetate</mark> were injected . 
After the injection , there was a reduction in radicular symptoms . 
Three hours later , she complained of perineal numbness and lower extremity weakness . 
The neurologic evaluation revealed loss of sensation in the saddle area and medial aspect of her right leg . 
There was a decrease in the perception of pinprick test . 
Deep - tendon reflexes were decreased especially in the right leg . 
She was unable to urinate . 
The patient ' s symptoms improved slightly over the next few hours . 
She had a gradual return of motor function and ability of feeling Foley catheter . 
All of the symptoms were completely resolved over the next 8 hours . 
CONCLUSION : Complications associated with epidural <mark>steroid</mark> injections are rare . 
Clinical examination and continued vigilance for neurologic deterioration after epidural <mark>steroid</mark> injections is important . 
High - dose <mark>testosterone</mark> is associated with atherosclerosis in postmenopausal women . 
OBJECTIVES : To study the long - term effects of androgen treatment on atherosclerosis in postmenopausal women . 
METHODS : In a population - based study in 513 naturally postmenopausal women aged 54 - 67 years , we studied the association between self - reported intramuscularly administered high - dose <mark>estrogen</mark> - <mark>testosterone</mark> therapy ( <mark>estradiol - and testosterone esters</mark> ) and aortic atherosclerosis . 
Aortic atherosclerosis was diagnosed by radiographic detection of calcified deposits in the abdominal aorta , which have been shown to reflect intima atherosclerosis . 
Hormone therapy users were compared with never users . 
RESULTS : Intramuscular hormone therapy use for 1 year or longer was reported by 25 women . 
In almost half of these women severe atherosclerosis of the aorta was present ( n = 11 ) , while in women without hormone use severe atherosclerosis of the aorta was present in less than 20 % ( OR 3 . 1 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 1 - 8 . 5 , adjusted for age , years since menopause , smoking , and body mass index ) . 
The association remained after additional adjustment for diabetes , <mark>cholesterol</mark> level , systolic blood pressure , or <mark>alcohol</mark> use . 
No association was found for hormone use less than 1 year . 
CONCLUSION : Our results suggest that high - dose <mark>testosterone</mark> therapy may adversely affect atherosclerosis in postmenopausal women and indicate that androgen replacement in these women may not be harmless . 
Optimising stroke prevention in non - valvular atrial fibrillation . 
Atrial fibrillation is associated with substantial morbidity and mortality . 
Pooled data from trials comparing antithrombotic treatment with placebo have shown that <mark>warfarin</mark> reduces the risk of stroke by 62 % , and that <mark>aspirin</mark> alone reduces the risk by 22 % . 
Overall , in high - risk patients , <mark>warfarin</mark> is superior to <mark>aspirin</mark> in preventing strokes , with a relative risk reduction of 36 % . 
<mark>Ximelagatran</mark> , an oral direct thrombin inhibitor , was found to be as efficient as <mark>vitamin K</mark> antagonist drugs in the prevention of embolic events , but has been recently withdrawn because of abnormal liver function tests . 
The ACTIVE - W ( Atrial Fibrillation <mark>Clopidogrel</mark> Trial with <mark>Irbesartan</mark> for Prevention of Vascular Events ) study has demonstrated that <mark>warfarin</mark> is superior to platelet therapy ( <mark>clopidogrel</mark> plus <mark>aspirin</mark> ) in the prevention af embolic events . 
<mark>Idraparinux</mark> , a Factor Xa inhibitor , is being evaluated in patients with atrial fibrillation . 
<mark>Angiotensin</mark> - converting enzyme inhibitors and <mark>angiotensin II</mark> receptor - blocking drugs hold promise in atrial fibrillation through cardiac remodelling . 
Preliminary studies suggest that <mark>statins</mark> could interfere with the risk of recurrence after electrical cardioversion . 
Finally , percutaneous methods for the exclusion of left atrial appendage are under investigation in high - risk patients .

1 . 
<mark>Dexamethasone</mark> ( <mark>Dex</mark> ) - induced hypertension is characterized by endothelial dysfunction associated with <mark>nitric oxide</mark> ( <mark>NO</mark> ) deficiency and increased <mark>superoxide</mark> ( <mark>O2 -</mark> ) production . 
<mark>Atorvastatin</mark> ( <mark>Ato</mark> ) possesses pleiotropic properties that have been reported to improve endothelial function through increased availability of <mark>NO</mark> and reduced <mark>O2 -</mark> production in various forms of hypertension .

2 .

<mark>Dexamethasone</mark> ( 10 microg / kg per day , s . c . ) or saline was started after 4 days in <mark>Ato</mark> - treated and non - treated rats and continued for 11 - 13 days . 
Systolic blood pressure ( SBP ) was measured on alternate days using the tail - cuff method . 
Endothelial function was assessed by <mark>acetylcholine</mark> - induced vasorelaxation and <mark>phenylephrine</mark> - induced vasoconstriction in aortic segments . 
Vascular eNOS mRNA was assessed by semi - quantitative reverse transcription - polymerase chain reaction . 
3 .

In the <mark>Ato</mark> + <mark>Dex</mark> group , SBP was increased from 113 + / - 2 to 119 + / - 2 mmHg on Days 4 to 14 , respectively ( P < 0 . 001 ) , but was significantly lower than SBP in the group treated with <mark>Dex</mark> alone ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 
Endothelial - dependent relaxation and eNOS mRNA expression were greater in the <mark>Dex</mark> + <mark>Ato</mark> group than in the <mark>Dex</mark> only group ( P < 0 . 05 and P < 0 . 0001 , respectively ) . 
Aortic <mark>superoxide</mark> production was lower in the <mark>Dex</mark> + <mark>Ato</mark> group compared with the group treated with <mark>Dex</mark> alone ( P < 0 . 0001 ) .

Treatment with <mark>Ato</mark> improved endothelial function , reduced <mark>superoxide</mark> production and reduced SBP in <mark>Dex</mark> - treated SD rats . 
Severe <mark>citrate</mark> toxicity complicating volunteer apheresis platelet donation . 
We report a case of severe <mark>citrate</mark> toxicity during volunteer donor apheresis platelet collection . 
The donor was a 40 - year - old female , first - time apheresis platelet donor . 
Past medical history was remarkable for hypertension , hyperlipidemia , and depression . 
Reported medications included <mark>bumetanide</mark> , <mark>pravastatin</mark> , and <mark>paroxetine</mark> . 
Thirty minutes from the start of the procedure , the donor noted tingling around the mouth , hands , and feet . 
She then very rapidly developed acute onset of severe facial and extremity tetany . 
Empirical treatment with intravenous <mark>calcium gluconate</mark> was initiated , and muscle contractions slowly subsided over approximately 10 to 15 minutes . 
The events are consistent with a severe reaction to <mark>calcium</mark> chelation by <mark>sodium citrate</mark> anticoagulant resulting in symptomatic systemic hypocalcemia . 
Upon additional retrospective analysis , it was noted that <mark>bumetanide</mark> is a <mark>loop diuretic</mark> that may cause significant hypocalcemia . 
We conclude that careful screening for medications and underlying conditions predisposing to hypocalcemia is recommended to help prevent severe reactions due to <mark>citrate</mark> toxicity . 
Laboratory measurement of pre - procedure serum <mark>calcium</mark> levels in selected donors may identify cases requiring heightened vigilance . 
The case also illustrates the importance of maintaining preparedness for managing rare but serious reactions in volunteer apheresis blood donors . 
<mark>Sirolimus</mark> - associated proteinuria and renal dysfunction . 
<mark>Sirolimus</mark> is a novel immunosuppressant with potent antiproliferative actions through its ability to inhibit the raptor - containing mammalian target of <mark>rapamycin</mark> protein kinase . 
<mark>Sirolimus</mark> represents a major therapeutic advance in the prevention of acute renal allograft rejection and chronic allograft nephropathy . 
Its role in the therapy of glomerulonephritis , autoimmunity , cystic renal diseases and renal cancer is under investigation . 
Because <mark>sirolimus</mark> does not share the vasomotor renal adverse effects exhibited by calcineurin inhibitors , it has been designated a ' non - nephrotoxic drug ' . 
However , clinical reports suggest that , under some circumstances , <mark>sirolimus</mark> is associated with proteinuria and acute renal dysfunction . 
A common risk factor appears to be presence of pre - existing chronic renal damage . 
The mechanisms of <mark>sirolimus</mark> - associated proteinuria are multifactorial and may be due to an increase in glomerular capillary pressure following calcineurin inhibitor withdrawal . 
It has also been suggested that <mark>sirolimus</mark> directly causes increased glomerular permeability / injury , but evidence for this mechanism is currently inconclusive . 
The acute renal dysfunction associated with <mark>sirolimus</mark> ( such as in delayed graft function ) may be due to suppression of compensatory renal cell proliferation and survival / repair processes . 
Although these adverse effects occur in some patients , their occurrence could be minimised by knowledge of the molecular effects of <mark>sirolimus</mark> on the kidney , the use of <mark>sirolimus</mark> in appropriate patient populations , close monitoring of proteinuria and renal function , use of <mark>angiotensin</mark> - converting enzyme inhibitors or <mark>angiotensin II</mark> receptor blockers if proteinuria occurs and withdrawal if needed . 
Further long - term analysis of renal allograft studies using <mark>sirolimus</mark> as de novo immunosuppression along with clinical and laboratory studies will refine these issues in the future . 
Proteinuria after conversion to <mark>sirolimus</mark> in renal transplant recipients . 
<mark>Sirolimus</mark> ( <mark>SRL</mark> ) is a new , potent immunosuppressive agent . 
More recently , proteinuria has been reported as a consequence of <mark>sirolimus</mark> therapy , although the mechanism has remained unclear . 
We retrospectively examined the records of 25 renal transplant patients , who developed or displayed increased proteinuria after <mark>SRL</mark> conversion . 
The patient cohort ( 14 men , 11 women ) was treated with <mark>SRL</mark> as conversion therapy , due to chronic allograft nephropathy ( CAN ) ( n = 15 ) neoplasia ( n = 8 ) ; Kaposi ' s sarcoma , Four skin cancers , One intestinal tumors , One renal cell carsinom ) or BK virus nephropathy ( n = 2 ) . 
<mark>SRL</mark> was started at a mean of 78 + / - 42 ( 15 to 163 ) months after transplantation . 
Mean follow - up on <mark>SRL</mark> therapy was 20 + / - 12 ( 6 to 43 ) months . 
Proteinuria increased from 0 . 445 ( 0 to 1 . 5 ) g / d before conversion to 3 . 2 g / dL ( 0 . 2 to 12 ) after conversion ( P = 0 . 001 ) . 
Before conversion 8 ( 32 % ) patients had no proteinuria , whereas afterwards all patients had proteinuria . 
In 28 % of patients proteinuria remained unchanged , whereas it increased in 68 % of patients . 
In 40 % it increased by more than 100 % . 
Twenty - eight percent of patients showed increased proteinuria to the nephrotic range . 
Biopsies performed in five patients revealed new pathological changes : One membranoproliferative glomerulopathy and interstitial nephritis . 
These patients showed persistently good graft function . 
Serum <mark>creatinine</mark> values did not change significantly : 1 . 98 + / - 0 . 8 mg / dL before <mark>SRL</mark> therapy and 2 . 53 + / - 1 . 9 mg / dL at last follow - up ( P = . 14 ) . 
Five grafts were lost and the patients returned to dialysis . 
Five patients displayed CAN and Kaposi ' s sarcoma . 
Mean urinary protein of patients who returned to dialysis was 1 . 26 ( 0 . 5 to 3 . 5 ) g / d before and 4 . 7 ( 3 to 12 ) g / d after conversion ( P = . 01 ) . 
Mean serum <mark>creatinine</mark> level before conversion was 2 . 21 mg / dL and thereafter , 4 . 93 mg / dL ( P = . 02 ) . 
Heavy proteinuria was common after the use of <mark>SRL</mark> as rescue therapy for renal transplantation . 
Therefore , conversion should be considered for patients who have not developed advanced CAN and proteinuria . 
The possibility of de novo glomerular pathology under <mark>SRL</mark> treatment requires further investigation by renal biopsy . 
Long - term follow - up of <mark>ifosfamide</mark> renal toxicity in children treated for malignant mesenchymal tumors : an International Society of Pediatric Oncology report . 
The renal function of 74 children with malignant mesenchymal tumors in complete remission and who have received the same <mark>ifosfamide</mark> chemotherapy protocol ( International Society of Pediatric Oncology Malignant Mesenchymal Tumor Study 84 [ SIOP MMT 84 ] ) were studied 1 year after the completion of treatment . 
Total cumulative doses were 36 or 60 g / m2 of <mark>ifosfamide</mark> ( six or 10 cycles of <mark>ifosfamide , vincristine , and dactinomycin</mark> [ <mark>IVA</mark> ] ) . 
None of them had received <mark>cisplatin</mark> chemotherapy . 
Ages ranged from 4 months to 17 years ; 58 patients were males and 42 females . 
The most common primary tumor site was the head and neck . 
Renal function was investigated by measuring plasma and urinary electrolytes , glucosuria , proteinuria , aminoaciduria , urinary pH , osmolarity , <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance , <mark>phosphate</mark> tubular reabsorption , beta 2 microglobulinuria , and lysozymuria . 
Fifty - eight patients ( 78 % ) had normal renal tests , whereas 16 patients ( 22 % ) had renal abnormalities . 
Two subsets of patients were identified from this latter group : the first included four patients ( 5 % of the total population ) who developed major toxicity resulting in Fanconi ' s syndrome ( TDFS ) ; and the second group included five patients with elevated beta 2 microglobulinuria and low <mark>phosphate</mark> reabsorption . 
The remaining seven patients had isolated beta 2 microglobulinuria . 
Severe toxicity was correlated with the higher cumulative dose of 60 g / m2 of <mark>ifosfamide</mark> , a younger age ( less than 2 1 / 2 years old ) , and a predominance of vesicoprostatic tumor involvement . 
This low percentage ( 5 % ) of TDFS must be evaluated with respect to the efficacy of <mark>ifosfamide</mark> in the treatment of mesenchymal tumors in children . 
Progressive myopathy with up - regulation of MHC - I associated with <mark>statin</mark> therapy . 
<mark>Statins</mark> can cause a necrotizing myopathy and hyperCKaemia which is reversible on cessation of the drug . 
What is less well known is a phenomenon whereby <mark>statins</mark> may induce a myopathy , which persists or may progress after stopping the drug . 
We investigated the muscle pathology in 8 such cases . 
All had myofibre necrosis but only 3 had an inflammatory infiltrate . 
In all cases there was diffuse or multifocal up - regulation of MHC - I expression even in non - necrotic fibres . 
Progressive improvement occurred in 7 cases after commencement of <mark>prednisolone</mark> and <mark>methotrexate</mark> , and in one case spontaneously . 
These observations suggest that <mark>statins</mark> may initiate an immune - mediated myopathy that persists after withdrawal of the drug and responds to immunosuppressive therapy . 
The mechanism of this myopathy is uncertain but may involve the induction by <mark>statins</mark> of an endoplasmic reticulum stress response with associated up - regulation of MHC - I expression and antigen presentation by muscle fibres . 
Use of chromosome substitution strains to identify seizure susceptibility loci in mice . 
Seizure susceptibility varies among inbred mouse strains . 
Chromosome substitution strains ( CSS ) , in which a single chromosome from one inbred strain ( donor ) has been transferred onto a second strain ( host ) by repeated backcrossing , may be used to identify quantitative trait loci ( QTLs ) that contribute to seizure susceptibility . 
QTLs for susceptibility to <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizures , a model of temporal lobe epilepsy , have not been reported , and CSS have not previously been used to localize seizure susceptibility genes . 
We report QTLs identified using a B6 ( host ) x A / J ( donor ) CSS panel to localize genes involved in susceptibility to <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizures . 
Three hundred fifty - five adult male CSS mice , 58 B6 , and 39 A / J were tested for susceptibility to <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizures . 
Highest stage reached and latency to each stage were recorded for all mice . 
B6 mice were resistant to seizures and slower to reach stages compared to A / J mice . 
The CSS for Chromosomes 10 and 18 progressed to the most severe stages , diverging dramatically from the B6 phenotype . 
Latencies to stages were also significantly shorter for CSS10 and CSS18 mice . 
CSS mapping suggests seizure susceptibility loci on mouse Chromosomes 10 and 18 . 
This approach provides a framework for identifying potentially novel homologous candidate genes for human temporal lobe epilepsy . 
In vitro characterization of parasympathetic and sympathetic responses in <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - induced cystitis in the rat . 
In <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - induced cystitis in the rat , detrusor function is impaired and the expression and effects of muscarinic receptors altered . 
Whether or not the neuronal transmission may be affected by cystitis was presently investigated . 
Responses of urinary strip preparations from control and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - pretreated rats to electrical field stimulation and to agonists were assessed in the absence and presence of muscarinic , adrenergic and purinergic receptor antagonists . 
Generally , <mark>atropine</mark> reduced contractions , but in contrast to controls , it also reduced responses to low electrical field stimulation intensity ( 1 - 5 Hz ) in inflamed preparations . 
In both types , purinoceptor desensitization with <mark>alpha , beta - methylene adenosine - 5 ' - triphosphate</mark> ( <mark>alpha , beta - meATP</mark> ) caused further reductions at low frequencies ( < 10 Hz ) . 
The muscarinic receptor antagonists <mark>atropine</mark> , <mark>4 - diphenylacetoxy - N - methylpiperidine</mark> ( <mark>4 - DAMP</mark> ) ( ' M ( 1 ) / M ( 3 ) / M ( 5 ) - selective ' ) , <mark>methoctramine</mark> ( ' M ( 2 ) - selective ' ) and <mark>pirenzepine</mark> ( ' M ( 1 ) - selective ' ) antagonized the tonic component of the electrical field stimulation - evoked contractile response more potently than the phasic component . 
<mark>4 - DAMP</mark> inhibited the tonic contractions in controls more potently than <mark>methoctramine</mark> and <mark>pirenzepine</mark> . 
In inflamed preparations , the muscarinic receptor antagonism on the phasic component of the electrical field stimulation - evoked contraction was decreased and the <mark>pirenzepine</mark> and <mark>4 - DAMP</mark> antagonism on the tonic component was much less efficient than in controls . 
In contrast to controls , <mark>methoctramine</mark> increased - - instead of decreased - - the tonic responses at high frequencies . 
While contractions to <mark>carbachol</mark> and <mark>ATP</mark> were the same in inflamed and in control strips when related to a reference <mark>potassium</mark> response , <mark>isoprenaline</mark> - induced relaxations were smaller in inflamed strips . 
Thus , in cystitis substantial changes of the efferent functional responses occur . 
While postjunctional beta - adrenoceptor - mediated relaxations are reduced , effects by prejunctional inhibitory muscarinic receptors may be increased . 
Direct inhibition of cardiac hyperpolarization - activated <mark>cyclic nucleotide</mark> - gated pacemaker channels by <mark>clonidine</mark> . 
BACKGROUND : Inhibition of cardiac sympathetic tone represents an important strategy for treatment of cardiovascular disease , including arrhythmia , coronary heart disease , and chronic heart failure . 
Activation of presynaptic alpha2 - adrenoceptors is the most widely accepted mechanism of action of the antisympathetic drug <mark>clonidine</mark> ; however , other target proteins have been postulated to contribute to the in vivo actions of <mark>clonidine</mark> . 
METHODS AND RESULTS : To test whether <mark>clonidine</mark> elicits pharmacological effects independent of alpha2 - adrenoceptors , we have generated mice with a targeted deletion of all 3 alpha2 - adrenoceptor subtypes ( alpha2ABC - / - ) . 
Alpha2ABC - / - mice were completely unresponsive to the analgesic and hypnotic effects of <mark>clonidine</mark> ; however , <mark>clonidine</mark> significantly lowered heart rate in alpha2ABC - / - mice by up to 150 bpm . 
<mark>Clonidine</mark> - induced bradycardia in conscious alpha2ABC - / - mice was 32 . 3 % ( 10 microg / kg ) and 26 . 6 % ( 100 microg / kg ) of the effect in wild - type mice . 
A similar bradycardic effect of <mark>clonidine</mark> was observed in isolated spontaneously beating right atria from alpha2ABC - knockout and wild - type mice . 
<mark>Clonidine</mark> inhibited the native pacemaker current ( I ( f ) ) in isolated sinoatrial node pacemaker cells and the I ( f ) - generating hyperpolarization - activated <mark>cyclic nucleotide</mark> - gated ( HCN ) 2 and HCN4 channels in transfected HEK293 cells . 
As a consequence of blocking I ( f ) , <mark>clonidine</mark> reduced the slope of the diastolic depolarization and the frequency of pacemaker potentials in sinoatrial node cells from wild - type and alpha2ABC - knockout mice . 
CONCLUSIONS : Direct inhibition of cardiac HCN pacemaker channels contributes to the bradycardic effects of <mark>clonidine</mark> gene - targeted mice in vivo , and thus , <mark>clonidine</mark> - like drugs represent novel structures for future HCN channel inhibitors . 
Granulomatous hepatitis due to <mark>combination of amoxicillin and clavulanic acid</mark> . 
We report the case of a patient with <mark>amoxicillin - clavulanic acid</mark> - induced hepatitis with histologic multiple granulomas . 
This type of lesion broadens the spectrum of liver injury due to this drug combination , mainly represented by a benign cholestatic syndrome . 
The association of granulomas and eosinophilia favor an immunoallergic mechanism . 
As <mark>penicillin</mark> derivatives and <mark>amoxicillin</mark> alone are known to induce such types of lesions , the <mark>amoxicillin</mark> component , with or without a potentiating effect of <mark>clavulanic acid</mark> , might have a major role . 
<mark>Dobutamine</mark> stress echocardiography : a sensitive indicator of diminished myocardial function in asymptomatic <mark>doxorubicin</mark> - treated long - term survivors of childhood cancer . 
<mark>Doxorubicin</mark> is an effective anticancer chemotherapeutic agent known to cause acute and chronic cardiomyopathy . 
To develop a more sensitive echocardiographic screening test for cardiac damage due to <mark>doxorubicin</mark> , a cohort study was performed using <mark>dobutamine</mark> infusion to differentiate asymptomatic long - term survivors of childhood cancer treated with <mark>doxorubicin</mark> from healthy control subjects . 
Echocardiographic data from the experimental group of 21 patients ( mean age 16 + / - 5 years ) treated from 1 . 6 to 14 . 3 years ( median 5 . 3 ) before this study with 27 to 532 mg / m2 of <mark>doxorubicin</mark> ( mean 196 ) were compared with echocardiographic data from 12 normal age - matched control subjects .

<mark>Dobutamine</mark> infusion at 10 micrograms / kg per min was discontinued after six studies secondary to a 50 % incidence rate of adverse symptoms . 
The most important findings were that compared with values in control subjects , end - systolic left ventricular posterior wall dimension and percent of left ventricular posterior wall thickening in <mark>doxorubicin</mark> - treated patients were decreased at baseline study and these findings were more clearly delineated with <mark>dobutamine</mark> stimulation .

End - systolic left ventricular posterior wall dimension at the 5 - micrograms / kg per min <mark>dobutamine</mark> infusion for the <mark>doxorubicin</mark> - treated group was 14 . 1 + / - 2 . 4 mm versus 19 . 3 + / - 2 . 6 mm for control subjects ( p less than 0 . 01 ) . Influence of <mark>smoking</mark> on developing cochlea . 
Does <mark>smoking</mark> during pregnancy affect the amplitudes of transient evoked otoacoustic emissions in newborns ? 
OBJECTIVE : Maternal tobacco <mark>smoking</mark> has negative effects on fetal growth . 
The influence of <mark>smoking</mark> during pregnancy on the developing cochlea has not been estimated , although <mark>smoking</mark> has been positively associated with hearing loss in adults . 
The objective of this study was to determine the effects of maternal <mark>smoking</mark> on transient evoked otoacoustic emissions ( TEOAEs ) of healthy neonates . 
METHODS : This study was undertaken as part of neonatal screening for hearing impairment and involved both ears of 200 newborns . 
Newborns whose mothers reported <mark>smoking</mark> during pregnancy ( n = 200 ears ) were compared to a control group of newborns ( n = 200 ears ) , whose mothers were non - smokers . 
Exposure to tobacco was characterized as low ( < 5 cigarettes per day , n = 88 ears ) , moderate ( 5 < or = cigarettes per day < 10 , n = 76 ) or high ( > or = 10 cigarettes per day , n = 36 ) . 
RESULTS : In exposed neonates , TEOAEs mean response ( across frequency ) and mean amplitude at 4000Hz was significantly lower than in non - exposed neonates . 
Comparisons between exposed newborns ' subgroups revealed no significant differences . 
However , by comparing each subgroup to control group , we found statistically significant decreases of TEOAEs amplitudes at 4000Hz for all three groups . 
Mean TEOAEs responses of highly exposed newborns were also significantly lower in comparison to our control group . 
CONCLUSION : In utero , exposure to tobacco <mark>smoking</mark> seems to have a small impact on outer hair cells . 
These effects seem to be equally true for all exposed newborns , regardless of the degree of exposure . 
Further studies are needed in order to establish a potential negative effect of maternal <mark>smoking</mark> on the neonate ' s hearing acuity . 
<mark>Simvastatin</mark> - induced bilateral leg compartment syndrome and myonecrosis associated with hypothyroidism . 
A 54 - year - old hypothyroid male taking <mark>thyroxine</mark> and <mark>simvastatin</mark> presented with bilateral leg compartment syndrome and myonecrosis . 
Urgent fasciotomies were performed and the patient made an uneventful recovery with the withdrawal of <mark>simvastatin</mark> . 
It is likely that this complication will be seen more often with the increased worldwide use of this drug and its approval for all arteriopathic patients . 
Neuroinflammation and behavioral abnormalities after neonatal <mark>terbutaline</mark> treatment in rats : implications for autism . 
Autism is a neurodevelopmental disorder presenting before 3 years of age with deficits in communication and social skills and repetitive behaviors . 
In addition to genetic influences , recent studies suggest that prenatal drug or chemical exposures are risk factors for autism . 
<mark>Terbutaline</mark> , a beta2 - adrenoceptor agonist used to arrest preterm labor , has been associated with increased concordance for autism in dizygotic twins . 
We studied the effects of <mark>terbutaline</mark> on microglial activation in different brain regions and behavioral outcomes in developing rats . 
Newborn rats were given <mark>terbutaline</mark> ( 10 mg / kg ) daily on postnatal days ( PN ) 2 to 5 or PN 11 to 14 and examined 24 h after the last dose and at PN 30 . 
Immunohistochemical studies showed that administration of <mark>terbutaline</mark> on PN 2 to 5 produced a robust increase in microglial activation on PN 30 in the cerebral cortex , as well as in cerebellar and cerebrocortical white matter . 
None of these effects occurred in animals given <mark>terbutaline</mark> on PN 11 to 14 . 
In behavioral tests , animals treated with <mark>terbutaline</mark> on PN 2 to 5 showed consistent patterns of hyper - reactivity to novelty and aversive stimuli when assessed in a novel open field , as well as in the acoustic startle response test . 
Our findings indicate that beta2 - adrenoceptor overstimulation during an early critical period results in microglial activation associated with innate neuroinflammatory pathways and behavioral abnormalities , similar to those described in autism . 
This study provides a useful animal model for understanding the neuropathological processes underlying autism spectrum disorders . 
Upregulation of brain expression of P - glycoprotein in MRP2 - deficient TR ( - ) rats resembles seizure - induced up - regulation of this drug efflux transporter in normal rats . 
PURPOSE : The multidrug resistance protein 2 ( MRP2 ) is a drug efflux transporter that is expressed predominantly at the apical domain of hepatocytes but seems also to be expressed at the apical membrane of brain capillary endothelial cells that form the blood - brain barrier ( BBB ) . 
MRP2 is absent in the transport - deficient ( TR ( - ) ) Wistar rat mutant , so that this rat strain was very helpful in defining substrates of MRP2 by comparing tissue concentrations or functional activities of compounds in MRP2 - deficient rats with those in transport - competent Wistar rats . 
By using this strategy to study the involvement of MRP2 in brain access of antiepileptic drugs ( AEDs ) , we recently reported that <mark>phenytoin</mark> is a substrate for MRP2 in the BBB . 
However , one drawback of such studies in genetically deficient rats is the fact that compensatory changes with upregulation of other transporters can occur . 
This prompted us to study the brain expression of P - glycoprotein ( Pgp ) , a major drug efflux transporter in many tissues , including the BBB , in TR ( - ) rats compared with nonmutant ( wild - type ) Wistar rats . 
METHODS : The expression of MRP2 and Pgp in brain and liver sections of TR ( - ) rats and normal Wistar rats was determined with immunohistochemistry , by using a novel , highly selective monoclonal MRP2 antibody and the monoclonal Pgp antibody C219 , respectively . 
RESULTS : Immunofluorescence staining with the MRP2 antibody was found to label a high number of microvessels throughout the brain in normal Wistar rats , whereas such labeling was absent in TR ( - ) rats . 
TR ( - ) rats exhibited a significant up - regulation of Pgp in brain capillary endothelial cells compared with wild - type controls . 
No such obvious upregulation of Pgp was observed in liver sections . 
A comparable overexpression of Pgp in the BBB was obtained after <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizures in wild - type Wistar rats . 
Experiments with systemic administration of the Pgp substrate <mark>phenobarbital</mark> and the selective Pgp inhibitor <mark>tariquidar</mark> in TR ( - ) rats substantiated that Pgp is functional and compensates for the lack of MRP2 in the BBB . 
CONCLUSIONS : The data on TR ( - ) rats indicate that Pgp plays an important role in the compensation of MRP2 deficiency in the BBB . 
Because such a compensatory mechanism most likely occurs to reduce injury to the brain from cytotoxic compounds , the present data substantiate the concept that MRP2 performs a protective role in the BBB . 
Furthermore , our data suggest that TR ( - ) rats are an interesting tool to study consequences of overexpression of Pgp in the BBB on access of drugs in the brain , without the need of inducing seizures or other Pgp - enhancing events for this purpose . 
Role of <mark>xanthine</mark> oxidase in <mark>dexamethasone</mark> - induced hypertension in rats . 
1 . 
Glucocorticoid - induced hypertension ( GC - HT ) in the rat is associated with <mark>nitric oxide</mark> - redox imbalance . 
2 . 
We studied the role of <mark>xanthine</mark> oxidase ( XO ) , which is implicated in the production of reactive oxygen species , in <mark>dexamethasone</mark> - induced hypertension ( <mark>dex</mark> - HT ) . 
3 . 
Thirty male Sprague - Dawley rats were divided randomly into four treatment groups : saline , <mark>dexamethasone</mark> ( <mark>dex</mark> ) , <mark>allopurinol</mark> plus saline , and <mark>allopurinol</mark> plus <mark>dex</mark> . 
4 . 
Systolic blood pressures ( SBP ) and bodyweights were recorded each alternate day . 
Thymus weight was used as a marker of glucocorticoid activity , and serum <mark>urate</mark> to assess XO inhibition . 
5 . 
<mark>Dex</mark> increased SBP ( 110 + / - 2 - 126 + / - 3 mmHg ; P < 0 . 001 ) and decreased thymus ( P < 0 . 001 ) and bodyweights ( P " < 0 . 01 ) . 
<mark>Allopurinol</mark> decreased serum <mark>urate</mark> from 76 + / - 5 to 30 + / - 3 micromol / L ( P < 0 . 001 ) in saline and from 84 + / - 13 to 28 + / - 2 micromol / L in <mark>dex</mark> - treated ( P < 0 . 01 ) groups . 
6 . 
<mark>Allopurinol</mark> did not prevent <mark>dex</mark> - HT . 
This , together with our previous findings that <mark>allopurinol</mark> failed to prevent adrenocorticotrophic hormone induced hypertension , suggests that XO activity is not a major determinant of GC - HT in the rat . 
Side effects of postoperative administration of <mark>methylprednisolone</mark> and <mark>gentamicin</mark> into the posterior sub - Tenon ' s space . 
PURPOSE : To assess the incidence of postoperative emetic side effects after the administration of <mark>methylprednisolone</mark> and <mark>gentamicin</mark> into the posterior sub - Tenon ' s space at the end of routine cataract surgery . 
SETTING : St . 
Luke ' s Hospital , Gwardamangia , Malta . 
METHODS : A double - blind double - armed prospective study comprised 40 patients who had uneventful sutureless phacoemulsification under sub - Tenon ' s local infiltration of 3 mL of plain <mark>lignocaine</mark> . 
At the end of the procedure , Group A ( n = 20 ) had 20 mg / 0 . 5 mL of <mark>methylprednisolone</mark> and 10 mg / 0 . 5 mL of <mark>gentamicin</mark> injected into the posterior sub - Tenon ' s space and Group B ( n = 20 ) had the same combination injected into the anterior sub - Tenon ' s space . 
Postoperatively , all patients were assessed for symptoms of nausea , vomiting , and headache . 
A chi - square test was used to assess the statistical significance of results . 
RESULTS : Sixty percent in Group A developed postoperative emetic symptoms , headache , or both ; 1 patient in Group B developed symptoms . 
CONCLUSIONS : The administration of <mark>methylprednisolone</mark> and <mark>gentamicin</mark> in the posterior sub - Tenon ' s space was related to a high incidence of side effects including nausea , vomiting , and headache .

Assessment of a new non - invasive index of cardiac performance for detection of <mark>dobutamine</mark> - induced myocardial ischemia . 
BACKGROUND : Electrocardiography has a very low sensitivity in detecting <mark>dobutamine</mark> - induced myocardial ischemia . 
OBJECTIVES : To assess the added diagnostic value of a new cardiac performance index ( dP / dtejc ) measurement , based on brachial artery flow changes , as compared to standard 12 - lead ECG , for detecting <mark>dobutamine</mark> - induced myocardial ischemia , using <mark>Tc99m - Sestamibi</mark> single - photon emission computed tomography as the gold standard of comparison to assess the presence or absence of ischemia . 
METHODS : The study group comprised 40 patients undergoing <mark>Sestamibi</mark> - SPECT / <mark>dobutamine</mark> stress test . 
Simultaneous measurements of ECG and brachial artery dP / dtejc were performed at each <mark>dobutamine</mark> level . 
In 19 of the 40 patients perfusion defects compatible with ischemia were detected on SPECT . 
The increase in dP / dtejc during infusion of <mark>dobutamine</mark> in this group was severely impaired as compared to the non - ischemic group . 
dP / dtejc outcome was combined with the ECG results , giving an ECG - enhanced value , and compared to ECG alone . 
RESULTS : The sensitivity improved dramatically from 16 % to 79 % , positive predictive value increased from 60 % to 68 % and negative predictive value from 54 % to 78 % , and specificity decreased from 90 % to 67 % . 
CONCLUSIONS : If ECG alone is used for specificity , the combination with dP / dtejc improved the sensitivity of the test and could be a cost - savings alternative to cardiac imaging or perfusion studies to detect myocardial ischemia , especially in patients unable to exercise . 
<mark>Cocaine</mark> - induced myocardial infarction : clinical observations and pathogenetic considerations . 
Clinical and experimental data published to date suggest several possible mechanisms by which <mark>cocaine</mark> may result in acute myocardial infarction . 
In individuals with preexisting , high - grade coronary arterial narrowing , acute myocardial infarction may result from an increase in myocardial <mark>oxygen</mark> demand associated with <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced increase in rate - pressure product . 
In other individuals with no underlying atherosclerotic obstruction , coronary occlusion may be due to spasm , thrombus , or both . 
With regard to spasm , the clinical findings are largely circumstantial , and the locus of <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced vasoconstriction remains speculative . 
Although certain clinical and experimental findings support the hypothesis that spasm involves the epicardial , medium - size vessels , other data suggest intramural vasoconstriction . 
Diffuse intramural vasoconstriction is not consistent with reports of segmental , discrete infarction . 
Whereas certain in vivo data suggest that these effects are alpha - mediated , other in vitro data suggest the opposite . 
The finding of <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced vasoconstriction in segments of ( noninnervated ) human umbilical artery suggests that the presence or absence of intact innervation is not sufficient to explain the discrepant data involving the possibility of alpha - mediated effects . 
Finally , the contribution of a primary , thrombotic effect of <mark>cocaine</mark> has not been excluded . 
Proteomic analysis of striatal proteins in the rat model of <mark>L - DOPA</mark> - induced dyskinesia . 
<mark>L - DOPA</mark> - induced dyskinesia ( LID ) is among the motor complications that arise in Parkinson ' s disease ( PD ) patients after a prolonged treatment with <mark>L - DOPA</mark> . 
To this day , transcriptome analysis has been performed in a rat model of LID [ Neurobiol . Dis . , 17 ( 2004 ) , 219 ] but information regarding the proteome is still lacking . 
In the present study , we investigated the changes occurring at the protein level in striatal samples obtained from the unilaterally <mark>6 - hydroxydopamine</mark> - lesion rat model of PD treated with saline , <mark>L - DOPA</mark> or <mark>bromocriptine</mark> using two - dimensional difference gel electrophoresis and mass spectrometry ( MS ) . 
Rats treated with <mark>L - DOPA</mark> were allocated to two groups based on the presence or absence of LID . 
Among the 2000 spots compared for statistical difference , 67 spots were significantly changed in abundance and identified using matrix - assisted laser desorption / ionization time - of - flight MS , atmospheric pressure matrix - assisted laser desorption / ionization and HPLC coupled tandem MS ( LC / MS / MS ) . 
Out of these 67 proteins , LID significantly changed the expression level of five proteins : alphabeta - crystalin , gamma - enolase , guanidoacetate methyltransferase , vinculin , and proteasome alpha - 2 subunit . 
Complementary techniques such as western immunoblotting and immunohistochemistry were performed to investigate the validity of the data obtained using the proteomic approach . 
In conclusion , this study provides new insights into the protein changes occurring in LID . 
Cardiac Angiography in Renally Impaired Patients ( CARE ) study : a randomized double - blind trial of contrast - induced nephropathy in patients with chronic kidney disease . 
BACKGROUND : No direct comparisons exist of the renal tolerability of the low - osmolality <mark>contrast medium</mark> <mark>iopamidol</mark> with that of the iso - osmolality <mark>contrast medium</mark> <mark>iodixanol</mark> in high - risk patients . 
METHODS AND RESULTS : The present study is a multicenter , randomized , double - blind comparison of <mark>iopamidol</mark> and <mark>iodixanol</mark> in patients with chronic kidney disease ( estimated glomerular filtration rate , 20 to 59 mL / min ) who underwent cardiac angiography or percutaneous coronary interventions . 
Serum <mark>creatinine</mark> ( SCr ) levels and estimated glomerular filtration rate were assessed at baseline and 2 to 5 days after receiving medications . 
The primary outcome was a postdose SCr increase > or = 0 . 5 mg / dL ( 44 . 2 micromol / L ) over baseline . 
Secondary outcomes were a postdose SCr increase > or = 25 % , a postdose estimated glomerular filtration rate decrease of > or = 25 % , and the mean peak change in SCr . 
In 414 patients , contrast volume , presence of diabetes mellitus , use of <mark>N - acetylcysteine</mark> , mean baseline SCr , and estimated glomerular filtration rate were comparable in the 2 groups . 
SCr increases > or = 0 . 5 mg / dL occurred in 4 . 4 % ( 9 of 204 patients ) after <mark>iopamidol</mark> and 6 . 7 % ( 14 of 210 patients ) after <mark>iodixanol</mark> ( P = 0 . 39 ) , whereas rates of SCr increases > or = 25 % were 9 . 8 % and 12 . 4 % , respectively ( P = 0 . 44 ) . 
In patients with diabetes , SCr increases > or = 0 . 5 mg / dL were 5 . 1 % ( 4 of 78 patients ) with <mark>iopamidol</mark> and 13 . 0 % ( 12 of 92 patients ) with <mark>iodixanol</mark> ( P = 0 . 11 ) , whereas SCr increases > or = 25 % were 10 . 3 % and 15 . 2 % , respectively ( P = 0 . 37 ) . 
Mean post - SCr increases were significantly less with <mark>iopamidol</mark> ( all patients : 0 . 07 versus 0 . 12 mg / dL , 6 . 2 versus 10 . 6 micromol / L , P = 0 . 03 ; patients with diabetes : 0 . 07 versus 0 . 16 mg / dL , 6 . 2 versus 14 . 1 micromol / L , P = 0 . 01 ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : The rate of contrast - induced nephropathy , defined by multiple end points , is not statistically different after the intraarterial administration of <mark>iopamidol</mark> or <mark>iodixanol</mark> to high - risk patients , with or without diabetes mellitus . 
Any true difference between the agents is small and not likely to be clinically significant . 
A novel compound , <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> , attenuates cognitive deficits and shows neuroprotective effects in vitro and in vivo dementia models . 
To develop a novel and effective drug that could enhance cognitive function and neuroprotection , we newly synthesized <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> by the esterification of <mark>maltol</mark> and <mark>p - coumaric acid</mark> . 
In the present study , we investigated whether <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> could improve cognitive decline in <mark>scopolamine</mark> - injected rats and in <mark>amyloid beta peptide ( 1 - 42 )</mark> - infused rats . 
<mark>Maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> was found to attenuate cognitive deficits in both rat models using passive avoidance test and to reduce apoptotic cell death observed in the hippocampus of the <mark>amyloid beta peptide ( 1 - 42 )</mark> - infused rats . 
We also examined the neuroprotective effects of <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> in vitro using SH - SY5Y cells . 
Cells were pretreated with <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> , before exposed to <mark>amyloid beta peptide ( 1 - 42 )</mark> , <mark>glutamate</mark> or <mark>H2O2</mark> . 
We found that <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> significantly decreased apoptotic cell death and reduced reactive oxygen species , cytochrome c release , and caspase 3 activation . 
Taking these in vitro and in vivo results together , our study suggests that <mark>maltolyl p - coumarate</mark> is a potentially effective candidate against Alzheimer ' s disease that is characterized by wide spread neuronal death and progressive decline of cognitive function . 
Attenuation of <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - induced nigrostriatal dopaminergic neurotoxicity in mice by <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> pretreatment . 
Immunological activation has been proposed to play a role in <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - induced dopaminergic terminal damage . 
In this study , we examined the roles of <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> , a pro - inflammatory and inflammatory factor , treatment in modulating the <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - induced nigrostriatal <mark>dopamine</mark> neurotoxicity . 
<mark>Lipopolysaccharide</mark> pretreatment did not affect the basal body temperature or <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - elicited hyperthermia three days later . 
Such systemic <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> treatment mitigated <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - induced striatal <mark>dopamine</mark> and <mark>3 , 4 - dihydroxyphenylacetic acid</mark> depletions in a dose - dependent manner . 
As the most potent dose ( 1 mg / kg ) of <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> was administered two weeks , one day before or after the <mark>methamphetamine</mark> dosing regimen , <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - induced striatal <mark>dopamine</mark> and <mark>3 , 4 - dihydroxyphenylacetic acid</mark> depletions remained unaltered . 
Moreover , systemic <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> pretreatment ( 1 mg / kg ) attenuated local <mark>methamphetamine</mark> infusion - produced <mark>dopamine</mark> and <mark>3 , 4 - dihydroxyphenylacetic acid</mark> depletions in the striatum , indicating that the protective effect of <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> is less likely due to interrupted peripheral distribution or metabolism of <mark>methamphetamine</mark> . 
We concluded a critical time window for systemic <mark>lipopolysaccharide</mark> pretreatment in exerting effective protection against <mark>methamphetamine</mark> - induced nigrostriatal <mark>dopamine</mark> neurotoxicity . 
Acute myocarditis associated with <mark>clozapine</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : A case of acute myocarditis associated with the commencement of <mark>clozapine</mark> is described , highlighting the onset , course and possible contributing factors . 
There is an urgent need to raise awareness about this potentially fatal complication of <mark>clozapine</mark> use . 
RESULTS : A 20 - year - old male with schizophrenia developed a sudden onset of myocarditis after commencement of <mark>clozapine</mark> . 
The patient recovered with intensive medical support . 
The symptoms occurred around 2 weeks after starting <mark>clozapine</mark> in an inpatient setting . 
Possible contributing factors may have been concomitant <mark>antidepressant</mark> use and unaccustomed physical activity . 
CONCLUSIONS : Myocarditis is an increasingly recognized complication associated with the use of <mark>clozapine</mark> . 
It can be fatal if not recognized and treated early . 
Considering that <mark>clozapine</mark> remains the gold standard in treatment of resistant psychosis , there is an urgent need to raise awareness among medical and paramedical staff involved in the care of these patients . 
There are also implications for recommendations and regulations regarding the use of <mark>clozapine</mark> . 
Severe rhabdomyolysis and acute renal failure secondary to concomitant use of <mark>simvastatin</mark> , <mark>amiodarone</mark> , and <mark>atazanavir</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : To report a case of a severe interaction between <mark>simvastatin</mark> , <mark>amiodarone</mark> , and <mark>atazanavir</mark> resulting in rhabdomyolysis and acute renal failure . 
BACKGROUND : A 72 - year - old white man with underlying human immunodeficiency virus , atrial fibrillation , coronary artery disease , and hyperlipidemia presented with generalized pain , fatigue , and dark orange urine for 3 days . 
The patient was taking 80 mg <mark>simvastatin</mark> at bedtime ( initiated 27 days earlier ) ; <mark>amiodarone</mark> at a dose of 400 mg daily for 7 days , then 200 mg daily ( initiated 19 days earlier ) ; and 400 mg <mark>atazanavir</mark> daily ( initiated at least 2 years previously ) . 
Laboratory evaluation revealed 66 , 680 U / L <mark>creatine</mark> kinase , 93 mg / dL <mark>blood urea nitrogen</mark> , 4 . 6 mg / dL <mark>creatinine</mark> , 1579 U / L <mark>aspartate</mark> aminotransferase , and 738 U / L <mark>alanine</mark> aminotransferase . 
<mark>Simvastatin</mark> , <mark>amiodarone</mark> , and the patient ' s human immunodeficiency virus medications were all temporarily discontinued and the patient was given forced alkaline diuresis and started on dialysis . 
Nine days later the patient ' s <mark>creatine</mark> kinase had dropped to 1695 U / L and <mark>creatinine</mark> was 3 . 3 mg / dL . 
The patient was discharged and continued outpatient dialysis for 1 month until his renal function recovered . 
DISCUSSION : The risk of rhabdomyolysis is increased in the presence of concomitant drugs that inhibit <mark>simvastatin</mark> metabolism . 
<mark>Simvastatin</mark> is metabolized by CYP3A4 . 
<mark>Amiodarone</mark> and <mark>atazanavir</mark> are recognized CYP3A4 inhibitors . 
CONCLUSIONS : Pharmacokinetic differences in <mark>statins</mark> are an important consideration for assessing the risk of potential drug interactions . 
In patients requiring the concurrent use of <mark>statins</mark> and CYP3A4 inhibitors , <mark>pravastatin</mark> , <mark>fluvastatin</mark> , and <mark>rosuvastatin</mark> carry the lowest risk of drug interactions ; <mark>atorvastatin</mark> carries moderate risk , whereas <mark>simvastatin</mark> and <mark>lovastatin</mark> have the highest risk and should be avoided in patients taking concomitant CYP3A4 inhibitors . 
Interaction between <mark>warfarin</mark> and <mark>levofloxacin</mark> : case series . 
<mark>Warfarin</mark> is the most widely used oral anticoagulant and is indicated for many clinical conditions . 
<mark>Levofloxacin</mark> , a <mark>fluoroquinolone</mark> , is one of the most commonly prescribed antibiotics in clinical practice and is effective against Gram - positive , Gram - negative , and atypical bacteria . 
While small prospective studies have not revealed any significant drug - drug interaction between <mark>warfarin</mark> and <mark>levofloxacin</mark> , several case reports have indicated that <mark>levofloxacin</mark> may significantly potentiate the anticoagulation effect of <mark>warfarin</mark> . 
We report 3 cases of serious bleeding complications that appear to be the result of the interaction between <mark>warfarin</mark> and <mark>levofloxacin</mark> . 
Physicians should be aware of this potential interaction and use caution when prescribing <mark>levofloxacin</mark> to patients taking <mark>warfarin</mark> . 
Mutations associated with <mark>lamivudine</mark> - resistance in therapy - <mark>na</mark> ve hepatitis B virus ( HBV ) infected patients with and without HIV co - infection : implications for antiretroviral therapy in HBV and HIV co - infected South African patients . 
This was an exploratory study to investigate <mark>lamivudine</mark> - resistant hepatitis B virus ( HBV ) strains in selected <mark>lamivudine</mark> - <mark>na</mark> ve HBV carriers with and without human immunodeficiency virus ( HIV ) co - infection in South African patients . 
Thirty - five <mark>lamivudine</mark> - <mark>na</mark> ve HBV infected patients with or without HIV co - infection were studied : 15 chronic HBV mono - infected patients and 20 HBV - HIV co - infected patients . 
The latter group was further sub - divided into 13 occult HBV ( <mark>HBsAg</mark> - negative ) and 7 overt HBV ( <mark>HBsAg</mark> - positive ) patients . 
<mark>HBsAg</mark> , anti - HBs , anti - HBc , and anti - HIV 1 / 2 were determined as part of routine diagnosis using Axsym assays ( Abbott Laboratories , North Chicago , IL ) . 
Serum samples were PCR amplified with HBV reverse transcriptase ( RT ) primers , followed by direct sequencing across the <mark>tyrosine</mark> - <mark>methionine</mark> - <mark>aspartate</mark> - <mark>aspartate</mark> ( YMDD ) motif of the major catalytic region in the C domain of the HBV RT enzyme . 
HBV viral load was performed with Amplicor HBV Monitor test v2 . 0 ( Roche Diagnostics , Penzberg , Germany ) . 
HBV <mark>lamivudine</mark> - resistant strains were detected in 3 of 15 mono - infected chronic hepatitis B patients and 10 of 20 HBV - HIV co - infected patients . 
To the best of our knowledge , this constitutes the first report of HBV <mark>lamivudine</mark> - resistant strains in therapy - <mark>na</mark> ve HBV - HIV co - infected patients . 
The HBV viral loads for mono - infected and co - infected patients ranged from 3 . 32 x 10 ( 2 ) to 3 . 82 x 10 ( 7 ) and < 200 to 4 . 40 x 10 ( 3 ) copies / ml , respectively . 
It remains to be seen whether such pre - existing antiviral mutations could result in widespread emergence of HBV resistant strains when <mark>lamivudine</mark> - containing highly active antiretroviral ( ARV ) treatment ( HAART ) regimens become widely applied in South Africa , as this is likely to have potential implications in the management of HBV - HIV co - infected patients . 
Rabbit syndrome , <mark>antidepressant</mark> use , and cerebral perfusion SPECT scan findings . 
The rabbit syndrome is an extrapyramidal side effect associated with chronic neuroleptic therapy . 
Its occurrence in a patient being treated with <mark>imipramine</mark> is described , representing the first reported case of this syndrome in conjunction with <mark>antidepressants</mark> . 
Repeated cerebral perfusion SPECT scans revealed decreased basal ganglia perfusion while the movement disorder was present , and a return to normal perfusion when the rabbit syndrome resolved . 
Estrogen prevents <mark>cholesteryl ester</mark> accumulation in macrophages induced by the HIV protease inhibitor <mark>ritonavir</mark> . 
Individuals with HIV can now live long lives with drug therapy that often includes protease inhibitors such as <mark>ritonavir</mark> . 
Many patients , however , develop negative long - term side effects such as premature atherosclerosis . 
We have previously demonstrated that <mark>ritonavir</mark> treatment increases atherosclerotic lesion formation in male mice to a greater extent than in female mice . 
Furthermore , peripheral blood monocytes isolated from <mark>ritonavir</mark> - treated females had less <mark>cholesteryl ester</mark> accumulation . 
In the present study , we have investigated the molecular mechanisms by which female hormones influence <mark>cholesterol</mark> metabolism in macrophages in response to the HIV protease inhibitor <mark>ritonavir</mark> . 
We have utilized the human monocyte cell line , THP - 1 as a model to address this question . 
Briefly , cells were differentiated for 72 h with 100 nM PMA to obtain a macrophage - like phenotype in the presence or absence of 1 nM <mark>17beta - estradiol</mark> ( <mark>E2</mark> ) , 100 nM <mark>progesterone</mark> or vehicle ( 0 . 01 % <mark>ethanol</mark> ) . 
Cells were then treated with 30 ng / ml <mark>ritonavir</mark> or vehicle in the presence of aggregated LDL for 24 h . 
Cell extracts were harvested , and lipid or total RNA was isolated . 
<mark>E2</mark> decreased the accumulation of <mark>cholesteryl esters</mark> in macrophages following <mark>ritonavir</mark> treatment . 
<mark>Ritonavir</mark> increased the expression of the scavenger receptor , CD36 mRNA , responsible for the uptake of LDL . 
Additionally , <mark>ritonavir</mark> treatment selectively increased the relative levels of PPARgamma mRNA , a transcription factor responsible for the regulation of CD36 mRNA expression . 
Treatment with <mark>E2</mark> , however , failed to prevent these increases at the mRNA level . 
<mark>E2</mark> did , however , significantly suppress CD36 protein levels as measured by fluorescent immunocytochemistry . 
This data suggests that <mark>E2</mark> modifies the expression of CD36 at the level of protein expression in monocyte - derived macrophages resulting in reduced <mark>cholesteryl ester</mark> accumulation following <mark>ritonavir</mark> treatment . 
Acute hepatitis attack after exposure to <mark>telithromycin</mark> . 
INTRODUCTION : Antibiotic - associated hepatotoxicity is rare . 
With widespread use of antimicrobial agents , however , hepatic injury occurs frequently , and among adverse drug reactions , idiosyncratic reactions are the most serious . 
CASE SUMMARY : A 25 - year - old male patient , with a height of 175 cm and weight of 72 kg presented to Marmara University Hospital Emergency Department , Istanbul , Turkey , with 5 days ' history of jaundice , malaise , nausea , and vomiting . 
He had been prescribed <mark>telithromycin</mark> 400 mg / d PO to treat an upper respiratory tract infection 7 days prior . 
Admission laboratory tests were as follows : <mark>alanine</mark> aminotransferase , 67 U / L ( reference range , 10 - 37 U / L ) ; <mark>aspartate</mark> aminotransferase , 98 U / L ( 10 - 40 U / L ) ; alkaline phosphatase , 513 U / L ( 0 - 270 U / L ) ; gamma - glutamyltransferase , 32 U / L ( 7 - 49 U / L ) ; amylase , 46 U / L ( 0 - 220 U / L ) ; total <mark>bilirubin</mark> , 20 . 1 mg / dL ( 0 . 2 - 1 . 0 mg / dL ) ; direct <mark>bilirubin</mark> , 14 . 8 mg / dL ( 0 - 0 . 3 mg / dL ) ; and albumin , 4 . 7 mg / dL ( 3 . 5 - 5 . 4 mg / dL ) . 
No toxin , <mark>alcohol</mark> , or other drugs were reported . 
The patient had suffered a previous episode of " acute hepatitis of unknown origin , " that occurred after <mark>telithromycin</mark> usage . 
Both incidents occurred within a year . 
DISCUSSION : <mark>Telithromycin</mark> is the first of the ketolide antibacterials to receive US Food and Drug Administration approval for clinical use . 
It has been associated with infrequent and usually reversible severe hepatic dysfunction . 
Based on a score of 8 on the Naranjo adverse drug reaction probability scale , <mark>telithromycin</mark> was the probable cause of acute hepatitis in this patient , and pathological findings suggested drug - induced toxic hepatitis . 
Recurrence of hepatitis attack might have been avoided if the initial incident had been communicated to the attending physician who prescribed <mark>telithromycin</mark> the second time . 
CONCLUSION : Here we report a case of acute hepatitis probably associated with the administration of <mark>telithromycin</mark> . 
A study on the effect of the duration of subcutaneous <mark>heparin</mark> injection on bruising and pain . 
AIM : This study was carried out to determine the effect of injection duration on bruising and pain following the administration of the subcutaneous injection of <mark>heparin</mark> . 
BACKGROUND : Although different methods to prevent bruising and pain following the subcutaneous injection of <mark>heparin</mark> have been widely studied and described , the effect of injection duration on the occurrence of bruising and pain is little documented . 
DESIGN : This study was designed as within - subject , quasi - experimental research . 
METHOD : The sample for the study consisted of 50 patients to whom subcutaneous <mark>heparin</mark> was administered . 
<mark>Heparin</mark> was injected over 10 seconds on the right abdominal site and 30 seconds on the left abdominal site . 
Injections areas were assessed for the presence of bruising at 48 and 72 hours after each injection . 
Dimensions of the bruising on the <mark>heparin</mark> applied areas were measured using transparent millimetric measuring paper . 
The visual analog scale ( VAS ) was used to measure pain intensity and a stop - watch was used to time the pain period . 
Data were analysed using chi - square test , Mann - Whitney U , Wilcoxon signed ranks tests and correlation . 
RESULTS : The percentage of bruising occurrence was 64 % with the injection of 10 seconds duration and 42 % in the 30 - second injection . 
It was determined that the size of the bruising was smaller in the 30 - second injection . 
Pain intensity and pain period were statistically significantly lower for the 30 - second injection than for the 10 - second injection . 
CONCLUSIONS : It was determined that injection duration had an effect on bruising and pain following the subcutaneous administration of <mark>heparin</mark> . 
This study should be repeated on a larger sample . 
RELEVANCE TO CLINICAL PRACTICE : When administering subcutaneous <mark>heparin</mark> injections , it is important to extend the duration of the injection . 
Acute liver failure in two patients with regular <mark>alcohol</mark> consumption ingesting <mark>paracetamol</mark> at therapeutic dosage . 
BACKGROUND : The possible role of <mark>alcohol</mark> in the development of hepatotoxicity associated with therapeutic doses of <mark>paracetamol</mark> ( <mark>acetaminophen</mark> ) is currently debated . 
CASE REPORT : We describe 2 patients who were regular consumers of <mark>alcohol</mark> and who developed liver failure within 3 - 5 days after hospitalization and stopping <mark>alcohol</mark> consumption while being treated with 4 g <mark>paracetamol</mark> / day .
