A <mark>paracetamol</mark> serum level obtained in one of these patients was not in the toxic range . 
Possible risk factors for the development of hepatotoxicity in patients treated with therapeutic doses of <mark>paracetamol</mark> are discussed . 
CONCLUSION : In patients with risk factors , e . g . regular consumption of <mark>alcohol</mark> , liver failure is possible when therapeutic doses are ingested . 
We propose that the <mark>paracetamol</mark> dose should not exceed 2 g / day in such patients and that their liver function should be monitored closely while being treated with <mark>paracetamol</mark> . 
Associations between use of <mark>benzodiazepines</mark> or related drugs and health , physical abilities and cognitive function : a non - randomised clinical study in the elderly . 
OBJECTIVE : To describe associations between the use of <mark>benzodiazepines</mark> or related drugs ( <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs ) and health , functional abilities and cognitive function in the elderly . 
METHODS : A non - randomised clinical study of patients aged > or = 65 years admitted to acute hospital wards during 1 month . 
164 patients ( mean age + / - standard deviation [ SD ] 81 . 6 + / - 6 . 8 years ) were admitted . 
Of these , nearly half ( n = 78 ) had used <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs before admission , and the remainder ( n = 86 ) were non - users . 
Cognitive ability was assessed by the Mini - Mental State Examination ( MMSE ) . 
Patients scoring > or = 20 MMSE sum points were interviewed ( n = 79 ) and questioned regarding symptoms and functional abilities during the week prior to admission . 
Data on use of <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs before admission , current medications and discharge diagnoses were collected from medical records . 
Health , physical abilities and cognitive function were compared between BZD / RD users and non - users , and adjustments were made for confounding variables . 
The residual serum concentrations of <mark>oxazepam</mark> , <mark>temazepam</mark> and <mark>zopiclone</mark> were analysed . 
RESULTS : The mean + / - SD duration of BZD / RD use was 7 + / - 7 years ( range 1 - 31 ) . 
Two or three <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs were concomitantly taken by 26 % of users ( n = 20 ) . 
Long - term use of these drugs was associated with female sex and use of a higher number of drugs with effects on the CNS , which tended to be related to diagnosed dementia . 
After adjustment for these variables as confounders , use of <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs was not associated with cognitive function as measured by the MMSE . 
However , use of <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs was associated with dizziness , inability to sleep after awaking at night and tiredness in the mornings during the week prior to admission and with stronger depressive symptoms measured at the beginning of the hospital stay . 
Use of <mark>BZDs</mark> / RDs tended to be associated with a reduced ability to walk and shorter night - time sleep during the week prior to admission . 
A higher residual serum concentration of <mark>temazepam</mark> correlated with a lower MMSE sum score after adjustment for confounding variables . 
CONCLUSIONS : Long - term use and concomitant use of more than one BZD / RD were common in elderly patients hospitalised because of acute illnesses . 
Long - term use was associated with daytime and night - time symptoms indicative of poorer health and potentially caused by the adverse effects of these drugs . 
Acute vocal fold palsy after acute <mark>disulfiram</mark> intoxication . 
Acute peripheral neuropathy caused by a <mark>disulfiram</mark> overdose is very rare and there is no report of it leading to vocal fold palsy . 
A 49 - year - old woman was transferred to our department because of quadriparesis , lancinating pain , sensory loss , and paresthesia of the distal limbs . 
One month previously , she had taken a single high dose of <mark>disulfiram</mark> ( 130 tablets of <mark>ALCOHOL</mark> STOP TAB , Shin - Poong Pharm . Co . , Ansan , Korea ) in a suicide attempt . 
She was not an alcoholic . 
For the first few days after ingestion , she was in a confused state and had mild to moderate ataxia and giddiness . 
She noticed hoarseness and distally accentuated motor and sensory dysfunction after she had recovered from this state . 
A nerve conduction study was consistent with severe sensorimotor axonal polyneuropathy . 
Laryngeal electromyography ( thyroarytenoid muscle ) showed ample denervation potentials . 
Laryngoscopy revealed asymmetric vocal fold movements during phonation . 
Her vocal change and weakness began to improve spontaneously about 3 weeks after transfer . 
This was a case of acute palsy of the recurrent laryngeal nerve and superimposed severe acute sensorimotor axonal polyneuropathy caused by high - dose <mark>disulfiram</mark> intoxication . 
Encephalopathy induced by <mark>levetiracetam</mark> added to <mark>valproate</mark> . 
BACKGROUND : We report on the manifestation of a <mark>levetiracetam</mark> ( <mark>LEV</mark> ) - induced encephalopathy . 
FINDINGS : A 28 - year - old man suffering from idiopathic epilepsy with generalized seizures was treated with <mark>LEV</mark> ( 3000 mg ) added to <mark>valproate</mark> ( <mark>VPA</mark> ) ( 2000 mg ) . 
Frequency of generalized tonic - clonic seizures increased from one per 6 months to two per month . 
Neuropsychological testing showed impaired word fluency , psychomotor speed and working memory . 
The interictal electroencephalogram ( EEG ) showed a generalized slowing to 5 per second theta rhythms with bilateral generalized high - amplitude discharges . 
OUTCOME : Following discontinuation of <mark>LEV</mark> , EEG and neuropsychological findings improved and seizure frequency decreased . 
<mark>Norepinephrine</mark> signaling through beta - adrenergic receptors is critical for expression of <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced anxiety . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Cocaine</mark> is a widely abused psychostimulant that has both rewarding and aversive properties . 
While the mechanisms underlying <mark>cocaine</mark> ' s rewarding effects have been studied extensively , less attention has been paid to the unpleasant behavioral states induced by <mark>cocaine</mark> , such as anxiety . 
METHODS : In this study , we evaluated the performance of <mark>dopamine</mark> beta - hydroxylase knockout ( Dbh - / - ) mice , which lack <mark>norepinephrine</mark> ( <mark>NE</mark> ) , in the elevated plus maze ( EPM ) to examine the contribution of noradrenergic signaling to <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced anxiety . 
RESULTS : We found that <mark>cocaine</mark> dose - dependently increased anxiety - like behavior in control ( Dbh + / - ) mice , as measured by a decrease in open arm exploration . 
The Dbh - / - mice had normal baseline performance in the EPM but were completely resistant to the anxiogenic effects of <mark>cocaine</mark> . 
<mark>Cocaine</mark> - induced anxiety was also attenuated in Dbh + / - mice following administration of <mark>disulfiram</mark> , a <mark>dopamine</mark> beta - hydroxylase ( DBH ) inhibitor . 
In experiments using specific adrenergic antagonists , we found that pretreatment with the beta - adrenergic receptor antagonist <mark>propranolol</mark> blocked <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced anxiety - like behavior in Dbh + / - and wild - type C57BL6 / J mice , while the alpha ( 1 ) antagonist <mark>prazosin</mark> and the alpha ( 2 ) antagonist <mark>yohimbine</mark> had no effect . 
CONCLUSIONS : These results indicate that noradrenergic signaling via beta - adrenergic receptors is required for <mark>cocaine</mark> - induced anxiety in mice . 
Hypothalamic prolactin receptor messenger <mark>ribonucleic acid</mark> levels , prolactin signaling , and hyperprolactinemic inhibition of pulsatile luteinizing hormone secretion are dependent on <mark>estradiol</mark> . 
Hyperprolactinemia can reduce fertility and libido . 
Although central prolactin actions are thought to contribute to this , the mechanisms are poorly understood . 
We first tested whether chronic hyperprolactinemia inhibited two neuroendocrine parameters necessary for female fertility : pulsatile LH secretion and the <mark>estrogen</mark> - induced LH surge . 
Chronic hyperprolactinemia induced by the <mark>dopamine</mark> antagonist <mark>sulpiride</mark> caused a 40 % reduction LH pulse frequency in ovariectomized rats , but only in the presence of chronic low levels of <mark>estradiol</mark> . 
<mark>Sulpiride</mark> did not affect the magnitude of a <mark>steroid</mark> - induced LH surge or the percentage of GnRH neurons activated during the surge . 
<mark>Estradiol</mark> is known to influence expression of the long form of prolactin receptors ( PRL - R ) and components of prolactin ' s signaling pathway . 
To test the hypothesis that <mark>estrogen</mark> increases PRL - R expression and sensitivity to prolactin , we next demonstrated that <mark>estradiol</mark> greatly augments prolactin - induced STAT5 activation . 
Lastly , we measured PRL - R and suppressor of cytokine signaling ( SOCS - 1 and - 3 and CIS , which reflect the level of prolactin signaling ) mRNAs in response to <mark>sulpiride</mark> and <mark>estradiol</mark> . 
<mark>Sulpiride</mark> induced only SOCS - 1 in the medial preoptic area , where GnRH neurons are regulated , but in the arcuate nucleus and choroid plexus , PRL - R , SOCS - 3 , and CIS mRNA levels were also induced . 
<mark>Estradiol</mark> enhanced these effects on SOCS - 3 and CIS . 
Interestingly , <mark>estradiol</mark> also induced PRL - R , SOCS - 3 , and CIS mRNA levels independently . 
These data show that GnRH pulse frequency is inhibited by chronic hyperprolactinemia in a <mark>steroid</mark> - dependent manner . 
They also provide evidence for <mark>estradiol</mark> - dependent and brain region - specific regulation of PRL - R expression and signaling responses by prolactin . 
<mark>Clonidine</mark> for attention - deficit / hyperactivity disorder : II . 
ECG changes and adverse events analysis . 
OBJECTIVE : To examine the safety and tolerability of <mark>clonidine</mark> used alone or with <mark>methylphenidate</mark> in children with attention - deficit / hyperactivity disorder ( ADHD ) . 
METHOD : In a 16 - week multicenter , double - blind trial , 122 children with ADHD were randomly assigned to <mark>clonidine</mark> ( n = 31 ) , <mark>methylphenidate</mark> ( n = 29 ) , <mark>clonidine</mark> and <mark>methylphenidate</mark> ( n = 32 ) , or placebo ( n = 30 ) . 
Doses were flexibly titrated up to 0 . 6 mg / day for <mark>clonidine</mark> and 60 mg / day for <mark>methylphenidate</mark> ( both with divided dosing ) . 
Groups were compared regarding adverse events and changes from baseline to week 16 in electrocardiograms and vital signs . 
RESULTS : There were more incidents of bradycardia in subjects treated with <mark>clonidine</mark> compared with those not treated with <mark>clonidine</mark> ( 17 . 5 % versus 3 . 4 % ; p = . 02 ) , but no other significant group differences regarding electrocardiogram and other cardiovascular outcomes . 
There were no suggestions of interactions between <mark>clonidine</mark> and <mark>methylphenidate</mark> regarding cardiovascular outcomes . 
Moderate or severe adverse events were more common in subjects on <mark>clonidine</mark> ( 79 . 4 % versus 49 . 2 % ; p = . 0006 ) but not associated with higher rates of early study withdrawal . 
Drowsiness was common on <mark>clonidine</mark> , but generally resolved by 6 to 8 weeks . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Clonidine</mark> , used alone or with <mark>methylphenidate</mark> , appears safe and well tolerated in childhood ADHD . 
Physicians prescribing <mark>clonidine</mark> should monitor for bradycardia and advise patients about the high likelihood of initial drowsiness . 
Renal Fanconi syndrome and myopathy after liver transplantation : drug - related mitochondrial cytopathy ? 
Advances in the field of transplantation provide a better quality of life and allow more favorable conditions for growth and development in children . 
However , combinations of different therapeutic regimens require consideration of potential adverse reactions . 
We describe a 15 - yr - old girl who had orthotopic liver transplantation because of Wilson ' s disease . 
<mark>Tacrolimus</mark> , <mark>MMF</mark> , and <mark>steroids</mark> were given as immunosuppressant . 
<mark>Lamivudine</mark> was added because of de nova hepatitis B infection during her follow - up . 
Three yr after transplantation she developed renal Fanconi syndrome with severe metabolic acidosis , hypophosphatemia , glycosuria , and aminoaciduria . 
Although <mark>tacrolimus</mark> was suspected to be the cause of late post - transplant renal acidosis and was replaced by <mark>sirolimus</mark> , acidosis , and electrolyte imbalance got worse . 
Proximal muscle weakness has developed during her follow - up . 
Fanconi syndrome , as well as myopathy , is well recognized in patients with mitochondrial disorders and caused by depletion of mtDNA . 
We suggest that our patient ' s tubular dysfunction and myopathy may have resulted from mitochondrial dysfunction which is triggered by <mark>tacrolimus</mark> and augmented by <mark>lamivudine</mark> . 
Higher optical density of an antigen assay predicts thrombosis in patients with <mark>heparin</mark> - induced thrombocytopenia . 
OBJECTIVES : To correlate optical density and percent inhibition of a two - step <mark>heparin</mark> - induced thrombocytopenia ( HIT ) antigen assay with thrombosis ; the assay utilizes reaction inhibition characteristics of a high <mark>heparin</mark> concentration . 
PATIENTS AND METHODS : Patients with more than 50 % decrease in platelet count or thrombocytopenia ( < 150 x 10 ( 9 ) / L ) after exposure to <mark>heparin</mark> , who had a positive two - step antigen assay [ optical density ( OD ) > 0 . 4 and > 50 inhibition with high concentration of <mark>heparin</mark> ] were included in the study . 
RESULTS : Forty of 94 HIT patients had thrombosis at diagnosis ; 54 / 94 had isolated - HIT without thrombosis . 
Eight of the isolated - HIT patients developed thrombosis within the next 30 d ; thus , a total of 48 patients had thrombosis at day 30 . 
At diagnosis there was no significant difference in OD between HIT patients with thrombosis and those with isolated - HIT . 
However , OD was significantly higher in all patients with thrombosis ( n = 48 , 1 . 34 + / - 0 . 89 ) , including isolated - HIT patients who later developed thrombosis within 30 d ( n = 8 , 1 . 84 + / - 0 . 64 ) as compared to isolated - HIT patients who did not develop thrombosis ( 0 . 96 + / - 0 . 75 ; P = 0 . 011 and P = 0 . 008 ) . 
The Receiver Operative Characteristic Curve showed that OD > 1 . 27 in the isolated - HIT group had a significantly higher chance of developing thrombosis by day 30 . 
None of these groups showed significant difference in percent inhibition . 
Multivariate analysis showed a 2 . 8 - fold increased risk of thrombosis in females . 
Similarly , thrombotic risk increased with age and OD values . 
CONCLUSION : Higher OD is associated with significant risk of subsequent thrombosis in patients with isolated - HIT ; percent inhibition , however , was not predictive . 
<mark>Thalidomide</mark> has limited single - agent activity in relapsed or refractory indolent non - Hodgkin lymphomas : a phase II trial of the Cancer and Leukemia Group B . 
<mark>Thalidomide</mark> is an immunomodulatory agent with demonstrated activity in multiple myeloma , mantle cell lymphoma and lymphoplasmacytic lymphoma . 
Its activity is believed to be due modulation of the tumour milieu , including downregulation of angiogenesis and inflammatory cytokines . 
Between July 2001 and April 2004 , 24 patients with relapsed / refractory indolent lymphomas received <mark>thalidomide</mark> 200 mg daily with escalation by 100 mg daily every 1 - 2 weeks as tolerated , up to a maximum of 800 mg daily . 
Patients had received a median of 2 ( range , 1 - 4 ) prior regimens . 
Of 24 evaluable patients , two achieved a complete remission and one achieved a partial remission for an overall response rate of 12 . 5 % ( 95 % confidence interval : 2 . 6 - 32 . 4 % ) . 
Eleven patients progressed during therapy . 
Grade 3 - 4 adverse effects included myelosuppression , fatigue , somnolence / depressed mood , neuropathy and dyspnea . 
Of concern was the occurrence of four thromboembolic events . 
Our results failed to demonstrate an important response rate to single agent <mark>thalidomide</mark> in indolent lymphomas and contrast with the higher activity level reported with the second generation immunomodulatory agent , <mark>lenalidomide</mark> . 
Sex differences in <mark>NMDA</mark> antagonist enhancement of <mark>morphine</mark> antihyperalgesia in a <mark>capsaicin</mark> model of persistent pain : comparisons to two models of acute pain . 
In acute pain models , <mark>N - methyl - D - aspartate</mark> ( <mark>NMDA</mark> ) antagonists enhance the antinociceptive effects of <mark>morphine</mark> to a greater extent in males than females . 
The purpose of this investigation was to extend these findings to a persistent pain model which could be distinguished from acute pain models on the basis of the nociceptive fibers activated , neurochemical substrates , and duration of the nociceptive stimulus . 
To this end , persistent hyperalgesia was induced by administration of <mark>capsaicin</mark> in the tail of gonadally intact F344 rats , following which the tail was immersed in a mildly noxious thermal stimulus , and tail - withdrawal latencies measured . 
For comparison , tests were conducted in two acute pain models , the hotplate and warm water tail - withdrawal procedures . 
In males , the non - competitive <mark>NMDA</mark> antagonist <mark>dextromethorphan</mark> enhanced the antihyperalgesic effect of low to moderate doses of <mark>morphine</mark> in a dose - and time - dependent manner . 
Across the doses and pretreatment times examined , enhancement was not observed in females . 
Enhancement of <mark>morphine</mark> antinociception by <mark>dextromethorphan</mark> was seen in both males and females in the acute pain models , with the magnitude of this effect being greater in males . 
These findings demonstrate a sexually - dimorphic interaction between <mark>NMDA</mark> antagonists and <mark>morphine</mark> in a persistent pain model that can be distinguished from those observed in acute pain models . 
Development of proteinuria after switch to <mark>sirolimus</mark> - based immunosuppression in long - term cardiac transplant patients . 
Calcineurin - inhibitor therapy can lead to renal dysfunction in heart transplantation patients . 
The novel immunosuppressive ( IS ) drug <mark>sirolmus</mark> ( <mark>Srl</mark> ) lacks nephrotoxic effects ; however , proteinuria associated with <mark>Srl</mark> has been reported following renal transplantation . 
In cardiac transplantation , the incidence of proteinuria associated with <mark>Srl</mark> is unknown . 
In this study , long - term cardiac transplant patients were switched from <mark>cyclosporine</mark> to <mark>Srl</mark> - based IS . 
Concomitant IS consisted of <mark>mycophenolate mofetil</mark> + / - <mark>steroids</mark> . 
Proteinuria increased significantly from a median of 0 . 13 g / day ( range 0 - 5 . 7 ) preswitch to 0 . 23 g / day ( 0 - 9 . 88 ) at 24 months postswitch ( p = 0 . 0024 ) . 
Before the switch , 11 . 5 % of patients had high - grade proteinuria ( > 1 . 0 g / day ) ; this increased to 22 . 9 % postswitch ( p = 0 . 006 ) . 
<mark>ACE inhibitor</mark> and <mark>angiotensin - releasing blocker</mark> ( <mark>ARB</mark> ) therapy reduced proteinuria development . 
Patients without proteinuria had increased renal function ( median 42 . 5 vs . 64 . 1 , p = 0 . 25 ) , whereas patients who developed high - grade proteinuria showed decreased renal function at the end of follow - up ( median 39 . 6 vs . 29 . 2 , p = 0 . 125 ) . 
Thus , proteinuria may develop in cardiac transplant patients after switch to <mark>Srl</mark> , which may have an adverse effect on renal function in these patients . 
<mark>Srl</mark> should be used with <mark>ACEi</mark> / <mark>ARB</mark> therapy and patients monitored for proteinuria and increased renal dysfunction . 
<mark>Ginsenoside Rg1</mark> restores the impairment of learning induced by chronic <mark>morphine</mark> administration in rats . 
<mark>Rg1</mark> , as a <mark>ginsenoside</mark> extracted from Panax ginseng , could ameliorate spatial learning impairment . 
Previous studies have demonstrated that <mark>Rg1</mark> might be a useful agent for the prevention and treatment of the adverse effects of <mark>morphine</mark> . 
The aim of this study was to investigate the effect of <mark>Rg1</mark> on learning impairment by chronic <mark>morphine</mark> administration and the mechanism responsible for this effect . 
Male rats were subcutaneously injected with <mark>morphine</mark> ( 10 mg / kg ) twice a day at 12 hour intervals for 10 days , and <mark>Rg1</mark> ( 30 mg / kg ) was intraperitoneally injected 2 hours after the second injection of <mark>morphine</mark> once a day for 10 days . 
Spatial learning capacity was assessed in the Morris water maze . 
The results showed that rats treated with <mark>Morphine</mark> / <mark>Rg1</mark> decreased escape latency and increased the time spent in platform quadrant and entering frequency . 
By implantation of electrodes and electrophysiological recording in vivo , the results showed that <mark>Rg1</mark> restored the long - term potentiation ( LTP ) impaired by <mark>morphine</mark> in both freely moving and anaesthetised rats . 
The electrophysiological recording in vitro showed that <mark>Rg1</mark> restored the LTP in slices from the rats treated with <mark>morphine</mark> , but not changed LTP in the slices from normal saline - or <mark>morphine</mark> / <mark>Rg1</mark> - treated rats ; this restoration could be inhibited by <mark>N - methyl - D - aspartate</mark> ( <mark>NMDA</mark> ) receptor antagonist <mark>MK801</mark> . 
We conclude that <mark>Rg1</mark> may significantly improve the spatial learning capacity impaired by chonic <mark>morphine</mark> administration and restore the <mark>morphine</mark> - inhibited LTP . 
This effect is <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor dependent . 
Synthesis of <mark>N - pyrimidinyl - 2 - phenoxyacetamides</mark> as <mark>adenosine</mark> A2A receptor antagonists . 
A series of <mark>N - pyrimidinyl - 2 - phenoxyacetamide</mark> <mark>adenosine</mark> A ( 2A ) antagonists is described . 
SAR studies led to compound 14 with excellent potency ( K ( i ) = 0 . 4 nM ) , selectivity ( A ( 1 ) / A ( 2A ) > 100 ) , and efficacy ( MED 10 mg / kg p . o . ) in the rat <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced catalepsy model for Parkinson ' s disease . 
Evidence for an involvement of D1 and D2 <mark>dopamine</mark> receptors in mediating <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced hyperactivity in rats . 
Previous studies have suggested that repeated exposure of rats to the drug or to the experimental environment is necessary to observe <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced locomotor stimulation . 
In the present study the role of habituation to the experimental environment on the stimulant effect of <mark>nicotine</mark> in rats was examined . 
In addition , the role of <mark>dopamine</mark> receptors in mediating <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced locomotor stimulation was investigated by examining the effects of selective D1 and D2 <mark>dopamine</mark> receptor antagonists on activity induced by <mark>nicotine</mark> . 
Locomotor activity was assessed in male Sprague - Dawley rats tested in photocell cages . 
<mark>Nicotine</mark> ( 1 . 0 mg / kg ) caused a significant increase in locomotor activity in rats that were habituated to the test environment , but had only a weak and delayed stimulant action in rats that were unfamiliar with the test environment . 
The stimulant action of <mark>nicotine</mark> was blocked by the central nicotinic antagonist <mark>mecamylamine</mark> but not by the peripheral nicotinic blocker <mark>hexamethonium</mark> , indicating that the response is probably mediated by central nicotinic receptors . 
<mark>Nicotine</mark> - induced hyperactivity was blocked by the selective D1 antagonist <mark>SCH 23390</mark> , the selective D2 antagonist <mark>raclopride</mark> and the D1 / D2 antagonist <mark>fluphenazine</mark> . 
Pretreatment with the D2 agonist <mark>PHNO</mark> enhanced <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced hyperactivity , whereas the D1 agonist <mark>SKF 38393</mark> had no effect . 
The results indicate that acute <mark>nicotine</mark> injection induces a pronounced hyperactivity in rats habituated to the test environment . 
The effect appears to be mediated by central <mark>nicotine</mark> receptors , possibly located on dopaminergic neurons , and also requires the activation of both D1 and D2 <mark>dopamine</mark> receptors . 
Central retinal vein occlusion associated with <mark>clomiphene</mark> - induced ovulation . 
OBJECTIVE : To report a case of central retinal vein occlusion associated with <mark>clomiphene citrate</mark> ( <mark>CC</mark> ) . 
DESIGN : Case study . 
SETTING : Ophthalmology clinic of an academic hospital . 
PATIENT ( S ) : A 36 - year - old woman referred from the infertility clinic for blurred vision . 
INTERVENTION ( S ) : Ophthalmic examination after <mark>CC</mark> therapy . 
MAIN OUTCOME MEASURE ( S ) : Central retinal vein occlusion after ovulation induction with <mark>CC</mark> . 
RESULT ( S ) : A 36 - year - old Chinese woman developed central retinal vein occlusion after eight courses of <mark>CC</mark> . 
A search of the literature on the thromboembolic complications of <mark>CC</mark> does not include this severe ophthalmic complication , although mild visual disturbance after <mark>CC</mark> intake is not uncommon . 
CONCLUSION ( S ) : This is the first reported case of central retinal vein occlusion after treatment with <mark>CC</mark> . 
Extra caution is warranted in treating infertility patients with <mark>CC</mark> , and patients should be well informed of this side effect before commencement of therapy . 
Acute bronchodilating effects of <mark>ipratropium bromide</mark> and <mark>theophylline</mark> in chronic obstructive pulmonary disease . 
The bronchodilator effects of a single dose of <mark>ipratropium bromide</mark> aerosol ( 36 micrograms ) and short - acting <mark>theophylline</mark> tablets ( dose titrated to produce serum levels of 10 - 20 micrograms / mL ) were compared in a double - blind , placebo - controlled crossover study in 21 patients with stable , chronic obstructive pulmonary disease . 
Mean peak forced expiratory volume in 1 second ( FEV1 ) increases over baseline and the proportion of patients attaining at least a 15 % increase in the FEV1 ( responders ) were 31 % and 90 % , respectively , for <mark>ipratropium</mark> and 17 % and 50 % , respectively , for <mark>theophylline</mark> . 
The average FEV1 increases during the 6 - hour observation period were 18 % for <mark>ipratropium</mark> and 8 % for <mark>theophylline</mark> . 
The mean duration of action was 3 . 8 hours with <mark>ipratropium</mark> and 2 . 4 hours with <mark>theophylline</mark> . 
While side effects were rare , those experienced after <mark>theophylline</mark> use did involve the cardiovascular and gastrointestinal systems . 
These results show that <mark>ipratropium</mark> is a more potent bronchodilator than oral <mark>theophylline</mark> in patients with chronic airflow obstruction . 
<mark>Methamphetamine</mark> - induced neurotoxicity and microglial activation are not mediated by fractalkine receptor signaling . 
<mark>Methamphetamine</mark> ( <mark>METH</mark> ) damages <mark>dopamine</mark> ( <mark>DA</mark> ) nerve endings by a process that has been linked to microglial activation but the signaling pathways that mediate this response have not yet been delineated . 
Cardona et al . 
[ Nat . Neurosci . 9 ( 2006 ) , 917 ] recently identified the microglial - specific fractalkine receptor ( CX3CR1 ) as an important mediator of <mark>MPTP</mark> - induced neurodegeneration of <mark>DA</mark> neurons . 
Because the CNS damage caused by <mark>METH</mark> and <mark>MPTP</mark> is highly selective for the <mark>DA</mark> neuronal system in mouse models of neurotoxicity , we hypothesized that the CX3CR1 plays a role in <mark>METH</mark> - induced neurotoxicity and microglial activation . 
Mice in which the CX3CR1 gene has been deleted and replaced with a cDNA encoding enhanced green fluorescent protein ( eGFP ) were treated with <mark>METH</mark> and examined for striatal neurotoxicity . 
<mark>METH</mark> depleted <mark>DA</mark> , caused microglial activation , and increased body temperature in CX3CR1 knockout mice to the same extent and over the same time course seen in wild - type controls . 
The effects of <mark>METH</mark> in CX3CR1 knockout mice were not gender - dependent and did not extend beyond the striatum . 
Striatal microglia expressing eGFP constitutively show morphological changes after <mark>METH</mark> that are characteristic of activation . 
This response was restricted to the striatum and contrasted sharply with unresponsive eGFP - microglia in surrounding brain areas that are not damaged by <mark>METH</mark> . 
We conclude from these studies that CX3CR1 signaling does not modulate <mark>METH</mark> neurotoxicity or microglial activation . 
Furthermore , it appears that striatal - resident microglia respond to <mark>METH</mark> with an activation cascade and then return to a surveying state without undergoing apoptosis or migration . 
<mark>Nicotine</mark> - induced nystagmus correlates with midpontine activation . 
The pathomechanism of <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced nystagmus ( NIN ) is unknown . 
The aim of this study was to delineate brain structures that are involved in NIN generation . 
Eight healthy volunteers inhaled <mark>nicotine</mark> in darkness during a functional magnetic resonance imaging ( fMRI ) experiment ; eye movements were registered using video - oculography . 
NIN correlated with blood <mark>oxygen</mark> level - dependent ( BOLD ) activity levels in a midpontine site in the posterior basis pontis . 
NIN - induced midpontine activation may correspond to activation of the dorsomedial pontine nuclei and the nucleus reticularis tegmenti pontis , structures known to participate in the generation of multidirectional saccades and smooth pursuit eye movements . 
Acute effects of <mark>N - ( 2 - propylpentanoyl ) urea</mark> on hippocampal <mark>amino acid</mark> neurotransmitters in <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizure in rats . 
The present study aimed to investigate the anticonvulsant activity as well as the effects on the level of hippocampal <mark>amino acid</mark> neurotransmitters ( <mark>glutamate</mark> , <mark>aspartate</mark> , <mark>glycine</mark> and <mark>GABA</mark> ) of <mark>N - ( 2 - propylpentanoyl ) urea</mark> ( <mark>VPU</mark> ) in comparison to its parent compound , <mark>valproic acid</mark> ( <mark>VPA</mark> ) . 
<mark>VPU</mark> was more potent than <mark>VPA</mark> , exhibiting the median effective dose ( ED ( 50 ) ) of 49 mg / kg in protecting rats against <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizure whereas the corresponding value for <mark>VPA</mark> was 322 mg / kg . 
In vivo microdialysis demonstrated that an intraperitoneal administration of <mark>pilocarpine</mark> induced a pronounced increment of hippocampal <mark>glutamate</mark> and <mark>aspartate</mark> whereas no significant change was observed on the level of <mark>glycine</mark> and <mark>GABA</mark> . 
Pretreatment with either <mark>VPU</mark> ( 50 and 100 mg / kg ) or <mark>VPA</mark> ( 300 and 600 mg / kg ) completely abolished <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - evoked increases in extracellular <mark>glutamate</mark> and <mark>aspartate</mark> . 
In addition , a statistically significant reduction was also observed on the level of <mark>GABA</mark> and <mark>glycine</mark> but less than a drastic reduction of <mark>glutamate</mark> and <mark>aspartate</mark> level . 
Based on the finding that <mark>VPU</mark> and <mark>VPA</mark> could protect the animals against <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizure it is suggested that the reduction of inhibitory <mark>amino acid</mark> neurotransmitters was comparatively minor and offset by a pronounced reduction of <mark>glutamate</mark> and <mark>aspartate</mark> . 
Therefore , like <mark>VPA</mark> , the finding that <mark>VPU</mark> could drastically reduce <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced increases in <mark>glutamate</mark> and <mark>aspartate</mark> should account , at least partly , for its anticonvulsant activity observed in <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced seizure in experimental animals . 
Some other mechanism than those being reported herein should be further investigated . 
Protective effect of <mark>verapamil</mark> on gastric hemorrhagic ulcers in severe atherosclerotic rats . 
Studies concerning with pathogenesis of gastric hemorrhage and mucosal ulceration produced in atherosclerotic rats are lacking . 
The aim of this study is to examine the role of gastric acid back - diffusion , mast cell <mark>histamine</mark> release , lipid peroxide ( LPO ) generation and mucosal microvascular permeability in modulating gastric hemorrhage and ulcer in rats with atherosclerosis induced by coadministration of <mark>vitamin D2</mark> and <mark>cholesterol</mark> . 
Additionally , the protective effect of <mark>verapamil</mark> on this ulcer model was evaluated . 
Male Wistar rats were challenged intragastrically once daily for 9 days with 1 . 0 ml / kg of corn oil containing <mark>vitamin D2</mark> and <mark>cholesterol</mark> to induce atherosclerosis . 
Control rats received corn oil only . 
After gastric surgery , rat stomachs were irrigated for 3 h with either simulated gastric juice or normal saline . 
Gastric acid back - diffusion , mucosal LPO generation , <mark>histamine</mark> concentration , microvascular permeability , <mark>luminal</mark> hemoglobin content and ulcer areas were determined . 
Elevated atherosclerotic parameters , such as serum <mark>calcium</mark> , total <mark>cholesterol</mark> and low - density lipoprotein concentration were obtained in atherosclerotic rats . 
Severe gastric ulcers accompanied with increased ulcerogenic factors , including gastric acid back - diffusion , <mark>histamine</mark> release , LPO generation and <mark>luminal</mark> hemoglobin content were also observed in these rats . 
Moreover , a positive correlation of <mark>histamine</mark> to gastric hemorrhage and to ulcer was found in those atherosclerotic rats . 
This hemorrhagic ulcer and various ulcerogenic parameters were dose - dependently ameliorated by daily intragastric <mark>verapamil</mark> . 
Atherosclerosis could produce gastric hemorrhagic ulcer via aggravation of gastric acid back - diffusion , LPO generation , <mark>histamine</mark> release and microvascular permeability that could be ameliorated by <mark>verapamil</mark> in rats . 
<mark>Lamivudine</mark> for the prevention of hepatitis B virus reactivation in <mark>hepatitis - B surface antigen</mark> ( <mark>HBSAG</mark> ) seropositive cancer patients undergoing cytotoxic chemotherapy . 
Hepatitis B virus ( HBV ) is one of the major causes of chronic liver disease worldwide . 
Cancer patients who are chronic carriers of HBV have a higher hepatic complication rate while receiving cytotoxic chemotherapy ( CT ) and this has mainly been attributed to HBV reactivation . 
In this study , cancer patients who have solid and hematological malignancies with chronic HBV infection received the antiviral agent <mark>lamivudine</mark> prior and during CT compared with historical control group who did not receive <mark>lamivudine</mark> . 
The objectives were to assess the efficacy of <mark>lamivudine</mark> in reducing the incidence of HBV reactivation , and diminishing morbidity and mortality during CT . 
Two groups were compared in this study . 
The prophylactic <mark>lamivudin</mark> group consisted of 37 patients who received prophylactic <mark>lamivudine</mark> treatment . 
The historical controls consisted of 50 consecutive patients who underwent CT without prophylactic <mark>lamivudine</mark> . 
They were followed up during and for 8 weeks after CT . 
The outcomes were compared for both groups . 
Of our control group ( n = 50 ) , 21 patients ( 42 % ) were established hepatitis . 
Twelve ( 24 % ) of them were evaluated as severe hepatitis . 
In the prophylactic <mark>lamivudine</mark> group severe hepatitis were observed only in 1 patient ( 2 . 7 % ) of 37 patients ( p < 0 . 006 ) . 
Comparison of the mean ALT values revealed significantly higher mean <mark>alanine</mark> aminotransferase ( ALT ) values in the control group than the prophylactic <mark>lamivudine</mark> group ; 154 : 64 ( p < 0 . 32 ) . 
Our study suggests that prophylactic <mark>lamivudine</mark> significantly decreases the incidence of HBV reactivation and overall morbidity in cancer patients during and after immunosuppressive therapy . 
Further studies are needed to determine the most appropriate <mark>nucleoside</mark> or <mark>nucleotide</mark> analogue for antiviral prophylaxis during CT and the optimal duration of administration after completion of CT . 
Recovery of <mark>tacrolimus</mark> - associated brachial neuritis after conversion to <mark>everolimus</mark> in a pediatric renal transplant recipient - - case report and review of the literature . 
<mark>TAC</mark> has been shown to be a potent immunosuppressive agent for solid organ transplantation in pediatrics . 
Neurotoxicity is a potentially serious toxic effect . 
It is characterized by encephalopathy , headaches , seizures , or neurological deficits . 
Here , we describe an eight - and - a - half - yr - old male renal transplant recipient with right BN . 
MRI demonstrated hyperintense T2 signals in the cervical cord and right brachial plexus roots indicative of both myelitis and right brachial plexitis . 
Symptoms persisted for three months despite <mark>TAC</mark> dose reduction , administration of IVIG and four doses of <mark>methylprednisolone</mark> pulse therapy . 
Improvement and eventually full recovery only occurred after <mark>TAC</mark> was completely discontinued and successfully replaced by <mark>everolimus</mark> . 
Omitting <mark>fentanyl</mark> reduces nausea and vomiting , without increasing pain , after <mark>sevoflurane</mark> for day surgery . 
BACKGROUND AND OBJECTIVE : Despite advantages of induction and maintenance of anaesthesia with <mark>sevoflurane</mark> , postoperative nausea and vomiting occurs frequently . 
<mark>Fentanyl</mark> is a commonly used supplement that may contribute to this , although it may also improve analgesia . 
METHODS : This double - blind study examined the incidence and severity of postoperative nausea and vomiting and pain in the first 24 h after <mark>sevoflurane</mark> anaesthesia in 216 adult day surgery patients . 
Patients were randomly allocated to either receive or not receive 1 1 <mark>fentanyl</mark> , while a third group received <mark>dexamethasone</mark> in addition to <mark>fentanyl</mark> . 
RESULTS : Omission of <mark>fentanyl</mark> did not reduce the overall incidence of postoperative nausea and vomiting , but did reduce the incidence of vomiting and / or moderate to severe nausea prior to discharge from 20 % and 17 % with <mark>fentanyl</mark> and <mark>fentanyl</mark> - <mark>dexamethasone</mark> , respectively , to 5 % ( P = 0 . 013 ) . 
Antiemetic requirements were reduced from 24 % and 31 % to 7 % ( P = 0 . 0012 ) . 
<mark>Dexamethasone</mark> had no significant effect on the incidence or severity of postoperative nausea and vomiting . 
Combining the two <mark>fentanyl</mark> groups revealed further significant benefits from the avoidance of opioids , reducing postoperative nausea and vomiting and nausea prior to discharge from 35 % and 33 % to 22 % and 19 % ( P = 0 . 049 and P = 0 . 035 ) , respectively , while nausea in the first 24 h was decreased from 42 % to 27 % ( P = 0 . 034 ) . 
Pain severity and analgesic requirements were unaffected by the omission of <mark>fentanyl</mark> . 
<mark>Fentanyl</mark> did reduce minor intraoperative movement but had no <mark>sevoflurane</mark> - sparing effect and increased respiratory depression , hypotension and bradycardia . 
CONCLUSION : As <mark>fentanyl</mark> exacerbated postoperative nausea and vomiting without an improvement in postoperative pain and also had adverse cardiorespiratory effects , it appears to be an unnecessary and possibly detrimental supplement to <mark>sevoflurane</mark> in day surgery . 
Valvular heart disease in patients with Parkinson ' s disease treated with <mark>pergolide</mark> . 
Course following treatment modifications . 
Valvular heart abnormalities have been reported in patients with Parkinson ' s disease ( PD ) treated with <mark>pergolide</mark> . 
However , the incidence and severity of these abnormalities vary from study to study and their course after drug withdrawal has not been systematically assessed . 
OBJECTIVES : To estimate the frequency and severity of valvular heart abnormality and its possible reversibility after drug withdrawal in a case - control study . 
METHODS : All PD patients in the Amiens area treated with <mark>pergolide</mark> were invited to attend a cardiologic assessment including transthoracic echocardiography . 
Thirty PD patients participated in the study . 
A second echocardiography was performed ( median interval : 13 months ) after <mark>pergolide</mark> withdrawal ( n = 10 patients ) . 
Controls were age - and sex - matched non - PD patients referred to the cardiology department . 
RESULTS : Compared to controls , aortic regurgitation ( OR : 3 . 1 ; 95 % IC : 1 . 1 - 8 . 8 ) and mitral regurgitation ( OR : 10 . 7 ; 95 % IC : 2 . 1 - 53 ) were more frequent in PD patients ( tricuspid : NS ) . 
The number of affected valves ( n = 2 . 4 + / - 0 . 7 ) and the sum of regurgitation grades ( n = 2 . 8 + / - 1 . 09 ) were higher ( p = 0 . 008 and p = 0 . 006 , respectively ) in the <mark>pergolide</mark> group . 
Severity of regurgitation was not correlated with <mark>pergolide</mark> cumulative dose . 
A restrictive pattern of valvular regurgitation , suggestive of the role of <mark>pergolide</mark> , was observed in 12 / 30 ( 40 % ) patients including two with heart failure . 
<mark>Pergolide</mark> was discontinued in 10 patients with valvular heart disease , resulting in a lower regurgitation grade ( p = 0 . 01 ) at the second transthoracic echocardiography and the two patients with heart failure returned to nearly normal clinical examination . 
This study supports the high frequency of restrictive valve regurgitation in PD patients treated with <mark>pergolide</mark> and reveals that a significant improvement is usual when the treatment is converted to non - ergot <mark>dopamine</mark> agonists . 
<mark>Adriamycin</mark> - induced autophagic cardiomyocyte death plays a pathogenic role in a rat model of heart failure . 
BACKGROUND : The mechanisms underlying heart failure induced by <mark>adriamycin</mark> are very complicated and still unclear . 
The aim of this study was to investigate whether autophagy was involved in the progression of heart failure induced by <mark>adriamycin</mark> , so that we can develop a novel treatment strategy for heart failure . 
METHODS : <mark>3 - methyladenine</mark> ( <mark>3MA</mark> ) , a specific inhibitor on autophagy was used in a heart failure model of rats induced by <mark>adriamycin</mark> . 
Neonatal cardiomyocytes were isolated from Sprague - Dawley rat hearts and randomly divided into controls , an <mark>adriamycin</mark> - treated group , and a <mark>3MA</mark> plus <mark>adriamycin</mark> - treated group . 
We then examined the morphology , expression of beclin 1 gene , mitochondrial permeability transition ( MPT ) , and Na + - <mark>K</mark> + ATPase activity in vivo . 
We also assessed cell viability , mitochondrial membrane potential changes and counted autophagic vacuoles in cultured cardiomyocytes . 
In addition , we analyzed the expression of autophagy associated gene , beclin 1 using RT - PCR and Western blotting in an animal model . 
RESULTS : <mark>3MA</mark> significantly improved cardiac function and reduced mitochondrial injury . 
Furthermore , <mark>adriamycin</mark> induced the formation of autophagic vacuoles , and <mark>3MA</mark> strongly downregulated the expression of beclin 1 in <mark>adriamycin</mark> - induced failing heart and inhibited the formation of autophagic vacuoles . 
CONCLUSION : Autophagic cardiomyocyte death plays an important role in the pathogenesis of heart failure in rats induced by <mark>adriamycin</mark> . 
Mitochondrial injury may be involved in the progression of heart failure caused by <mark>adriamycin</mark> via the autophagy pathway . 
mToR inhibitors - induced proteinuria : mechanisms , significance , and management . 
Massive urinary protein excretion has been observed after conversion from calcineurin inhibitors to mammalian target of <mark>rapamycin</mark> ( mToR ) inhibitors , especially <mark>sirolimus</mark> , in renal transplant recipients with chronic allograft nephropathy . 
Because proteinuria is a major predictive factor of poor transplantation outcome , many studies focused on this adverse event during the past years . 
Whether proteinuria was due to <mark>sirolimus</mark> or only a consequence of calcineurin inhibitors withdrawal remained unsolved until high range proteinuria has been observed during <mark>sirolimus</mark> therapy in islet transplantation and in patients who received <mark>sirolimus</mark> de novo . 
Podocyte injury and focal segmental glomerulosclerosis have been related to mToR inhibition in some patients , but the pathways underlying these lesions remain hypothetic . 
We discuss herein the possible mechanisms and the significance of mToR blockade - induced proteinuria . 
Neuropsychiatric side effects after the use of <mark>mefloquine</mark> . 
This study describes neuropsychiatric side effects in patients after treatment with <mark>mefloquine</mark> . 
Reactions consisted mainly of seizures , acute psychoses , anxiety neurosis , and major disturbances of sleep - wake rhythm . 
Side effects occurred after both therapeutic and prophylactic intake and were graded from moderate to severe . 
In a risk analysis of neuropsychiatric side effects in Germany , it is estimated that one of 8 , 000 <mark>mefloquine</mark> users suffers from such reactions . 
The incidence calculation revealed that one of 215 therapeutic users had reactions , compared with one of 13 , 000 in the prophylaxis group , making the risk of neuropsychiatric reactions after <mark>mefloquine</mark> treatment 60 times higher than after prophylaxis . 
Therefore , certain limitations for malaria prophylaxis and treatment with <mark>mefloquine</mark> are recommended . 
Prenatal protein deprivation alters <mark>dopamine</mark> - mediated behaviors and dopaminergic and glutamatergic receptor binding . 
Epidemiological evidence indicates that prenatal nutritional deprivation may increase the risk of schizophrenia . 
The goal of these studies was to use an animal model to examine the effects of prenatal protein deprivation on behaviors and receptor binding with relevance to schizophrenia . 
We report that prenatally protein deprived ( PD ) female rats showed an increased stereotypic response to <mark>apomorphine</mark> and an increased locomotor response to <mark>amphetamine</mark> in adulthood . 
These differences were not observed during puberty . 
No changes in <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced catalepsy or <mark>MK - 801</mark> - induced locomotion were seen following PD . 
In addition , PD female rats showed increased ( 3 ) <mark>H</mark> - <mark>MK - 801</mark> binding in the striatum and hippocampus , but not in the cortex . 
PD female rats also showed increased ( 3 ) <mark>H</mark> - <mark>haloperidol</mark> binding and decreased <mark>dopamine</mark> transporter binding in striatum . 
No statistically significant changes in behavior or receptor binding were found in PD males with the exception of increased ( 3 ) <mark>H</mark> - <mark>MK - 801</mark> binding in cortex . 
This animal model may be useful to explore the mechanisms by which prenatal nutritional deficiency enhances risk for schizophrenia in humans and may also have implications for developmental processes leading to differential sensitivity to drugs of abuse . 
Adverse effects of topical <mark>papaverine</mark> on auditory nerve function . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Papaverine hydrochloride</mark> is a direct - acting vasodilator used to manage vasospasm during various neurosurgical operations . 
Transient cranial nerve dysfunction has been described in a few cases with topical <mark>papaverine</mark> . 
This study supports previous reports and provides neurophysiological evidence of an adverse effect on the auditory nerve . 
METHODS : We conducted a retrospective review of 70 consecutive microvascular decompression operations and studied those patients who received topical <mark>papaverine</mark> for vasospasm . 
Topical <mark>papaverine</mark> was used as a direct therapeutic action to manage vasospasm in a total of 11 patients . 
The timing of <mark>papaverine</mark> application and ongoing operative events was reviewed relative to changes in neurophysiological recordings . 
Brainstem auditory evoked potentials ( BAEPs ) were routinely used to monitor cochlear nerve function during these operations . 
FINDINGS : A temporal relationship was found between topical <mark>papaverine</mark> and BAEP changes leading to complete waveform loss . 
The average temporal delay between <mark>papaverine</mark> and the onset of an adverse BAEP change was 5 min . 
In 10 of 11 patients , BAEP waves II / III - V completely disappeared within 2 to 25 min after <mark>papaverine</mark> . 
Eight of these 10 patients had complete loss of BAEP waveforms within 10 min . 
One patient showed no recovery of later waves and a delayed profound sensorineural hearing loss . 
The average recovery time of BAEP waveforms to pre - <mark>papaverine</mark> baseline values was 39 min . 
CONCLUSIONS : Topical <mark>papaverine</mark> for the treatment of vasospasm was associated with the onset of a transient disturbance in neurophysiological function of the ascending auditory brainstem pathway . 
The complete disappearance of BAEP waveforms with a consistent temporal delay suggests a possible adverse effect on the proximal eighth nerve . 
Recommendations to avoid potential cranial nerve deficits from <mark>papaverine</mark> are provided . 
<mark>Simvastatin - ezetimibe</mark> - induced hepatic failure necessitating liver transplantation . 
Abstract Serum aminotransferase elevations are a commonly known adverse effect of 3 - hydroxy - 3 - methylglutaryl coenzyme A reductase inhibitor ( <mark>statin</mark> ) therapy . 
However , hepatotoxic events have not been widely published with <mark>ezetimibe</mark> or the combination agent <mark>simvastatin - ezetimibe</mark> . 
We describe a 70 - year - old Hispanic woman who developed fulminant hepatic failure necessitating liver transplantation 10 weeks after conversion from <mark>simvastatin</mark> 40 mg / day to <mark>simvastatin 10 mg - ezetimibe 40 mg</mark> / day . 
The patient ' s lipid panel had been maintained with <mark>simvastatin</mark> for 18 months before the conversion without evidence of hepatotoxicity . 
A routine laboratory work - up 10 weeks after conversion revealed elevated serum aminotransferase levels . 
<mark>Simvastatinezetimibe</mark> and <mark>escitalopram</mark> ( which she was taking for depression ) were discontinued , and other potential causes of hepatotoxicity were excluded . 
A repeat work - up revealed further elevations in aminotransferase levels , and liver biopsy revealed evidence of moderate - to - severe drug toxicity . 
She underwent liver transplantation with an uneventful postoperative course . 
Her aminotransferase levels returned to normal by postoperative day 23 , and her 2 - year follow - up showed no adverse events . 
<mark>Ezetimibe</mark> undergoes extensive glucuronidation by <mark>uridine diphosphate</mark> glucoronosyltransferases ( UGT ) in the intestine and liver and may have inhibited the glucuronidation of <mark><mark>simvastatin</mark> hydroxy acid</mark> , resulting in increased simvastatin exposure and subsequent hepatotoxicity . 
To our knowledge , this is the first case report of <mark>simvastatin - ezetimibe</mark> - induced liver failure that resulted in liver transplantation . 
We postulate that the mechanism of the <mark>simvastatinezetimibe</mark> - induced hepatotoxicity is the increased <mark>simvastatin</mark> exposure by <mark>ezetimibe</mark> inhibition of UGT enzymes . 
Clinicians should be aware of potential hepatotoxicity with <mark>simvastatin - ezetimibe</mark> especially in elderly patients and should carefully monitor serum aminotransferase levels when starting therapy and titrating the dosage . 
Massive proteinuria and acute renal failure after oral <mark>bisphosphonate</mark> ( <mark>alendronate</mark> ) administration in a patient with focal segmental glomerulosclerosis . 
A 61 - year - old Japanese man with nephrotic syndrome due to focal segmental glomerulosclerosis was initially responding well to <mark>steroid</mark> therapy . 
The amount of daily urinary protein decreased from 15 . 6 to 2 . 8 g . 
Within 14 days of the oral <mark>bisphosphonate</mark> ( <mark>alendronate sodium</mark> ) administration , the amount of daily urinary protein increased rapidly up to 12 . 8 g with acute renal failure . 
After discontinuing the oral <mark>alendronate</mark> , the patient underwent six cycles of hemodialysis and four cycles of LDL apheresis . 
Urinary volume and serum <mark>creatinine</mark> levels recovered to the normal range , with urinary protein disappearing completely within 40 days . 
This report demonstrates that not only intravenous , but also oral <mark>bisphosphonates</mark> can aggravate proteinuria and acute renal failure . 
Serum - and glucocorticoid - inducible kinase 1 in <mark>doxorubicin</mark> - induced nephrotic syndrome . 
<mark>Doxorubicin</mark> - induced nephropathy leads to epithelial <mark>sodium</mark> channel ( ENaC ) - dependent volume retention and renal fibrosis . 
The <mark>aldosterone</mark> - sensitive serum - and glucocorticoid - inducible kinase SGK1 has been shown to participate in the stimulation of ENaC and to mediate renal fibrosis following mineralocorticoid and salt excess . 
The present study was performed to elucidate the role of SGK1 in the volume retention and fibrosis during nephrotic syndrome . 
To this end , <mark>doxorubicin</mark> ( 15 mug / g body wt ) was injected intravenously into gene - targeted mice lacking SGK1 ( sgk1 ( - / - ) ) and their wild - type littermates ( sgk1 ( + / + ) ) . 
<mark>Doxorubicin</mark> treatment resulted in heavy proteinuria ( > 100 mg protein / mg crea ) in 15 / 44 of sgk1 ( + / + ) and 15 / 44 of sgk1 ( - / - ) mice leading to severe nephrotic syndrome with ascites , lipidemia , and hypoalbuminemia in both genotypes . 
Plasma <mark>aldosterone</mark> levels increased in nephrotic mice of both genotypes and was followed by increased SGK1 protein expression in sgk1 ( + / + ) mice . 
Urinary <mark>sodium</mark> excretion reached signficantly lower values in sgk1 ( + / + ) mice ( 15 + / - 5 mumol / mg crea ) than in sgk1 ( - / - ) mice ( 35 + / - 5 mumol / mg crea ) and was associated with a significantly higher body weight gain in sgk1 ( + / + ) compared with sgk1 ( - / - ) mice ( + 6 . 6 + / - 0 . 7 vs . + 4 . 1 + / - 0 . 8 g ) . 
During the course of nephrotic syndrome , serum <mark>urea</mark> concentrations increased significantly faster in sgk1 ( - / - ) mice than in sgk1 ( + / + ) mice leading to uremia and a reduced median survival in sgk1 ( - / - ) mice ( 29 vs . 40 days in sgk1 ( + / + ) mice ) . 
In conclusion , gene - targeted mice lacking SGK1 showed blunted volume retention , yet were not protected against renal fibrosis during experimental nephrotic syndrome . 
Severe thrombocytopenia and haemolytic anaemia associated with <mark>ciprofloxacin</mark> : a case report with fatal outcome . 
Haematological adverse reactions associated with fatal outcome are rare during treatment with <mark>ciprofloxacin</mark> . 
A 30 - year old Caucasian man reported with abdominal pain and jaundice after 3 - day administration of oral <mark>ciprofloxacin</mark> for a suspect of urinary tract infection . 
Clinical evaluations suggested an initial diagnosis of severe thrombocytopenia and haemolysis . 
The patient progressively developed petechiae and purpura on thorax and lower limbs . 
Despite pharmacological and supportive interventions , laboratory parameters worsened and the patient died 17 hours after admission . 
An accurate autopsy revealed most organs with diffuse petechial haemorrhages . 
No signs of bone marrow depression were found . 
No thrombi or signs of microangiopathies were observed in arterial vessels . 
Blood and urine cultures did not show any bacterial growth . 
This case report shows that <mark>ciprofloxacin</mark> may precipitate life - threatening thrombocytopenia and haemolytic anaemia , even in the early phases of treatment and without apparent previous exposures . 
<mark>Alpha - lipoic acid</mark> prevents mitochondrial damage and neurotoxicity in experimental chemotherapy neuropathy . 
The study investigates if <mark>alpha - lipoic acid</mark> is neuroprotective against chemotherapy induced neurotoxicity , if mitochondrial damage plays a critical role in toxic neurodegenerative cascade , and if neuroprotective effects of <mark>alpha - lipoic acid</mark> depend on mitochondria protection . 
We used an in vitro model of chemotherapy induced peripheral neuropathy that closely mimic the in vivo condition by exposing primary cultures of dorsal root ganglion ( DRG ) sensory neurons to <mark>paclitaxel</mark> and <mark>cisplatin</mark> , two widely used and highly effective chemotherapeutic drugs . 
This approach allowed investigating the efficacy of <mark>alpha - lipoic acid</mark> in preventing axonal damage and apoptosis and the function and ultrastructural morphology of mitochondria after exposure to toxic agents and <mark>alpha - lipoic acid</mark> . 
Our results demonstrate that both <mark>cisplatin</mark> and <mark>paclitaxel</mark> cause early mitochondrial impairment with loss of membrane potential and induction of autophagic vacuoles in neurons . 
<mark>Alpha - lipoic acid</mark> exerts neuroprotective effects against chemotherapy induced neurotoxicity in sensory neurons : it rescues the mitochondrial toxicity and induces the expression of frataxin , an essential mitochondrial protein with anti - oxidant and chaperone properties . 
In conclusion mitochondrial toxicity is an early common event both in <mark>paclitaxel</mark> and <mark>cisplatin</mark> induced neurotoxicity . 
<mark>Alpha - lipoic acid</mark> protects sensory neurons through its anti - oxidant and mitochondrial regulatory functions , possibly inducing the expression of frataxin . 
These findings suggest that <mark>alpha - lipoic acid</mark> might reduce the risk of developing peripheral nerve toxicity in patients undergoing chemotherapy and encourage further confirmatory clinical trials . 
Toxicity in rhesus monkeys following administration of the <mark>8 - aminoquinoline</mark> <mark>8 - [ ( 4 - amino - l - methylbutyl ) amino ] - 5 - ( l - hexyloxy ) - 6 - methoxy - 4 - methylquinoline</mark> ( <mark>WR242511</mark> ) . 
INTRODUCTION : Many substances that form methemoglobin ( MHb ) effectively counter cyanide ( CN ) toxicity . 
Although MHb formers are generally applied as treatments for CN poisoning , it has been proposed that a stable , long - acting MHb former could serve as a CN pretreatment . 
Using this rationale , the <mark>8 - aminoquinoline</mark> <mark>WR242511</mark> , a potent long - lasting MHb former in rodents and beagle dogs , was studied in the rhesus monkey for advanced development as a potential CN pretreatment . 
METHODS : In this study , <mark>WR242511</mark> was administered intravenously ( IV ) in 2 female and 4 male rhesus monkeys in doses of 3 . 5 and / or 7 . 0 mg / kg ; a single male also received <mark>WR242511</mark> orally ( PO ) at 7 . 0 mg / kg . 
Health status and MHb levels were monitored following exposure . 
RESULTS : The selected doses of <mark>WR242511</mark> , which produced significant methemoglobinemia in beagle dogs in earlier studies conducted elsewhere , produced very little MHb ( mean < 2 . 0 % ) in the rhesus monkey . 
Furthermore , transient hemoglobinuria was noted approximately 60 minutes postinjection of <mark>WR242511</mark> ( 3 . 5 or 7 . 0 mg / kg ) , and 2 lethalities occurred ( one IV and one PO ) following the 7 . 0 mg / kg dose . 
Myoglobinuria was also observed following the 7 . 0 mg / kg dose . 
Histopathology analyses in the 2 animals that died revealed liver and kidney toxicity , with greater severity in the orally - treated animal . 
CONCLUSIONS : These data demonstrate direct and / or indirect drug - induced toxicity . 
It is concluded that <mark>WR242511</mark> should not be pursued as a pretreatment for CN poisoning unless the anti - CN characteristics of this compound can be successfully dissociated from those producing undesirable toxicity . 
Repetitive transcranial magnetic stimulation for <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesias in Parkinson ' s disease . 
In a placebo - controlled , single - blinded , crossover study , we assessed the effect of " real " repetitive transcranial magnetic stimulation ( rTMS ) versus " sham " rTMS ( placebo ) on peak dose dyskinesias in patients with Parkinson ' s disease ( PD ) . 
Ten patients with PD and prominent dyskinesias had rTMS ( 1 , 800 pulses ; 1 Hz rate ) delivered over the motor cortex for 4 consecutive days twice , once real stimuli and once sham stimulation were used ; evaluations were done at the baseline and 1 day after the end of each of the treatment series . 
Direct comparison between sham and real rTMS effects showed no significant difference in clinician - assessed dyskinesia severity . 
However , comparison with the baseline showed small but significant reduction in dyskinesia severity following real rTMS but not placebo . 
The major effect was on dystonia subscore . 
Similarly , in patient diaries , although both treatments caused reduction in subjective dyskinesia scores during the days of intervention , the effect was sustained for 3 days after the intervention for the real rTMS only . 
Following rTMS , no side effects and no adverse effects on motor function and PD symptoms were noted . 
The results suggest the existence of residual beneficial clinical aftereffects of consecutive daily applications of low - frequency rTMS on dyskinesias in PD . 
The effects may be further exploited for potential therapeutic uses . 
Intracavernous <mark>epinephrine</mark> : a minimally invasive treatment for priapism in the emergency department . 
Priapism is the prolonged erection of the penis in the absence of sexual arousal . 
A 45 - year - old man , an admitted frequent <mark>cocaine</mark> user , presented to the Emergency Department ( ED ) on two separate occasions with a history of priapism after <mark>cocaine</mark> use . 
The management options in the ED , as exemplified by four individual case reports , in particular the use of a minimally invasive method of intracorporal <mark>epinephrine</mark> instillation , are discussed . 
Prophylactic use of <mark>lamivudine</mark> with chronic immunosuppressive therapy for rheumatologic disorders . 
The objective of this study was to report our experience concerning the effectiveness of the prophylactic administration of <mark>lamivudine</mark> in <mark>hepatitis B virus surface antigen</mark> ( <mark>HBs Ag</mark> ) positive patients with rheumatologic disease . 
From June 2004 to October 2006 , 11 <mark>HBs Ag</mark> positive patients with rheumatologic diseases , who were on both immunosuppressive and prophylactic <mark>lamivudine</mark> therapies , were retrospectively assessed . 
Liver function tests , hepatitis B virus ( HBV ) serologic markers , and HBV DNA levels of the patients during follow - up were obtained from hospital file records . 
Eleven patients ( six male ) with median age 47 years ( range 27 - 73 ) , median disease duration 50 months ( range 9 - 178 ) and median follow - up period of patients 13 . 8 months ( range 5 - 27 ) were enrolled in this study . 
<mark>Lamivudine</mark> therapy was started 3 - 7 days prior to immunosuppressive therapy in all patients . 
Baseline , liver function tests were elevated in two patients ( fourth patient : ALT : 122 IU / l , AST : 111 IU / l , tenth patient : ALT : 294 IU / l , AST : 274 IU / l , with minimal changes in the liver biopsy in both ) . 
Shortly after treatment their tests normalized and during follow - up period none of the patients had abnormal liver function tests . 
In four patients HBV DNA levels were higher than normal at baseline . 
Two of these normalized and the others increased later . 
In three additional patients , HBV DNA levels were increased during follow - up . 
None of the patients had significant clinical sings of HBV activation . 
<mark>Lamivudine</mark> was well tolerated and was continued in all patients . 
Prophylactic administration of <mark>lamivudine</mark> in patients who required immunosuppressive therapy seems to be safe , well tolerated and effective in preventing HBV reactivation . 
Effect of <mark>green tea</mark> and <mark>vitamin E</mark> combination in <mark>isoproterenol</mark> induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
The present study was aimed to investigate the combined effects of <mark>green tea</mark> and <mark>vitamin E</mark> on heart weight , body weight , serum marker enzymes , lipid peroxidation , endogenous antioxidants and membrane bound ATPases in <mark>isoproterenol</mark> ( <mark>ISO</mark> ) - induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
Adult male albino rats , treated with <mark>ISO</mark> ( 200 mg / kg , s . c . ) for 2 days at an interval of 24 h caused a significant ( P < 0 . 05 ) elevation of heart weight , serum marker enzymes , lipid peroxidation and <mark>Ca</mark> + 2 ATPase level whereas there was a significant ( P < 0 . 05 ) decrease in body weight , endogenous antioxidants , <mark>Na</mark> + / <mark>K</mark> + ATPase and <mark>Mg</mark> + 2 ATPase levels . 
Administration of <mark>green tea</mark> ( 100 mg / kg / day , p . o . ) and <mark>vitamin E</mark> ( 100 mg / kg / day , p . o . ) together for 30 consecutive days and challenged with <mark>ISO</mark> on the day 29th and 30th , showed a significant ( P < 0 . 05 ) decrease in heart weight , serum marker enzymes , lipid peroxidation , <mark>Ca</mark> + 2 ATPase and a significant increase in the body weight , endogenous antioxidants , <mark>Na</mark> + / <mark>K</mark> + ATPase and <mark>Mg</mark> + 2 ATPase when compared with <mark>ISO</mark> treated group and <mark>green tea</mark> or <mark>vitamin E</mark> alone treated groups . 
These findings indicate the synergistic protective effect of <mark>green tea</mark> and <mark>vitamin E</mark> during <mark>ISO</mark> induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
Irreversible damage to the medullary interstitium in experimental analgesic nephropathy in F344 rats . 
Renal papillary necrosis ( RPN ) and a decreased urinary concentrating ability developed during continuous long - term treatment with <mark>aspirin</mark> and <mark>paracetamol</mark> in female Fischer 344 rats . 
Renal structure and concentrating ability were examined after a recovery period of up to 18 weeks , when no analgesics were given , to investigate whether the analgesic - induced changes were reversible . 
There was no evidence of repair to the damaged medullary interstitial matrix , or proliferation of remaining undamaged type 1 medullary interstitial cells after the recovery period following analgesic treatment . 
The recovery of urinary concentrating ability was related to the length of analgesic treatment and the extent of the resulting inner medullary structural damage . 
During the early stages of analgesic treatment , the changes in urinary concentrating ability were reversible , but after prolonged analgesic treatment , maximum urinary concentrating ability failed to recover . 
This study shows that prolonged analgesic treatment in Fischer 344 rats causes progressive and irreversible damage to the interstitial matrix and type 1 interstitial cells leading to RPN . 
The associated urinary concentrating defect is reversible only during the early stages of structural damage to the inner medulla . 
<mark>Testosterone</mark> - dependent hypertension and upregulation of intrarenal angiotensinogen in Dahl <mark>salt</mark> - sensitive rats . 
Blood pressure ( BP ) is more <mark>salt</mark> sensitive in men than in premenopausal women . 
In Dahl <mark>salt</mark> - sensitive rats ( DS ) , high - <mark>salt</mark> ( HS ) diet increases BP more in males than females . 
In contrast to the systemic renin - <mark>angiotensin</mark> system , which is suppressed in response to HS in male DS , intrarenal angiotensinogen expression is increased , and intrarenal levels of ANG II are not suppressed . 
In this study , the hypothesis was tested that there is a sexual dimorphism in HS - induced upregulation of intrarenal angiotensinogen mediated by <mark>testosterone</mark> that also causes increases in BP and renal injury . 
On a low - <mark>salt</mark> ( LS ) diet , male DS had higher levels of intrarenal angiotensinogen mRNA than females . 
HS diet for 4 wk increased renal cortical angiotensinogen mRNA and protein only in male DS , which was prevented by castration . 
Ovariectomy of female DS had no effect on intrarenal angiotensinogen expression on either diet . 
Radiotelemetric BP was similar between males and castrated rats on LS diet . 
HS diet for 4 wk caused a progressive increase in BP , protein and albumin excretion , and glomerular sclerosis in male DS rats , which were attenuated by castration . 
<mark>Testosterone</mark> replacement in castrated DS rats increased BP , renal injury , and upregulation of renal angiotensinogen associated with HS diet . 
<mark>Testosterone</mark> contributes to the development of hypertension and renal injury in male DS rats on HS diet possibly through upregulation of the intrarenal renin - <mark>angiotensin</mark> system . 
Explicit episodic memory for sensory - discriminative components of <mark>capsaicin</mark> - induced pain : immediate and delayed ratings . 
Pain memory is thought to affect future pain sensitivity and thus contribute to clinical pain conditions . 
Systematic investigations of the human capacity to remember sensory features of experimental pain are sparse . 
In order to address long - term pain memory , nine healthy male volunteers received intradermal injections of three doses of <mark>capsaicin</mark> ( 0 . 05 , 1 and 20 microg , separated by 15 min breaks ) , each given three times in a balanced design across three sessions at one week intervals . 
Pain rating was performed using a computerized visual analogue scale ( 0 - 100 ) digitized at 1 / s , either immediately online or one hour or one day after injection . 
Subjects also recalled their pains one week later . 
<mark>Capsaicin</mark> injection reliably induced a dose - dependent flare ( p < 0 . 001 ) without any difference within or across sessions . 
The strong burning pain decayed exponentially within a few minutes . 
Subjects were able to reliably discriminate pain magnitude and duration across <mark>capsaicin</mark> doses ( both p < 0 . 001 ) , regardless of whether first - time ratings were requested immediately , after one hour or after one day . 
Pain recall after one week was similarly precise ( magnitude : p < 0 . 01 , duration : p < 0 . 05 ) . 
Correlation with rating recall after one week was best when first - time ratings were requested as late as one day after injection ( R ( 2 ) = 0 . 79 ) indicating that both rating retrievals utilized similar memory traces . 
These results indicate a reliable memory for magnitude and duration of experimentally induced pain . 
The data further suggest that the consolidation of this memory is an important interim stage , and may take up to one day . 
Severe and long lasting cholestasis after high - dose <mark>co - trimoxazole</mark> treatment for Pneumocystis pneumonia in HIV - infected patients - - a report of two cases . 
Pneumocystis pneumonia ( PCP ) , a common opportunistic infection in HIV - infected individuals , is generally treated with high doses of <mark>co - trimoxazole</mark> . 
However , treatment is often limited by adverse effects . 
Here , we report two cases of severely immunocompromised HIV - infected patients who developed severe intrahepatic cholestasis , and in one patient lesions mimicking liver abscess formation on radiologic exams , during <mark>co - trimoxazole</mark> treatment for PCP . 
Whereas patient 1 showed lesions of up to 1 cm readily detectable on magnetic resonance imaging under prolonged <mark>co - trimoxazole</mark> treatment , therapy of patient 2 was switched early . 
<mark>Bradykinin</mark> receptors antagonists and <mark>nitric oxide</mark> synthase inhibitors in <mark>vincristine</mark> and <mark>streptozotocin</mark> induced hyperalgesia in chemotherapy and diabetic neuropathy rat model . 
PURPOSE : The influence of an irreversible inhibitor of constitutive <mark>NO</mark> synthase ( L - NOArg ; 1 . 0 mg / kg ip ) , a relatively selective inhibitor of inducible <mark>NO</mark> synthase ( L - NIL ; 1 . 0 mg / kg ip ) and a relatively specific inhibitor of neuronal <mark>NO</mark> synthase ( 7 - NI ; 0 . 1 mg / kg ip ) , on antihyperalgesic action of selective antagonists of B2 and B1 receptors : D - Arg - [ Hyp3 , Thi5 , D - Tic7 , Oic8 ] <mark>bradykinin</mark> ( <mark>HOE 140</mark> ; 70 nmol / kg ip ) or <mark>des Arg10 HOE 140</mark> ( 70 nmol / kg ip ) respectively , in model of diabetic ( streptozotocin - induced ) and toxic ( vincristine - induced ) neuropathy was investigated . 
METHODS : The changes in pain thresholds were determined using mechanical stimuli - - the modification of the classic paw withdrawal test described by Randall - Selitto . 
RESULTS : The results of this paper confirm that inhibition of <mark>bradykinin</mark> receptors and inducible <mark>NO</mark> synthase but not neuronal <mark>NO</mark> synthase activity reduces diabetic hyperalgesia . 
Pretreatment with L - NOArg and L - NIL but not 7 - NI , significantly increases antihyperalgesic activity both <mark>HOE 140</mark> and <mark>des Arg10 HOE 140</mark> . 
It was also shown that both products of inducible <mark>NO</mark> synthase and neuronal <mark>NO</mark> synthase activation as well as <mark>bradykinin</mark> are involved in hyperalgesia produced by <mark>vincristine</mark> . 
Moreover , L - NOArg and 7 - NI but not L - NIL intensify antihyperalgesic activity of <mark>HOE 140</mark> or <mark>des - Arg10HOE 140</mark> in toxic neuropathy . 
CONCLUSIONS : Results of these studies suggest that B1 and B2 receptors are engaged in transmission of nociceptive stimuli in both diabetic and toxic neuropathy . 
In <mark>streptozotocin</mark> - induced hyperalgesia , inducible <mark>NO</mark> synthase participates in pronociceptive activity of <mark>bradykinin</mark> , whereas in <mark>vincristine</mark> - induced hyperalgesia <mark>bradykinin</mark> seemed to activate neuronal <mark>NO</mark> synthase pathway . 
Therefore , concomitant administration of small doses of <mark>bradykinin</mark> receptor antagonists and <mark>NO</mark> synthase inhibitors can be effective in alleviation of neuropathic pain , even in hospital care . 
Confusion , a rather serious adverse drug reaction with <mark>valproic acid</mark> : a review of the French Pharmacovigilance database . 
INTRODUCTION : Confusion is an adverse drug reaction frequently observed with <mark>valproic acid</mark> . 
Some case reports are published in the literature but no systematic study from a sample of patients has been published . 
We performed this study in order to describe the main characteristics of this adverse drug reaction . 
METHODS : Using the French Pharmacovigilance database , we selected the cases of confusion reported since 1985 with <mark>valproic acid</mark> . 
RESULTS : 272 cases of confusion were reported with <mark>valproic acid</mark> : 153 women and 119 men . 
Confusion mostly occurred during the two first weeks following <mark>valproic acid</mark> exposure ( 39 . 7 % ) . 
It was " serious " for almost 2 / 3 of the patients ( 62 . 5 % ) and its outcome favourable in most of the cases ( 82 % ) . 
The occurrence of this ADR was more frequent in patients aged between 61 and 80 years . 
CONCLUSION : This work shows that confusion with <mark>valproic acid</mark> is a serious , rather frequent but reversible adverse drug reaction . 
It occurs especially in older patients and during the first two weeks of treatment . 
Reversible inferior colliculus lesion in <mark>metronidazole</mark> - induced encephalopathy : magnetic resonance findings on diffusion - weighted and fluid attenuated inversion recovery imaging . 
OBJECTIVE : This is to present reversible inferior colliculus lesions in <mark>metronidazole</mark> - induced encephalopathy , to focus on the diffusion - weighted imaging ( DWI ) and fluid attenuated inversion recovery ( FLAIR ) imaging . 
MATERIALS AND METHODS : From November 2005 to September 2007 , 8 patients ( 5 men and 3 women ) were diagnosed as having <mark>metronidazole</mark> - induced encephalopathy ( age range ; 43 - 78 years ) . 
They had been taking <mark>metronidazole</mark> ( total dosage , 45 - 120 g ; duration , 30 days to 2 months ) to treat the infection in various organs . 
Initial brain magnetic resonance imaging ( MRI ) were obtained after the hospitalization , including DWI ( 8 / 8 ) , apparent diffusion coefficient ( ADC ) map ( 4 / 8 ) , FLAIR ( 7 / 8 ) , and T2 - weighted image ( 8 / 8 ) . 
Follow - up MRIs were performed on 5 patients from third to 14th days after discontinuation of <mark>metronidazole</mark> administration . 
Findings of initial and follow - up MRIs were retrospectively evaluated by 2 neuroradiologists by consensus , to analyze the presence of abnormal signal intensities , their locations , and signal changes on follow - up images . 
RESULTS : Initial MRIs showed abnormal high signal intensities on DWI and FLAIR ( or T2 - weighted image ) at the dentate nucleus ( 8 / 8 ) , inferior colliculus ( 6 / 8 ) , corpus callosum ( 2 / 8 ) , pons ( 2 / 8 ) , medulla ( 1 / 8 ) , and bilateral cerebral white matter ( 1 / 8 ) . 
High - signal intensity lesions on DWI tended to show low signal intensity on ADC map ( 3 / 4 ) , but in one patient , high signal intensity was shown at bilateral dentate nuclei on not only DWI but also ADC map . 
All the lesions in dentate , inferior colliculus , pons , and medullas had been resolved completely on follow - up MRIs in 5 patients , but in 1 patient of them , corpus callosal lesion persisted .
