CONCLUSIONS : Reversible inferior colliculus lesions could be considered as the characteristic for <mark>metronidazole</mark> - induced encephalopathy , next to the dentate nucleus involvement . 
Clinically significant proteinuria following the administration of <mark>sirolimus</mark> to renal transplant recipients . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Sirolimus</mark> is the latest immunosuppressive agent used to prevent rejection , and may have less nephrotoxicity than calcineurin inhibitor ( CNI ) - based regimens . 
To date there has been little documentation of clinically significant proteinuria linked with the use of <mark>sirolimus</mark> . 
We have encountered several patients who developed substantial proteinuria associated with <mark>sirolimus</mark> use . 
In each patient , the close temporal association between the commencement of <mark>sirolimus</mark> therapy and proteinuria implicated <mark>sirolimus</mark> as the most likely etiology of the proteinuria . 
METHODS : We analyzed the clinical and laboratory information available for all 119 patients transplanted at the Washington Hospital Center between 1999 - 2003 for whom <mark>sirolimus</mark> was a component of their immunosuppressant regimen . 
In these patients , the magnitude of proteinuria was assessed on morning urine samples by turbidometric measurement or random urine protein : <mark>creatinine</mark> ratios , an estimate of grams of proteinuria / day . 
Laboratory results were compared between prior , during and following <mark>sirolimus</mark> use . 
RESULTS : Twenty - eight patients ( 24 % ) developed increased proteinuria from baseline during their post - transplantation course . 
In 21 patients an alternative cause of proteinuria was either obvious or insufficient data was available to be conclusive . 
In 7 of the 28 patients there was a striking temporal association between the initiation of <mark>sirolimus</mark> and the development of nephrotic - range proteinuria . 
Proteinuria correlated most strongly with <mark>sirolimus</mark> therapy when compared to other demographic and clinical variables . 
In most patients , discontinuation of <mark>sirolimus</mark> resulted in a decrease , but not resolution , of proteinuria . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Sirolimus</mark> induces or aggravates pre - existing proteinuria in an unpredictable subset of renal allograft recipients . 
Proteinuria may improve , but does not resolve , when <mark>sirolimus</mark> is withdrawn . 
Components of lemon essential oil attenuate dementia induced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> . 
The anti - dementia effects of <mark>s - limonene</mark> and <mark>s - perillyl alcohol</mark> were observed using the passive avoidance test ( PA ) and the open field habituation test ( OFH ) . 
These lemon essential oils showed strong ability to improve memory impaired by <mark>scopolamine</mark> ; however , <mark>s - perillyl alcohol</mark> relieved the deficit of associative memory in PA only , and did not improve non - associative memory significantly in OFH . 
Analysis of neurotransmitter concentration in some brain regions on the test day showed that <mark>dopamine</mark> concentration of the vehicle / <mark>scopolamine</mark> group was significantly lower than that of the vehicle / vehicle group , but this phenomenon was reversed when <mark>s - limonene</mark> or <mark>s - perillyl alcohol</mark> were administered before the injection of <mark>scopolamine</mark> . 
Simultaneously , we found that these two lemon essential oil components could inhibit acetylcholinesterase activity in vitro using the Ellman method . 
Attentional modulation of perceived pain intensity in <mark>capsaicin</mark> - induced secondary hyperalgesia . 
Perceived pain intensity is modulated by attention . 
However , it is not known that how pain intensity ratings are affected by attention in <mark>capsaicin</mark> - induced secondary hyperalgesia . 
Here we show that perceived pain intensity in secondary hyperalgesia is decreased when attention is distracted away from the painful pinprick stimulus with a visual task . 
Furthermore , it was found that the magnitude of attentional modulation in secondary hyperalgesia is very similar to that of <mark>capsaicin</mark> - untreated , control condition . 
Our findings , showing no interaction between <mark>capsaicin</mark> treatment and attentional modulation suggest that <mark>capsaicin</mark> - induced secondary hyperalgesia and attention might affect mechanical pain through independent mechanisms . 
Cardioprotective effect of <mark>salvianolic acid A</mark> on <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
The present study was designed to evaluate the cardioprotective potential of <mark>salvianolic acid A</mark> on <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced myocardial infarction in rats . 
Hemodynamic parameters and lead II electrocardiograph were monitored and recorded continuously . 
Cardiac marker enzymes and antioxidative parameters in serum and heart tissues were measured . 
Assay for mitochondrial respiratory function and histopathological examination of heart tissues were performed . 
<mark>Isoproterenol</mark> - treated rats showed significant increases in the levels of <mark>lactate</mark> dehydrogenase , <mark>aspartate</mark> transaminase , <mark>creatine</mark> kinase and <mark>malondialdehyde</mark> and significant decreases in the activities of <mark>superoxide</mark> dismutase , catalase and <mark>glutathione</mark> peroxidase in serum and heart . 
These rats also showed declines in left ventricular systolic pressure , maximum and minimum rate of developed left ventricular pressure , and elevation of left ventricular end - diastolic pressure and ST - segment . 
In addition , mitochondrial respiratory dysfunction characterized by decreased respiratory control ratio and <mark>ADP</mark> / O was observed in <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - treated rats . 
Administration of <mark>salvianolic acid A</mark> for a period of 8 days significantly attenuated <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced cardiac dysfunction and myocardial injury and improved mitochondrial respiratory function . 
The protective role of <mark>salvianolic acid A</mark> against <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced myocardial damage was further confirmed by histopathological examination . 
The results of our study suggest that <mark>salvianolic acid A</mark> possessing antioxidant activity has a significant protective effect against <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced myocardial infarction . 
Long - term <mark>glutamate</mark> supplementation failed to protect against peripheral neurotoxicity of <mark>paclitaxel</mark> . 
Toxic peripheral neuropathy is still a significant limiting factor for chemotherapy with <mark>paclitaxel</mark> ( <mark>PAC</mark> ) , although <mark>glutamate</mark> and its closely related <mark>amino acid</mark> <mark>glutamine</mark> were claimed to ameliorate <mark>PAC</mark> neurotoxicity . 
This pilot trial aimed to evaluate the role of <mark>glutamate</mark> supplementation for preventing <mark>PAC</mark> - induced peripheral neuropathy in a randomized , placebo - controlled , double - blinded clinical and electro - diagnostic study . 
Forty - three ovarian cancer patients were available for analysis following six cycles of the same <mark>PAC</mark> - containing regimen : 23 had been supplemented by <mark>glutamate</mark> all along the treatment period , at a daily dose of three times 500 mg ( group G ) , and 20 had received a placebo ( group P ) . 
Patients were evaluated by neurological examinations , questionnaires and sensory - motor nerve conduction studies . 
There was no significant difference in the frequency of signs or symptoms between the two groups although neurotoxicity symptoms presented mostly with lower scores of severity in group G . 
However , this difference reached statistical significance only with regard to reported pain sensation ( P = 0 . 011 ) . 
Also the frequency of abnormal electro - diagnostic findings showed similarity between the two groups ( G : 7 / 23 = 30 . 4 % ; P : 6 / 20 = 30 % ) . 
This pilot study leads to the conclusion that <mark>glutamate</mark> supplementation at the chosen regimen fails to protect against peripheral neurotoxicity of <mark>PAC</mark> . 
Development of ocular myasthenia during <mark>pegylated interferon</mark> and <mark>ribavirin</mark> treatment for chronic hepatitis C . 
A 63 - year - old male experienced sudden diplopia after 9 weeks of administration of <mark>pegylated interferon ( IFN ) alpha - 2b</mark> and <mark>ribavirin</mark> for chronic hepatitis C ( CHC ) . 
Ophthalmologic examinations showed ptosis on the right upper lid and restricted right eye movement without any other neurological signs . 
A brain imaging study and repetitive nerve stimulation test indicated no abnormality . 
The <mark>acetylcholine</mark> receptor antibody titer and response to acetylcholinesterase inhibitors were negative , and the results of thyroid function tests were normal . 
The patient ' s ophthalmological symptoms improved rapidly 3 weeks after discontinuation of <mark>pegylated IFN alpha - 2b</mark> and <mark>ribavirin</mark> . 
The ocular myasthenia associated with combination therapy of <mark>pegylated <mark>IFN</mark> alpha - 2b</mark> and <mark>ribavirin</mark> for CHC is very rarely reported ; therefore , we present this case with a review of the various eye complications of IFN therapy . 
Learning and memory deficits in <mark>ecstasy</mark> users and their neural correlates during a face - learning task . 
It has been consistently shown that <mark>ecstasy</mark> users display impairments in learning and memory performance . 
In addition , working memory processing in <mark>ecstasy</mark> users has been shown to be associated with neural alterations in hippocampal and / or cortical regions as measured by functional magnetic resonance imaging ( fMRI ) . 
Using functional imaging and a face - learning task , we investigated neural correlates of encoding and recalling face - name associations in 20 recreational drug users whose predominant drug use was <mark>ecstasy</mark> and 20 controls . 
To address the potential confounding effects of the <mark>cannabis</mark> use of the <mark>ecstasy</mark> using group , a second analysis included 14 previously tested <mark>cannabis</mark> users ( Nestor , L . , Roberts , G . , Garavan , H . , Hester , R . , 2008 . Deficits in learning and memory : parahippocampal hyperactivity and frontocortical hypoactivity in <mark>cannabis</mark> users . Neuroimage 40 , 1328 - 1339 ) . 
<mark>Ecstasy</mark> users performed significantly worse in learning and memory compared to controls and <mark>cannabis</mark> users . 
A conjunction analysis of the encode and recall phases of the task revealed <mark>ecstasy</mark> - specific hyperactivity in bilateral frontal regions , left temporal , right parietal , bilateral temporal , and bilateral occipital brain regions . 
<mark>Ecstasy</mark> - specific hypoactivity was evident in the right dorsal anterior cingulated cortex ( ACC ) and left posterior cingulated cortex . 
In both <mark>ecstasy</mark> and <mark>cannabis</mark> groups brain activation was decreased in the right medial frontal gyrus , left parahippocampal gyrus , left dorsal cingulate gyrus , and left caudate . 
These results elucidated <mark>ecstasy</mark> - related deficits , only some of which might be attributed to <mark>cannabis</mark> use . 
These <mark>ecstasy</mark> - specific effects may be related to the vulnerability of isocortical and allocortical regions to the neurotoxic effects of <mark>ecstasy</mark> . 
<mark>Disulfiram</mark> - like syndrome after <mark>hydrogen cyanamide</mark> professional skin exposure : two case reports in France . 
<mark>Hydrogen cyanamide</mark> is a plant growth regulator used in agriculture to induce bud break in fruit trees . 
Contact with the skin can result in percutaneous absorption of the substance that inhibits <mark>aldehyde</mark> dehydrogenase and can induce <mark>acetaldehyde</mark> syndrome in case of <mark>alcohol</mark> use . 
The purpose of this report is to describe two cases of a <mark>disulfiram</mark> - like syndrome following occupational exposure to <mark>hydrogen cyanamide</mark> . 
The first case involved a 59 - year - old man who used <mark>Dormex</mark> , which contains <mark>hydrogen cyanamide</mark> , without protection after consuming a large amount of <mark>alcohol</mark> during a meal . 
In less than 1 hour after the ingestion of <mark>alcohol</mark> , he developed malaise with flushing of the face , tachycardia , and dyspnea . 
Manifestations regressed spontaneously under surveillance in the hospital . 
The second case occurred in a 55 - year - old farmer following cutaneous contact with <mark>Dormex</mark> . 
Five hours after exposure , he developed <mark>disulfiram</mark> - like syndrome with flushing , tachycardia , and arterial hypotension after consuming three glasses of wine . 
The patient recovered spontaneously in 3 hours under surveillance in the hospital . 
These cases confirm the necessity of avoiding <mark>alcohol</mark> consumption as recommended in the instructions for use of <mark>Dormex</mark> and of preventing cutaneous contact during use . 
<mark>Sulpiride</mark> - induced tardive dystonia . 
<mark>Sulpiride</mark> is a selective D2 - receptor antagonist with antipsychotic and <mark>antidepressant</mark> properties . 
Although initially thought to be free of extrapyramidal side effects , <mark>sulpiride</mark> - induced tardive dyskinesia and parkinsonism have been reported occasionally . 
We studied a 37 - year - old man who developed persistent segmental dystonia within 2 months after starting <mark>sulpiride</mark> therapy . 
We could not find any previous reports of <mark>sulpiride</mark> - induced tardive dystonia . 
Comparative cognitive and subjective side effects of immediate - release <mark>oxycodone</mark> in healthy middle - aged and older adults . 
This study measured the objective and subjective neurocognitive effects of a single 10 - mg dose of immediate - release <mark>oxycodone</mark> in healthy , older ( > 65 years ) , and middle - aged ( 35 to 55 years ) adults who were not suffering from chronic or significant daily pain . 
Seventy - one participants completed 2 separate study days and were blind to medication condition ( placebo , 10 - mg <mark>oxycodone</mark> ) . 
Plasma <mark>oxycodone</mark> concentration peaked between 60 and 90 minutes postdose ( P < . 01 ) and pupil size , an indication of physiological effects of the medication , peaked at approximately 90 to 120 minutes postdose ( P < . 01 ) . 
Significant declines in simple and sustained attention , working memory , and verbal memory were observed at 1 hour postdose compared to baseline for both age groups with a trend toward return to baseline by 5 hours postdose . 
For almost all cognitive measures , there were no medication by age - interaction effects , which indicates that the 2 age groups exhibited similar responses to the medication challenge . 
This study suggests that for healthy older adults who are not suffering from chronic pain , neurocognitive and pharmacodynamic changes in response to a 10 - mg dose of immediate - release <mark>oxycodone</mark> are similar to those observed for middle - aged adults . 
PERSPECTIVE : Study findings indicate that the metabolism , neurocognitive effects , and physical side effects of oral <mark>oxycodone</mark> are similar for healthy middle - aged and older adults . 
Therefore , clinicians should not avoid prescribing oral opioids to older adults based on the belief that older adults are at higher risk for side effects than younger adults . 
The <mark>glycine</mark> transporter - 1 inhibitor <mark>SSR103800</mark> displays a selective and specific antipsychotic - like profile in normal and transgenic mice . 
Schizophrenia has been initially associated with dysfunction in <mark>dopamine</mark> neurotransmission . 
However , the observation that antagonists of the <mark>glutamate</mark> <mark>N - methyl - D - aspartate</mark> ( <mark>NMDA</mark> ) receptor produce schizophrenic - like symptoms in humans has led to the idea of a dysfunctioning of the glutamatergic system via its <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor . 
As a result , there is a growing interest in the development of pharmacological agents with potential antipsychotic properties that enhance the activity of the glutamatergic system via a modulation of the <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor . 
Among them are <mark>glycine</mark> transporter - 1 ( GlyT1 ) inhibitors such as <mark>SSR103800</mark> , which indirectly enhance <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor function by increasing the <mark>glycine</mark> ( a co - agonist for the <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor ) levels in the synapse . 
This study aimed at investigating the potential antipsychotic - like properties of <mark>SSR103800</mark> , with a particular focus on models of hyperactivity , involving either drug challenge ( ie , <mark>amphetamine</mark> and <mark>MK - 801</mark> ) or transgenic mice ( ie , <mark>NMDA</mark> Nr1 ( neo - / - ) and DAT ( - / - ) ) . 
Results showed that <mark>SSR103800</mark> ( 10 - 30 mg / kg p . o . ) blocked hyperactivity induced by the non - competitive <mark>NMDA</mark> receptor antagonist , <mark>MK - 801</mark> and partially reversed spontaneous hyperactivity of <mark>NMDA</mark> Nr1 ( neo - / - ) mice . 
In contrast , <mark>SSR103800</mark> failed to affect hyperactivity induced by <mark>amphetamine</mark> or naturally observed in <mark>dopamine</mark> transporter ( DAT ( - / - ) ) knockout mice ( 10 - 30 mg / kg p . o . ) . 
Importantly , both classical ( <mark>haloperidol</mark> ) and atypical ( <mark>olanzapine</mark> , <mark>clozapine</mark> and <mark>aripiprazole</mark> ) antipsychotics were effective in all these models of hyperactivity . 
However , unlike these latter , <mark>SSR103800</mark> did not produce catalepsy ( retention on the bar test ) up to 30 mg / kg p . o . 
Together these findings show that the GlyT1 inhibitor , <mark>SSR103800</mark> , produces antipsychotic - like effects , which differ from those observed with compounds primarily targeting the dopaminergic system , and has a reduced side - effect potential as compared with these latter drugs . 
<mark>Pyrrolidine dithiocarbamate</mark> protects the piriform cortex in the <mark>pilocarpine</mark> status epilepticus model . 
<mark>Pyrrolidine dithiocarbamate</mark> ( <mark>PDTC</mark> ) has a dual mechanism of action as an antioxidant and an inhibitor of the transcription factor kappa - beta . 
Both , production of reactive <mark>oxygen</mark> species as well as activation of NF - kappaB have been implicated in severe neuronal damage in different sub - regions of the hippocampus as well as in the surrounding cortices . 
The effect of <mark>PDTC</mark> on status epilepticus - associated cell loss in the hippocampus and piriform cortex was evaluated in the rat fractionated <mark>pilocarpine</mark> model . 
Treatment with 150 mg / kg <mark>PDTC</mark> before and following status epilepticus significantly increased the mortality rate to 100 % . 
Administration of 50 mg / kg <mark>PDTC</mark> ( low - dose ) did not exert major effects on the development of a status epilepticus or the mortality rate . 
In vehicle - treated rats , status epilepticus caused pronounced neuronal damage in the piriform cortex comprising both pyramidal cells and interneurons . 
Low - dose <mark>PDTC</mark> treatment almost completely protected from lesions in the piriform cortex . 
A significant decrease in neuronal density of the hippocampal hilar formation was identified in vehicle - and <mark>PDTC</mark> - treated rats following status epilepticus . 
In conclusion , the NF - kappaB inhibitor and antioxidant <mark>PDTC</mark> protected the piriform cortex , whereas it did not affect hilar neuronal loss . 
These data might indicate that the generation of reactive <mark>oxygen</mark> species and activation of NF - kappaB plays a more central role in seizure - associated neuronal damage in the temporal cortex as compared to the hippocampal hilus . 
However , future investigations are necessary to exactly analyze the biochemical mechanisms by which <mark>PDTC</mark> exerted its beneficial effects in the piriform cortex . 
Anaesthetists ' nightmare : masseter spasm after induction in an undiagnosed case of myotonia congenita . 
We report an undiagnosed case of myotonia congenita in a 24 - year - old previously healthy primigravida , who developed life threatening masseter spasm following a standard dose of intravenous <mark>suxamethonium</mark> for induction of anaesthesia . 
Neither the patient nor the anaesthetist was aware of the diagnosis before this potentially lethal complication occurred . 
Twin preterm neonates with cardiac toxicity related to <mark>lopinavir / ritonavir</mark> therapy . 
We report twin neonates who were born prematurely at 32 weeks of gestation to a mother with human immunodeficiency virus infection . 
One of the twins developed complete heart block and dilated cardiomyopathy related to <mark>lopinavir / ritonavir</mark> therapy , a boosted protease - inhibitor agent , while the other twin developed mild bradycardia . 
We recommend caution in the use of <mark>lopinavir / ritonavir</mark> in the immediate neonatal period . 
When drugs disappear from the patient : elimination of intravenous medication by hemodiafiltration . 
Twenty - three hours after heart transplantation , life - threatening acute right heart failure was diagnosed in a patient requiring continuous venovenous hemodiafiltration ( CVVHDF ) . 
Increasing doses of <mark>catecholamines</mark> , sedatives , and muscle relaxants administered through a central venous catheter were ineffective . 
However , a bolus of <mark>epinephrine</mark> injected through an alternative catheter provoked a hypertensive crisis . 
Thus , interference with the central venous infusion by the dialysis catheter was suspected . 
The catheters were changed , and hemodynamics stabilized at lower <mark>catecholamine</mark> doses . 
When the effects of IV drugs are inadequate in patients receiving CVVHDF , interference with adjacent catheters resulting in elimination of the drug by CVVHDF should be suspected . 
Less frequent <mark>lithium</mark> administration and lower urine volume . 
OBJECTIVE : This study was designed to determine whether patients maintained on a regimen of <mark>lithium</mark> on a once - per - day schedule have lower urine volumes than do patients receiving multiple doses per day . 
METHOD : This was a cross - sectional study of 85 patients from a <mark>lithium</mark> clinic who received different dose schedules . 
Patients were admitted to the hospital for measurement of <mark>lithium</mark> level , <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance , urine volume , and maximum osmolality . 
RESULTS : Multiple daily doses of <mark>lithium</mark> were associated with higher urine volumes . 
The dosing schedule , duration of <mark>lithium</mark> treatment , and daily dose of <mark>lithium</mark> did not affect maximum osmolality or <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance . 
CONCLUSIONS : Urine volume can be reduced by giving <mark>lithium</mark> once daily and / or by lowering the total daily dose . 
<mark>Lithium</mark> - induced polyuria seems to be related to extrarenal as well as to renal effects . 
Antibacterial medication use during pregnancy and risk of birth defects : National Birth Defects Prevention Study . 
OBJECTIVE : To estimate the association between antibacterial medications and selected birth defects . 
DESIGN , SETTING , AND PARTICIPANTS : Population - based , multisite , case - control study of women who had pregnancies affected by 1 of more than 30 eligible major birth defects identified via birth defect surveillance programs in 10 states ( n = 13 155 ) and control women randomly selected from the same geographical regions ( n = 4941 ) . 
MAIN EXPOSURE : Reported maternal use of antibacterials ( 1 month before pregnancy through the end of the first trimester ) . 
MAIN OUTCOME MEASURE : Odds ratios ( ORs ) measuring the association between antibacterial use and selected birth defects adjusted for potential confounders . 
RESULTS : The reported use of antibacterials increased during pregnancy , peaking during the third month . 
<mark>Sulfonamides</mark> were associated with anencephaly ( adjusted OR [ AOR ] = 3 . 4 ; 95 % confidence interval [ CI ] , 1 . 3 - 8 . 8 ) , hypoplastic left heart syndrome ( AOR = 3 . 2 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 3 - 7 . 6 ) , coarctation of the aorta ( AOR = 2 . 7 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 3 - 5 . 6 ) , choanal atresia ( AOR = 8 . 0 ; 95 % CI , 2 . 7 - 23 . 5 ) , transverse limb deficiency ( AOR = 2 . 5 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 0 - 5 . 9 ) , and diaphragmatic hernia ( AOR = 2 . 4 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 1 - 5 . 4 ) . 
<mark>Nitrofurantoins</mark> were associated with anophthalmia or microphthalmos ( AOR = 3 . 7 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 1 - 12 . 2 ) , hypoplastic left heart syndrome ( AOR = 4 . 2 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 9 - 9 . 1 ) , atrial septal defects ( AOR = 1 . 9 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 1 - 3 . 4 ) , and cleft lip with cleft palate ( AOR = 2 . 1 ; 95 % CI , 1 . 2 - 3 . 9 ) . 
Other antibacterial agents that showed associations included <mark>erythromycins</mark> ( 2 defects ) , <mark>penicillins</mark> ( 1 defect ) , <mark>cephalosporins</mark> ( 1 defect ) , and <mark>quinolones</mark> ( 1 defect ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : Reassuringly , <mark>penicillins</mark> , <mark>erythromycins</mark> , and <mark>cephalosporins</mark> , although used commonly by pregnant women , were not associated with many birth defects . 
<mark>Sulfonamides</mark> and <mark>nitrofurantoins</mark> were associated with several birth defects , indicating a need for additional scrutiny . 
Differential impact of immune escape mutations G145R and P120T on the replication of <mark>lamivudine</mark> - resistant <mark>hepatitis B virus e antigen</mark> - positive and - negative strains . 
Immune escape variants of the hepatitis B virus ( HBV ) represent an emerging clinical challenge , because they can be associated with vaccine escape , HBV reactivation , and failure of diagnostic tests . 
Recent data suggest a preferential selection of immune escape mutants in distinct peripheral blood leukocyte compartments of infected individuals . 
We therefore systematically analyzed the functional impact of the most prevalent immune escape variants , the sG145R and sP120T mutants , on the viral replication efficacy and antiviral drug susceptibility of common treatment - associated mutants with resistance to <mark>lamivudine</mark> ( <mark>LAM</mark> ) and / or <mark>HBeAg</mark> negativity . 
Replication - competent HBV strains with sG145R or sP120T and <mark>LAM</mark> resistance ( rtM204I or rtL180M / rtM204V ) were generated on an <mark>HBeAg</mark> - positive and an <mark>HBeAg</mark> - negative background with precore ( PC ) and basal core promoter ( BCP ) mutants . 
The sG145R mutation strongly reduced <mark>HBsAg</mark> levels and was able to fully restore the impaired replication of <mark>LAM</mark> - resistant HBV mutants to the levels of wild - type HBV , and PC or BCP mutations further enhanced viral replication . 
Although the sP120T substitution also impaired <mark>HBsAg</mark> secretion , it did not enhance the replication of <mark>LAM</mark> - resistant clones . 
However , the concomitant occurrence of <mark>HBeAg</mark> negativity ( PC / BCP ) , sP120T , and <mark>LAM</mark> resistance resulted in the restoration of replication to levels of wild - type HBV . 
In all clones with combined immune escape and <mark>LAM</mark> resistance mutations , the <mark>nucleotide</mark> analogues <mark>adefovir</mark> and <mark>tenofovir</mark> remained effective in suppressing viral replication in vitro . 
These findings reveal the differential impact of immune escape variants on the replication and drug susceptibility of complex HBV mutants , supporting the need of close surveillance and treatment adjustment in response to the selection of distinct mutational patterns . 
Hemolytic anemia associated with the use of <mark>omeprazole</mark> . 
<mark>Omeprazole</mark> is the first drug designed to block the final step in the acid secretory process within the parietal cell . 
It has been shown to be extremely effective in the treatment of peptic ulcer disease , reflux esophagitis , and the Zollinger - Ellison syndrome . 
Although clinical experience with <mark>omeprazole</mark> is still limited , many controlled studies have established the short - term safety of this drug . 
We report the first case of a serious short - term adverse reaction with the use of <mark>omeprazole</mark> : hemolytic anemia . 
The patient developed weakness , lethargy , and shortness of breath 2 days after starting therapy with <mark>omeprazole</mark> . 
Two weeks after the initiation of therapy , her hematocrit had decreased from 44 . 1 % to 20 . 4 % , and she had a positive direct Coombs antiglobulin test and an elevated indirect <mark>bilirubin</mark> . 
After she discontinued the <mark>omeprazole</mark> , her hemoglobin and hematocrit gradually returned to normal . 
The mechanism by which <mark>omeprazole</mark> caused the patient ' s hemolytic anemia is uncertain , but physicians should be alerted to this possible adverse effect . 
<mark>Phenylephrine</mark> but not <mark>ephedrine</mark> reduces frontal lobe oxygenation following anesthesia - induced hypotension . 
BACKGROUND : Vasopressor agents are used to correct anesthesia - induced hypotension . 
We describe the effect of <mark>phenylephrine</mark> and <mark>ephedrine</mark> on frontal lobe oxygenation ( S ( c ) O ( 2 ) ) following anesthesia - induced hypotension . 
METHODS : Following induction of anesthesia by <mark>fentanyl</mark> ( 0 . 15 mg kg ( - 1 ) ) and <mark>propofol</mark> ( 2 . 0 mg kg ( - 1 ) ) , 13 patients received <mark>phenylephrine</mark> ( 0 . 1 mg iv ) and 12 patients received <mark>ephedrine</mark> ( 10 mg iv ) to restore mean arterial pressure ( MAP ) . 
Heart rate ( HR ) , MAP , stroke volume ( SV ) , cardiac output ( CO ) , and frontal lobe oxygenation ( S ( c ) O ( 2 ) ) were registered . 
RESULTS : Induction of anesthesia was followed by a decrease in MAP , HR , SV , and CO concomitant with an elevation in S ( c ) O ( 2 ) . 
After administration of <mark>phenylephrine</mark> , MAP increased ( 51 + / - 12 to 81 + / - 13 mmHg ; P < 0 . 001 ; mean + / - SD ) . 
However , a 14 % ( from 70 + / - 8 % to 60 + / - 7 % ) reduction in S ( c ) O ( 2 ) ( P < 0 . 05 ) followed with no change in CO ( 3 . 7 + / - 1 . 1 to 3 . 4 + / - 0 . 9 l min ( - 1 ) ) . 
The administration of <mark>ephedrine</mark> led to a similar increase in MAP ( 53 + / - 9 to 79 + / - 8 mmHg ; P < 0 . 001 ) , restored CO ( 3 . 2 + / - 1 . 2 to 5 . 0 + / - 1 . 3 l min ( - 1 ) ) , and preserved S ( c ) O ( 2 ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : The utilization of <mark>phenylephrine</mark> to correct hypotension induced by anesthesia has a negative impact on S ( c ) O ( 2 ) while <mark>ephedrine</mark> maintains frontal lobe oxygenation potentially related to an increase in CO . 
Prolonged elevation of plasma <mark>argatroban</mark> in a cardiac transplant patient with a suspected history of <mark>heparin</mark> - induced thrombocytopenia with thrombosis . 
BACKGROUND : Direct thrombin inhibitors ( DTIs ) provide an alternative method of anticoagulation for patients with a history of <mark>heparin</mark> - induced thrombocytopenia ( HIT ) or HIT with thrombosis ( HITT ) undergoing cardiopulmonary bypass ( CPB ) . 
In the following report , a 65 - year - old critically ill patient with a suspected history of HITT was administered <mark>argatroban</mark> for anticoagulation on bypass during heart transplantation . 
The patient required massive transfusion support ( 55 units of red blood cells , 42 units of fresh - frozen plasma , 40 units of cryoprecipitate , 40 units of platelets , and three doses of recombinant Factor VIIa ) for severe intraoperative and postoperative bleeding . 
STUDY DESIGN AND METHODS : Plasma samples from before and after CPB were analyzed postoperatively for <mark>argatroban</mark> concentration using a modified ecarin clotting time ( ECT ) assay . 
RESULTS : Unexpectedly high concentrations of <mark>argatroban</mark> were measured in these samples ( range , 0 - 32 microg / mL ) , and a prolonged plasma <mark>argatroban</mark> half life ( t ( 1 / 2 ) ) of 514 minutes was observed ( published elimination t ( 1 / 2 ) is 39 - 51 minutes [ < or = 181 minutes with hepatic impairment ] ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : Correlation of plasma <mark>argatroban</mark> concentration versus the patient ' s coagulation variables and clinical course suggest that prolonged elevated levels of plasma <mark>argatroban</mark> may have contributed to the patient ' s extended coagulopathy . 
Because DTIs do not have reversal agents , surgical teams and transfusion services should remain aware of the possibility of massive transfusion events during anticoagulation with these agents . 
This is the first report to measure plasma <mark>argatroban</mark> concentration in the context of CPB and extended coagulopathy . 
The effects of the adjunctive <mark>bupropion</mark> on male sexual dysfunction induced by a <mark>selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor</mark> : a double - blind placebo - controlled and randomized study . 
OBJECTIVE : To determine the safety and efficacy of adjunctive <mark>bupropion</mark> sustained - release ( SR ) on male sexual dysfunction ( SD ) induced by a <mark>selective serotonin reuptake inhibitor</mark> ( <mark>SSRI</mark> ) , as SD is a common side - effect of <mark>SSRIs</mark> and the most effective treatments have yet to be determined . 
PATIENTS AND METHODS : The randomized sample consisted of 234 euthymic men who were receiving some type of <mark>SSRI</mark> . 
The men were randomly assigned to <mark>bupropion</mark> SR ( 150 mg twice daily , 117 ) or placebo ( twice daily , 117 ) for 12 weeks . 
Efficacy was evaluated using the Clinical Global Impression - Sexual Function ( CGI - SF ; the primary outcome measure ) , the International Index of Erectile Function ( IIEF ) , Arizona Sexual Experience Scale ( ASEX ) , and Erectile Dysfunction Inventory of Treatment Satisfaction ( EDITS ) ( secondary outcome measures ) . 
Participants were followed biweekly during study period . 
RESULTS : After 12 weeks of treatment , the mean ( sd ) scores for CGI - SF were significantly lower , i . e . better , in patients on <mark>bupropion</mark> SR , at 2 . 4 ( 1 . 2 ) , than in the placebo group , at 3 . 9 ( 1 . 1 ) ( P = 0 . 01 ) . 
Men who received <mark>bupropion</mark> had a significant increase in the total IIEF score ( 54 . 4 % vs 1 . 2 % ; P = 0 . 003 ) , and in the five different domains of the IIEF . 
Total ASEX scores were significantly lower , i . e . better , among men who received <mark>bupropion</mark> than placebo , at 15 . 5 ( 4 . 3 ) vs 21 . 5 ( 4 . 7 ) ( P = 0 . 002 ) . 
The EDITS scores were 67 . 4 ( 10 . 2 ) for the <mark>bupropion</mark> and 36 . 3 ( 11 . 7 ) for the placebo group ( P = 0 . 001 ) . 
The ASEX score and CGI - SF score were correlated ( P = 0 . 003 ) . 
In linear regression analyses the CGI - SF score was not affected significantly by the duration of SD , type of <mark>SSRI</mark> used and age . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Bupropion</mark> is an effective treatment for male SD induced by <mark>SSRIs</mark> . 
These results provide empirical support for conducting a further study of <mark>bupropion</mark> . 
Prevention of seizures and reorganization of hippocampal functions by transplantation of bone marrow cells in the acute phase of experimental epilepsy . 
In this study , we investigated the therapeutic potential of bone marrow mononuclear cells ( BMCs ) in a model of epilepsy induced by <mark>pilocarpine</mark> in rats . 
BMCs obtained from green fluorescent protein ( GFP ) transgenic mice or rats were transplanted intravenously after induction of status epilepticus ( SE ) . 
Spontaneous recurrent seizures ( SRS ) were monitored using Racine ' s seizure severity scale . 
All of the rats in the saline - treated epileptic control group developed SRS , whereas none of the BMC - treated epileptic animals had seizures in the short term ( 15 days after transplantation ) , regardless of the BMC source . 
Over the long - term chronic phase ( 120 days after transplantation ) , only 25 % of BMC - treated epileptic animals had seizures , but with a lower frequency and duration compared to the epileptic control group . 
The density of hippocampal neurons in the brains of animals treated with BMCs was markedly preserved . 
At hippocampal Schaeffer collateral - CA1 synapses , long - term potentiation was preserved in BMC - transplanted rats compared to epileptic controls . 
The donor - derived GFP ( + ) cells were rarely found in the brains of transplanted epileptic rats . 
In conclusion , treatment with BMCs can prevent the development of chronic seizures , reduce neuronal loss , and influence the reorganization of the hippocampal neuronal network . 
Normalizing effects of <mark>modafinil</mark> on sleep in chronic <mark>cocaine</mark> users . 
OBJECTIVE : The purpose of the present study was to determine the effect of morning - dosed <mark>modafinil</mark> on sleep and daytime sleepiness in chronic <mark>cocaine</mark> users . 
METHOD : Twenty <mark>cocaine</mark> - dependent participants were randomly assigned to receive <mark>modafinil</mark> , 400 mg ( N = 10 ) , or placebo ( N = 10 ) every morning at 7 : 30 a . m . for 16 days in an inpatient , double - blind randomized trial . 
Participants underwent polysomnographic sleep recordings on days 1 to 3 , 7 to 9 , and 14 to 16 ( first , second , and third weeks of abstinence ) . 
The Multiple Sleep Latency Test was performed at 11 : 30 a . m . , 2 : 00 p . m . , and 4 : 30 p . m . on days 2 , 8 , and 15 . 
For comparison of sleep architecture variables , 12 healthy comparison participants underwent a single night of experimental polysomnography that followed 1 night of accommodation polysomnography . 
RESULTS : Progressive abstinence from <mark>cocaine</mark> was associated with worsening of all measured polysomnographic sleep outcomes . 
Compared with placebo , <mark>modafinil</mark> decreased nighttime sleep latency and increased slow - wave sleep time in <mark>cocaine</mark> - dependent participants . 
The effect of <mark>modafinil</mark> interacted with the abstinence week and was associated with longer total sleep time and shorter REM sleep latency in the third week of abstinence . 
Comparison of slow - wave sleep time , total sleep time , and sleep latency in <mark>cocaine</mark> - dependent and healthy participants revealed a normalizing effect of <mark>modafinil</mark> in <mark>cocaine</mark> - dependent participants . 
<mark>Modafinil</mark> was associated with increased daytime sleep latency , as measured by the Multiple Sleep Latency Test , and a nearly significant decrease in subjective daytime sleepiness . 
CONCLUSIONS : Morning - dosed <mark>modafinil</mark> promotes nocturnal sleep , normalizes sleep architecture , and decreases daytime sleepiness in abstinent <mark>cocaine</mark> users . 
These effects may be relevant in the treatment of <mark>cocaine</mark> dependence . 
Safety of transesophageal echocardiography in adults : study in a multidisciplinary hospital . 
BACKGROUND : TEE is a semi - invasive tool broadly used and its utilization associated to sedatives drugs might to affect the procedure safety . 
OBJECTIVE : to analyze aspects of TEE safety associated to the use of <mark>Midazolan</mark> ( <mark>MZ</mark> ) and <mark>Flumazenil</mark> ( <mark>FL</mark> ) and the influence of the clinical variables on the event rate . 
METHOD : prospective study with 137 patients that underwent TEE with <mark>MZ</mark> associated to moderate sedation . 
We analyzed the following events : complications related with the topical anesthesia , with <mark>MZ</mark> use and with the procedure . 
Uni - and multivariate analyses were used to test the influence of the clinical variables : age , sex , stroke , myocardiopathy ( MP ) , duration of the test , mitral regurgitation ( MR ) and the <mark>MZ</mark> dose . 
RESULTS : All patients ( 65 + / - 16 yrs ; 58 % males ) finished the examination . 
The mean doses of <mark>MZ</mark> and <mark>FL</mark> were 4 . 3 + / - 1 . 9 mg and 0 . 28 + / - 0 . 2 mg , respectively . 
The duration of the examination and the mean ejection fraction ( EF ) were 16 . 4 + / - 6 . 1 minutes and 60 + / - 9 % , respectively . 
Mild hypoxia ( SO2 < 90 % ) was the most common event ( 11 patients ) ; 3 patients ( 2 % ) presented transient hypoxia due to upper airway obstruction by probe introduction and 8 ( 5 . 8 % ) due to hypoxia caused by <mark>MZ</mark> use . 
Transient hypotension ( SAP < 90mmHg ) occurred in 1 patient ( 0 . 7 % ) . 
The multivariate analysis showed that severe MR , MP ( EF < 45 % ) and high doses of <mark>MZ</mark> ( > 5mg ) were associated with events ( p < 0 . 001 ) . 
The EF was 40 % , in the group with MP and 44 % in the group with severe MR and it can be a factor associated with clinical events in the last group . 
CONCLUSION : TEE with sedation presents a low rate of events . 
There were no severe events and there was no need to interrupt the examinations . 
Effect of direct intracoronary administration of <mark>methylergonovine</mark> in patients with and without variant angina . 
The effects of intracoronary administration of <mark>methylergonovine</mark> were studied in 21 patients with variant angina and 22 patients with atypical chest pain and in others without angina pectoris ( control group ) . 
<mark>Methylergonovine</mark> was administered continuously at a rate of 10 micrograms / min up to 50 micrograms . 
In all patients with variant angina , coronary spasm was provoked at a mean dose of 28 + / - 13 micrograms ( mean + / - SD ) . 
In the control group neither ischemic ST change nor localized spasm occurred . 
The basal tone of the right coronary artery was significantly lower than that of the left coronary artery . 
The percentage of vasoconstriction of the right coronary artery was significantly higher than that of the left coronary artery . 
These results suggest that spasm provocation tests , which use an intracoronary injection of a relatively low dose of <mark>methylergonovine</mark> , have a high sensitivity in variant angina and the vasoreactivity of the right coronary artery may be greater than that of the other coronary arteries . 
Oral manifestations of " meth mouth " : a case report . 
AIM : The aim of the documentation of this clinical case is to make clinicians aware of " meth mouth " and the medical risks associated with this serious condition . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Methamphetamine</mark> is a very addictive , powerful stimulant that increases wakefulness and physical activity and can produce other effects such as cardiac dysrhythmias , hypertension , hallucinations , and violent behavior . 
Dental patients abusing <mark>methamphetamine</mark> can present with poor oral hygiene , xerostomia , rampant caries ( " meth mouth " ) , and excessive tooth wear . 
Oral rehabilitation of patients using <mark>methamphetamine</mark> can be challenging . 
CASE DESCRIPTION : A 30 - year - old Caucasian woman presented with dental pain , bad breath , and self - reported poor esthetics . 
A comprehensive examination including her medical history , panoramic radiograph , and intraoral examination revealed 19 carious lesions , which is not very common for a healthy adult . 
She reported her use of <mark>methamphetamine</mark> for five years and had not experienced any major carious episodes before she started using the drug . 
SUMMARY : The patient ' s medical and dental histories along with radiographic and clinical findings lead to a diagnosis of " meth mouth . " Although three different dental treatment modalities ( either conventional or implant - supported ) have been offered to the patient since August 2007 , the patient has yet to initiate any treatment . 
CLINICAL SIGNIFICANCE : This clinical case showing oral manifestations of meth mouth was presented to help dental practitioners recognize and manage patients who may be abusing <mark>methamphetamines</mark> . 
Dental practitioners also may be skeptical about the reliability of appointment keeping by these patients , as they frequently miss their appointments without reasonable justification . 
<mark>Antituberculosis</mark> therapy - induced acute liver failure : magnitude , profile , prognosis , and predictors of outcome . 
<mark>Antituberculosis</mark> therapy ( ATT ) - associated acute liver failure ( ATT - ALF ) is the commonest drug - induced ALF in South Asia . 
Prospective studies on ATT - ALF are lacking . 
The current study prospectively evaluated the magnitude , clinical course , outcome , and prognostic factors in ATT - ALF . 
From January 1986 to January 2009 , 1223 consecutive ALF patients were evaluated : ATT alone was the cause in 70 ( 5 . 7 % ) patients . 
Another 15 ( 1 . 2 % ) had ATT and simultaneous hepatitis virus infection . 
In 44 ( 62 . 8 % ) patients , ATT was prescribed empirically without definitive evidence of tuberculosis . 
ATT - ALF patients were younger ( 32 . 87 [ + / - 15 . 8 ] years ) , and 49 ( 70 % ) of them were women . 
Most had hyperacute presentation ; the median icterus encephalopathy interval was 4 . 5 ( 0 - 30 ) days . 
The median duration of ATT before ALF was 30 ( 7 - 350 ) days . 
At presentation , advanced encephalopathy and cerebral edema were present in 51 ( 76 % ) and 29 ( 41 . 4 % ) patients , respectively . 
Gastrointestinal bleed , seizures , infection , and acute renal failure were documented in seven ( 10 % ) , five ( 7 . 1 % ) , 26 ( 37 . 1 % ) , and seven ( 10 % ) patients , respectively . 
Compared with hepatitis E virus ( HEV ) and non - A non - E - induced ALF , ATT - ALF patients had nearly similar presentations except for older age and less elevation of liver enzymes . 
The mortality rate among patients with ATT - ALF was high ( 67 . 1 % , n = 47 ) , and only 23 ( 32 . 9 % ) patients recovered with medical treatment . 
In multivariate analysis , three factors independently predicted mortality : serum <mark>bilirubin</mark> ( > or = 10 . 8 mg / dL ) , prothrombin time ( PT ) prolongation ( > or = 26 seconds ) , and grade III / IV encephalopathy at presentation . 
CONCLUSION : ATT - ALF constituted 5 . 7 % of ALF at our center and had a high mortality rate . 
Because the mortality rate is so high , determining which factors are predictors is less important . 
A high proportion of patients had consumed ATT empirically , which could have been prevented . 
Design and analysis of the HYPREN - trial : safety of <mark>enalapril</mark> and <mark>prazosin</mark> in the initial treatment phase of patients with congestive heart failure . 
Since the introduction of <mark>angiotensin converting enzyme ( ACE ) inhibitors</mark> into the adjunctive treatment of patients with congestive heart failure , cases of severe hypotension , especially on the first day of treatment , have occasionally been reported . 
To assess the safety of the <mark>ACE inhibitor</mark> <mark>enalapril</mark> a multicenter , randomized , <mark>prazosin</mark> - controlled trial was designed that compared the incidence and severity of symptomatic hypotension on the first day of treatment . 
Trial medication was 2 . 5 mg <mark>enalapril</mark> or 0 . 5 <mark>prazosin</mark> . 
Subjects were 1210 inpatients with New York Heart Association ( NYHA ) functional class II and III . 
Patients who received <mark>enalapril</mark> experienced clinically and statistically significantly less symptomatic hypotension ( 5 . 2 % ) than the patients who received <mark>prazosin</mark> ( 12 . 9 % ) . 
All patients recovered . 
It was concluded that treatment with <mark>enalapril</mark> was well tolerated and it is , therefore , unreasonable to restrict the initiation of treatment with <mark>enalapril</mark> to inpatients . 
Central nervous system complications during treatment of acute lymphoblastic leukemia in a single pediatric institution . 
Central nervous system ( CNS ) complications during treatment of childhood acute lymphoblastic leukemia ( ALL ) remain a challenging clinical problem . 
Outcome improvement with more intensive chemotherapy has significantly increased the incidence and severity of adverse events . 
This study analyzed the incidence of neurological complications during ALL treatment in a single pediatric institution , focusing on clinical , radiological , and electrophysiological findings . 
Exclusion criteria included CNS leukemic infiltration at diagnosis , therapy - related peripheral neuropathy , late - onset encephalopathy , or long - term neurocognitive defects . 
During a 9 - year period , we retrospectively collected 27 neurological events ( 11 % ) in as many patients , from 253 children enrolled in the ALL front - line protocol . 
CNS complications included posterior reversible leukoencephalopathy syndrome ( n = 10 ) , stroke ( n = 5 ) , temporal lobe epilepsy ( n = 2 ) , high - dose <mark>methotrexate</mark> toxicity ( n = 2 ) , syndrome of inappropriate antidiuretic hormone secretion ( n = 1 ) , and other unclassified events ( n = 7 ) . 
In conclusion , CNS complications are frequent events during ALL therapy , and require rapid detection and prompt treatment to limit permanent damage . 
<mark>Cocaine</mark> causes memory and learning impairments in rats : involvement of nuclear factor kappa B and oxidative stress , and prevention by <mark>topiramate</mark> . 
Different mechanisms have been suggested for <mark>cocaine</mark> toxicity including an increase in oxidative stress but the association between oxidative status in the brain and <mark>cocaine</mark> induced - behaviour is poorly understood . 
Nuclear factor kappa B ( NFkappaB ) is a sensor of oxidative stress and participates in memory formation that could be involved in drug toxicity and addiction mechanisms . 
Therefore NFkappaB activity , oxidative stress , neuronal <mark>nitric oxide</mark> synthase ( nNOS ) activity , spatial learning and memory as well as the effect of <mark>topiramate</mark> , a previously proposed therapy for <mark>cocaine</mark> addiction , were evaluated in an experimental model of cocaine administration in rats . 
NFkappaB activity was decreased in the frontal cortex of <mark>cocaine</mark> treated rats , as well as <mark>GSH</mark> concentration and <mark>glutathione</mark> peroxidase activity in the hippocampus , whereas nNOS activity in the hippocampus was increased . 
Memory retrieval of experiences acquired prior to <mark>cocaine</mark> administration was impaired and negatively correlated with NFkappaB activity in the frontal cortex . 
In contrast , learning of new tasks was enhanced and correlated with the increase of nNOS activity and the decrease of <mark>glutathione</mark> peroxidase . 
These results provide evidence for a possible mechanistic role of oxidative and nitrosative stress and NFkappaB in the alterations induced by <mark>cocaine</mark> . 
<mark>Topiramate</mark> prevented all the alterations observed , showing novel neuroprotective properties . 
Efficacy and safety of <mark>asenapine</mark> in a placebo - and <mark>haloperidol</mark> - controlled trial in patients with acute exacerbation of schizophrenia . 
<mark>Asenapine</mark> is approved by the Food and Drugs Administration in adults for acute treatment of schizophrenia or of manic or mixed episodes associated with bipolar I disorder with or without psychotic features . 
In a double - blind 6 - week trial , 458 patients with acute schizophrenia were randomly assigned to fixed - dose treatment with <mark>asenapine</mark> at 5 mg twice daily ( BID ) , <mark>asenapine</mark> at 10 mg BID , placebo , or <mark>haloperidol</mark> at 4 mg BID ( to verify assay sensitivity ) . 
With last observations carried forward ( LOCF ) , mean Positive and Negative Syndrome Scale total score reductions from baseline to endpoint were significantly greater with <mark>asenapine</mark> at 5 mg BID ( - 16 . 2 ) and <mark>haloperidol</mark> ( - 15 . 4 ) than placebo ( - 10 . 7 ; both P < 0 . 05 ) ; using mixed model for repeated measures ( MMRM ) , changes at day 42 were significantly greater with <mark>asenapine</mark> at 5 and 10 mg BID ( - 21 . 3 and - 19 . 4 , respectively ) and <mark>haloperidol</mark> ( - 20 . 0 ) than placebo ( - 14 . 6 ; all P < 0 . 05 ) . 
On the Positive and Negative Syndrome Scale positive subscale , all treatments were superior to placebo with LOCF and MMRM ; <mark>asenapine</mark> at 5 mg BID was superior to placebo on the negative subscale with MMRM and on the general psychopathology subscale with LOCF and MMRM . 
Treatment - related adverse events ( AEs ) occurred in 44 % and 52 % , 57 % , and 41 % of the <mark>asenapine</mark> at 5 and 10 mg BID , <mark>haloperidol</mark> , and placebo groups , respectively . 
Extrapyramidal symptoms reported as AEs occurred in 15 % and 18 % , 34 % , and 10 % of the <mark>asenapine</mark> at 5 and 10 mg BID , <mark>haloperidol</mark> , and placebo groups , respectively . 
Across all groups , no more than 5 % of patients had clinically significant weight change . 
Post hoc analyses indicated that efficacy was similar with <mark>asenapine</mark> and <mark>haloperidol</mark> ; greater contrasts were seen in AEs , especially extrapyramidal symptoms . 
Salvage therapy with <mark>nelarabine</mark> , <mark>etoposide</mark> , and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> in relapsed / refractory paediatric T - cell lymphoblastic leukaemia and lymphoma . 
A combination of 5 d of <mark>nelarabine</mark> ( <mark>AraG</mark> ) with 5 d of <mark>etoposide</mark> ( <mark>VP</mark> ) and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> ( <mark>CPM</mark> ) and prophylactic intrathecal chemotherapy was used as salvage therapy in seven children with refractory or relapsed T - cell leukaemia or lymphoma . 
The most common side effects attributable to the <mark>AraG</mark> included Grade 2 and 3 sensory and motor neuropathy and musculoskeletal pain . 
Haematological toxicity was greater for the combination than <mark>AraG</mark> alone , although median time to neutrophil and platelet recovery was consistent with other salvage therapies . 
All patients had some response to the combined therapy and five of the seven went into complete remission after one or two courses of <mark>AraG</mark> / <mark>VP</mark> / <mark>CPM</mark> . 
Our experience supports the safety of giving <mark>AraG</mark> as salvage therapy in synchrony with <mark>etoposide</mark> and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> , although neurological toxicity must be closely monitored . 
Effect of <mark>adriamycin</mark> combined with whole body hyperthermia on tumor and normal tissues . 
Thermal enhancement of <mark>Adriamycin</mark> - mediated antitumor activity and normal tissue toxicities by whole body hyperthermia were compared using a F344 rat model . 
Antitumor activity was studied using a tumor growth delay assay . 
Acute normal tissue toxicities ( i . e . , leukopenia and thrombocytopenia ) and late normal tissue toxicities ( i . e . , myocardial and kidney injury ) were evaluated by functional / physiological assays and by morphological techniques . 
Whole body hyperthermia ( 120 min at 41 . 5 degrees C ) enhanced both <mark>Adriamycin</mark> - mediated antitumor activity and toxic side effects . 
The thermal enhancement ratio calculated for antitumor activity was 1 . 6 . 
Thermal enhancement ratios estimated for " acute " hematological changes were 1 . 3 , whereas those estimated for " late " damage ( based on morphological cardiac and renal lesions ) varied between 2 . 4 and 4 . 3 . 
Thus , while whole body hyperthermia enhances <mark>Adriamycin</mark> - mediated antitumor effect , normal tissue toxicity is also increased , and the potential therapeutic gain of the combined modality treatment is eroded . 
Permeability , ultrastructural changes , and distribution of novel proteins in the glomerular barrier in early <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> nephrosis . 
BACKGROUND / AIMS : It is still unclear what happens in the glomerulus when proteinuria starts . 
Using <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> nephrosis ( PAN ) rats , we studied early ultrastructural and permeability changes in relation to the expression of the podocyte - associated molecules nephrin , a - actinin , dendrin , and plekhh2 , the last two of which were only recently discovered in podocytes . 
METHODS : Using immune stainings , semiquantitative measurement was performed under the electron microscope . 
Permeability was assessed using isolated kidney perfusion with tracers . 
Possible effects of ACE inhibition were tested . 
RESULTS : By day 2 , some patchy foot process effacement , but no proteinuria , appeared . 
The amount of nephrin was reduced in both diseased and normal areas . 
The other proteins showed few changes , which were limited to diseased areas . 
By day 4 , foot process effacement was complete and proteinuria appeared in parallel with signs of size barrier damage . 
Nephrin decreased further , while dendrin and plekhh2 also decreased but a - actinin remained unchanged . 
ACE inhibition had no significant protective effect . 
CONCLUSIONS : PAN glomeruli already showed significant pathology by day 4 , despite relatively mild proteinuria . 
This was preceded by altered nephrin expression , supporting its pivotal role in podocyte morphology . 
The novel proteins dendrin and plekhh2 were both reduced , suggesting roles in PAN , whereas a - actinin was unchanged . 
A novel , multiple symptom model of obsessive - compulsive - like behaviors in animals . 
BACKGROUND : Current animal models of obsessive - compulsive disorder ( OCD ) typically involve acute , drug - induced symptom provocation or a genetic association with stereotypies or anxiety . 
None of these current models demonstrate multiple OCD - like behaviors . 
METHODS : Neonatal rats were treated with the tricyclic <mark>antidepressant</mark> <mark>clomipramine</mark> or vehicle between days 9 and 16 twice daily and behaviorally tested in adulthood . 
RESULTS : <mark>Clomipramine</mark> exposure in immature rats produced significant behavioral and biochemical changes that include enhanced anxiety ( elevated plus maze and marble burying ) , behavioral inflexibility ( perseveration in the spontaneous alternation task and impaired reversal learning ) , working memory impairment ( e . g . , win - shift paradigm ) , hoarding , and corticostriatal dysfunction . 
<mark>Dopamine</mark> D2 receptors were elevated in the striatum , whereas <mark>serotonin</mark> 2C , but not <mark>serotonin</mark> 1A , receptors were elevated in the orbital frontal cortex . 
CONCLUSIONS : This is the first demonstration of multiple symptoms consistent with an OCD - like profile in animals . 
Moreover , these behaviors are accompanied by biochemical changes in brain regions previously identified as relevant to OCD . 
This novel model of OCD demonstrates that drug exposure during a sensitive period can program disease - like systems permanently , which could have implications for current and future therapeutic strategies for this and other psychiatric disorders . 
Elevation of ADAM10 , ADAM17 , MMP - 2 and MMP - 9 expression with media degeneration features <mark>CaCl2</mark> - induced thoracic aortic aneurysm in a rat model . 
PURPOSE : This study was designed to establish a rat model of thoracic aortic aneurysm ( TAA ) by <mark>calcium chloride</mark> ( <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> ) - induced arterial injury and to explore the potential role of a disintegrin and metalloproteinase ( ADAM ) , matrix metalloproteinases ( MMPs ) and their endogenous inhibitors ( TIMPs ) in TAA formation . 
METHODS : Thoracic aorta of male Sprague - Dawley rats was exposed to 0 . 5M <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> or normal saline ( <mark>NaCl</mark> ) . 
After 12weeks , animals were euthanized , and <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - treated , <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - untreated ( n = 12 ) and <mark>NaCl</mark> - treated aortic segments ( n = 12 ) were collected for histological and molecular assessments . 
MMP - TIMP and ADAM mRNAs were semi - quantitatively analyzed and protein expressions were determined by immunohistochemistry . 
RESULTS : Despite similar external diameters among <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - treated , non - <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - treated and <mark>NaCl</mark> - treated segments , aneurymal alteration ( n = 6 , 50 % ) , media degeneration with regional disruption , fragmentation of elastic fiber , and increased collagen deposition ( n = 12 , 100 % ) were demonstrated in <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - treated segments . 
MMP - 2 , MMP - 9 , ADAM - 10 and ADAM - 17 mRNA levels were increased in <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - treated segments ( all p < 0 . 01 ) , with trends of elevation in <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - untreated segments , as compared with <mark>NaCl</mark> - treated segments . 
Immunohistochemistry displayed significantly increased expressions of MMP - 2 , MMP - 9 , ADAM - 10 and ADAM - 17 ( all p < 0 . 01 ) in intima and media for <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> - treated segments . 
TIMP mRNA and tissue levels did not differ obviously among the three aortic segments . 
CONCLUSION : This study establishes a TAA model by periarterial <mark>CaCl ( 2 )</mark> exposure in rats , and demonstrates a significant elevation of expression of MMP - 2 , MMP - 9 , ADAM10 and ADAM17 in the pathogenesis of vascular remodeling .

<mark>Suxamethonium</mark> causes prolonged apnea in patients in whom pseudocholinesterase enzyme gets deactivated by <mark>organophosphorus ( OP ) poisons</mark> . 
Here , we present a similar incident in a severely depressed patient who received electroconvulsive therapy ( ECT ) .
