<mark>Curcumin</mark> ameliorates cognitive dysfunction and oxidative damage in <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> administered rats . 
The antiepileptic drugs , <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> are well known to cause cognitive impairment on chronic use . 
The increase in free radical generation has been implicated as one of the important mechanisms of cognitive impairment by antiepileptic drugs . 
<mark>Curcumin</mark> has shown antioxidant , anti - inflammatory and neuro - protective properties . 
Therefore , the present study was carried out to investigate the effect of chronic <mark>curcumin</mark> administration on <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> - and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> - induced cognitive impairment and oxidative stress in rats . 
Pharmacokinetic interactions of <mark>curcumin</mark> with <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> were also studied . 
Vehicle / drugs were administered daily for 21days to male Wistar rats . 
Passive avoidance paradigm and elevated plus maze test were used to assess cognitive function . 
At the end of study period , serum <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> , whole brain <mark>malondialdehyde</mark> and reduced <mark>glutathione</mark> levels were estimated . 
The administration of <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> for 21days caused a significant impairment of learning and memory as well as an increased oxidative stress . 
Concomitant <mark>curcumin</mark> administration prevented the cognitive impairment and decreased the increased oxidative stress induced by these antiepileptic drugs . 
<mark>Curcumin</mark> co - administration did not cause any significant alteration in the serum concentrations of both <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> as well as <mark>carbamazepine</mark> . 
These results show that <mark>curcumin</mark> has beneficial effect in mitigating the deterioration of cognitive functions and oxidative damage in rats treated with <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> without significantly altering their serum concentrations . 
The findings suggest that <mark>curcumin</mark> can be considered as a potential safe and effective adjuvant to <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> and <mark>carbamazepine</mark> therapy in preventing cognitive impairment associated with these drugs . 
Can angiogenesis be a target of treatment for <mark>ribavirin</mark> associated hemolytic anemia ? 
BACKGROUND / AIMS : Recently <mark>ribavirin</mark> has been found to inhibit angiogenesis and a number of angiogenesis inhibitors such as <mark>sunitinib</mark> and <mark>sorafenib</mark> have been found to cause acute hemolysis . 
We aimed to investigate whether there is a relation between hemoglobin , haptoglobin and angiogenesis soluble markers which are modifiable and can help in developing strategies against anemia . 
METHODS : Fourteen patients chronically infected with hepatitis C virus were treated by <mark>pegylated interferon alpha 2a</mark> and <mark>ribavirin</mark> . 
Serum hemoglobin , haptoglobin and angiogenesis markers of vascular endothelial growth factor and angiopoetin - 2 were investigated before and after therapy . 
RESULTS : We observed a significant decrease in haptoglobin levels at the end of the treatment period . 
Hemoglobin levels also decreased but insignificantly by treatment . 
In contrast with the literature , serum levels of angiogenesis factors did not change significantly by <mark>pegylated interferon</mark> and <mark>ribavirin</mark> therapy . 
We found no correlation of angiogenesis soluble markers with either hemoglobin or haptoglobin . 
CONCLUSION : This is the first study in the literature investigating a link between angiogenesis soluble markers and <mark>ribavirin</mark> induced anemia in patients with hepatitis C and we could not find any relation . 
Future research with larger number of patients is needed to find out modifiable factors that will improve the safety of <mark>ribavirin</mark> therapy . 
Reduction in injection pain using buffered <mark>lidocaine</mark> as a local anesthetic before cardiac catheterization . 
Previous reports have suggested that pain associated with the injection of <mark>lidocaine</mark> is related to the acidic pH of the solution . 
To determine if the addition of a buffering solution to adjust the pH of <mark>lidocaine</mark> into the physiologic range would reduce pain during injection , we performed a blinded randomized study in patients undergoing cardiac catheterization . 
Twenty patients were asked to quantify the severity of pain after receiving standard <mark>lidocaine</mark> in one femoral area and buffered <mark>lidocaine</mark> in the opposite femoral area . 
The mean pain score for buffered <mark>lidocaine</mark> was significantly lower than the mean score for standard <mark>lidocaine</mark> ( 2 . 7 + / - 1 . 9 vs . 3 . 8 + / - 2 . 2 , P = 0 . 03 ) . 
The pH adjustment of standard <mark>lidocaine</mark> can be accomplished easily in the catheterization laboratory before injection and results in a reduction of the pain occurring during the infiltration of tissues . 
Effect of <mark>L - alpha - glyceryl - phosphorylcholine</mark> on amnesia caused by <mark>scopolamine</mark> . 
The present study was carried out to test the effects of <mark>L - alpha - glycerylphosphorylcholine</mark> ( <mark>L - alpha - GFC</mark> ) on memory impairment induced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> in man . 
Thirty - two healthy young volunteers were randomly allocated to four different groups . 
They were given a ten day pretreatment with either <mark>L - alpha - GFC</mark> or placebo , p . o . , and on the eleventh day either <mark>scopolamine</mark> or placebo , i . m . 
Before and 0 . 5 , 1 , 2 , 3 , and 6 h after injection the subjects were given attention and mnemonic tests . 
The findings of this study indicate that the drug is able to antagonize impairment of attention and memory induced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> . 
Safety of <mark>capecitabine</mark> : a review . 
IMPORTANCE OF THE FIELD : <mark>Fluoropyrimidines</mark> , in particular <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> ( <mark>5 - FU</mark> ) , have been the mainstay of treatment for several solid tumors , including colorectal , breast and head and neck cancers , for > 40 years . 
AREAS COVERED IN THIS REVIEW : This article reviews the pharmacology and efficacy of <mark>capecitabine</mark> with a special emphasis on its safety . 
WHAT THE READER WILL GAIN : The reader will gain better insight into the safety of <mark>capecitabine</mark> in special populations such as patients with advanced age , renal and kidney disease . 
We also explore different dosing and schedules of <mark>capecitabine</mark> administration . 
TAKE HOME MESSAGE : <mark>Capecitabine</mark> is an oral prodrug of <mark>5 - FU</mark> and was developed to fulfill the need for a more convenient therapy and provide an improved safety / efficacy profile . 
It has shown promising results alone or in combination with other chemotherapeutic agents in colorectal , breast , pancreaticobiliary , gastric , renal cell and head and neck cancers . 
The most commonly reported toxic effects of <mark>capecitabine</mark> are diarrhea , nausea , vomiting , stomatitis and hand - foot syndrome . 
<mark>Capecitabine</mark> has a well - established safety profile and can be given safely to patients with advanced age , hepatic and renal dysfunctions . 
<mark>Levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesias in patients with Parkinson ' s disease : filling the bench - to - bedside gap . 
<mark>Levodopa</mark> is the most effective drug for the treatment of Parkinson ' s disease . 
However , the long - term use of this <mark>dopamine</mark> precursor is complicated by highly disabling fluctuations and dyskinesias . 
Although preclinical and clinical findings suggest pulsatile stimulation of striatal postsynaptic receptors as a key mechanism underlying <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesias , their pathogenesis is still unclear . 
In recent years , evidence from animal models of Parkinson ' s disease has provided important information to understand the effect of specific receptor and post - receptor molecular mechanisms underlying the development of dyskinetic movements . 
Recent preclinical and clinical data from promising lines of research focus on the differential role of presynaptic versus postsynaptic mechanisms , <mark>dopamine</mark> receptor subtypes , ionotropic and metabotropic <mark>glutamate</mark> receptors , and non - dopaminergic neurotransmitter systems in the pathophysiology of <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesias . 
Effects of pallidal <mark>neurotensin</mark> on <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced parkinsonian catalepsy : behavioral and electrophysiological studies . 
OBJECTIVE : The globus pallidus plays a critical role in movement regulation . 
Previous studies have indicated that the globus pallidus receives neurotensinergic innervation from the striatum , and systemic administration of a <mark>neurotensin</mark> analog could produce antiparkinsonian effects . 
The present study aimed to investigate the effects of pallidal <mark>neurotensin</mark> on <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced parkinsonian symptoms . 
METHODS : Behavioral experiments and electrophysiological recordings were performed in the present study . 
RESULTS : Bilateral infusions of <mark>neurotensin</mark> into the globus pallidus reversed <mark>haloperidol</mark> - induced parkinsonian catalepsy in rats . 
Electrophysiological recordings showed that microinjection of <mark>neurotensin</mark> induced excitation of pallidal neurons in the presence of systemic <mark>haloperidol</mark> administration . 
The <mark><mark>neurotensin</mark> type - 1 receptor antagonist</mark> <mark>SR48692</mark> blocked both the behavioral and the electrophysiological effects induced by neurotensin . 
CONCLUSION : Activation of pallidal <mark>neurotensin</mark> receptors may be involved in <mark>neurotensin</mark> - induced antiparkinsonian effects . 
<mark>Carmofur</mark> - induced organic mental disorders . 
Organic mental disorder was observed in a 29 - year - old female in the prognostic period after the onset of <mark>carmofur</mark> - induced leukoencephalopathy . 
Symptoms such as euphoria , emotional lability and puerile attitude noted in the patient were diagnosed as organic personality syndrome according to the criteria defined in the DSM - III - R . 
It is referred to as a frontal lobe syndrome . 
Brain CT revealed a periventricular low density area in the frontal white matter and moderate dilatation of the lateral ventricles especially at the bilateral anterior horns . 
Consequently , <mark>carmofur</mark> - induced leukoencephalopathy may uncommonly result in organic personality syndrome in the residual state . 
It may be attributed to the structural damage to the frontal lobe . 
Butyrylcholinesterase gene mutations in patients with prolonged apnea after <mark>succinylcholine</mark> for electroconvulsive therapy . 
BACKGROUND : patients undergoing electroconvulsive therapy ( ECT ) often receive <mark>succinylcholine</mark> as part of the anesthetic procedure . 
The duration of action may be prolonged in patients with genetic variants of the butyrylcholinesterase enzyme ( BChE ) , the most common being the K - and the A - variants . 
The aim of the study was to assess the clinical significance of genetic variants in butyrylcholinesterase gene ( BCHE ) in patients with a suspected prolonged duration of action of <mark>succinylcholine</mark> after ECT . 
METHODS : a total of 13 patients were referred to the Danish Cholinesterase Research Unit after ECT during 38 months . 
We determined the BChE activity and the BCHE genotype using molecular genetic methods , the duration of apnea , time to sufficient spontaneous ventilation and whether neuromuscular monitoring was used . 
The duration of apnea was compared with published data on normal subjects . 
RESULTS : in 11 patients , mutations were found in the BCHE gene , the K - variant being the most frequent . 
The duration of apnea was 5 - 15 min compared with 3 - 5 . 3 min from the literature . 
Severe distress was noted in the recovery phase in two patients . 
Neuromuscular monitoring was used in two patients . 
CONCLUSION : eleven of 13 patients with a prolonged duration of action of <mark>succinylcholine</mark> had mutations in BCHE , indicating that this is the possible reason for a prolonged period of apnea . 
We recommend objective neuromuscular monitoring during the first ECT . 
<mark>Perhexiline maleate</mark> and peripheral neuropathy . 
Peripheral neuropathy has been noted as a complication of therapy with <mark>perhexiline maleate</mark> , a drug widely used in France ( and in clinical trials in the United States ) for the prophylactic treatment of angina pectoris . 
In 24 patients with this complication , the marked slowing of motor nerve conduction velocity and the electromyographic changes imply mainly a demyelinating disorder . 
Improvement was noted with cessation of therapy . 
In a few cases the presence of active denervation signified a poor prognosis , with only slight improvement . 
The underlying mechanism causing the neuropathy is not yet fully known , although some evidence indicates that it may be a lipid storage process . 
A phase I study of <mark>4 ' - 0 - tetrahydropyranyladriamycin</mark> . 
Clinical pharmacology and pharmacokinetics . 
A Phase I study of intravenous ( IV ) bolus <mark>4 ' - 0 - tetrahydropyranyladriamycin</mark> ( <mark>Pirarubicin</mark> ) was done in 55 patients in good performance status with refractory tumors . 
Twenty - six had minimal prior therapy ( good risk ) , 23 had extensive prior therapy ( poor risk ) , and six had renal and / or hepatic dysfunction . 
A total of 167 courses at doses of 15 to 70 mg / m2 were evaluable . 
Maximum tolerated dose in good - risk patients was 70 mg / m2 , and in poor - risk patients , 60 mg / m2 . 
The dose - limiting toxic effect was transient noncumulative granulocytopenia . 
Granulocyte nadir was on day 14 ( range , 4 - 22 ) . 
Less frequent toxic effects included thrombocytopenia , anemia , nausea , mild alopecia , phlebitis , and mucositis . 
Myelosuppression was more in patients with hepatic dysfunction . 
Pharmacokinetic analyses in 21 patients revealed <mark>Pirarubicin</mark> plasma T 1 / 2 alpha ( + / - SE ) of 2 . 5 + / - 0 . 85 minutes , T beta 1 / 2 of 25 . 6 + / - 6 . 5 minutes , and T 1 / 2 gamma of 23 . 6 + / - 7 . 6 hours . 
The area under the curve was 537 + / - 149 ng / ml x hours , volume of distribution ( Vd ) 3504 + / - 644 l / m2 , and total clearance ( ClT ) was 204 + 39 . 3 l / hour / m2 . 
<mark>Adriamycinol</mark> , <mark>doxorubicin</mark> , <mark>adriamycinone</mark> , and <mark>tetrahydropyranyladriamycinol</mark> were the metabolites detected in plasma and the amount of <mark>doxorubicin</mark> was less than or equal to 10 % of the total metabolites . 
Urinary excretion of <mark>Pirarubicin</mark> in the first 24 hours was less than or equal to 10 % . 
Activity was noted in mesothelioma , leiomyosarcoma , and basal cell carcinoma . 
The recommended starting dose for Phase II trials is 60 mg / m2 IV bolus every 3 weeks . 
Ocular and auditory toxicity in hemodialyzed patients receiving <mark>desferrioxamine</mark> . 
During an 18 - month period of study 41 hemodialyzed patients receiving <mark>desferrioxamine</mark> ( 10 - 40 mg / kg BW / 3 times weekly ) for the first time were monitored for detection of audiovisual toxicity . 
6 patients presented clinical symptoms of visual or auditory toxicity . 
Moreover , detailed ophthalmologic and audiologic studies disclosed abnormalities in 7 more asymptomatic patients . 
Visual toxicity was of retinal origin and was characterized by a tritan - type dyschromatopsy , sometimes associated with a loss of visual acuity and pigmentary retinal deposits . 
Auditory toxicity was characterized by a mid - to high - frequency neurosensorial hearing loss and the lesion was of the cochlear type . 
<mark>Desferrioxamine</mark> withdrawal resulted in a complete recovery of visual function in 1 patient and partial recovery in 3 , and a complete reversal of hearing loss in 3 patients and partial recovery in 3 . 
This toxicity appeared in patients receiving the higher doses of <mark>desferrioxamine</mark> or coincided with the normalization of ferritin or <mark>aluminium</mark> serum levels . 
The data indicate that audiovisual toxicity is not an infrequent complication in hemodialyzed patients receiving <mark>desferrioxamine</mark> . 
Periodical audiovisual monitoring should be performed on hemodialyzed patients receiving the drug in order to detect adverse effects as early as possible . 
Serial epilepsy caused by <mark>levodopa / carbidopa</mark> administration in two patients on hemodialysis . 
Two patients with similar clinical features are presented : both patients had chronic renal failure , on hemodialysis for many years but recently begun on a high - flux dialyzer ; both had been receiving a <mark>carbidopa / levodopa</mark> preparation ; and both had the onset of hallucinosis and recurrent seizures , which were refractory to anticonvulsants . 
The first patient died without a diagnosis ; the second patient had a dramatic recovery following the administration of <mark>vitamin B6</mark> . 
Neither patient was considered to have a renal state sufficiently severe enough to explain their presentation . 
Randomized , double - blind trial of <mark>mazindol</mark> in Duchenne dystrophy . 
There is evidence that growth hormone may be related to the progression of weakness in Duchenne dystrophy . 
We conducted a 12 - month controlled trial of <mark>mazindol</mark> , a putative growth hormone secretion inhibitor , in 83 boys with Duchenne dystrophy . 
Muscle strength , contractures , functional ability and pulmonary function were tested at baseline , and 6 and 12 months after treatment with <mark>mazindol</mark> ( 3 mg / d ) or placebo . 
The study was designed to have a power of greater than 0 . 90 to detect a slowing to 25 % of the expected rate of progression of weakness at P less than 0 . 05 . 
<mark>Mazindol</mark> did not benefit strength at any point in the study . 
Side effects attributable to <mark>mazindol</mark> included decreased appetite ( 36 % ) , dry mouth ( 10 % ) , behavioral change ( 22 % ) , and gastrointestinal symptoms ( 18 % ) ; <mark>mazindol</mark> dosage was reduced in 43 % of patients . 
The effect of <mark>mazindol</mark> on GH secretion was estimated indirectly by comparing the postabsorptive IGF - I levels obtained following 3 , 6 , 9 , and 12 months in the <mark>mazindol</mark> treated to those in the placebo groups . 
Although <mark>mazindol</mark> - treated patients gained less weight and height than placebo - treated patients , no significant effect on IGF - I levels was observed . 
<mark>Mazindol</mark> doses not slow the progression of weakness in Duchenne dystrophy . 
Facilitation of memory retrieval by pre - test <mark>morphine</mark> and its state dependency in the step - through type passive avoidance learning test in mice . 
Amnesia produced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> and <mark>cycloheximide</mark> were reversed by <mark>morphine</mark> given 30 min before the test trial ( pre - test ) , and pre - test <mark>morphine</mark> also facilitated the memory retrieval in the animals administered <mark>naloxone</mark> during the training trial . 
Similarly , pre - test <mark>scopolamine</mark> partially reversed the <mark>scopolamine</mark> - induced amnesia , but not significantly ; and pre - test <mark>cycloheximide</mark> failed to reverse the <mark>cycloheximide</mark> - induced amnesia . 
These results suggest that the facilitation of memory retrieval by pre - test <mark>morphine</mark> might be the direct action of <mark>morphine</mark> rather than a state dependent effect . 
<mark>Naloxone</mark> reverses the antihypertensive effect of <mark>clonidine</mark> . 
In unanesthetized , spontaneously hypertensive rats the decrease in blood pressure and heart rate produced by intravenous <mark>clonidine</mark> , 5 to 20 micrograms / kg , was inhibited or reversed by <mark>nalozone</mark> , 0 . 2 to 2 mg / kg . 
The hypotensive effect of 100 mg / kg <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> was also partially reversed by <mark>naloxone</mark> . 
<mark>Naloxone</mark> alone did not affect either blood pressure or heart rate . 
In brain membranes from spontaneously hypertensive rats <mark>clonidine</mark> , 10 ( - 8 ) to 10 ( - 5 ) M , did not influence stereoselective binding of <mark>[ 3H ] - naloxone</mark> ( 8 nM ) , and <mark>naloxone</mark> , 10 ( - 8 ) to 10 ( - 4 ) M , did not influence <mark>clonidine</mark> - suppressible binding of <mark>[ 3H ] - dihydroergocryptine</mark> ( 1 nM ) . 
These findings indicate that in spontaneously hypertensive rats the effects of central alpha - adrenoceptor stimulation involve activation of opiate receptors . 
As <mark>naloxone</mark> and <mark>clonidine</mark> do not appear to interact with the same receptor site , the observed functional antagonism suggests the release of an endogenous opiate by <mark>clonidine</mark> or <mark>alpha - methyldopa</mark> and the possible role of the opiate in the central control of sympathetic tone . 
Neurotoxicity of <mark>halogenated hydroxyquinolines</mark> : clinical analysis of cases reported outside Japan . 
An analysis is presented of 220 cases of possible neurotoxic reactions to <mark>halogenated hydroxyquinolines</mark> reported from outside Japan . 
In 80 cases insufficient information was available for adequate comment and in 29 a relationship to the administration of <mark>clioquinol</mark> could be excluded . 
Of the remainder , a relationship to <mark>clioquinol</mark> was considered probable in 42 and possible in 69 cases . 
In six of the probable cases the neurological disturbance consisted of an acute reversible encephalopathy usually related to the ingestion of a high dose of <mark>clioquinol</mark> over a short period . 
The most common manifestation , observed in 15 further cases , was isolated optic atrophy . 
This was most frequently found in children , many of whom had received <mark>clioquinol</mark> as treatment for acrodermatitis enteropathica . 
In the remaining cases , a combination of myelopathy , visual disturbance , and peripheral neuropathy was the most common manifestation . 
Isolated myelopathy or peripheral neuropathy , or these manifestations occurring together , were infrequent . 
The onset of all manifestations ( except toxic encephalopathy ) was usually subacute , with subsequent partial recovery . 
Older subjects tended to display more side effects . 
The full syndrome of subacute myelo - optic neuropathy was more frequent in women , but they tended to have taken greater quantities of the drug . 
<mark>Prazosin</mark> - induced stress incontinence . 
A case of genuine stress incontinence due to <mark>prazosin</mark> , a common antihypertensive drug , is presented . 
<mark>Prazosin</mark> exerts its antihypertensive effects through vasodilatation caused by selective blockade of postsynaptic alpha - 1 adrenergic receptors . 
As an alpha - blocker , it also exerts a significant relaxant effect on the bladder neck and urethra . 
The patient ' s clinical course is described and correlated with initial urodynamic studies while on <mark>prazosin</mark> and subsequent studies while taking <mark>verapamil</mark> . 
Her incontinence resolved with the change of medication . 
The restoration of continence was accompanied by a substantial rise in maximum urethral pressure , maximum urethral closure pressure , and functional urethral length . 
Patients who present with stress incontinence while taking <mark>prazosin</mark> should change their antihypertensive medication before considering surgery , because their incontinence may resolve spontaneously with a change in drug therapy . 
Myocardial infarction following sublingual administration of <mark>isosorbide dinitrate</mark> . 
A 78 - year - old with healed septal necrosis suffered a recurrent myocardial infarction of the anterior wall following the administration of <mark>isosorbide dinitrate</mark> 5 mg sublingually . 
After detailing the course of events , we discuss the role of paradoxical coronary spasm and hypotension - mediated myocardial ischemia occurring downstream to significant coronary arterial stenosis in the pathophysiology of acute coronary insufficiency . 
Comparison of the respiratory effects of i . v . infusions of <mark>morphine</mark> and regional analgesia by extradural block . 
The incidence of postoperative respiratory apnoea was compared between five patients receiving a continuous i . v . infusion of <mark>morphine</mark> ( mean 73 . 6 mg ) and five patients receiving a continuous extradural infusion of 0 . 25 % <mark>bupivacaine</mark> ( mean 192 mg ) in the 24 - h period following upper abdominal surgery . 
Monitoring consisted of airflow detection by a <mark>carbon dioxide</mark> analyser , chest wall movement detected by pneumatic capsules , and continuous electrocardiograph recorded with a Holter ambulatory monitor . 
Both obstructive ( P less than 0 . 05 ) and central apnoea ( P less than 0 . 05 ) occurred more frequently in patients who had a <mark>morphine</mark> infusion . 
There was also a higher incidence of tachyarrhythmias ( P less than 0 . 05 ) and ventricular ectopic beats ( P less than 0 . 05 ) in the <mark>morphine</mark> infusion group . 
Effects of <mark>aminophylline</mark> on the threshold for initiating ventricular fibrillation during respiratory failure . 
Cardiac arrhythmias have frequently been reported in association with respiratory failure . 
The possible additive role of pharmacologic agents in precipitating cardiac disturbances in patients with respiratory failure has only recently been emphasized . 
The effects of <mark>aminophylline</mark> on the ventricular fibrillation threshold during normal acid - base conditions and during respiratory failure were studied in anesthetized open chest dogs . 
The ventricular fibrillation threshold was measured by passing a gated train of 12 constant current pulses through the ventricular myocardium during the vulnerable period of the cardiac cycle . 
During the infusion of <mark>aminophylline</mark> , the ventricular fibrillation threshold was reduced by 30 to 40 percent of the control when pH and partial pressures of <mark>oxygen</mark> ( <mark>PO2</mark> ) and <mark>carbon dioxide</mark> ( <mark>CO2</mark> ) were kept within normal limits . 
When respiratory failure was produced by hypoventilation ( pH 7 . 05 to 7 . 25 ; PC02 70 to 100 mm Hg : P02 20 to 40 mm Hg ) , infusion of <mark>aminophylline</mark> resulted in an even greater decrease in ventricular fibrillation threshold to 60 percent of the control level . 
These experiments suggest that although many factors may contribute to the increased incidence of ventricular arrhythmias in respiratory failure , pharmacologic agents , particularly <mark>aminophylline</mark> , may play a significant role . 
<mark>Pentoxifylline</mark> ( <mark>Trental</mark> ) does not inhibit <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - induced coronary hyperemia : implications for <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - <mark>thallium</mark> - 201 myocardial imaging . 
<mark>Dipyridamole</mark> - <mark>thallium</mark> - 201 imaging is often performed in patients unable to exercise because of peripheral vascular disease . 
Many of these patients are taking <mark>pentoxifylline</mark> ( <mark>Trental</mark> ) , a <mark>methylxanthine</mark> derivative which may improve intermittent claudication . 
Whether <mark>pentoxifylline</mark> inhibits <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - induced coronary hyperemia like other <mark>methylxanthines</mark> such as <mark>theophylline</mark> and should be stopped prior to <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - <mark>thallium</mark> - 201 imaging is unknown . 
Therefore , we studied the hyperemic response to <mark>dipyridamole</mark> in seven open - chest anesthetized dogs after pretreatment with either <mark>pentoxifylline</mark> ( 0 , 7 . 5 , or 15 mg / kg i . v . ) or <mark>theophylline</mark> ( 3 mg / kg i . v . ) . 
Baseline circumflex coronary blood flows did not differ significantly among treatment groups . 
<mark>Dipyridamole</mark> significantly increased coronary blood flow before and after 7 . 5 or 15 mm / kg i . v . <mark>pentoxifylline</mark> ( p less than 0 . 002 ) . 
Neither dose of <mark>pentoxifylline</mark> significantly decreased the <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - induced hyperemia , while peak coronary blood flow was significantly lower after <mark>theophylline</mark> ( p less than 0 . 01 ) . 
We conclude that <mark>pentoxyifylline</mark> does not inhibit <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - induced coronary hyperemia even at high doses . 
Cause of death among patients with Parkinson ' s disease : a rare mortality due to cerebral haemorrhage . 
Causes of death , with special reference to cerebral haemorrhage , among 240 patients with pathologically verified Parkinson ' s disease were investigated using the Annuals of the Pathological Autopsy Cases in Japan from 1981 to 1985 . 
The leading causes of death were pneumonia and bronchitis ( 44 . 1 % ) , malignant neoplasms ( 11 . 6 % ) , heart diseases ( 4 . 1 % ) , cerebral infarction ( 3 . 7 % ) and septicaemia ( 3 . 3 % ) . 
Cerebral haemorrhage was the 11th most frequent cause of death , accounting for only 0 . 8 % of deaths among the patients , whereas it was the 5th most common cause of death among the Japanese general population in 1985 . 
The low incidence of cerebral haemorrhage as a cause of death in patients with Parkinson ' s disease may reflect the hypotensive effect of <mark>levodopa</mark> and a hypotensive mechanism due to reduced <mark>noradrenaline</mark> levels in the parkinsonian brain . 
Possible intramuscular <mark>midazolam</mark> - associated cardiorespiratory arrest and death . 
<mark>Midazolam hydrochloride</mark> is commonly used for dental or endoscopic procedures . 
Although generally consisted safe when given intramuscularly , intravenous administration is known to cause respiratory and cardiovascular depression . 
This report describes the first published case of cardiorespiratory arrest and death associated with intramuscular administration of <mark>midazolam</mark> . 
Information regarding <mark>midazolam</mark> use is reviewed to provide recommendation for safe administration . 
Myasthenia gravis presenting as weakness after <mark>magnesium</mark> administration . 
We studied a patient with no prior history of neuromuscular disease who became virtually quadriplegic after parenteral <mark>magnesium</mark> administration for preeclampsia . 
The serum <mark>magnesium</mark> concentration was 3 . 0 mEq / L , which is usually well tolerated . 
The <mark>magnesium</mark> was stopped and she recovered over a few days . 
While she was weak , 2 - Hz repetitive stimulation revealed a decrement without significant facilitation at rapid rates or after exercise , suggesting postsynaptic neuromuscular blockade . 
After her strength returned , repetitive stimulation was normal , but single fiber EMG revealed increased jitter and blocking . 
Her <mark>acetylcholine</mark> receptor antibody level was markedly elevated . 
Although paralysis after <mark>magnesium</mark> administration has been described in patients with known myasthenia gravis , it has not previously been reported to be the initial or only manifestation of the disease . 
Patients who are unusually sensitive to the neuromuscular effects of <mark>magnesium</mark> should be suspected of having an underlying disorder of neuromuscular transmission . 
No enhancement by <mark>phenobarbital</mark> of the hepatocarcinogenicity of a <mark>choline</mark> - devoid diet in the rat . 
An experiment was performed to test whether inclusion of <mark>phenobarbital</mark> in a <mark>choline</mark> - devoid diet would increase the hepatocarcinogenicity of the diet . 
Groups of 5 - week old male Fischer - 344 rats were fed for 7 - 25 months semipurified <mark>choline</mark> - devoid or <mark>choline</mark> - supplemented diets , containing or not 0 . 06 % <mark>phenobarbital</mark> . 
No hepatic preneoplastic nodules or hepatocellular carcinomas developed in rats fed the plain <mark>choline</mark> - supplemented diet , while one preneoplastic nodule and one hepatocellular carcinoma developed in two rats fed the same diet containing <mark>phenobarbital</mark> . 
The incidence of preneoplastic nodules and of hepatocellular carcinomas was 10 % and 37 % , respectively , in rats fed the plain <mark>choline</mark> - devoid diet , and 17 % and 30 % , in rats fed the <mark>phenobarbital</mark> - containing <mark>choline</mark> - devoid diet . 
The results evinced no enhancement of the hepatocarcinogenicity of the <mark>choline</mark> - devoid diet by <mark>phenobarbital</mark> . 
Sporadic neoplastic lesions were observed in organs other than the liver of some of the animals , irrespective of the diet fed . 
On two paradoxical side - effects of <mark>prednisolone</mark> in rats , ribosomal RNA biosyntheses , and a mechanism of action . 
Liver enlargement and muscle wastage occurred in Wistar rats following the subcutaneous administration of <mark>prednisolone</mark> . 
In the liver both the content of RNA and the biosynthesis of ribosomal RNA increased while both the RNA content and ribosomal RNA biosynthesis were reduced in the gastrocnemius muscle . 
It is suggested that the drug acted in a selective and tissue - specific manner to enhance ribosomal RNA synthesis in the liver and depress such synthesis in the muscle . 
This view supports the contention that the liver and muscle are independent sites of <mark>prednisolone</mark> action . 
Differential effects of <mark>gamma - hexachlorocyclohexane</mark> ( <mark>lindane</mark> ) on pharmacologically - induced seizures . 
<mark>Gamma - hexachlorocyclohexane</mark> ( <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> ) , the active ingredient of the insecticide <mark>lindane</mark> , has been shown to decrease seizure threshold to pentylenetrazol ( <mark>PTZ</mark> ) 3 h after exposure to <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> and conversely increase threshold to <mark>PTZ</mark> - induced seizures 24 h after exposure to <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> ( Vohland et al . 1981 ) . 
In this study , the severity of response to other seizure - inducing agents was tested in mice 1 and 24 h after intraperitoneal administration of 80 mg / kg <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> . 
One hour after the administration of <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> , the activity of seizure - inducing agents was increased , regardless of their mechanism , while 24 h after <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> a differential response was observed . 
Seizure activity due to <mark>PTZ</mark> and <mark>picrotoxin</mark> ( <mark>PTX</mark> ) was significantly decreased ; however , seizure activity due to <mark>3 - mercaptopropionic acid</mark> ( <mark>MPA</mark> ) , <mark>bicuculline</mark> ( <mark>BCC</mark> ) , <mark>methyl 6 , 7 - dimethoxy - 4 - ethyl - B - carboline - 3 - carboxylate</mark> ( <mark>DMCM</mark> ) , or <mark>strychnine</mark> ( <mark>STR</mark> ) was not different from control . 
In vitro , <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> , <mark>pentylenetetrazol</mark> and <mark>picrotoxin</mark> were shown to inhibit <mark>3H - TBOB</mark> binding in mouse whole brain , with IC50 values of 4 . 6 , 404 and 9 . 4 microM , respectively . 
<mark>MPA</mark> , <mark>BCC</mark> , <mark>DMCM</mark> , and <mark>STR</mark> showed no inhibition of <mark>3H - TBOB</mark> ( <mark>t - butyl bicyclo - orthobenzoate</mark> ) binding at concentrations of 100 micron . 
The pharmacological challenge data suggest that tolerance may occur to seizure activity induced by <mark>PTZ</mark> and <mark>PTX</mark> 24 h after <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> , since the response to only these two seizure - inducing agents is decreased . 
The in vitro data suggest that the site responsible for the decrease in seizure activity 24 h after <mark>gamma - HCH</mark> may be the <mark>GABA</mark> - A receptor - linked chloride channel . 
Tolerance and antiviral effect of <mark>ribavirin</mark> in patients with Argentine hemorrhagic fever . 
Tolerance and antiviral effect of <mark>ribavirin</mark> was studied in 6 patients with Argentine hemorrhagic fever ( AHF ) of more than 8 days of evolution . 
Administration of <mark>ribavirin</mark> resulted in a neutralization of viremia and a drop of endogenous interferon titers . 
The average time of death was delayed . 
A reversible anemia was the only adverse effect observed . 
From these results , we conclude that <mark>ribavirin</mark> has an antiviral effect in advanced cases of AHF , and that anemia , the only secondary reaction observed , can be easily managed . 
The possible beneficial effect of <mark>ribavirin</mark> during the initial days of AHF is discussed . 
Is the treatment of scabies hazardous ? 
Treatment for scabies is usually initiated by general practitioners ; most consider <mark>lindane</mark> ( <mark>gamma benzene hexachloride</mark> ) the treatment of choice . 
<mark>Lindane</mark> is also widely used as an agricultural and industrial pesticide , and as a result the toxic profile of this insecticide is well understood . 
Evidence is accumulating that <mark>lindane</mark> can be toxic to the central nervous system and may be associated with aplastic anaemia . 
Preparations containing <mark>lindane</mark> continue to be sold over the counter and may represent a hazard to poorly informed patients . 
This literature review suggests that general practitioners should prescribe scabicides with increased caution for certain at - risk groups , and give adequate warnings regarding potential toxicity . 
Mouse strain - dependent effect of <mark>amantadine</mark> on motility and brain biogenic <mark>amines</mark> . 
The effect of <mark>amantadine hydrochloride</mark> , injected i . p . in 6 increments of 100 mg / kg each over 30 hr , on mouse motility and whole brain content of selected biogenic <mark>amines</mark> and major metabolites was studied in 4 strains of mice . 
These were the albino Sprague - Dawley ICR and BALB / C , the black C57BL / 6 and the brown CDF - I mouse strains . 
<mark>Amantadine</mark> treatment produced a biphasic effect on mouse motility . 
The initial dose of <mark>amantadine</mark> depressed locomotor activity in all mouse strains studied with the BALB / C mice being the most sensitive . 
Subsequent <mark>amantadine</mark> treatments produced enhancement of motility from corresponding control in all mouse strains with the BALB / C mice being the least sensitive . 
The locomotor activity was decreased from corresponding controls in all strains studied , except for the ICR mice , during an overnight drug - free period following the fourth <mark>amantadine</mark> treatment . 
Readministration of <mark>amantadine</mark> , after a drug - free overnight period , increased motility from respective saline control in all strains with exception of the BALB / C mice where suppression of motility occurred . 
Treatment with <mark>amantadine</mark> did not alter whole brain <mark>dopamine</mark> levels but decreased the amounts of <mark>3 , 4 - dihydroxyphenylacetic acid</mark> in the BALB / C mice compared to saline control . 
Conversely , brain <mark>normetanephrine</mark> concentration was increased from saline control by <mark>amantadine</mark> in the BALB / C mice . 
The results suggest a strain - dependent effect of <mark>amantadine</mark> on motility and indicate a differential response to the acute and multiple dose regimens used . 
The BALB / C mouse was the most sensitive strain and could serve as the strain of choice for evaluating the side effects of <mark>amantadine</mark> . 
The biochemical results of brain biogenic <mark>amines</mark> of BALB / C mouse strain suggest a probable decrease of <mark>catecholamine</mark> turnover rate and / or metabolism by monoamine oxidase and a resulting increase in O - methylation of <mark>norepinephrine</mark> which may account for a behavioral depression caused by <mark>amantadine</mark> in the BALB / C mice . 
<mark>Chloroacetaldehyde</mark> and its contribution to urotoxicity during treatment with <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> or <mark>ifosfamide</mark> . 
An experimental study / short communication . 
Based on clinical data , indicating that <mark>chloroacetaldehyde</mark> ( <mark>CAA</mark> ) is an important metabolite of oxazaphosphorine cytostatics , an experimental study was carried out in order to elucidate the role of <mark>CAA</mark> in the development of hemorrhagic cystitis . 
The data demonstrate that <mark>CAA</mark> after i . v . administration does not contribute to bladder damage . 
When instilled directly into the bladder , <mark>CAA</mark> exerts urotoxic effects , it is , however , susceptible to detoxification with <mark>mesna</mark> . 
Source of pain and primitive dysfunction in migraine : an identical site ? 
Twenty common migraine patients received a one sided frontotemporal application of <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> ( 10 patients ) or placebo ointment ( 10 patients ) in a double blind study . 
Early onset migraine attacks were induced by <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> in seven out of 10 patients versus no patient in the placebo group . 
Subsequently 20 migraine patients , who developed an early onset attack with frontotemporal <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> , received the drug in a second induction test at other body areas . 
No early onset migraine was observed . 
Thus the migraine - inducing effect of <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> seems to depend on direct stimulation of the habitual site of pain , suggesting that the frontotemporal region is of crucial importance in the development of a migraine crisis . 
This is not consistent with a CNS origin of migraine attack . 
Hypersensitivity to <mark>carbamazepine</mark> presenting with a leukemoid reaction , eosinophilia , erythroderma , and renal failure . 
We report a patient in whom hypersensitivity to <mark>carbamazepine</mark> presented with generalized erythroderma , a severe leukemoid reaction , eosinophilia , hyponatremia , and renal failure . 
This is the first report of such an unusual reaction to <mark>carbamazepine</mark> . 
<mark>Fluoxetine</mark> - induced akathisia : clinical and theoretical implications . 
Five patients receiving <mark>fluoxetine</mark> for the treatment of obsessive compulsive disorder or major depression developed akathisia . 
The typical <mark>fluoxetine</mark> - induced symptoms of restlessness , constant pacing , purposeless movements of the feet and legs , and marked anxiety were indistinguishable from those of neuroleptic - induced akathisia . 
Three patients who had experienced neuroleptic - induced akathisia in the past reported that the symptoms of <mark>fluoxetine</mark> - induced akathisia were identical , although somewhat milder . 
Akathisia appeared to be a common side effect of <mark>fluoxetine</mark> and generally responded well to treatment with the beta - adrenergic antagonist <mark>propranolol</mark> , dose reduction , or both . 
The authors suggest that <mark>fluoxetine</mark> - induced akathisia may be caused by serotonergically mediated inhibition of dopaminergic neurotransmission and that the pathophysiology of <mark>fluoxetine</mark> - induced akathisia and tricyclic <mark>antidepressant</mark> - induced " jitteriness " may be identical . 
Effect of converting enzyme inhibition on the course of <mark>adriamycin</mark> - induced nephropathy . 
The effect of the converting enzyme inhibitor ( CEI ) <mark>enalapril</mark> was assessed in Munich - Wistar rats with established <mark>adriamycin</mark> nephrosis . 
Rats were given a single dose of <mark>adriamycin</mark> and one month later divided into four groups matched for albuminuria , blood pressure , and plasma albumin concentration . 
Groups 1 and 3 remained untreated while groups 2 and 4 received <mark>enalapril</mark> . 
Groups 1 and 2 underwent micropuncture studies after 10 days . 
These short - term studies showed that <mark>enalapril</mark> reduced arterial blood pressure ( 101 + / - 2 vs . 124 + / - 3 mm Hg , group 2 vs . 1 , P less than 0 . 05 ) and glomerular capillary pressure ( 54 + / - 1 vs . 61 + / - 2 mm Hg , P less than 0 . 05 ) without reducing albuminuria ( 617 + / - 50 vs . 570 + / - 47 mg / day ) or GFR ( 1 . 03 + / - 0 . 04 vs . 1 . 04 + / - 0 . 11 ml / min ) . 
Groups 3 and 4 were studied at four and at six months to assess the effect of <mark>enalapril</mark> on progression of renal injury in <mark>adriamycin</mark> nephrosis . 
Chronic <mark>enalapril</mark> treatment reduced blood pressure without reducing albuminuria in group 4 . 
Untreated group 3 rats exhibited a progressive reduction in GFR ( 0 . 35 + / - 0 . 08 ml / min at 4 months , 0 . 27 + / - 0 . 07 ml / min at 6 months ) . 
<mark>Enalapril</mark> treatment blunted but did not prevent reduction in GFR in group 4 ( 0 . 86 + / - 0 . 15 ml / min at 4 months , 0 . 69 + / - 0 . 13 ml / min at 6 months , both P less than 0 . 05 vs . group 3 ) . 
Reduction in GFR was associated with the development of glomerular sclerosis in both treated and untreated rats . ( ABSTRACT TRUNCATED AT 250 WORDS ) 
<mark>Clotiazepam</mark> - induced acute hepatitis . 
We report the case of a patient who developed acute hepatitis with extensive hepatocellular necrosis , 7 months after the onset of administration of <mark>clotiazepam</mark> , a <mark>thienodiazepine</mark> derivative . 
<mark>Clotiazepam</mark> withdrawal was followed by prompt recovery . 
The administration of several <mark>benzodiazepines</mark> , chemically related to <mark>clotiazepam</mark> , did not interfere with recovery and did not induce any relapse of hepatitis . 
This observation shows that <mark>clotiazepam</mark> can induce acute hepatitis and suggests that there is no cross hepatotoxicity between <mark>clotiazepam</mark> and several <mark>benzodiazepines</mark> . 
<mark>5 - azacytidine</mark> potentiates initiation induced by carcinogens in rat liver . 
To test the validity of the hypothesis that hypomethylation of DNA plays an important role in the initiation of carcinogenic process , <mark>5 - azacytidine</mark> ( <mark>5 - AzC</mark> ) ( 10 mg / kg ) , an inhibitor of DNA methylation , was given to rats during the phase of repair synthesis induced by the three carcinogens , <mark>benzo [ a ] - pyrene</mark> ( 200 mg / kg ) , <mark>N - methyl - N - nitrosourea</mark> ( 60 mg / kg ) and <mark>1 , 2 - dimethylhydrazine</mark> ( <mark>1 , 2 - DMH</mark> ) ( 100 mg / kg ) . 
The initiated hepatocytes in the liver were assayed as the gamma - glutamyltransferase ( gamma - GT ) positive foci formed following a 2 - week selection regimen consisting of dietary 0 . 02 % <mark>2 - acetylaminofluorene</mark> coupled with a necrogenic dose of <mark>CCl4</mark> . 
The results obtained indicate that with all three carcinogens , administration of <mark>5 - AzC</mark> during repair synthesis increased the incidence of initiated hepatocytes , for example 10 - 20 foci / cm2 in <mark>5 - AzC</mark> and carcinogen - treated rats compared with 3 - 5 foci / cm2 in rats treated with carcinogen only . 
Administration of <mark>[ 3H ] - 5 - azadeoxycytidine</mark> during the repair synthesis induced by <mark>1 , 2 - DMH</mark> further showed that 0 . 019 mol % of <mark>cytosine</mark> residues in DNA were substituted by the analogue , indicating that incorporation of <mark>5 - AzC</mark> occurs during repair synthesis . 
In the absence of the carcinogen , <mark>5 - AzC</mark> given after a two thirds partial hepatectomy , when its incorporation should be maximum , failed to induce any gamma - GT positive foci . 
The results suggest that hypomethylation of DNA per se may not be sufficient for initiation . 
Perhaps two events might be necessary for initiation , the first caused by the carcinogen and a second involving hypomethylation of DNA . 
Antihypertensive drugs and depression : a reappraisal . 
Eighty - nine new referral hypertensive out - patients and 46 new referral non - hypertensive chronically physically ill out - patients completed a mood rating scale at regular intervals for one year . 
The results showed a high prevalence of depression in both groups of patients , with no preponderance in the hypertensive group . 
Hypertensive patients with psychiatric histories had a higher prevalence of depression than the comparison patients . 
This was accounted for by a significant number of depressions occurring in <mark>methyl dopa</mark> treated patients with psychiatric histories . 
Chronic active hepatitis associated with <mark>diclofenac sodium</mark> therapy . 
<mark>Diclofenac sodium</mark> ( <mark>Voltarol</mark> , Geigy Pharmaceuticals ) is a non - steroidal anti - inflammatory derivative of <mark>phenylacetic acid</mark> . 
Although generally well - tolerated , asymptomatic abnormalities of liver function have been recorded and , less commonly , severe hepatitis induced by <mark>diclofenac</mark> . 
The patient described developed chronic active hepatitis after six months therapy with <mark>diclofenac sodium</mark> which progressed despite the withdrawal of the drug , a finding not previously reported . 
Arterial hypertension as a complication of prolonged <mark>ketoconazole</mark> treatment . 
Two of 14 patients with Cushing ' s syndrome treated on a long - term basis with <mark>ketoconazole</mark> developed sustained hypertension . 
In both cases normal plasma and urinary free <mark>cortisol</mark> levels had been achieved following <mark>ketoconazole</mark> therapy , yet continuous blood pressure monitoring demonstrated hypertension 31 ( patient 1 ) and 52 weeks ( patient 2 ) after treatment . 
In patient 1 , plasma levels of <mark>deoxycorticosterone</mark> and <mark>11 - deoxycortisol</mark> were elevated . 
In patient 2 , in addition to an increase in both <mark>deoxycorticosterone</mark> and <mark>11 - deoxycortisol</mark> levels , plasma <mark>aldosterone</mark> values were raised , with a concomitant suppression of renin levels . 
Our findings show that long - term treatment with high doses of <mark>ketoconazole</mark> may induce enzyme blockade leading to mineralocorticoid - related hypertension . 
Effects of an inhibitor of <mark>angiotensin</mark> converting enzyme ( <mark>Captopril</mark> ) on pulmonary and renal insufficiency due to intravascular coagulation in the rat . 
Induction of intravascular coagulation and inhibition of fibrinolysis by injection of thrombin and <mark>tranexamic acid</mark> ( <mark>AMCA</mark> ) in the rat gives rise to pulmonary and renal insufficiency resembling that occurring after trauma or sepsis in man . 
Injection of <mark>Captopril</mark> ( 1 mg / kg ) , an inhibitor of <mark>angiotensin</mark> converting enzyme ( ACE ) , reduced both pulmonary and renal insufficiency in this rat model . 
The lung weights were lower and PaO2 was improved in rats given this enzyme - blocking agent . 
The contents of albumin in the lungs were not changed , indicating that <mark>Captopril</mark> did not influence the extravasation of protein . 
Renal damage as reflected by an increase in serum <mark>urea</mark> and in kidney weight was prevented by <mark>Captopril</mark> . 
The amount of fibrin in the kidneys was also considerably lower than in animals which received thrombin and <mark>AMCA</mark> alone . 
It is suggested that the effects of <mark>Captopril</mark> on the lungs may be attributable to a vasodilatory effect due to a reduction in the circulating level of <mark>Angiotension II</mark> and an increase in <mark>prostacyclin</mark> ( secondary to an increase in <mark>bradykinin</mark> ) . 
<mark>Captopril</mark> may , by the same mechanism , reduce the increase in glomerular filtration that is known to occur after an injection of thrombin , thereby diminishing the aggregation of fibrin monomers in the glomeruli , with the result that less fibrin will be deposited and thus less kidney damage will be produced . 
Stroke associated with <mark>cocaine</mark> use . 
We describe eight patients in whom <mark>cocaine</mark> use was related to stroke and review 39 cases from the literature . 
Among these 47 patients the mean ( + / - SD ) age was 32 . 5 + / - 12 . 1 years ; 76 % ( 34 / 45 ) were men . 
Stroke followed <mark>cocaine</mark> use by inhalation , intranasal , intravenous , and intramuscular routes . 
Intracranial aneurysms or arteriovenous malformations were present in 17 of 32 patients studied angiographically or at autopsy ; cerebral vasculitis was present in two patients . 
Cerebral infarction occurred in 10 patients ( 22 % ) , intracerebral hemorrhage in 22 ( 49 % ) , and subarachnoid hemorrhage in 13 ( 29 % ) . 
These data indicate that ( 1 ) the apparent incidence of stroke related to <mark>cocaine</mark> use is increasing ; ( 2 ) <mark>cocaine</mark> - associated stroke occurs primarily in young adults ; ( 3 ) stroke may follow any route of <mark>cocaine</mark> administration ; ( 4 ) stroke after <mark>cocaine</mark> use is frequently associated with intracranial aneurysms and arteriovenous malformations ; and ( 5 ) in <mark>cocaine</mark> - associated stroke , the frequency of intracranial hemorrhage exceeds that of cerebral infarction . 
A randomized comparison of <mark>labetalol</mark> and <mark>nitroprusside</mark> for induced hypotension . 
In a randomized study , <mark>labetalol</mark> - induced hypotension and <mark>nitroprusside</mark> - induced hypotension were compared in 20 patients ( 10 in each group ) scheduled for major orthopedic procedures . 
Each patient was subjected to an identical anesthetic protocol and similar drug - induced reductions in mean arterial blood pressure ( BP ) ( 50 to 55 mmHg ) . 
Nitroprusside infusion was associated with a significant ( p less than 0 . 05 ) increase in heart rate and cardiac output ; rebound hypertension was observed in three patients after discontinuation of <mark>nitroprusside</mark> . 
<mark>Labetalol</mark> administration was not associated with any of these findings . 
Arterial <mark>PO2</mark> decreased in both groups . 
It was concluded that <mark>labetalol</mark> offers advantages over <mark>nitroprusside</mark> . 
<mark>Sodium</mark> status influences chronic <mark>amphotericin B</mark> nephrotoxicity in rats . 
The nephrotoxic potential of <mark>amphotericin B</mark> ( 5 mg / kg per day intraperitoneally for 3 weeks ) has been investigated in salt - depleted , normal - salt , and salt - loaded rats . 
In salt - depleted rats , <mark>amphotericin B</mark> decreased <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance linearly with time , with an 85 % reduction by week 3 . 
In contrast , in normal - salt rats <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance was decreased but to a lesser extent at week 2 and 3 , and in salt - loaded rats <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance did not change for 2 weeks and was decreased by 43 % at week 3 . 
All rats in the <mark>sodium</mark> - depleted group had histopathological evidence of patchy tubular cytoplasmic degeneration in tubules that was not observed in any normal - salt or salt - loaded rat . 
Concentrations of <mark>amphotericin B</mark> in plasma were not significantly different among the three groups at any time during the study . 
However , at the end of 3 weeks , <mark>amphotericin B</mark> levels in the kidneys and liver were significantly higher in salt - depleted and normal - salt rats than those in salt - loaded rats , with plasma / kidney ratios of 21 , 14 , and 8 in salt - depleted , normal - salt , and salt - loaded rats , respectively . 
In conclusion , reductions in <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance and renal <mark>amphotericin B</mark> accumulation after chronic <mark>amphotericin B</mark> administration were enhanced by salt depletion and attenuated by <mark>sodium</mark> loading in rats . 
<mark>Flestolol</mark> : an ultra - short - acting beta - adrenergic blocking agent . 
<mark>Flestolol</mark> ( <mark>ACC - 9089</mark> ) is a nonselective , competitive , ultra - short - acting beta - adrenergic blocking agent , without any intrinsic sympathomimetic activity . 
<mark>Flestolol</mark> is metabolized by plasma esterases and has an elimination half - life of approximately 6 . 5 minutes . 
This agent was well tolerated in healthy volunteers at doses up to 100 micrograms / kg / min . 
In long - term infusion studies , <mark>flestolol</mark> was well tolerated at the effective beta - blocking dose ( 5 micrograms / kg / min ) for up to seven days . 
<mark>Flestolol</mark> blood concentrations increased linearly with increasing dose and good correlation exists between blood concentrations of <mark>flestolol</mark> and beta - adrenergic blockade . 
<mark>Flestolol</mark> produced a dose - dependent attenuation of <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced tachycardia . 
Electrophysiologic and hemodynamic effects of <mark>flestolol</mark> are similar to those of other beta blockers . 
In contrast with other beta blockers , <mark>flestolol</mark> - induced effects reverse rapidly ( within 30 minutes ) following discontinuation because of its short half - life . 
<mark>Flestolol</mark> effectively reduced heart rate in patients with supraventricular tachyarrhythmia . 
In patients with unstable angina , <mark>flestolol</mark> infusion was found to be safe and effective in controlling chest pain . 
It is concluded that <mark>flestolol</mark> is a potent , well - tolerated , ultra - short - acting beta - adrenergic blocking agent . 
Use of <mark>flestolol</mark> in the critical care setting is currently undergoing investigation . 
Immunohistochemical , electron microscopic and morphometric studies of <mark>estrogen</mark> - induced rat prolactinomas after <mark>bromocriptine</mark> treatment . 
To clarify the effects of <mark>bromocriptine</mark> on prolactinoma cells in vivo , immunohistochemical , ultrastructural and morphometrical analyses were applied to <mark>estrogen</mark> - induced rat prolactinoma cells 1 h and 6 h after injection of <mark>bromocriptine</mark> ( 3 mg / kg of body weight ) . 
One h after treatment , serum prolactin levels decreased markedly . 
Electron microscopy disclosed many secretory granules , slightly distorted rough endoplasmic reticulum , and partially dilated Golgi cisternae in the prolactinoma cells . 
Morphometric analysis revealed that the volume density of secretory granules increased , while the volume density of cytoplasmic microtubules decreased . 
These findings suggest that lowered serum prolactin levels in the early phase of <mark>bromocriptine</mark> treatment may result from an impaired secretion of prolactin due to decreasing numbers of cytoplasmic microtubules . 
At 6 h after injection , serum prolactin levels were still considerably lower than in controls . 
The prolactinoma cells at this time were well granulated , with vesiculated rough endoplasmic reticulum and markedly dilated Golgi cisternae . 
Electron microscopical immunohistochemistry revealed positive reaction products noted on the secretory granules , Golgi cisternae , and endoplasmic reticulum of the untreated rat prolactinoma cells . 
However , only secretory granules showed the positive reaction products for prolactin 6 h after <mark>bromocriptine</mark> treatment of the adenoma cells . 
An increase in the volume density of secretory granules and a decrease in the volume densities of rough endoplasmic reticulum and microtubules was determined by morphometric analysis , suggesting that <mark>bromocriptine</mark> inhibits protein synthesis as well as bringing about a disturbance of the prolactin secretion . 
<mark>Sulfasalazine</mark> - induced lupus erythematosus . 
Pneumonitis , bilateral pleural effusions , echocardiographic evidence of cardiac tamponade , and positive autoantibodies developed in a 43 - year - old man , who was receiving long - term <mark>sulfasalazine</mark> therapy for chronic ulcerative colitis . 
After cessation of the <mark>sulfasalazine</mark> and completion of a six - week course of corticosteroids , these problems resolved over a period of four to six months . 
It is suggested that the patient had <mark>sulfasalazine</mark> - induced lupus , which manifested with serositis and pulmonary parenchymal involvement in the absence of joint symptoms . 
Physicians who use <mark>sulfasalazine</mark> to treat patients with inflammatory bowel disease should be aware of the signs of <mark>sulfasalazine</mark> - induced lupus syndrome . 
Chronic <mark>carbamazepine</mark> treatment in the rat : efficacy , toxicity , and effect on plasma and tissue <mark>folate</mark> concentrations . 
<mark>Folate</mark> depletion has often been a problem in chronic antiepileptic drug ( AED ) therapy . 
<mark>Carbamazepine</mark> ( <mark>CBZ</mark> ) , a commonly used AED , has been implicated in some clinical studies . 
A rat model was developed to examine the effects of chronic <mark>CBZ</mark> treatment on <mark>folate</mark> concentrations in the rat . 
In the course of developing this model , a common vehicle , <mark>propylene glycol</mark> , by itself in high doses , was found to exhibit protective properties against induced seizures and inhibited weight gain . 
Seizures induced by <mark>hexafluorodiethyl ether</mark> ( <mark>HFDE</mark> ) were also found to be a more sensitive measure of protection by <mark>CBZ</mark> than seizures induced by maximal electroshock ( MES ) . 
Oral administration of <mark>CBZ</mark> as an aqueous suspension every 8 h at a dose of 250 mg / kg was continuously protective against <mark>HFDE</mark> - induced seizures and was minimally toxic as measured by weight gain over 8 weeks of treatment . 
The <mark>CBZ</mark> levels measured in plasma and brain of these animals , however , were below those normally considered protective . 
This treatment with <mark>CBZ</mark> had no apparent adverse effect on <mark>folate</mark> concentrations in the rat , and , indeed , the <mark>folate</mark> concentration increased in liver after 6 weeks of treatment and in plasma at 8 weeks of treatment . 
<mark>Dipyridamole</mark> - induced myocardial ischemia . 
Angina and ischemic electrocardiographic changes occurred after administration of oral <mark>dipyridamole</mark> in four patients awaiting urgent myocardial revascularization procedures . 
To our knowledge , this has not previously been reported as a side effect of preoperative <mark>dipyridamole</mark> therapy , although <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - induced myocardial ischemia has been demonstrated to occur in animals and humans with coronary artery disease . 
Epicardial coronary collateral vessels were demonstrated in all four patients ; a coronary " steal " phenomenon may be the mechanism of the <mark>dipyridamole</mark> - induced ischemia observed . 
Inhibition of sympathoadrenal activity by atrial natriuretic factor in dogs . 
In six conscious , trained dogs , maintained on a normal <mark>sodium</mark> intake of 2 to 4 mEq / kg / day , sympathetic activity was assessed as the release rate of <mark>norepinephrine</mark> and <mark>epinephrine</mark> during 15 - minute i . v . infusions of human alpha - atrial natriuretic factor . 
Mean arterial pressure ( as a percentage of control + / - SEM ) during randomized infusions of 0 . 03 , 0 . 1 , 0 . 3 , or 1 . 0 microgram / kg / min was 99 + / - 1 , 95 + / - 1 ( p less than 0 . 05 ) , 93 + / - 1 ( p less than 0 . 01 ) , or 79 + / - 6 % ( p less than 0 . 001 ) , respectively , but no tachycardia and no augmentation of the <mark>norepinephrine</mark> release rate ( up to 0 . 3 microgram / kg / min ) were observed , which is in contrast to comparable hypotension induced by <mark>hydralazine</mark> or <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> . 
The release rate of <mark>epinephrine</mark> ( control , 6 . 7 + / - 0 . 6 ng / kg / min ) declined immediately during infusions of atrial natriuretic factor to a minimum of 49 + / - 5 % of control ( p less than 0 . 001 ) during 0 . 1 microgram / kg / min and to 63 + / - 5 % ( 0 . 1 greater than p greater than 0 . 05 ) or 95 + / - 13 % ( not significant ) during 0 . 3 or 1 . 0 microgram / kg / min .

Inhibition of immunoreactive corticotropin - releasing factor secretion into the hypophysial - portal circulation by delayed glucocorticoid feedback . 
<mark>Nitroprusside</mark> - induced hypotension evokes ACTH secretion which is primarily mediated by enhanced secretion of immunoreactive corticotropin - releasing factor ( irCRF ) into the hypophysial - portal circulation . 
Portal plasma concentrations of neither <mark>arginine vasopressin</mark> nor <mark>oxytocin</mark> are significantly altered in this paradigm . 
Application of a delayed feedback signal , in the form of a 2 - h systemic <mark>corticosterone</mark> infusion in <mark>urethane</mark> - anesthetized rats with pharmacological blockade of glucocorticoid synthesis , is without effect on the resting secretion of <mark>arginine vasopressin</mark> and <mark>oxytocin</mark> at any <mark>corticosterone</mark> feedback dose tested . 
Resting irCRF levels are suppressed only at the highest <mark>corticosterone</mark> infusion rate , which resulted in systemic <mark>corticosterone</mark> levels of 40 micrograms / dl . 
Suppression of irCRF secretion in response to <mark>nitroprusside</mark> - induced hypotension is observed and occurs at a plasma <mark>corticosterone</mark> level between 8 - 12 micrograms / dl . 
These studies provide further evidence for a strong central component of the delayed feedback process which is mediated by modulation of irCRF release . 
Noradrenergic involvement in catalepsy induced by <mark>delta 9 - tetrahydrocannabinol</mark> . 
In order to elucidate the role of the catecholaminergic system in the cataleptogenic effect of <mark>delta 9 - tetrahydrocannabinol</mark> ( <mark>THC</mark> ) , the effect of pretreatment with <mark>6 - hydroxydopamine</mark> ( <mark>6 - OHDA</mark> ) or with <mark>desipramine</mark> and <mark>6 - OHDA</mark> and lesions of the locus coeruleus were investigated in rats . 
The cataleptogenic effect of <mark>THC</mark> was significantly reduced in rats treated with <mark>6 - OHDA</mark> and in rats with lesions of the locus coeruleus but not in rats treated with <mark>desipramine</mark> and <mark>6 - OHDA</mark> , as compared with control rats . 
On the contrary , the cataleptogenic effect of <mark>haloperidol</mark> was significantly reduced in rats treated with <mark>desipramine</mark> and <mark>6 - OHDA</mark> but not in rats treated with <mark>6 - OHDA</mark> or in rats with lesions of the locus coeruleus . 
These results indicate that noradrenergic neurons have an important role in the manifestation of catalepsy induced by <mark>THC</mark> , whereas dopaminergic neurons are important in catalepsy induced by <mark>haloperidol</mark> . 
Reversibility of <mark>captopril</mark> - induced renal insufficiency after prolonged use in an unusual case of renovascular hypertension . 
We report a case of severe hypertension with an occluded renal artery to a solitary kidney , who developed sudden deterioration of renal function following treatment with <mark>captopril</mark> . 
His renal function remained impaired but stable during 2 years ' treatment with <mark>captopril</mark> but returned to pre - treatment levels soon after cessation of the drug . 
This indicates reversibility in <mark>captopril</mark> - induced renal failure even after its prolonged use and suggests that no organic damage occurs to glomerular arterioles following chronic ACE inhibition . 
HMG CoA reductase inhibitors . 
Current clinical experience . 
<mark>Lovastatin</mark> and <mark>simvastatin</mark> are the 2 best - known members of the class of hypolipidaemic agents known as HMG CoA reductase inhibitors . 
Clinical experience with <mark>lovastatin</mark> includes over 5000 patients , 700 of whom have been treated for 2 years or more , and experience with <mark>simvastatin</mark> includes over 3500 patients , of whom 350 have been treated for 18 months or more . 
<mark>Lovastatin</mark> has been marketed in the United States for over 6 months . 
Both agents show substantial clinical efficacy , with reductions in total <mark>cholesterol</mark> of over 30 % and in LDL - <mark>cholesterol</mark> of 40 % in clinical studies . 
Modest increases in HDL - <mark>cholesterol</mark> levels of about 10 % are also reported . 
Clinical tolerability of both agents has been good , with fewer than 3 % of patients withdrawn from treatment because of clinical adverse experiences . 
Ophthalmological examinations in over 1100 patients treated with one or the other agent have revealed no evidence of significant short term ( up to 2 years ) cataractogenic potential . 
One to 2 % of patients have elevations of serum transaminases to greater than 3 times the upper limit of normal . 
These episodes are asymptomatic and reversible when therapy is discontinued . 
Minor elevations of <mark>creatine</mark> kinase levels are reported in about 5 % of patients . 
Myopathy , associated in some cases with myoglobinuria , and in 2 cases with transient renal failure , has been rarely reported with <mark>lovastatin</mark> , especially in patients concomitantly treated with <mark>cyclosporin</mark> , <mark>gemfibrozil</mark> or <mark>niacin</mark> . 
<mark>Lovastatin</mark> and <mark>simvastatin</mark> are both effective and well - tolerated agents for lowering elevated levels of serum <mark>cholesterol</mark> . 
As wider use confirms their safety profile , they will gain increasing importance in the therapeutic approach to hypercholesterolaemia and its consequences . 
Hepatic reactions associated with <mark>ketoconazole</mark> in the United Kingdom . 
<mark>Ketoconazole</mark> was introduced in the United Kingdom in 1981 . 
By November 1984 the Committee on Safety of Medicines had received 82 reports of possible hepatotoxicity associated with the drug , including five deaths . 
An analysis of the 75 cases that had been adequately followed up suggested that 16 , including three deaths , were probably related to treatment with the drug . 
Of the remainder , 48 were possibly related to treatment , five were unlikely to be so , and six were unclassifiable . 
The mean age of patients in the 16 probable cases was 57 . 9 , with hepatotoxicity being more common in women . 
The average duration of treatment before the onset of jaundice was 61 days . 
None of these well validated cases occurred within the first 10 days after treatment . 
The results of serum liver function tests suggested hepatocellular injury in 10 ( 63 % ) ; the rest showed a mixed pattern . 
In contrast , the results of histological examination of the liver often showed evidence of cholestasis . 
The characteristics of the 48 patients in the possible cases were similar . 
Allergic manifestations such as rash and eosinophilia were rare . 
Hepatitis was usually reversible when treatment was stopped , with the results of liver function tests returning to normal after an average of 3 . 1 months . 
In two of the three deaths probably associated with <mark>ketoconazole</mark> treatment the drug had been continued after the onset of jaundice and other symptoms of hepatitis . 
Clinical and biochemical monitoring at regular intervals for evidence of hepatitis is advised during long term treatment with <mark>ketoconazole</mark> to prevent possible serious hepatic injury . 
<mark>Glyburide</mark> - induced hepatitis . 
Drug - induced hepatotoxicity , although common , has been reported only infrequently with <mark>sulfonylureas</mark> . 
For <mark>glyburide</mark> , a second - generation <mark>sulfonylurea</mark> , only two brief reports of hepatotoxicity exist . 
Two patients with type II diabetes mellitus developed an acute hepatitis - like syndrome soon after initiation of <mark>glyburide</mark> therapy . 
There was no serologic evidence of viral infection , and a liver biopsy sample showed a histologic pattern consistent with drug - induced hepatitis . 
Both patients recovered quickly after stopping <mark>glyburide</mark> therapy and have remained well for a follow - up period of 1 year . 
<mark>Glyburide</mark> can produce an acute hepatitis - like illness in some persons . 
Intracranial pressure increases during <mark>alfentanil</mark> - induced rigidity . 
Intracranial pressure ( ICP ) was measured during <mark>alfentanil</mark> - induced rigidity in rats . 
Ten rats had arterial , central venous ( CVP ) , and subdural cannulae inserted under <mark>halothane</mark> anesthesia . 
The animals were mechanically ventilated to achieve normocarbia ( PCO2 = 42 + / - 1 mmHg , mean + / - SE ) . 
Following instrumentation , <mark>halothane</mark> was discontinued and <mark>alfentanil</mark> ( 125 mu / kg ) administered iv during emergence from <mark>halothane</mark> anesthesia . 
In the five rats that developed somatic rigidity , ICP and CVP increased significantly above baseline ( delta ICP 7 . 5 + / - 1 . 0 mmHg , delta CVP 5 . 9 + / - 1 . 3 mmHg ) . 
These variables returned to baseline when rigidity was abolished with <mark>metocurine</mark> . 
In five rats that did not become rigid , ICP and CVP did not change following <mark>alfentanil</mark> . 
These observations suggest that rigidity should be prevented when <mark>alfentanil</mark> , and , presumably , other opiates , are used in the anesthetic management of patients with ICP problems . 
<mark>Verapamil</mark> withdrawal as a possible cause of myocardial infarction in a hypertensive woman with a normal coronary angiogram . 
<mark>Verapamil</mark> is an effective and relatively - safe antihypertensive drug . 
Serious adverse effects are uncommon and mainly have been related to the depression of cardiac contractility and conduction , especially when the drug is combined with beta - blocking agents . 
We report a case in which myocardial infarction coincided with the introduction of <mark>captopril</mark> and the withdrawal of <mark>verapamil</mark> in a previously asymptomatic woman with severe hypertension . 
Possible mechanisms that involve a <mark>verapamil</mark> - related increase in platelet and / or vascular alpha 2 - adrenoreceptor affinity for <mark>catecholamines</mark> are discussed . 
Haemolytic - uraemic syndrome after treatment with <mark>metronidazole</mark> . 
This paper describes the clinical features of six children who developed the haemolytic - uraemic syndrome after treatment with <mark>metronidazole</mark> . 
These children were older and were more likely to have undergone recent bowel surgery than are other children with this condition . 
While the involvement of <mark>metronidazole</mark> in the aetiology of the haemolytic - uraemic syndrome is not established firmly , the action of this drug in sensitizing tissues to oxidation injury and the reported evidence of oxidation changes in the haemolytic - uraemic syndrome suggest a possible link between <mark>metronidazole</mark> treatment and some cases of the haemolytic - uraemic syndrome . 
Adverse cardiac effects during induction chemotherapy treatment with <mark>cis - platin</mark> and <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> . 
Survival for patients with advanced head and neck carcinoma and esophageal carcinoma is poor with radiotherapy and / or surgery . 
Obviously , there is a need for effective chemotherapy . 
In the present study , <mark>cis - platin</mark> ( 80 - 120 mg / m2BSA ) and <mark>5 - FU</mark> ( 1000 mg / m2BSA daily as a continuous infusion during 5 days ) were given to 76 patients before radiotherapy and surgery . 
The aim of the study was to clarify the incidence and severity of adverse cardiac effects to this treatment . 
Before treatment all patients had a cardiac evaluation and during treatment serial ECG recordings were performed . 
In the pre - treatment evaluation , signs of cardiovascular disease were found in 33 patients ( 43 % ) . 
During treatment , adverse cardiac effects were observed in 14 patients ( 18 % ) . 
The mean age of these patients was the same as for the entire group , 64 years . 
The incidence of cardiotoxicity was not higher in patients with signs of cardiovascular disease than in those without in the pre - treatment evaluation . 
The most common signs of cardiotoxicity were chest pain , ST - T wave changes and atrial fibrillation . 
This was followed by ventricular fibrillation in one patient and sudden death in another . 
It is concluded that patients on <mark>5 - FU</mark> treatment should be under close supervision and that the treatment should be discontinued if chest pain or tachyarrhythmia is observed . 
Death from chemotherapy in gestational trophoblastic disease . 
Multiple cytotoxic drug administration is the generally accepted treatment of patients with a high - risk stage of choriocarcinoma . 
Based on this principle a 27 - year old woman , classified as being in the high - risk group ( Goldstein and Berkowitz score : 11 ) , was treated with multiple cytotoxic drugs . 
The multiple drug schema consisted of : <mark>Etoposide</mark> 16 . 213 , <mark>Methotrexate</mark> , <mark>Cyclophosphamide</mark> , <mark>Actomycin - D</mark> , and <mark>Cisplatin</mark> . 
On the first day of the schedule , moderate high doses of <mark>Methotrexate</mark> , <mark>Etoposide</mark> and <mark>Cyclophosphamide</mark> were administered . 
Within 8 hours after initiation of therapy the patient died with a clinical picture resembling massive pulmonary obstruction due to choriocarcinomic tissue plugs , probably originating from the uterus . 
Formation of these plugs was probably due to extensive tumor necrosis at the level of the walls of the major uterine veins , which resulted in an open exchange of tumor plugs to the vascular spaces ; decrease in tumor tissue coherence secondary to chemotherapy may have further contributed to the formation of tumor emboli . 
In view of the close time association between the start of chemotherapy and the acute onset of massive embolism other explanations , such as spontaneous necrosis , must be considered less likely . 
Patients with large pelvic tumor loads are , according to existing classifications , at high risk to die and to develop drug resistance . 
Notwithstanding these facts our findings suggest that these patients might benefit from relatively mild initial treatment , especially true for patients not previously exposed to this drug . 
Close observation of the response status both clinically and with beta - hCG values may indicate whether and when more agressive combination chemotherapy should be started . ( ABSTRACT TRUNCATED AT 250 WORDS ) 
Pulmonary shunt and cardiovascular responses to CPAP during <mark>nitroprusside</mark> - induced hypotension . 
The effects of continuous positive airway pressure ( CPAP ) on cardiovascular dynamics and pulmonary shunt ( QS / QT ) were investigated in 12 dogs before and during <mark>sodium nitroprusside</mark> infusion that decreased mean arterial blood pressure 40 - 50 per cent . 
Before <mark>nitroprusside</mark> infusion , 5 cm <mark>H2O</mark> CPAP significantly , P less than . 05 , decreased arterial blood pressure , but did not significantly alter heart rate , cardiac output , systemic vascular resistance , or QS / QT . 
Ten cm <mark>H2O</mark> CPAP before <mark>nitroprusside</mark> infusion produced a further decrease in arterial blood pressure and significantly increased heart rate and decreased cardiac output and QS / QT .
