<mark>Nitroprusside</mark> caused significant decreases in arterial blood pressure and systemic vascular resistance and increases in heart rate , but did not change cardiac output or QS / QT . 
Five cm <mark>H2O</mark> CPAP during <mark>nitroprusside</mark> did not further alter any of the above - mentioned variables . 
However , 10 cm <mark>H2O</mark> CPAP decreased arterial blood pressure , cardiac output , and QS / QT . 
These data indicate that <mark>nitroprusside</mark> infusion rates that decrease mean arterial blood pressure by 40 - 50 per cent do not change cardiac output or QS / QT . 
During <mark>nitroprusside</mark> infusion low levels of CPAP do not markedly alter cardiovascular dynamics , but high levels of CPAP ( 10 cm <mark>H2O</mark> ) , while decreasing QS / QT , produce marked decreases in arterial blood pressure and cardiac output . 
Systolic pressure variation is greater during hemorrhage than during <mark>sodium nitroprusside</mark> - induced hypotension in ventilated dogs . 
The systolic pressure variation ( SPV ) , which is the difference between the maximal and minimal values of the systolic blood pressure ( SBP ) after one positive - pressure breath , was studied in ventilated dogs subjected to hypotension . 
Mean arterial pressure was decreased to 50 mm Hg for 30 minutes either by hemorrhage ( HEM , n = 7 ) or by continuous infusion of <mark>sodium nitroprusside</mark> ( <mark>SNP</mark> , n = 7 ) . 
During HEM - induced hypotension the cardiac output was significantly lower and systemic vascular resistance higher compared with that in the <mark>SNP</mark> group . 
The systemic , central venous , pulmonary capillary wedge pressures , and heart rates , were similar in the two groups . 
Analysis of the respiratory changes in the arterial pressure waveform enabled differentiation between the two groups . 
The SPV during hypotension was 15 . 7 + / - 6 . 7 mm Hg in the HEM group , compared with 9 . 1 + / - 2 . 0 mm Hg in the <mark>SNP</mark> group ( P less than 0 . 02 ) . 
The delta down , which is the measure of decrease of SBP after a mechanical breath , was 20 . 3 + / - 8 . 4 and 10 . 1 + / - 3 . 8 mm Hg in the HEM and <mark>SNP</mark> groups , respectively , during hypotension ( P less than 0 . 02 ) . 
It is concluded that increases in the SPV and the delta down are characteristic of a hypotensive state due to a predominant decrease in preload . 
They are thus more important during absolute hypovolemia than during deliberate hypotension . 
Ventricular tachyarrhythmias during cesarean section after <mark>ritodrine</mark> therapy : interaction with anesthetics . 
This case illustrates that patients receiving <mark>ritodrine</mark> for preterm labor may risk interactions between the residual betamimetic effects of <mark>ritodrine</mark> and the effects of anesthetics during cesarean section . 
Such interactions may result in serious cardiovascular complications even after cessation of an infusion of <mark>ritodrine</mark> . 
Preoperative assessment should focus on cardiovascular status and serum <mark>potassium</mark> level . 
Delaying induction of anesthesia should be considered whenever possible . 
Careful fluid administration and cautious use of titrated doses of <mark>ephedrine</mark> are advised . 
After delivery of the infant , there should be no contraindication to the use of an alpha - adrenergic vasopressor such as <mark>phenylephrine</mark> to treat hypotensive patients with tachycardia . 
<mark>Verapamil</mark> - induced <mark>carbamazepine</mark> neurotoxicity . 
A report of two cases . 
Two patients with signs of <mark>carbamazepine</mark> neurotoxicity after combined treatment with <mark>verapamil</mark> showed complete recovery after discontinuation of the <mark>calcium</mark> entry blocker . 
Use of <mark>verapamil</mark> in combination with <mark>carbamazepine</mark> should either be avoided or prescribed only with appropriate adjustment of the <mark>carbamazepine</mark> dose ( usually reduction of the <mark>carbamazepine</mark> dose by one half ) . 
<mark>Paracetamol</mark> - associated coma , metabolic acidosis , renal and hepatic failure . 
A case of metabolic acidosis , acute renal failure and hepatic failure following <mark>paracetamol</mark> ingestion is presented . 
The diagnostic difficulty at presentation is highlighted . 
Continuous arteriovenous haemofiltration proved a valuable means of maintaining fluid and electrolyte balance . 
The patient recovered . 
Sexual dysfunction among patients with arthritis . 
The relationship of arthritis and sexual dysfunction was investigated among 169 patients with rheumatoid arthritis , osteoarthritis and spondyloarthropathy , 130 of whom were pair - matched to controls . 
Assessments of marital happiness and depressed mood were also made using the CES - D and the Azrin Marital Happiness Scale ( AMHS ) . 
Sexual dysfunctions were found to be common among patients and controls , the majority in both groups reporting one or more dysfunctions . 
Impotence was more common among male patients than controls and was found to be associated with co - morbidity and the taking of <mark>methotrexate</mark> . 
Depressed mood was more common among patients and was associated with certain sexual difficulties , but not with impotence . 
Marital unhappiness , as indicated by AMHS scores , was not associated with arthritis but was associated with sexual dysfunction , sexual dissatisfaction and being female . 
Does <mark>paracetamol</mark> cause urothelial cancer or renal papillary necrosis ? 
The risk of developing renal papillary necrosis or cancer of the renal pelvis , ureter or bladder associated with consumption of either <mark>phenacetin</mark> or <mark>paracetamol</mark> was calculated from data acquired by questionnaire from 381 cases and 808 controls . 
The risk of renal papillary necrosis was increased nearly 20 - fold by consumption of <mark>phenacetin</mark> , which also increased the risk for cancer of the renal pelvis and bladder but not for ureteric cancer . 
By contrast , we were unable to substantiate an increased risk from <mark>paracetamol</mark> consumption for renal papillary necrosis or any of these cancers although there was a suggestion of an association with cancer of the ureter . 
<mark>Dapsone</mark> - associated Heinz body hemolytic anemia in a Cambodian woman with hemoglobin E trait . 
A Cambodian woman with hemoglobin E trait ( AE ) and leprosy developed a Heinz body hemolytic anemia while taking a dose of <mark>dapsone</mark> ( 50 mg / day ) not usually associated with clinical hemolysis . 
Her red blood cells ( RBCs ) had increased incubated Heinz body formation , decreased reduced <mark>glutathione</mark> ( <mark>GSH</mark> ) , and decreased <mark>GSH</mark> stability . 
The <mark>pentose phosphate</mark> shunt activity of the <mark>dapsone</mark> - exposed AE RBCs was increased compared to normal RBCs . 
Although the AE RBCs from an individual not taking <mark>dapsone</mark> had increased incubated Heinz body formation , the <mark>GSH</mark> content and <mark>GSH</mark> stability were normal . 
The <mark>pentose phosphate</mark> shunt activity of the non - <mark>dapsone</mark> - exposed AE RBCs was decreased compared to normal RBCs . 
Thus , AE RBCs appear to have an increased sensitivity to oxidant stress both in vitro and in vivo , since <mark>dapsone</mark> does not cause hemolytic anemia at this dose in hematologically normal individuals . 
Given the influx of Southeast Asians into the United States , oxidant medications should be used with caution , especially if an infection is present , in individuals of ethnic backgrounds that have an increased prevalence of hemoglobin E . 
Severe complications of antianginal drug therapy in a patient identified as a poor metabolizer of <mark>metoprolol</mark> , <mark>propafenone</mark> , <mark>diltiazem</mark> , and <mark>sparteine</mark> . 
A 47 - year - old patient suffering from coronary artery disease was admitted to the CCU in shock with III . 
AV block , severe hypotension , and impairment of ventricular function . 
One week prior to admission a therapy with standard doses of <mark>metoprolol</mark> ( 100 mg t . i . d . and then 100 mg b . i . d . ) had been initiated . 
Two days before admission <mark>diltiazem</mark> ( 60 mg b . i . d . ) was prescribed in addition . 
Analyses of a blood sample revealed unusually high plasma concentrations of <mark>metoprolol</mark> ( greater than 3000 ng / ml ) and <mark>diltiazem</mark> ( 526 ng / ml ) . 
The patient recovered within 1 week following discontinuation of antianginal therapy . 
Three months later the patient was exposed to a single dose of <mark>metoprolol</mark> , <mark>diltiazem</mark> , <mark>propafenone</mark> ( since he had received this drug in the past ) , and <mark>sparteine</mark> ( as a probe for the <mark>debrisoquine</mark> / <mark>sparteine</mark> type polymorphism of oxidative drug metabolism ) . 
It was found that he was a poor metabolizer of all four drugs , indicating that their metabolism is under the same genetic control . 
Therefore , patients belonging to the poor - metabolizer phenotype of <mark>sparteine</mark> / <mark>debrisoquine</mark> polymorphism in drug metabolism , which constitutes 6 . 4 % of the German population , may experience adverse drug reactions when treated with standard doses of one of these drugs alone . 
Moreover , the coadministration of these frequently used drugs is expected to be especially harmful in this subgroup of patients . 
Clinical experiences in an open and a double - blind trial . 
A total of sixty patients were trated with <mark>bromperidol</mark> first in open conditions ( 20 patients ) , then on a double blind basis ( 40 patients ) with <mark>haloperidol</mark> as the reference substance . 
The open study lasted for four weeks ; the drug was administrated in the form of 1 mg tablets . 
The daily dose ( initial dose : 1 mg ; mean dose at the end of the trial : 4 . 47 mg ) was always administered in one single dose . 
Nineteen patients finished the trial , and in 18 cases the therapeutic result was considered very good to good . 
These results were confirmed by statistical analysis . 
Nine patients exhibited mild to moderate extrapyramidal concomitant symptoms ; no other side effects were observed . 
The results of detailed laboratory tests and evaluations of various quantitative and qualitative tolerability parameters were not indicative of toxic effects . 
In the double blind study with <mark>haloperidol</mark> , both substances were found to be highly effective in the treatment of psychotic syndromes belonging predominantly to the schizophrenia group . 
Certain clues , including the onset of action , seem to be indicative of the superiority of <mark>bromperidol</mark> . 
No differences were observed with respect to side effects and general tolerability . 
Prolonged cholestasis after <mark>troleandomycin</mark> - induced acute hepatitis . 
We report the case of a patient in whom <mark>troleandomycin</mark> - induced hepatitis was followed by prolonged anicteric cholestasis . 
Jaundice occurred after administration of <mark>troleandomycin</mark> for 7 days and was associated with hypereosinophilia . 
Jaundice disappeared within 3 months but was followed by prolonged anicteric cholestasis marked by pruritus and high levels of alkaline phosphatase and gammaglutamyltransferase activities . 
Finally , pruritus disappeared within 19 months , and liver tests returned to normal 27 months after the onset of hepatitis . 
This observation demonstrates that prolonged cholestasis can follow <mark>troleandomycin</mark> - induced acute hepatitis . 
Serial studies of auditory neurotoxicity in patients receiving <mark>deferoxamine</mark> therapy . 
Visual and auditory neurotoxicity was previously documented in 42 of 89 patients with transfusion - dependent anemia who were receiving <mark>iron</mark> chelation therapy with daily subcutaneous <mark>deferoxamine</mark> . 
Twenty - two patients in the affected group had abnormal audiograms with deficits mostly in the high frequency range of 4 , 000 to 8 , 000 Hz and in the hearing threshold levels of 30 to 100 decibels . 
When <mark>deferoxamine</mark> therapy was discontinued and serial studies were performed , audiograms in seven cases reverted to normal or near normal within two to three weeks , and nine of 13 patients with symptoms became asymptomatic . 
Audiograms from 15 patients remained abnormal and four patients required hearing aids because of permanent disability . 
Since 18 of the 22 patients were initially receiving <mark>deferoxamine</mark> doses in excess of the commonly recommended 50 mg / kg per dose , therapy was restarted with lower doses , usually 50 mg / kg per dose or less depending on the degree of auditory abnormality , and with the exception of two cases no further toxicity was demonstrated . 
Auditory deterioration and improvement , demonstrated serially in individual patients receiving and not receiving <mark>deferoxamine</mark> , respectively , provided convincing evidence for a cause - and - effect relation between <mark>deferoxamine</mark> administration and ototoxicity . 
Based on these data , a plan of management was developed that allows effective yet safe administration of <mark>deferoxamine</mark> . 
A dose of 50 mg / kg is recommended in those without audiogram abnormalities . 
With mild toxicity , a reduction to 30 or 40 mg / kg per dose should result in a reversal of the abnormal results to normal within four weeks . 
Moderate abnormalities require a reduction of <mark>deferoxamine</mark> to 25 mg / kg per dose with careful monitoring . 
In those with symptoms of hearing loss , the drug should be stopped for four weeks , and when the audiogram is stable or improved , therapy should be restarted at 10 to 25 mg / kg per dose . 
Serial audiograms should be performed every six months in those without problems and more frequently in young patients with normal serum ferritin values and in those with auditory dysfunction . 
<mark>Lidocaine</mark> - induced cardiac asystole . 
Intravenous administration of a single 50 - mg bolus of <mark>lidocaine</mark> in a 67 - year - old man resulted in profound depression of the activity of the sinoatrial and atrioventricular nodal pacemakers . 
The patient had no apparent associated conditions which might have predisposed him to the development of bradyarrhythmias ; and , thus , this probably represented a true idiosyncrasy to <mark>lidocaine</mark> . 
<mark>Flurbiprofen</mark> in the treatment of juvenile rheumatoid arthritis . 
Thirty - four patients with juvenile rheumatoid arthritis , who were treated with <mark>flurbiprofen</mark> at a maximum dose of 4 mg / kg / day , had statistically significant decreases from baseline in 6 arthritis indices after 12 weeks of treatment . 
Improvements were seen in the number of tender joints , the severity of swelling and tenderness , the time of walk 50 feet , the duration of morning stiffness and the circumference of the left knee . 
The most frequently observed side effect was fecal occult blood ( 25 % of patients ) ; however , there was no other evidence of gastrointestinal ( GI ) bleeding in these patients . 
One patient was prematurely discontinued from the study for severe headache and abdominal pain . 
Most side effects were mild and related to the GI tract . 
Hyperkalemia associated with <mark>sulindac</mark> therapy . 
Hyperkalemia has recently been recognized as a complication of nonsteroidal antiinflammatory agents ( NSAID ) such as <mark>indomethacin</mark> . 
Several recent studies have stressed the renal sparing features of <mark>sulindac</mark> , owing to its lack of interference with renal <mark>prostacyclin</mark> synthesis . 
We describe 4 patients in whom hyperkalemia ranging from 6 . 1 to 6 . 9 mEq / l developed within 3 to 8 days of <mark>sulindac</mark> administration . 
In all of them normal serum <mark>potassium</mark> levels reached within 2 to 4 days of stopping <mark>sulindac</mark> . 
As no other medications known to effect serum <mark>potassium</mark> had been given concomitantly , this course of events is suggestive of a cause - and - effect relationship between <mark>sulindac</mark> and hyperkalemia . 
These observations indicate that initial hopes that <mark>sulindac</mark> may not be associated with the adverse renal effects of other NSAID are probably not justified . 
Drug - induced arterial spasm relieved by <mark>lidocaine</mark> . 
Case report . 
Following major intracranial surgery in a 35 - year - old man , <mark>sodium pentothal</mark> was intravenously infused to minimize cerebral ischaemia . 
Intense vasospasm with threatened gangrene arose in the arm used for the infusion . 
Since the cranial condition precluded use of more usual methods , <mark>lidocaine</mark> was given intra - arterially , with careful cardiovascular monitoring , to counteract the vasospasm . 
The treatment was rapidly successful . 
Regional localization of the antagonism of <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced hyperactivity by intracerebral <mark>calcitonin</mark> injections . 
<mark>Calcitonin</mark> receptors are found in the brain , and intracerebral infusions of <mark>calcitonin</mark> can produce behavioral effects . 
Among these behavioral effects are decreases in food intake and decreases in <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced locomotor activity . 
In previous experiments we found that decreases in food intake were induced by local administration of <mark>calcitonin</mark> into several hypothalamic sites and into the nucleus accumbens . 
In the present experiment <mark>calcitonin</mark> decreased locomotor activity when locally injected into the same sites where it decreases food intake . 
The areas where <mark>calcitonin</mark> is most effective in decreasing locomotor activity are located in the hypothalamus and nucleus accumbens , suggesting that these areas are the major sites of action of <mark>calcitonin</mark> in inhibiting <mark>amphetamine</mark> - induced locomotor activity . 
The hematologic effects of <mark>cefonicid</mark> and <mark>cefazedone</mark> in the dog : a potential model of <mark>cephalosporin</mark> hematotoxicity in man . 
<mark>Cephalosporin</mark> antibiotics cause a variety of hematologic disturbances in man , the pathogeneses and hematopathology of which remain poorly characterized . 
There is a need for a well - defined animal model in which these blood dyscrasias can be studied . 
In four subacute toxicity studies , the intravenous administration of <mark>cefonicid</mark> or <mark>cefazedone</mark> to beagle dogs caused a dose - dependent incidence of anemia , neutropenia , and thrombocytopenia after 1 - 3 months of treatment . 
A nonregenerative anemia was the most compromising of the cytopenias and occurred in approximately 50 % of dogs receiving 400 - 500 mg / kg <mark>cefonicid</mark> or 540 - 840 mg / kg <mark>cefazedone</mark> . 
All three cytopenias were completely reversible following cessation of treatment ; the time required for recovery of the erythron ( approximately 1 month ) was considerably longer than that of the granulocytes and platelets ( hours to a few days ) . 
Upon rechallenge with either <mark>cephalosporin</mark> , the hematologic syndrome was reproduced in most dogs tested ; <mark>cefonicid</mark> ( but not <mark>cefazedone</mark> ) - treated dogs showed a substantially reduced induction period ( 15 + / - 5 days ) compared to that of the first exposure to the drug ( 61 + / - 24 days ) . 
This observation , along with the rapid rate of decline in red cell mass parameters of affected dogs , suggests that a hemolytic component complicated the red cell production problem and that multiple toxicologic mechanisms contributed to the cytopenia . 
We conclude that the administration of high doses of <mark>cefonicid</mark> or <mark>cefazedone</mark> to dogs can induce hematotoxicity similar to the <mark>cephalosporin</mark> - induced blood dyscrasias described in man and thus provides a useful model for studying the mechanisms of these disorders . 
Cerebral blood flow and metabolism during <mark>isoflurane</mark> - induced hypotension in patients subjected to surgery for cerebral aneurysms . 
Cerebral blood flow and cerebral metabolic rate for <mark>oxygen</mark> were measured during <mark>isoflurane</mark> - induced hypotension in 10 patients subjected to craniotomy for clipping of a cerebral aneurysm . 
Flow and metabolism were measured 5 - 13 days after the subarachnoid haemorrhage by a modification of the classical Kety - Schmidt technique using <mark>xenon</mark> - 133 i . v . Anaesthesia was maintained with an inspired <mark>isoflurane</mark> concentration of 0 . 75 % ( plus 67 % <mark>nitrous oxide</mark> in <mark>oxygen</mark> ) , during which CBF and CMRO2 were 34 . 3 + / - 2 . 1 ml / 100 g min - 1 and 2 . 32 + / - 0 . 16 ml / 100 g min - 1 at PaCO2 4 . 1 + / - 0 . 1 kPa ( mean + / - SEM ) . 
Controlled hypotension to an average MAP of 50 - 55 mm <mark>Hg</mark> was induced by increasing the dose of <mark>isoflurane</mark> , and maintained at an inspired concentration of 2 . 2 + / - 0 . 2 % . 
This resulted in a significant decrease in CMRO2 ( to 1 . 73 + / - 0 . 16 ml / 100 g min - 1 ) , while CBF was unchanged . 
After the clipping of the aneurysm the <mark>isoflurane</mark> concentration was reduced to 0 . 75 % . 
There was a significant increase in CBF , although CMRO2 was unchanged , compared with pre - hypotensive values . 
These changes might offer protection to brain tissue during periods of induced hypotension . 
<mark>Triazolam</mark> - induced brief episodes of secondary mania in a depressed patient . 
Large doses of <mark>triazolam</mark> repeatedly induced brief episodes of mania in a depressed elderly woman . 
Features of organic mental disorder ( delirium ) were not present . 
Manic excitement was coincident with the duration of action of <mark>triazolam</mark> . 
The possible contribution of the <mark>triazolo</mark> group to changes in affective status is discussed . 
The correlation between neurotoxic esterase inhibition and <mark>mipafox</mark> - induced neuropathic damage in rats . 
The correlation between neuropathic damage and inhibition of neurotoxic esterase or neuropathy target enzyme ( NTE ) was examined in rats acutely exposed to <mark>Mipafox</mark> ( <mark>N , N ' - diisopropylphosphorodiamidofluoridate</mark> ) , a neurotoxic <mark>organophosphate</mark> . 
Brain and spinal cord NTE activities were measured in Long - Evans male rats 1 hr post - exposure to various dosages of <mark>Mipafox</mark> ( ip , 1 - 15 mg / kg ) . 
These data were correlated with histologically scored cervical cord damage in a separate group of similarly dosed rats sampled 14 - 21 days post - exposure . 
Those dosages ( greater than or equal to 10 mg / kg ) that inhibited mean NTE activity in the spinal cord greater than or equal to 73 % and brain greater than or equal to 67 % of control values produced severe ( greater than or equal to 3 ) cervical cord pathology in 85 % of the rats . 
In contrast , dosages of <mark>Mipafox</mark> ( less than or equal to 5 mg / kg ) which inhibited mean NTE activity in spinal cord less than or equal to 61 % and brain less than or equal to 60 % produced this degree of cord damage in only 9 % of the animals . 
These data indicate that a critical percentage of NTE inhibition in brain and spinal cord sampled shortly after <mark>Mipafox</mark> exposure can predict neuropathic damage in rats several weeks later . 
Allergic reaction to <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> infusion . 
An allergic reaction consisting of angioneurotic edema secondary to continuous infusion <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> occurred in a patient with recurrent carcinoma of the oral cavity , cirrhosis , and <mark>cisplatin</mark> - induced impaired renal function . 
This reaction occurred during the sixth and seventh courses of infusional chemotherapy . 
Oral <mark>diphenhydramine</mark> and <mark>prednisone</mark> were ineffective in preventing the recurrence of the allergic reaction . 
Discontinuance of effective chemotherapy in this patient during partial remission resulted in fatal disease progression . 
Myasthenia gravis caused by <mark>penicillamine</mark> and <mark>chloroquine</mark> therapy for rheumatoid arthritis . 
We have described a unique patient who had reversible and dose - related myasthenia gravis after <mark>penicillamine</mark> and <mark>chloroquine</mark> therapy for rheumatoid arthritis . 
Although <mark>acetylcholine</mark> receptor antibodies were not detectable , the time course was consistent with an autoimmune process . 
On the mechanisms of the development of tolerance to the muscular rigidity produced by <mark>morphine</mark> in rats . 
The development of tolerance to the muscular rigidity produced by <mark>morphine</mark> was studied in rats . 
Saline - pretreated controls given a test dose of <mark>morphine</mark> ( 20 mg / kg i . p . ) showed a pronounced rigidity recorded as tonic activity in the electromyogram . 
Rats treated for 11 days with <mark>morphine</mark> and withdrawn for 36 - 40 h showed differences in the development of tolerance : about half of the animals showed a rigidity after the test dose of <mark>morphine</mark> that was not significantly less than in the controls and were akinetic ( A group ) . 
The other rats showed a strong decrease in the rigidity and the occurrence of stereotyped ( S ) licking and / or gnawing in presence of akinetic or hyperkinetic ( K ) behaviour ( AS / KS group ) , suggesting signs of dopaminergic activation . 
The rigidity was considerably decreased in both groups after 20 days ' treatment . 
In a further series of experiments , <mark>haloperidol</mark> ( 0 . 2 mg / kg i . p . ) was used in order to block the dopaminergic activation and to estimate the real degree of the tolerance to the rigidity without any dopaminergic interference . 
<mark>Haloperidol</mark> enhanced the rigidity in the A group . 
However , the level in the AS / KS group remained considerably lower than in the A group . 
The results suggest that rigidity , which is assumed to be due to an action of <mark>morphine</mark> in the striatum , can be antagonized by another process leading to dopaminergic activation in the striatum . 
Nevertheless , there occurs some real tolerance to this effect . 
The rapid alternations of rigidity and the signs of dopaminergic activation observed in the animals of the AS / KS group might be due to rapid shifts in the predominance of various DA - innervated structures . 
A case of massive rhabdomyolysis following <mark>molindone</mark> administration . 
Rhabdomyolysis is a potentially lethal syndrome that psychiatric patients seem predisposed to develop . 
The clinical signs and symptoms , typical laboratory features , and complications of rhabdomyolysis are presented . 
The case of a schizophrenic patient is reported to illustrate massive rhabdomyolysis and subsequent acute renal failure following <mark>molindone</mark> administration . 
Physicians who prescribe <mark>molindone</mark> should be aware of this reaction . 
Compression neuropathy of the radial nerve due to <mark>pentazocine</mark> - induced fibrous myopathy . 
Fibrous myopathy is a common , well - known side effect of repeated <mark>pentazocine</mark> injection . 
However , compression neuropathy due to fibrotic muscle affected by <mark>pentazocine</mark> - induced myopathy has not previously been reported . 
In a 37 - year - old woman with documented <mark>pentazocine</mark> - induced fibrous myopathy of triceps and deltoid muscles bilaterally and a three - week history of right wrist drop , electrodiagnostic examination showed a severe but partial lesion of the right radial nerve distal to the branches to the triceps , in addition to the fibrous myopathy . 
Surgery revealed the right radial nerve to be severely compressed by the densely fibrotic lateral head of the triceps . 
Decompression and neurolysis were performed with good subsequent recovery of function . 
Recurrent reversible acute renal failure from <mark>amphotericin</mark> . 
A patient with cryptogenic cirrhosis and disseminated sporotrichosis developed acute renal failure immediately following the administration of <mark>amphotericin B</mark> on four separate occasions . 
The abruptness of the renal failure and its reversibility within days suggests that there was a functional component to the renal dysfunction . 
We propose that <mark>amphotericin</mark> , in the setting of reduced effective arterial volume , may activate tubuloglomerular feedback , thereby contributing to acute renal failure . 
Cerebral infarction with a single oral dose of <mark>phenylpropanolamine</mark> . 
<mark>Phenylpropanolamine</mark> ( <mark>PPA</mark> ) , a synthetic sympathomimetic that is structurally similar to <mark>amphetamine</mark> , is available over the counter in anorectics , nasal congestants , and cold preparations . 
Its prolonged use or overuse has been associated with seizures , intracerebral hemorrhage , neuropsychiatric symptoms , and nonhemorrhagic cerebral infarction . 
We report the case of a young woman who suffered a cerebral infarction after taking a single oral dose of <mark>PPA</mark> . 
Remission induction of meningeal leukemia with high - dose intravenous <mark>methotrexate</mark> . 
Twenty children with acute lymphoblastic leukemia who developed meningeal disease were treated with a high - dose intravenous <mark>methotrexate</mark> regimen that was designed to achieve and maintain CSF <mark>methotrexate</mark> concentrations of 10 ( - 5 ) mol / L without the need for concomitant intrathecal dosing . 
The <mark>methotrexate</mark> was administered as a loading dose of 6 , 000 mg / m2 for a period of one hour followed by an infusion of 1 , 200 mg / m2 / h for 23 hours . 
<mark>Leucovorin</mark> rescue was initiated 12 hours after the end of the infusion with a loading dose of 200 mg / m2 followed by 12 mg / m2 every three hours for six doses and then every six hours until the plasma <mark>methotrexate</mark> level decreased to less than 1 X 10 ( - 7 ) mol / L . 
The mean steady - state plasma and CSF <mark>methotrexate</mark> concentrations achieved were 1 . 1 X 10 ( - 3 ) mol / L and 3 . 6 X 10 ( - 5 ) mol / L , respectively . 
All 20 patients responded to this regimen , 16 / 20 ( 80 % ) achieved a complete remission , and 20 % obtained a partial remission . 
The most common toxicities encountered were transient serum transaminase and <mark>bilirubin</mark> elevations , neutropenia , and mucositis . 
One patient had focal seizures and transient hemiparesis but recovered completely . 
High - dose intravenous <mark>methotrexate</mark> is an effective treatment for the induction of remission after meningeal relapse in acute lymphoblastic leukemia . 
Interaction of <mark>cyclosporin A</mark> with antineoplastic agents . 
A synergistic effect of <mark>etoposide</mark> and <mark>cyclosporin A</mark> was observed in a patient with acute T - lymphocytic leukemia in relapse . 
The concomitant administration of <mark>etoposide</mark> and <mark>cyclosporin A</mark> resulted in eradication of hitherto refractory leukemic infiltration of bone marrow . 
Severe side effects in terms of mental confusion and progressive hyperbilirubinemia , however , point to an enhancement not only of antineoplastic effects but also of toxicity in normal tissues . 
This report demonstrates for the first time that the pharmacodynamic properties of <mark>cyclosporin A</mark> may not be confined strictly to suppression of normal T - cell functions . 
Incidence of neoplasms in patients with rheumatoid arthritis exposed to different treatment regimens . 
Immunosuppressive drugs have been used during the last 30 years in treatment of patients with severe rheumatoid arthritis . 
The drugs commonly used are <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> and <mark>chlorambucil</mark> ( <mark>alkylating agents</mark> ) , <mark>azathioprine</mark> ( <mark>purine</mark> analogue ) , and <mark>methotrexate</mark> ( <mark>folic acid</mark> analogue ) . 
There is evidence that all four immunosuppressive drugs can reduce synovitis , but disease activity almost always recurs after therapy is stopped . 
Since adverse reactions are frequent , less than 50 percent of patients are able to continue a particular drug for more than one year . 
Since it takes three to 12 months to achieve maximal effects , those patients who are unable to continue the drug receive little benefit from it . 
Patients treated with <mark>alkylating agents</mark> have an increased risk of development of acute nonlymphocytic leukemia , and both <mark>alkylating agents</mark> and <mark>azathioprine</mark> are associated with the development of non - Hodgkin ' s lymphoma . 
<mark>Cyclophosphamide</mark> therapy increases the risk of carcinoma of the bladder . 
There have been several long - term studies of patients with rheumatoid arthritis treated with <mark>azathioprine</mark> and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> and the incidence of most of the common cancers is not increased . 
Data on the possible increased risk of malignancy in rheumatoid arthritis are still being collected , and until further information is available , the use of immunosuppressive drugs , particularly <mark>alkylating agents</mark> , in the treatment of rheumatoid arthritis should be reserved for patients with severe progressive disease or life - threatening complications . 
<mark>Warfarin</mark> - induced iliopsoas hemorrhage with subsequent femoral nerve palsy . 
We present the case of a 28 - year - old man on chronic <mark>warfarin</mark> therapy who sustained a minor muscle tear and developed increasing pain and a flexure contracture of the right hip . 
Surgical exploration revealed an iliopsoas hematoma and femoral nerve entrapment , resulting in a femoral nerve palsy and partial loss of quadriceps functions . 
Anticoagulant - induced femoral nerve palsy represents the most common form of <mark>warfarin</mark> - induced peripheral neuropathy ; it is characterized by severe pain in the inguinal region , varying degrees of motor and sensory impairment , and flexure contracture of the involved extremity . 
Pneumonitis with pleural and pericardial effusion and neuropathy during <mark>amiodarone</mark> therapy . 
A patient with sinuatrial disease and implanted pacemaker was treated with <mark>amiodarone</mark> ( maximum dose 1000 mg , maintenance dose 800 mg daily ) for 10 months , for control of supraventricular tachyarrhythmias . 
He developed pneumonitis , pleural and pericardial effusions , and a predominantly proximal motor neuropathy . 
Immediate but gradual improvement followed withdrawal of <mark>amiodarone</mark> and treatment with <mark>prednisolone</mark> . 
Review of this and previously reported cases indicates the need for early diagnosis of <mark>amiodarone</mark> pneumonitis , immediate withdrawal of <mark>amiodarone</mark> , and prompt but continued <mark>steroid</mark> therapy to ensure full recovery . 
<mark>Amiodarone</mark> - induced sinoatrial block . 
We observed sinoatrial block due to chronic <mark>amiodarone</mark> administration in a 5 - year - old boy with primary cardiomyopathy , Wolff - Parkinson - White syndrome and supraventricular tachycardia . 
Reduction in the dosage of <mark>amiodarone</mark> resulted in the disappearance of the sinoatrial block and the persistence of asymptomatic sinus bradycardia . 
<mark>Desipramine</mark> - induced delirium at " subtherapeutic " concentrations : a case report . 
An elderly patient treated with low dose <mark>Desipramine</mark> developed a delirium while her plasma level was in the " subtherapeutic " range . 
Delirium , which may be induced by tricyclic drug therapy in the elderly , can be caused by tricyclics with low anticholinergic potency . 
Therapeutic ranges for <mark>antidepressants</mark> that have been derived from general adult population studies may not be appropriate for the elderly . 
Further studies of specifically elderly patients are now required to establish safer and more appropriate guidelines for drug therapy . 
<mark>Indomethacin</mark> - induced renal insufficiency : recurrence on rechallenge . 
We have reported a case of acute oliguric renal failure with hyperkalemia in a patient with cirrhosis , ascites , and cor pulmonale after <mark>indomethacin</mark> therapy . 
Prompt restoration of renal function followed drug withdrawal , while re - exposure to a single dose of <mark>indomethacin</mark> caused recurrence of acute reversible oliguria . 
Our case supports the hypothesis that endogenous renal <mark>prostaglandins</mark> play a role in the maintenance of renal blood flow when circulating plasma volume is diminished . 
Since nonsteroidal anti - inflammatory agents interfere with this compensatory mechanism and may cause acute renal failure , they should be used with caution in such patients . 
Patterns of hepatic injury induced by <mark>methyldopa</mark> . 
Twelve patients with liver disease related to <mark>methyldopa</mark> were seen between 1967 and 1977 . 
Illness occurred within 1 - - 9 weeks of commencement of therapy in 9 patients , the remaining 3 patients having received the drug for 13 months , 15 months and 7 years before experiencing symptoms . 
Jaundice with tender hepatomegaly , usually preceded by symptoms of malaise , anorexia , nausea and vomiting , and associated with upper abdominal pain , was an invariable finding in all patients . 
Biochemical liver function tests indicated hepatocellular necrosis and correlated with histopathological evidence of hepatic injury , the spectrum of which ranged from fatty change and focal hepatocellular necrosis to massive hepatic necrosis . 
Most patients showed moderate to severe acute hepatitis or chronic active hepatitis with associated cholestasis . 
The drug was withdrawn on presentation to hospital in 11 patients , with rapid clinical improvement in 9 . 
One patient died , having presented in hepatic failure , and another , who had been taking <mark>methyldopa</mark> for 7 years , showed slower clinical and biochemical resolution over a period of several months . 
The remaining patient in the series developed fulminant hepatitis when the drug was accidentally recommenced 1 year after a prior episode of <mark>methyldopa</mark> - induced hepatitis . 
In this latter patient , and in 2 others , the causal relationship between <mark>methyldopa</mark> and hepatic dysfunction was proved with the recurrence of hepatitis within 2 weeks of re - exposure to the drug . 
<mark>Suxamethonium</mark> infusion rate and observed fasciculations . 
A dose - response study . 
<mark>Suxamethonium chloride</mark> ( <mark>Sch</mark> ) was administered i . v . to 36 adult males at six rates : 0 . 25 mg s - 1 to 20 mg s - 1 . 
The infusion was discontinued either when there was no muscular response to tetanic stimulation of the ulnar nerve or when <mark>Sch</mark> 120 mg was exceeded . 
Six additional patients received a 30 - mg i . v . bolus dose . 
Fasciculations in six areas of the body were scored from 0 to 3 and summated as a total fasciculation score . 
The times to first fasciculation , twitch suppression and tetanus suppression were inversely related to the infusion rates . 
Fasciculations in the six areas and the total fasciculation score were related directly to the rate of infusion . 
Total fasciculation scores in the 30 - mg bolus group and the 5 - mg s - 1 and 20 - mg s - 1 infusion groups were not significantly different . 
Treatment of psoriasis with <mark>azathioprine</mark> . 
<mark>Azathioprine</mark> treatment benefited 19 ( 66 % ) out of 29 patients suffering from severe psoriasis . 
Haematological complications were not troublesome and results of biochemical liver function tests remained normal . 
Minimal cholestasis was seen in two cases and portal fibrosis of a reversible degree in eight . 
Liver biopsies should be undertaken at regular intervals if <mark>azathioprine</mark> therapy is continued so that structural liver damage may be detected at an early and reversible stage . 
Angiosarcoma of the liver associated with <mark>diethylstilbestrol</mark> . 
Angiosarcoma of the liver occurred in a 76 - year - old man who had been treated for a well - differentiated adenocarcinoma of the liver with <mark>diethylstilbestrol</mark> for 13 years . 
Angiosarcoma was also present within pulmonary and renal arteries . 
The possibility that the intraarterial lesions might represent independent primary tumors is considered . 
<mark>Galanthamine hydrobromide</mark> , a longer acting anticholinesterase drug , in the treatment of the central effects of <mark>scopolamine</mark> ( <mark>Hyoscine</mark> ) . 
<mark>Galanthamine hydrobromide</mark> , an anticholinesterase drug capable of penetrating the blood - brain barrier , was used in a patient demonstrating central effects of <mark>scopolamine</mark> ( <mark>hyoscine</mark> ) overdosage . 
It is longer acting than <mark>physostigmine</mark> and is used in anaesthesia to reverse the non - depolarizing neuromuscular block . 
However , studies into the dose necessary to combating <mark>scopolamine</mark> intoxication are indicated . 
Comparison of the subjective effects and plasma concentrations following oral and i . m . administration of <mark>flunitrazepam</mark> in volunteers . 
<mark>Flunitrazepam</mark> 0 . 5 , 1 . 0 or 2 . 0 mg was given by the oral or i . m . routes to groups of volunteers and its effects compared . 
Plasma concentrations of the drug were estimated by gas - liquid chromatography , in a smaller number of the subjects . 
The most striking effect was sedation which increased with the dose , 2 mg producing deep sleep although the subjects could still be aroused . 
The effects of i . m . administration were apparent earlier and sometimes lasted longer than those following oral administration . 
Dizziness was less marked than sedation , but increased with the dose . 
There was pain on i . m . injection of <mark>flunitrazepam</mark> significantly more often than with isotonic saline . 
Plasma concentrations varied with dose and route and corresponded qualitatively with the subjective effects . 
The drug was still present in measurable quantities after 24 h even with the smallest dose . 
Possible teratogenicity of <mark>sulphasalazine</mark> . 
Three infants , born of two mothers with inflammatory bowel disease who received treatment with <mark>sulphasalazine</mark> throughout pregnancy , were found to have major congenital anomalies . 
In the singleton pregnancy , the mother had ulcerative colitis , and the infant , a male , had coarctation of the aorta and a ventricular septal defect . 
In the twin pregnancy , the mother had Crohn ' s disease . 
The first twin , a female , had a left Potter - type IIa polycystic kidney and a rudimentary left uterine cornu . 
The second twin , a male , had some features of Potter ' s facies , hypoplastic lungs , absent kidneys and ureters , and talipes equinovarus . 
Despite reports to the contrary , it is suggested that <mark>sulphasalazine</mark> may be teratogenic . 
Thrombotic microangiopathy and renal failure associated with antineoplastic chemotherapy . 
Five patients with carcinoma developed thrombotic microangiopathy ( characterized by renal insufficiency , microangiopathic hemolytic anemia , and usually thrombocytopenia ) after treatment with <mark>cisplatin</mark> , <mark>bleomycin</mark> , and a <mark>vinca alkaloid</mark> . 
One patient had thrombotic thrombocytopenic purpura , three the hemolytic - uremic syndrome , and one an apparent forme fruste of one of these disorders . 
Histologic examination of the renal tissue showed evidence of intravascular coagulation , primarily affecting the small arteries , arterioles , and glomeruli . 
Because each patient was tumor - free or had only a small tumor at the onset of this syndrome , the thrombotic microangiopathy may have been induced by chemotherapy . 
Diagnosis of this potentially fatal complication may be delayed or missed if renal tissue or the peripheral blood smear is not examined , because renal failure may be ascribed to <mark>cisplatin</mark> nephrotoxicity and the anemia and thrombocytopenia to drug - induced bone marrow suppression . 
International <mark>mexiletine</mark> and placebo antiarrhythmic coronary trial : I . 
Report on arrhythmia and other findings . 
Impact Research Group . 
The antiarrhythmic effects of the sustained release form of <mark>mexiletine</mark> ( <mark>Mexitil - Perlongets</mark> ) were evaluated in a double - blind placebo trial in 630 patients with recent documented myocardial infarction . 
The primary response variable was based on central reading of 24 hour ambulatory electrocardiographic recordings and was defined as the occurrence of 30 or more single premature ventricular complexes in any two consecutive 30 minute blocks or one or more runs of two or more premature ventricular complexes in the entire 24 hour electrocardiographic recording . 
Large differences , regarded as statistically significant , between the <mark>mexiletine</mark> and placebo groups were noted in that end point at months 1 and 4 , but only trends were observed at month 12 . 
These differences were observed even though the serum <mark>mexiletine</mark> levels obtained in this study were generally lower than those observed in studies that have used the regular form of the drug . 
There were more deaths in the <mark>mexiletine</mark> group ( 7 . 6 % ) than in the placebo group ( 4 . 8 % ) ; the difference was not statistically significant . 
The incidence of coronary events was similar in both groups . 
Previously recognized side effects , particularly tremor and gastrointestinal problems , were more frequent in the <mark>mexiletine</mark> group than in the placebo group . 
Changes in heart size during long - term <mark>timolol</mark> treatment after myocardial infarction . 
The effect of long - term <mark>timolol</mark> treatment on heart size after myocardial infarction was evaluated by X - ray in a double - blind study including 241 patients ( placebo 126 , <mark>timolol</mark> 115 ) . 
The follow - up period was 12 months . 
The <mark>timolol</mark> - treated patients showed a small but significant increase in heart size from baseline in contrast to a decrease in the placebo group . 
These differences may be caused by <mark>timolol</mark> - induced bradycardia and a compensatory increase in end - diastolic volume . 
The <mark>timolol</mark> - related increase in heart size was observed only in patients with normal and borderline heart size . 
In patients with cardiomegaly , the increase in heart size was similar in both groups . 
After re - infarction , heart size increased in the placebo group and remained unchanged in the <mark>timolol</mark> group . 
<mark>Vitamin D3</mark> toxicity in dairy cows . 
Large parenteral doses of <mark>vitamin D3</mark> ( 15 to 17 . 5 x 10 ( 6 ) IU <mark>vitamin D3</mark> ) were associated with prolonged hypercalcemia , hyperphosphatemia , and large increases of <mark>vitamin D3</mark> and its metabolites in the blood plasma of nonlactating nonpregnant and pregnant Jersey cows . 
<mark>Calcium</mark> concentrations 1 day postpartum were higher in cows treated with <mark>vitamin D3</mark> about 32 days prepartum ( 8 . 8 mg / 100 ml ) than in control cows ( 5 . 5 mg / 100 ml ) . 
None of the cows treated with <mark>vitamin D3</mark> showed signs of milk fever during the peripartal period ; however , 22 % of the control cows developed clinical signs of milk fever during this period . 
Signs of <mark>vitamin D3</mark> toxicity were not observed in nonlactating nonpregnant cows ; however , pregnant cows commonly developed severe signs of <mark>vitamin D3</mark> toxicity and 10 of 17 cows died . 
There was widespread metastatic calcification in the cows that died . 
Because of the extreme toxicity of <mark>vitamin D3</mark> in pregnant Jersey cows and the low margin of safety between doses of <mark>vitamin D3</mark> that prevent milk fever and doses that induce milk fever , we concluded that <mark>vitamin D3</mark> cannot be used practically to prevent milk fever when injected several weeks prepartum . 
Diseases of peripheral nerves as seen in the Nigerian African . 
The anatomical and aetiological diagnoses of peripheral nerve disease excluding its primary benign and malignant disorders , as seen in 358 Nigerians are presented . 
There is a male preponderance and the peak incidence is in the fourth decade . 
Sensori - motor neuropathy was the commonest presentation ( 50 % ) . 
Guillain - Barr syndrome was the commonest identifiable cause ( 15 . 6 % ) , accounting for half of the cases with motor neuropathy . 
Peripheral neuropathy due to nutritional deficiency of <mark>thiamine</mark> and <mark>riboflavin</mark> was common ( 10 . 1 % ) and presented mainly as sensory and sensori - motor neuropathy . 
Diabetes mellitus was the major cause of autonomic neuropathy . 
<mark>Isoniazid</mark> was the most frequent agent in drug - induced neuropathy . 
Migraine ( 20 % ) was not an uncommon cause of cranial neuropathy although malignancies arising from the reticuloendothelial system or related structures of the head and neck were more frequent ( 26 % ) . 
In 26 . 5 % of all the cases , the aetiology of the neuropathy was undetermined . 
Heredofamilial and connective tissue disorders were rare . 
Some of the factors related to the clinical presentation and pathogenesis of the neuropathies are briefly discussed . 
Reduction in <mark>caffeine</mark> toxicity by <mark>acetaminophen</mark> . 
A patient who allegedly consumed 100 tablets of an over - the - counter analgesic containing <mark>sodium acetylsalicylate</mark> , <mark>caffeine</mark> , and <mark>acetaminophen</mark> displayed no significant CNS stimulation despite the presence of 175 micrograms of <mark>caffeine</mark> per mL of serum . 
Because salicylates have been reported to augment the stimulatory effects of <mark>caffeine</mark> on the CNS , attention was focused on the possibility that the presence of <mark>acetaminophen</mark> ( 52 micrograms / mL ) reduced the CNS toxicity of <mark>caffeine</mark> . 
Studies in DBA / 2J mice showed that : 1 ) pretreatment with <mark>acetaminophen</mark> ( 100 mg / kg ) increased the interval between the administration of <mark>caffeine</mark> ( 300 to 450 mg / kg IP ) and the onset of fatal convulsions by a factor of about two ; and 2 ) pretreatment with <mark>acetaminophen</mark> ( 75 mg / kg ) reduced the incidence of audiogenic seizures produced in the presence of <mark>caffeine</mark> ( 12 . 5 to 75 mg / kg IP ) . 
The frequency of sound - induced seizures after 12 . 5 or 25 mg / kg <mark>caffeine</mark> was reduced from 50 to 5 % by <mark>acetaminophen</mark> . 
In the absence of <mark>caffeine</mark> , <mark>acetaminophen</mark> ( up to 300 mg / kg ) did not modify the seizures induced by maximal electroshock and did not alter the convulsant dose of <mark>pentylenetetrezol</mark> in mice ( tests performed by the Anticonvulsant Screening Project of NINCDS ) . 
<mark>Acetaminophen</mark> ( up to 150 micrograms / mL ) did not retard the incorporation of radioactive <mark>adenosine</mark> into <mark>ATP</mark> in slices of rat cerebral cortex . 
Thus the mechanism by which <mark>acetaminophen</mark> antagonizes the actions of <mark>caffeine</mark> in the CNS remains unknown . 
A double - blind study of the efficacy and safety of <mark>dothiepin hydrochloride</mark> in the treatment of major depressive disorder . 
In a 6 - week double - blind parallel treatment study , <mark>dothiepin</mark> and <mark>amitriptyline</mark> were compared to placebo in the treatment of 33 depressed outpatients . 
<mark>Dothiepin</mark> and <mark>amitriptyline</mark> were equally effective in alleviating the symptoms of depressive illness , and both were significantly superior to placebo . 
The overall incidence of side effects and the frequency and severity of blurred vision , dry mouth , and drowsiness were significantly less with <mark>dothiepin</mark> than with <mark>amitriptyline</mark> . 
<mark>Dothiepin</mark> also produced fewer CNS and cardiovascular effects . 
There were no clinically important changes in laboratory parameters . 
<mark>Dothiepin</mark> thus was found to be an effective <mark>antidepressant</mark> drug associated with fewer side effects than <mark>amitriptyline</mark> in the treatment of depressed outpatients . 
Behavioral effects of <mark>diazepam</mark> and <mark>propranolol</mark> in patients with panic disorder and agoraphobia . 
The effects of oral doses of <mark>diazepam</mark> ( single dose of 10 mg and a median dose of 30 mg / day for 2 weeks ) and <mark>propranolol</mark> ( single dose of 80 mg and a median dose of 240 mg / day for 2 weeks ) on psychological performance of patients with panic disorders and agoraphobia were investigated in a double - blind , randomized and crossover design . 
Both drugs impaired immediate free recall but the decrease was greater for <mark>diazepam</mark> than <mark>propranolol</mark> . 
Delayed free recall was also impaired but the two drugs did not differ . 
Patients tapped faster after <mark>propranolol</mark> than <mark>diazepam</mark> and they were more sedated after <mark>diazepam</mark> than <mark>propranolol</mark> . 
After 2 weeks of treatment , patients tested 5 - 8 h after the last dose of medication did not show any decrement of performance . 
These results are similar to those previously found in healthy subjects . 
Accumulation of drugs was not reflected in prolonged behavioral impairment . 
Comparison of i . v . <mark>glycopyrrolate</mark> and <mark>atropine</mark> in the prevention of bradycardia and arrhythmias following repeated doses of <mark>suxamethonium</mark> in children . 
The effectiveness of administration of <mark>glycopyrrolate</mark> 5 and 10 micrograms kg - 1 and <mark>atropine</mark> 10 and 20 micrograms kg - 1 i . v . immediately before the induction of anaesthesia , to prevent arrhythmia and bradycardia following repeated doses of <mark>suxamethonium</mark> in children , was studied . 
A control group was included for comparison with the lower dose range of <mark>glycopyrrolate</mark> and <mark>atropine</mark> . 
A frequency of bradycardia of 50 % was noted in the control group , but this was not significantly different from the frequency with the active drugs . 
Bradycardia ( defined as a decrease in heart rate to less than 50 beat min - 1 ) was prevented when the larger dose of either active drug was used . 
It is recommended that either <mark>glycopyrrolate</mark> 10 micrograms kg - 1 or <mark>atropine</mark> 20 micrograms kg - 1 i . v . should immediately precede induction of anaesthesia , in children , if the repeated administration of <mark>suxamethonium</mark> is anticipated . 
Veno - occlusive liver disease after <mark>dacarbazine</mark> therapy ( <mark>DTIC</mark> ) for melanoma . 
A case of veno - occlusive disease of the liver with fatal outcome after <mark>dacarbazine</mark> ( <mark>DTIC</mark> ) therapy for melanoma is reported . 
There was a fulminant clinical course from start of symptoms until death . 
At autopsy the liver was enlarged and firm with signs of venous congestion . 
Small - and medium - sized hepatic veins were blocked by thrombosis . 
Eosinophilic infiltrations were found around the vessels . 
Published cases from the literature are reviewed and pertinent features discussed . 
Maternal <mark>lithium</mark> and neonatal Ebstein ' s anomaly : evaluation with cross - sectional echocardiography . 
Cross - sectional echocardiography was used to evaluate two neonates whose mothers ingested <mark>lithium</mark> during pregnancy . 
In one infant , Ebstein ' s anomaly of the tricuspid valve was identified . 
In the other infant cross - sectional echocardiography provided reassurance that the infant did not have Ebstein ' s anomaly . 
Cross - sectional echocardiographic screening of newborns exposed to <mark>lithium</mark> during gestation can provide highly accurate , noninvasive assessment of the presence or absence of <mark>lithium</mark> - induced cardiac malformations . 
Effects of training on the extent of experimental myocardial infarction in aging rats . 
The effects of exercise on the severity of <mark>isoproterenol</mark> - induced myocardial infarction were studied in female albino rats of 20 , 40 , 60 and 80 weeks of age . 
The rats were trained to swim for a specific duration and for a particular period . 
The occurrence of infarcts were confirmed by histological methods . 
Elevations in the serum GOT and GPT were maximum in the sedentary - <mark>isoproterenols</mark> and minimum in the exercise - controls . 
These changes in the serum transaminases were associated with corresponding depletions in the cardiac GOT and GPT . 
However , age was seen to interfere with the responses exhibited by the young and old rats . 
Studies dealing with myocardial infarction are more informative when dealt with age . 
Effect of <mark>polyethylene glycol 400</mark> on <mark>adriamycin</mark> toxicity in mice . 
The effect of a widely used organic solvent , <mark>polyethylene glycol 400</mark> ( <mark>PEG 400</mark> ) , on the toxic action of an acute or chronic treatment with <mark>adriamycin</mark> ( <mark>ADR</mark> ) was evaluated in mice . 
<mark>PEG 400</mark> impressively decreased both acute high - dose and chronic low - dose - <mark>ADR</mark> - associated lethality . 
Light microscopic analysis showed a significant protection against <mark>ADR</mark> - induced cardiac morphological alterations . 
Such treatment did not diminish the <mark>ADR</mark> antitumor activity in L1210 leukemia and in Ehrlich ascites tumor . 
Sublingual absorption of the <mark>quaternary ammonium</mark> antiarrhythmic agent , <mark>UM - 272</mark> . 
<mark>UM - 272</mark> ( <mark>N , N - dimethylpropranolol</mark> ) , a quaternary antiarrhythmic agent , was administered sublingually to dogs with <mark>ouabain</mark> - induced ventricular tachycardias . 
Both anti - arrhythmic efficacy and bioavailability were compared to oral drug . 
Sublingual <mark>UM - 272</mark> converted ventricular tachycardia to sinus rhythm in all 5 dogs . 
The area under the plasma concentration time curve at 90 min was 4 - 12 times greater than for oral drug , suggesting the existence of an absorption - limiting process in the intestine , and providing an alternate form of administration for quaternary drugs . 
Early adjuvant <mark>adriamycin</mark> in superficial bladder carcinoma . 
A multicenter study was performed in 110 patients with superficial transitional cell carcinoma of the bladder . 
<mark>Adriamycin</mark> ( 50 mg / 50 ml ) was administered intravesically within 24 h after transurethral resection of TA - T1 ( O - A ) bladder tumors . 
Instillation was repeated twice during the first week , then weekly during the first month and afterwards monthly for 1 year . 
The tolerance was evaluated in these 110 patients , and 29 patients presented with local side - effects . 
In 24 of these patients chemical cystitis was severe enough for them to drop out of the study . 
No systemic side - effects were observed . 
Recurrence was studied in 82 evaluable patients after 1 year of follow - up and in 72 patients followed for 2 - 3 years ( mean 32 months ) . 
Of the 82 patients studied after 1 year , 23 had primary and 59 recurrent disease . 
Of the 82 evaluable patients , 50 did not show any recurrence after 1 year ( 61 % ) , while 32 presented with one or more recurrences ( 39 % ) . 
Of these recurrences , 27 were T1 tumors while five progressed to more highly invasive lesions . 
In patients that were free of recurrence during the first year , 80 % remained tumor - free during the 2 - to 3 - year follow - up period . 
Of the patients developing one or more recurrences during the first year , only 50 % presented with further recurrence once the instillations were stopped . 
The beneficial effect of <mark>Adriamycin</mark> appears obvious and might be related to the drug itself , the early and repeated instillations after TUR , or both . 
<mark>D - penicillamine</mark> - induced angiopathy in rats . 
The effect of high dose <mark>D - penicillamine</mark> treatment on aortic permeability to albumin and on the ultrastructure of the vessel . 
Male Sprague - Dawley rats were treated with <mark>D - penicillamine</mark> ( <mark>D - pen</mark> ) 500 mg / kg / day for 10 or 42 days . 
Pair fed rats served as controls . 
Changes in aortic morphology were examined by light - and transmission - electron microscopy ( TEM ) . 
In addition , the endothelial permeability and the penetration through the aortic wall of albumin were studied 10 minutes , 24 and 48 hours after i . v . injection of human serum 131I - albumin ( 131I - HSA ) . 
TEM revealed extensive elastolysis in the arterial wall of <mark>D - pen</mark> - treated rats , consistent with an inhibitory effect on crosslink formation . 
In experimental animals excess deposition of collagen and glycoaminoglycans was observed in the subendothelial and medial layer of the aortic wall , together with prominent basal membrane substance around aortic smooth muscle cells . 
The aorta / serum - ratio and the radioactive build - up 24 and 48 hours after injection of 131I - HSA was reduced in animals treated with <mark>D - pen</mark> for 42 days , indicating an impeded transmural transport of tracer which may be caused by a steric exclusion effect of abundant <mark>hyaluronate</mark> . 
The endothelial ultrastructure was unaffected by <mark>D - pen</mark> , and no differences in aortic 131I - HSA radioactivity or aorta / serum - ratio were recorded between experimental and control groups 10 minutes after tracer injection , indicating that the permeability of the endothelial barrier to albumin remained unaffected by <mark>D - pen</mark> treatment . 
These observations support the hypothesis that treatment with high doses of <mark>D - pen</mark> may induce a fibroproliferative response in rat aorta , possibly by an inhibitory effect on the cross - linking of collagen and elastin . 
Effect of <mark>aspirin</mark> on <mark>N - [ 4 - ( 5 - nitro - 2 - furyl ) - 2 - thiazolyl ] - formamide</mark> - induced epithelial proliferation in the urinary bladder and forestomach of the rat . 
The co - administration of <mark>aspirin</mark> with <mark>N - [ 4 - ( 5 - nitro - 2 - furyl ) - 2 - thiazolyl ] - formamide</mark> ( <mark>FANFT</mark> ) to rats resulted in a reduced incidence of <mark>FANFT</mark> - induced bladder carcinomas but a concomitant induction of forestomach tumors . 
An autoradiographic study was performed on male F - 344 rats fed diet containing <mark>FANFT</mark> at a level of 0 . 2 % and / or <mark>aspirin</mark> at a level of 0 . 5 % to evaluate the effect of <mark>aspirin</mark> on the increased cell proliferation induced by <mark>FANFT</mark> in the forestomach and bladder . 
<mark>FANFT</mark> - induced cell proliferation in the bladder was significantly suppressed by <mark>aspirin</mark> co - administration after 4 weeks but not after 12 weeks . 
In the forestomach , and also in the liver , <mark>aspirin</mark> did not affect the <mark>FANFT</mark> - induced increase in labeling index . 
The present results are consistent with the carcinogenicity experiment suggesting that different mechanisms are involved in <mark>FANFT</mark> carcinogenesis in the bladder and forestomach , and that <mark>aspirin</mark> ' s effect on <mark>FANFT</mark> in the forestomach is not due to an irritant effect associated with increased cell proliferation . 
Also , there appears to be an adaptation by the rats to the chronic ingestion of <mark>aspirin</mark> . 
A case of tardive dyskinesia caused by <mark>metoclopramide</mark> . 
Abnormal involuntary movements appeared in the mouth , tongue , neck and abdomen of a 64 - year - old male patient after he took <mark>metoclopramide</mark> for gastrointestinal disorder in a regimen of 30 mg per day for a total of about 260 days . 
The symptoms exacerbated to a maximum in a month . 
When the <mark>metoclopramide</mark> administration was discontinued , the abnormal movements gradually improved to a considerable extent . 
Attention to the possible induction of specific tardive dyskinesia is called for in the use of this drug . 
Intra - arterial <mark>BCNU</mark> chemotherapy for treatment of malignant gliomas of the central nervous system . 
Because of the rapid systemic clearance of <mark>BCNU</mark> ( <mark>1 , 3 - bis - ( 2 - chloroethyl ) - 1 - nitrosourea</mark> ) , intra - arterial administration should provide a substantial advantage over intravenous administration for the treatment of malignant gliomas . 
Thirty - six patients were treated with <mark>BCNU</mark> every 6 to 8 weeks , either by transfemoral catheterization of the internal carotid or vertebral artery or through a fully implantable intracarotid drug delivery system , beginning with a dose of 200 mg / sq m body surface area . 
Twelve patients with Grade III or IV astrocytomas were treated after partial resection of the tumor without prior radiation therapy . 
After two to seven cycles of chemotherapy , nine patients showed a decrease in tumor size and surrounding edema on contrast - enhanced computerized tomography scans . 
In the nine responders , median duration of chemotherapy response from the time of operation was 25 weeks ( range 12 to more than 91 weeks ) . 
The median duration of survival in the 12 patients was 54 weeks ( range 21 to more than 156 weeks ) , with an 18 - month survival rate of 42 % . 
Twenty - four patients with recurrent Grade I to IV astrocytomas , whose resection and irradiation therapy had failed , received two to eight courses of intra - arterial <mark>BCNU</mark> therapy . 
Seventeen of these had a response or were stable for a median of 20 weeks ( range 6 to more than 66 weeks ) . 
The catheterization procedure is safe , with no immediate complication in 111 infusions of <mark>BCNU</mark> . 
A delayed complication in nine patients has been unilateral loss of vision secondary to a retinal vasculitis . 
The frequency of visual loss decreased after the concentration of the <mark>ethanol</mark> diluent was lowered . 
Provocation of postural hypotension by <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> in diabetic autonomic neuropathy ? 
The effect of <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> on heart rate and systolic blood pressure was compared in 5 normal subjects , 12 diabetic subjects without autonomic neuropathy , and 5 diabetic subjects with autonomic neuropathy . 
The magnitude and time course of the increase in heart rate and the decrease in systolic blood pressure after <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> were similar in the normal and diabetic subjects without autonomic neuropathy , whereas a lesser increase in heart rate and a greater decrease in systolic blood pressure occurred in the diabetic subjects with autonomic neuropathy . 
It is therefore suggested that caution should be exercised when prescribing vasodilator drugs in diabetic patients , particularly those with autonomic neuropathy . 
Blood pressure response to chronic low - dose intrarenal <mark>noradrenaline</mark> infusion in conscious rats . 
<mark>Sodium chloride</mark> solution ( 0 . 9 % ) or <mark>noradrenaline</mark> in doses of 4 , 12 and 36 micrograms h - 1 kg - 1 was infused for five consecutive days , either intrarenally ( by a new technique ) or intravenously into rats with one kidney removed . 
Intrarenal infusion of <mark>noradrenaline</mark> caused hypertension at doses which did not do so when infused intravenously . 
Intrarenal compared with intravenous infusion of <mark>noradrenaline</mark> caused higher plasma <mark>noradrenaline</mark> concentrations and a shift of the plasma <mark>noradrenaline</mark> concentration - blood pressure effect curve towards lower plasma <mark>noradrenaline</mark> levels . 
These results suggest that hypertension after chronic intrarenal <mark>noradrenaline</mark> infusion is produced by relatively higher levels of circulating <mark>noradrenaline</mark> and by triggering of an additional intrarenal pressor mechanism . 
Characterization of <mark>estrogen</mark> - induced adenohypophyseal tumors in the Fischer 344 rat . 
Pituitary tumors were induced in F344 female rats by chronic treatment with <mark>diethylstilbestrol</mark> ( <mark>DES</mark> , 8 - 10 mg ) implanted subcutaneously in silastic capsules . 
Over a range of 1 - 150 days of <mark>DES</mark> treatment , pairs of control and <mark>DES</mark> - treated rats were sacrificed , and their pituitaries dissociated enzymatically into single - cell preparations . 
The cell populations were examined regarding total cell recovery correlated with gland weight , intracellular prolactin ( PRL ) content and subsequent release in primary culture , immunocytochemical PRL staining , density and / or size alterations via separation on Ficoll - Hypaque and by unit gravity sedimentation , and cell cycle analysis , after <mark>acriflavine</mark> DNA staining , by laser flow cytometry . 
Total cell yields from <mark>DES</mark> - treated pituitaries increased from 1 . 3 times control yields at 8 days of treatment to 58 . 9 times control values by day 150 . 
Intracellular PRL content ranged from 1 . 9 to 9 . 4 times control levels , and PRL release in vitro was significantly and consistently higher than controls , after at least 8 days of <mark>DES</mark> exposure . 
Beyond 8 days of <mark>DES</mark> exposure , the immunochemically PRL - positive proportion of cells increased to over 50 % of the total population . 
Increased density and / or size and PRL content were indicated for the majority of the PRL cell population in both types of separation protocols . 
All these effects of <mark>DES</mark> were more pronounced among previously ovariectomized animals . 
The data extend the findings of other investigators , further establishing the <mark>DES</mark> - induced tumor as a model for study of PRL cellular control mechanisms . 
Age and renal clearance of <mark>cimetidine</mark> . 
In 35 patients ( ages 20 to 86 yr ) receiving <mark>cimetidine</mark> therapeutically two serum samples and all urine formed in the interim were collected for analysis of <mark>cimetidine</mark> by high - pressure liquid chromatography and for <mark>creatinine</mark> . 
<mark>Cimetidine</mark> clearance decreased with age . 
The extrapolated 6 - hr serum concentration of <mark>cimetidine</mark> per unit dose , after intravenous <mark>cimetidine</mark> , increased with age of the patients . 
The ratio of <mark>cimetidine</mark> clearance to <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance ( Rc ) averaged 4 . 8 + / - 2 . 0 , indicating net tubular secretion for <mark>cimetidine</mark> . 
Rc seemed to be independent of age and decreased with increasing serum concentration of <mark>cimetidine</mark> , suggesting that secretion of <mark>cimetidine</mark> is a saturable process . 
There was only one case of dementia possibly due to <mark>cimetidine</mark> ( with a drug level of 1 . 9 microgram / ml 6 hr after a dose ) in a group of 13 patients without liver or kidney disease who had <mark>cimetidine</mark> levels above 1 . 25 microgram / ml . 
Thus , high <mark>cimetidine</mark> levels alone do not always induce dementia . 
Further observations on the electrophysiologic effects of oral <mark>amiodarone</mark> therapy . 
A case is presented of a reversible intra - Hisian block occurring under <mark>amiodarone</mark> treatment for atrial tachycardia in a patient without clear intraventricular conduction abnormalities . 
His bundle recordings showed an atrial tachycardia with intermittent exit block and greatly prolonged BH and HV intervals ( 40 and 100 msec , respectively ) . 
Thirty days after <mark>amiodarone</mark> discontinuation , His bundle electrograms showed atrial flutter without intra - Hisian or infra - Hisian delay . 
<mark>Amiodarone</mark> should be used with caution during long - term oral therapy in patients with or without clear intraventricular conduction defects . 
Development of clear cell adenocarcinoma in <mark>DES</mark> - exposed offspring under observation . 
Two cases of clear cell adenocarcinoma of the vagina detected at follow - up in young women exposed in utero to <mark>diethylstilbestrol</mark> are reported . 
One patient , aged 23 , had been followed for 2 years before carcinoma was diagnosed ; the second patient , aged 22 , had been seen on a regular basis for 5 years , 8 months . 
In both instances , suspicion of the presence of carcinoma was aroused by the palpation of a small nodule in the vaginal fornix . 
Hysterosalpingography was performed on both patients and , in 1 instance , an abnormal x - ray film was reflected by the gross appearance of the uterine cavity found in the surgical specimen . 
Neurologic effects of subarachnoid administration of <mark>2 - chloroprocaine - CE</mark> , <mark>bupivacaine</mark> , and low pH normal saline in dogs . 
The purpose of this study was to evaluate the neurologic consequences of deliberate subarachnoid injection of large volumes of <mark>2 - chloroprocaine - CE</mark> in experimental animals . 
The possible role of low pH as well as total volume as potential factors in causing neurotoxicity was evaluated . 
The 65 dogs in the study received injections in the subarachnoid space as follows : 6 to 8 ml of <mark>bupivacaine</mark> ( N = 15 ) , <mark>2 - chloroprocaine - CE</mark> ( N = 20 ) , low pH normal saline ( pH 3 . 0 ) ( N = 20 ) , or normal saline ( N = 10 ) . 
Of the 20 animals that received subarachnoid injection of <mark>2 - chloroprocaine - CE</mark> seven ( 35 % ) developed hind - limb paralysis . 
None of the animals that received <mark>bupivacaine</mark> , normal saline , or normal saline titrated to a pH 3 . 0 developed hind - limb paralysis . 
Of the 15 spinal cords of the animals that received <mark>2 - chloroprocaine - CE</mark> , 13 showed subpial necrosis ; the nerve roots and subarachnoid vessels were normal . 
The spinal cords of the animals that received <mark>bupivacaine</mark> , low pH normal saline ( pH 3 . 0 ) , or normal saline did not show abnormal findings . 
<mark>Procainamide</mark> - induced polymorphous ventricular tachycardia . 
Seven cases of <mark>procainamide</mark> - induced polymorphous ventricular tachycardia are presented . 
In four patients , polymorphous ventricular tachycardia appeared after intravenous administration of 200 to 400 mg of <mark>procainamide</mark> for the treatment of sustained ventricular tachycardia . 
In the remaining three patients , <mark>procainamide</mark> was administered orally for treatment of chronic premature ventricular contractions or atrial flutter . 
These patients had Q - T prolongation and recurrent syncope due to polymorphous ventricular tachycardia . 
In four patients , the arrhythmia was rapidly diagnosed and treated with disappearance of further episodes of the arrhythmia . 
In two patients , the arrhythmia degenerated into irreversible ventricular fibrillation and both patients died . 
In the seventh patient , a permanent ventricular pacemaker was inserted and , despite continuation of <mark>procainamide</mark> therapy , polymorphous ventricular tachycardia did not reoccur . 
These seven cases demonstrate that <mark>procainamide</mark> can produce an acquired prolonged Q - T syndrome with polymorphous ventricular tachycardia . 
<mark>Phenobarbitone</mark> - induced enlargement of the liver in the rat : its relationship to <mark>carbon tetrachloride</mark> - induced cirrhosis . 
The yield of severe cirrhosis of the liver ( defined as a shrunken finely nodular liver with micronodular histology , ascites greater than 30 ml , plasma albumin less than 2 . 2 g / dl , splenomegaly 2 - 3 times normal , and testicular atrophy approximately half normal weight ) after 12 doses of <mark>carbon tetrachloride</mark> given intragastrically in the <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> - primed rat was increased from 25 % to 56 % by giving the initial " calibrating " dose of <mark>carbon tetrachloride</mark> at the peak of the <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> - induced enlargement of the liver . 
At this point it was assumed that the cytochrome P450 / <mark>CCl4</mark> toxic state was both maximal and stable . 
The optimal rat size to begin <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> was determined as 100 g , and this size as a group had a mean maximum relative liver weight increase 47 % greater than normal rats of the same body weight . 
The optimal time for the initial dose of <mark>carbon tetrachloride</mark> was after 14 days on <mark>phenobarbitone</mark> . 
<mark>Triamterene</mark> nephrolithiasis complicating <mark>dyazide</mark> therapy . 
A case of <mark>triamterene</mark> nephrolithiasis is reported in a man after 4 years of <mark>hydrochlorothiazide - triamterene</mark> therapy for hypertension . 
The stone passed spontaneously and was found to contain a <mark>triamterene</mark> metabolite admixed with <mark>uric acid salts</mark> . 
Factors affecting <mark>triamterene</mark> nephrolithiasis are discussed and 2 previously reported cases are reviewed . 
<mark>Busulfan</mark> - induced hemorrhagic cystitis . 
A case of a <mark>busulfan</mark> - induced hemorrhage cystitis is reported . 
Spontaneous resolution occurred following cessation of the drug . 
The similarity between the histologic appearances of <mark>busulfan</mark> cystitis and both radiation and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> - induced cystitis is discussed and the world literature reviewed . 
In view of the known tendency of <mark>busulfan</mark> to induce cellular atypia and carcinoma in other sites , periodic urinary cytology is suggested in patients on long - term therapy . 
Variant ventricular tachycardia in <mark>desipramine</mark> toxicity . 
We report a case of variant ventricular tachycardia induced by <mark>desipramine</mark> toxicity . 
Unusual features of the arrhythmia are repetitive group beating , progressive shortening of the R - R interval , progressive widening of the QRS complex with eventual failure of intraventricular conduction , and changes in direction of the QRS axis . 
Recognition of variant ventricular tachycardia is important because therapy differs from that of classic ventricular tachycardia . 
Rebound hypertensive after <mark>sodium nitroprusside</mark> prevented by <mark>saralasin</mark> in rats . 
The role of the renin - - <mark>angiotensin</mark> system in the maintenance of blood pressure during <mark>halothane</mark> anesthesia and <mark>sodium nitroprusside</mark> ( <mark>SNP</mark> ) - induced hypotension was evaluated . 
Control rats received <mark>halothane</mark> anesthesia ( 1 MAC ) for one hour , followed by <mark>SNP</mark> infusion , 40 microgram / kg / min , for 30 min , followed by a 30 - min recovery period . 
A second group of rats was treated identically and , in addition , received an infusion of <mark>saralasin</mark> ( a competitive inhibitor of <mark>angiotensin II</mark> ) throughout the experimental period . 
In each group , <mark>SNP</mark> infusion resulted in an initial decrease in blood pressure from 86 torr and 83 torr , respectively , to 48 torr . 
During the <mark>SNP</mark> infusion the control animals demonstrated a progressive increase in blood pressure to 61 torr , whereas the <mark>saralasin</mark> - treated animals showed no change .
