Following discontinuation of <mark>SNP</mark> , blood pressure in the control animals rebounded to 94 torr , as compared with 78 torr in the <mark>saralasin</mark> - treated rats . 
This study indicates that with stable <mark>halothane</mark> anesthesia , the partial recovery of blood pressure during <mark>SNP</mark> infusion and the post - <mark>SNP</mark> rebound of blood pressure can be completely blocked by <mark>saralasin</mark> . 
This demonstrates the participation of the renin - - <mark>angiotensin</mark> system in antagonizing the combined hypotensive effects of <mark>halothane</mark> and <mark>SNP</mark> . 
Clinical nephrotoxicity of <mark>tobramycin</mark> and <mark>gentamicin</mark> . 
A prospective study . 
Nearly 3 . 2 million people in this country receive <mark>aminoglycoside</mark> antibiotics annually . 
<mark>Gentamicin sulfate</mark> and <mark>tobramycin sulfate</mark> continue to demonstrate ototoxicity and nephrotoxicity in both animal and clinical studies . 
In this study , 62 patients with confirmed initial normal renal function and treated with 2 to 5 mg / kg / day of <mark>gentamicin sulfate</mark> or <mark>tobramycin sulfate</mark> for a minimum of seven days were followed up prospectively for the development of <mark>aminoglycoside</mark> - related renal failure , defined as at least a one - third reduction in renal function . 
In these 62 patients , no other causes for renal failure could be identified . 
Five of 33 ( 15 % ) of the <mark>tobramycin</mark> - treated patients and 16 of 29 ( 55 . 2 % ) of the <mark>gentamicin</mark> - treated patients had renal failure . 
Thus , <mark>gentamicin</mark> was associated with renal failure more than three times as often as was <mark>tobramycin</mark> . 
Metabolic involvement in <mark>adriamycin</mark> cardiotoxicity . 
The cardiotoxic effects of <mark>adriamycin</mark> were studied in mammalian myocardial cells in culture as a model system . 
<mark>Adriamycin</mark> inhibited cell growth and the rhythmic contractions characteristic of myocardial cells in culture . 
A possible involvement of energy metabolism was suggested previously , and in this study the adenylate energy charge and <mark>phosphorylcreatine</mark> mole fraction were determined in the <mark>adriamycin</mark> - treated cells . 
The adenylate energy charge was found to be significantly decreased , while the <mark>phophorylcreatine</mark> mole fraction was unchanged . 
Such disparity suggests an inhibition of <mark>creatine</mark> phosphokinase . 
The addition of 1 mM <mark>adenosine</mark> to the myocardial cell cultures markedly increases the <mark>ATP</mark> concentration through a pathway reportedly leading to a compartmentalized <mark>ATP</mark> pool . 
In the <mark>adriamycin</mark> - treated cells , the addition of <mark>adenosine</mark> increased the adenylate charge and , concomitant with this inrcease , the cells ' functional integrity , in terms of percentage of beating cells and rate of contractions , was maintained . 
Age - dependent sensitivity of the rat to neurotoxic effects of <mark>streptomycin</mark> . 
<mark>Streptomycin</mark> sulfate ( 300 mg / kg s . c . ) was injected for various periods into preweanling rats and for 3 weeks into weanling rats . 
Beginning at 8 days of age , body movement and hearing were examined for 6 and up to 17 weeks , respectively . 
Abnormal movements and deafness occurred only in rats treated during the preweaning period ; within this period the greatest sensitivities for these abnormalities occurred from 2 to 11 - 17 and 5 to 11 days of age , respectively , indicating that the cochlea is more sensitive to <mark>streptomycin</mark> than the site ( vestibular or central ) responsible for the dyskinesias . 
Late , late <mark>doxorubicin</mark> cardiotoxicity . 
Cardiac toxicity is a major complication which limits the use of <mark>adriamycin</mark> as a chemotherapeutic agent . 
Cardiomyopathy is frequent when the total dose exceeds 600 mg / m2 and occurs within one to six months after cessation of therapy . 
A patient is reported who developed progressive cardiomyopathy two and one - half years after receiving 580 mg / m2 which apparently represents late , late cardiotoxicity . 
Attenuation of the <mark>lithium</mark> - induced diabetes - insipidus - like syndrome by <mark>amiloride</mark> in rats . 
The effect of <mark>amiloride</mark> on <mark>lithium</mark> - induced polydipsia and polyuria and on the <mark>lithium</mark> concentration in the plasma , brain , kidney , thyroid and red blood cells was investigated in rats , chronically treated with <mark>LiCl</mark> . 
<mark>Amiloride</mark> reduced the drinking and urine volume of rats in an acute ( 6 or 12 h ) and a subacute ( 3 days ) experiment . 
6 h after the administration of <mark>amiloride</mark> , a reduction was observed in the <mark>lithium</mark> content of the renal medulla but not in the other organs studied . 
At 12 h , all the tissues showed a slight increase in <mark>lithium</mark> levels . 
After 3 days of combined treatment , a marked elevation in plasma and tissue <mark>lithium</mark> levels accompanied a reduction in water intake . 
In all the experiments , the attenuation of the <mark>lithium</mark> - induced diabetes - insipidus - like syndrome by <mark>amiloride</mark> was accompanied by a reduction of the ratio between the <mark>lithium</mark> concentration in the renal medulla and its levels in the blood and an elevation in the plasma <mark>potassium</mark> level . 
It is concluded that acute <mark>amiloride</mark> administration to <mark>lithium</mark> - treated patients suffering from polydipsia and polyuria might relieve these patients but prolonged <mark>amiloride</mark> supplementation would result in elevated <mark>lithium</mark> levels and might be hazardous . 
Cardiovascular complications associated with <mark>terbutaline</mark> treatment for preterm labor . 
Severe cardiovascular complications occurred in eight of 160 patients treated with <mark>terbutaline</mark> for preterm labor . 
Associated corticosteroid therapy and twin gestations appear to be predisposing factors . 
Potential mechanisms of the pathophysiology are briefly discussed . 
Toxic hepatitis induced by antithyroid drugs : four cases including one with cross - reactivity between <mark>carbimazole</mark> and <mark>benzylthiouracil</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : This study was conducted to assess the occurrence of hepatic adverse effects encountered with antithyroid drugs . 
METHODS : Retrospective review of medical records of 236 patients with hyperthyroidism admitted in our department ( in - or out - patients ) from 1986 to 1992 . 
RESULTS : Four patients ( 1 . 7 % ) were identified with toxic hepatitis which could reasonably be attributed to the use of antithyroid agent . 
Two patients had a cholestatic hepatitis induced by <mark>carbimazole</mark> ( <mark>N omercazole</mark> ) . 
Two others had a mixed ( cholestatic and cytolytic ) hepatitis following <mark>carbimazole</mark> . 
One of the latter two patients further experienced a cytolytic hepatitis which appeared after <mark>Benzylthiouracil</mark> ( <mark>Basd ne</mark> ) had replaced <mark>carbimazole</mark> . 
Biological features of hepatitis disappeared in all cases after cessation of the incriminated drug , while biliary , viral and immunological searches were negative . 
Only 2 patients of our retrospective study experienced a mild or severe neutropenia . 
CONCLUSION : Toxic hepatitis is a potential adverse effect of antithyroid drugs which warrants , as for haematological disturbances , a pre - therapeutic determination and a careful follow - up of relevant biological markers . 
Moreover , hepatotoxicity may not be restricted to one class of antithyroid agents . 
Interactive effects of variations in [ <mark>Na</mark> ] o and [ <mark>Ca</mark> ] o on rat atrial spontaneous frequency . 
The effects of varying the extracellular concentrations of <mark>Na</mark> and <mark>Ca</mark> ( [ <mark>Na</mark> ] o and [ <mark>Ca</mark> ] o ) on both , the spontaneous beating and the negative chronotropic action of <mark>verapamil</mark> , were studied in the isolated rat atria . 
Basal frequency ( BF ) evaluated by surface electrogram was 223 + / - 4 beats / min . in control Krebs - Ringer containing 137 mM <mark>Na</mark> and 1 . 35 mM <mark>Ca</mark> ( N ) . 
It decreased by 16 + / - 3 % by lowering [ <mark>Na</mark> ] o to 78 mM ( L<mark>Na</mark> ) , 23 + / - 2 % by lowering simultaneously [ <mark>Na</mark> ] o to 78 mM and [ <mark>Ca</mark> ] o to 0 . 675 mM ( LNa + L<mark>Ca</mark> ) and 31 + / - 5 % by lowering [ Na ] o to 78 mM plus increasing [ Ca ] o to 3 . 6 mM ( LNa + HCa ) . 
At normal [ <mark>Na</mark> ] o , decrease ( 0 . 675 mM ) or increase ( 3 . 6 mM ) of [ <mark>Ca</mark> ] o did not modify BF ; a reduction of ten times ( 0 . 135 mM of normal [ <mark>Ca</mark> ] o was effective to reduce BF by 40 + / - 13 % . 
All negative chronotropic effects were BF - dependent . 
Dose - dependent bradycardia induced by <mark>verapamil</mark> was potentiated by LNa , LCa , and HCa . 
Independent but not additive effects of <mark>Na</mark> and <mark>Ca</mark> are shown by decreases in the values of [ <mark>verapamil</mark> ] o needed to reduce BF by 30 % ( IC30 ) with the following order of inhibitory potency : LNa > LCa > HCa > N , resulting LNa + HCa similar to LNa . 
The [ <mark>verapamil</mark> ] o that arrested atrial beating ( AC ) was also potentiated with the order LNa = LNa + LCa = LNa + HCa = LCa > HCa = N . 
The results indicate that rat atrial spontaneous beating is more dependent on [ <mark>Na</mark> ] o than on [ <mark>Ca</mark> ] o in a range of + / - 50 % of their normal concentration . 
Also the enhancement of <mark>verapamil</mark> effects on atrial beating was more pronounced at LNa than at LCa . ( ABSTRACT TRUNCATED AT 250 WORDS ) 
Pseudo - allergic reactions to <mark>corticosteroids</mark> : diagnosis and alternatives . 
Two patients treated with parenteral <mark>paramethasone</mark> ( Triniol ) and <mark>dexamethasone</mark> ( Sedionbel ) are described . 
A few minutes after administration of the drugs , they presented urticaria ( patients 1 and 2 ) and conjunctivitis ( patient 1 ) . 
The purpose of our study was to determine the cause of the patients ' reactions , the immunological mechanisms involved and whether these patients would be able to tolerate any kind of corticoid . 
Clinical examinations and skin , oral and parenteral challenges with different <mark>corticosteroids</mark> and ELISA tests were performed . 
In the two patients , skin and ELISA tests with <mark>paramethasone</mark> were negative , as was the prick test with each of its excipients . 
A single - blind parenteral challenge with Triniol was positive in both patients after the administration of 1 ml of the drug , and negative with its excipients . 
We also carried out oral and parenteral challenges with other <mark>corticosteroids</mark> and found intolerance to some of them . 
These results suggest that <mark>paramethasone</mark> caused pseudoallergic reactions in our patients . 
Corticosteroids different from <mark>paramethasone</mark> also produced hypersensitivity reactions in these patients ; however , a few of them were tolerated . 
The basic mechanisms of those reactions are not yet fully understood . 
To our knowledge , this is the first report of a pseudo - allergy caused by <mark>paramethasone</mark> . 
Study of the role of <mark>vitamin B12</mark> and <mark>folinic acid</mark> supplementation in preventing hematologic toxicity of <mark>zidovudine</mark> . 
A prospective , randomized study was conducted to evaluate the role of <mark>vitamin B12</mark> and <mark>folinic acid</mark> supplementation in preventing <mark>zidovudine</mark> ( <mark>ZDV</mark> ) - induced bone marrow suppression . 
Seventy - five human immunodeficiency virus ( HIV ) - infected patients with CD4 + cell counts < 500 / mm3 were randomized to receive either <mark>ZDV</mark> ( 500 mg daily ) alone ( group I , n = 38 ) or in combination with <mark>folinic acid</mark> ( 15 mg daily ) and intramascular <mark>vitamin B12</mark> ( 1000 micrograms monthly ) ( group II , n = 37 ) . 
Finally , 15 patients were excluded from the study ( noncompliance 14 , death 1 ) ; thus , 60 patients ( 31 in group I and 29 in group II ) were eligible for analysis . 
No significant differences between groups were found at enrollment . 
During the study , <mark>vitamin B12</mark> and <mark>folate</mark> levels were significantly higher in group II patients ; however , no differences in hemoglobin , hematocrit , mean corpuscular volume , and white - cell , neutrophil and platelet counts were observed between groups at 3 , 6 , 9 and 12 months . 
Severe hematologic toxicity ( neutrophil count < 1000 / mm3 and / or hemoglobin < 8 g / dl ) occurred in 4 patients assigned to group I and 7 assigned to group II . 
There was no correlation between <mark>vitamin B12</mark> or <mark>folate</mark> levels and development of myelosuppression . 
<mark>Vitamin B12</mark> and <mark>folinic acid</mark> supplementation of <mark>ZDV</mark> therapy does not seem useful in preventing or reducing <mark>ZDV</mark> - induced myelotoxicity in the overall treated population , although a beneficial effect in certain subgroups of patients cannot be excluded . 
Safety and side - effects of <mark>alprazolam</mark> . 
Controlled study in agoraphobia with panic disorder . 
BACKGROUND : The widespread use of <mark>benzodiazepines</mark> has led to increasing recognition of their unwanted effects . 
The efficacy of <mark>alprazolam</mark> and placebo in panic disorder with agoraphobia , and the side - effect and adverse effect profiles of both drug groups were measured . 
METHOD : In London and Toronto 154 patients who met DSM - III criteria for panic disorder with agoraphobia were randomised to <mark>alprazolam</mark> or placebo . 
Subjects in each drug group also received either exposure or relaxation . 
Treatment was from weeks 0 to 8 and was then tapered from weeks 8 to 16 . 
RESULTS : Mean <mark>alprazolam</mark> dose was 5 mg daily . 
Compared with placebo subjects , <mark>alprazolam</mark> patients developed more adverse reactions ( 21 % v . 0 % ) of depression , enuresis , disinhibition and aggression ; and more side - effects , particularly sedation , irritability , impaired memory , weight loss and ataxia . 
Side - effects tended to diminish during treatment but remained significant at week 8 . 
Despite this , the drop - out rate was low . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Alprazolam</mark> caused side - effects and adverse effects during treatment but many patients were willing to accept these . 
Crescentic fibrillary glomerulonephritis associated with intermittent <mark>rifampin</mark> therapy for pulmonary tuberculosis . 
This case study reveals an unusual finding of rapidly proliferative crescentic glomerulonephritis in a patient treated with <mark>rifampin</mark> who had no other identifiable causes for developing this disease . 
This patient underwent a 10 - month regimen of <mark>rifampin</mark> and <mark>isoniazid</mark> for pulmonary tuberculosis and was discovered to have developed signs of severe renal failure five weeks after completion of therapy . 
Renal biopsy revealed severe glomerulonephritis with crescents , electron dense fibrillar deposits and moderate lymphocytic interstitial infiltrate . 
Other possible causes of rapidly progressive glomerulonephritis were investigated and ruled out . 
This report documents the unusual occurrence of rapidly progressive glomerulonephritis with crescents and fibrillar glomerulonephritis in a patient treated with <mark>rifampin</mark> . 
Acute confusion induced by a high - dose infusion of <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> and <mark>folinic acid</mark> . 
A 61 - year - old man was treated with combination chemotherapy incorporating <mark>cisplatinum</mark> , <mark>etoposide</mark> , high - dose <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> ( 2 , 250 mg / m2 / 24 hours ) and <mark>folinic acid</mark> for an inoperable gastric adenocarcinoma . 
He developed acute neurologic symptoms of mental confusion , disorientation and irritability , and then lapsed into a deep coma , lasting for approximately 40 hours during the first dose ( day 2 ) of <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> and <mark>folinic acid</mark> infusion . 
This complication reappeared on day 25 during the second dose of <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> and <mark>folinic acid</mark> , which were then the only drugs given . 
Because <mark>folinic acid</mark> was unlikely to be associated with this condition , neurotoxicity due to high - dose <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> was highly suspected . 
The pathogenesis of <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> neurotoxicity may be due to a Krebs cycle blockade by <mark>fluoroacetate</mark> and <mark>fluorocitrate</mark> , <mark>thiamine</mark> deficiency , or <mark>dihydrouracil</mark> dehydrogenase deficiency . 
High - dose <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> / <mark>folinic acid</mark> infusion therapy has recently become a popular regimen for various cancers . 
It is necessary that both oncologists and neurologists be fully aware of this unusual complication . 
Effect of switching <mark>carbamazepine</mark> to <mark>oxcarbazepine</mark> on the plasma levels of neuroleptics . 
A case report . 
<mark>Carbamazepine</mark> was switched to its 10 - keto analogue <mark>oxcarbazepine</mark> among six difficult - to - treat schizophrenic or organic psychotic patients using concomitantly <mark>haloperidol</mark> , <mark>chlorpromazine</mark> or <mark>clozapine</mark> . 
This change resulted within 2 - 4 weeks in the 50 - 200 % increase in the plasma levels of these neuroleptics and the appearance of extrapyramidal symptoms . 
None of the patients showed any clinical deteriotation during the following 3 - 6 months . 
The results of this case report support the idea that in contrast with <mark>carbamazepine</mark> <mark>oxcarbazepine</mark> does not induce the hepatic microsomal enzyme systems regulating the inactivation of antipsychotic drugs . 
Time course of lipid peroxidation in <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> - induced nephropathy . 
Reactive <mark>oxygen</mark> species have been implicated in the pathogenesis of acute <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> ( <mark>PAN</mark> ) - induced nephropathy , with antioxidants significantly reducing the proteinuria . 
The temporal relationship between lipid peroxidation in the kidney and proteinuria was examined in this study . 
Rats were treated with a single IV injection of <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> , ( <mark>PAN</mark> , 7 . 5 mg / kg ) and 24 hour urine samples were obtained prior to sacrifice on days 3 , 5 , 7 , 10 , 17 , 27 , 41 ( N = 5 - 10 per group ) . 
The kidneys were removed , flushed with ice cold TRIS buffer . 
Kidney cortices from each animal were used to prepare homogenates . 
Tissue lipid peroxidation was measured in whole homogenates as well as in lipid extracts from homogenates as <mark>thiobarbituric acid</mark> reactive substances . 
Proteinuria was evident at day 5 , peaked at day 7 and persisted to day 27 . 
Lipid peroxidation in homogenates was maximal at day 3 and declined rapidly to control levels by day 17 . 
This study supports the role of lipid peroxidation in mediating the proteinuric injury in <mark>PAN</mark> nephropathy . 
Composition of gall bladder stones associated with <mark>octreotide</mark> : response to oral <mark>ursodeoxycholic acid</mark> . 
<mark>Octreotide</mark> , an effective treatment for acromegaly , induces gall bladder stones in 13 - 60 % of patients . 
Because knowledge of stone composition is essential for studies of their pathogenesis , treatment , and prevention , this was investigated by direct and indirect methods in 14 <mark>octreotide</mark> treated acromegalic patients with gall stones . 
Chemical analysis of gall stones retrieved at cholecystectomy from two patients , showed that they contained 71 % and 87 % <mark>cholesterol</mark> by weight . 
In the remaining 12 patients , localised computed tomography of the gall bladder showed that eight had stones with maximum attenuation scores of < 100 Hounsfield units ( values of < 100 HU predict <mark>cholesterol</mark> rich , dissolvable stones ) . 
Gall bladder bile was obtained by ultrasound guided , fine needle puncture from six patients . 
All six patients had supersaturated bile ( mean ( SEM ) <mark>cholesterol</mark> saturation index of 1 . 19 ( 0 . 08 ) ( range 1 . 01 - 1 . 53 ) ) and all had abnormally rapid <mark>cholesterol</mark> microcrystal nucleation times ( < 4 days ( range 1 - 4 ) ) , whilst in four , the bile contained <mark>cholesterol</mark> microcrystals immediately after sampling . 
Of the 12 patients considered for oral <mark>ursodeoxycholic acid</mark> ( <mark>UDCA</mark> ) treatment , two had a blocked cystic duct and were not started on <mark>UDCA</mark> while one was lost to follow up . 
After one year of treatment , five of the remaining nine patients showed either partial ( n = 3 ) or complete ( n = 2 ) gall stone dissolution , suggesting that their stones were <mark>cholesterol</mark> rich . 
This corresponds , by actuarial ( life table ) analysis , to a combined gall stone dissolution rate of 58 . 3 ( 15 . 9 % ) . 
In conclusion , <mark>octreotide</mark> induced gall stones are generally small , multiple , and <mark>cholesterol</mark> rich although , in common with spontaneous gall stone disease , at presentation some patients will have a blocked cystic duct and some gall stones containing <mark>calcium</mark> . 
Erythema multiforme and hypersensitivity myocarditis caused by <mark>ampicillin</mark> . 
OBJECTIVE : To report a case of erythema multiforme and hypersensitivity myocarditis caused by <mark>ampicillin</mark> . 
CASE SUMMARY : A 13 - year - old boy was treated with <mark>ampicillin</mark> and <mark>gentamicin</mark> because of suspected septicemia . 
Medications were discontinued when erythema multiforme and congestive heart failure caused by myocarditis occurred . 
The patient was treated with <mark>methylprednisolone</mark> and gradually improved . 
Macrophage - migration inhibition ( MIF ) test with <mark>ampicillin</mark> was positive . 
DISCUSSION : After most infections causing erythema multiforme and myocarditis were ruled out , a drug - induced allergic reaction was suspected . 
Positive MIF test for <mark>ampicillin</mark> showed sensitization of the patient ' s lymphocytes to <mark>ampicillin</mark> . 
CONCLUSIONS : Hypersensitivity myocarditis is a rare and dangerous manifestation of allergy to <mark>penicillins</mark> . 
<mark>Clomipramine</mark> - induced sleep disturbance does not impair its prolactin - releasing action . 
The present study was undertaken to examine the role of sleep disturbance , induced by <mark>clomipramine</mark> administration , on the secretory rate of prolactin ( PRL ) in addition to the direct drug effect . 
Two groups of supine subjects were studied under placebo - controlled conditions , one during the night , when sleeping ( n = 7 ) and the other at daytime , when awake ( n = 6 ) . 
Each subject received a single 50 mg dose of <mark>clomipramine</mark> given orally 2 hours before blood collection . 
Plasma PRL concentrations were analysed at 10 min intervals and underlying secretory rates calculated by a deconvolution procedure . 
For both experiments the drug intake led to significant increases in PRL secretion , acting preferentially on tonic secretion as pulse amplitude and frequency did not differ significantly from corresponding control values . 
During the night <mark>clomipramine</mark> ingestion altered the complete sleep architecture in that it suppressed REM sleep and the sleep cycles and induced increased wakefulness . 
As the relative increase in PRL secretion expressed as a percentage of the mean did not significantly differ between the night and day time studies ( 46 + / - 19 % vs 34 + / - 10 % ) , it can be concluded that the observed sleep disturbance did not interfere with the drug action per se . 
The presence of REM sleep was shown not to be a determining factor either for secretory pulse amplitude and frequency , as , for both , mean nocturnal values were similar with and without prior <mark>clomipramine</mark> ingestion . 
Survey of complications of <mark>indocyanine green</mark> angiography in Japan . 
PURPOSE : We evaluated the safety of <mark>indocyanine green</mark> for use in fundus angiography . 
METHODS : We sent a questionnaire concerning complications of <mark>indocyanine green</mark> to 32 institutions in Japan , which were selected on the basis of the client list from the Topcon Company , which manufactures the <mark>indocyanine green</mark> fundus camera . 
RESULTS : Ophthalmologists at 15 institutions responded , reporting a total of 3 , 774 <mark>indocyanine green</mark> angiograms performed on 2 , 820 patients between June 1984 and September 1992 . 
Before angiography , intradermal or intravenous <mark>indocyanine green</mark> testing , or both was performed at 13 of 15 institutions . 
For three patients , the decision was made not to proceed with angiography after positive preangiographic testing . 
The dosage of <mark>indocyanine green</mark> used for angiography varied from 25 to 75 mg , depending upon the institution . 
There were 13 cases of adverse reactions ( 0 . 34 % ) , ten of which were mild reactions such as nausea , exanthema , urtication , itchiness , and urgency to defecate , and did not require treatment . 
Also recorded were one case of pain of the vein , which required treatment , and two cases of hypotension . 
The two hypotensive patients required treatment for shock . 
CONCLUSIONS : A comparison of frequency of adverse reactions to <mark>indocyanine green</mark> with the previously reported frequency of such reactions to <mark><mark>fluorescein</mark> sodium</mark> indicated that <mark>indocyanine green</mark> is a safe as fluorescein for use in angiography . 
Angioedema following the intravenous administration of <mark>metoprolol</mark> . 
A 72 - year - old woman was admitted to the hospital with " flash " pulmonary edema , preceded by chest pain , requiring intubation . 
Her medical history included coronary artery disease with previous myocardial infarctions , hypertension , and diabetes mellitus . 
A history of angioedema secondary to <mark>lisinopril</mark> therapy was elicited . 
Current medications did not include <mark>angiotensin</mark> - converting enzyme inhibitors or beta - blockers . 
She had no previous beta - blocking drug exposure . 
During the first day of hospitalization ( while intubated ) , intravenous <mark>metoprolol</mark> was given , resulting in severe angioedema . 
The angioedema resolved after therapy with intravenous <mark>steroids</mark> and <mark>diphenhydramine</mark> hydrochloride . 
Effect of <mark>coniine</mark> on the developing chick embryo . 
<mark>Coniine</mark> , an alkaloid from Conium maculatum ( poison hemlock ) , has been shown to be teratogenic in livestock . 
The major teratogenic outcome is arthrogryposis , presumably due to nicotinic receptor blockade . 
However , <mark>coniine</mark> has failed to produce arthrogryposis in rats or mice and is only weakly teratogenic in rabbits . 
The purpose of this study was to evaluate and compare the effects of <mark>coniine</mark> and <mark>nicotine</mark> in the developing chick . 
Concentrations of <mark>coniine</mark> and <mark>nicotine</mark> sulfate were 0 . 015 % , 0 . 03 % , 0 . 075 % , 0 . 15 % , 0 . 75 % , 1 . 5 % , 3 % , and 6 % and 1 % , 5 % , and 10 % , respectively . 
Both compounds caused deformations and lethality in a dose - dependent manner . 
All concentrations of <mark>nicotine</mark> sulfate caused some lethality but a no effect level for <mark>coniine</mark> lethality was 0 . 75 % . 
The deformations caused by both <mark>coniine</mark> and <mark>nicotine</mark> sulfate were excessive flexion or extension of one or more toes . 
No histopathological alterations or differences in bone formation were seen in the limbs or toes of any chicks from any group ; however , extensive cranial hemorrhage occurred in all <mark>nicotine</mark> sulfate - treated chicks . 
There was a statistically significant ( P < or = 0 . 01 ) decrease in movement in <mark>coniine</mark> and <mark>nicotine</mark> sulfate treated chicks as determined by ultrasound . 
Control chicks were in motion an average of 33 . 67 % of the time , while <mark>coniine</mark> - treated chicks were only moving 8 . 95 % of a 5 - min interval , and no movement was observed for <mark>nicotine</mark> sulfate treated chicks . 
In summary , the chick embryo provides a reliable and simple experimental animal model of <mark>coniine</mark> - induced arthrogryposis . 
Data from this model support a mechanism involving nicotinic receptor blockade with subsequent decreased fetal movement . 
Immediate allergic reactions to <mark>amoxicillin</mark> . 
A large group of patients with suspected allergic reactions to <mark>beta - lactam</mark> antibiotics was evaluated . 
A detailed clinical history , together with skin tests , RAST ( radioallergosorbent test ) , and controlled challenge tests , was used to establish whether patients allergic to <mark>beta - lactam</mark> antibiotics had selective immediate allergic responses to <mark>amoxicillin</mark> ( <mark>AX</mark> ) or were cross - reacting with other <mark>penicillin</mark> derivatives . 
Skin tests were performed with <mark>benzylpenicilloyl - poly - L - lysine</mark> ( <mark>BPO - PLL</mark> ) , <mark>benzylpenicilloate</mark> , <mark>benzylpenicillin</mark> ( <mark>PG</mark> ) , <mark>ampicillin</mark> ( <mark>AMP</mark> ) , and <mark>AX</mark> . 
RAST for <mark>BPO - PLL</mark> and <mark>AX</mark> - PLL was done . 
When both skin test and RAST for <mark>BPO</mark> were negative , single - blind , placebo - controlled challenge tests were done to ensure tolerance of <mark>PG</mark> or sensitivity to <mark>AX</mark> . 
A total of 177 patients were diagnosed as allergic to <mark>beta - lactam</mark> antibiotics . 
We selected the 54 ( 30 . 5 % ) cases of immediate <mark>AX</mark> allergy with good tolerance of <mark>PG</mark> . 
Anaphylaxis was seen in 37 patients ( 69 % ) , the other 17 ( 31 % ) having urticaria and / or angioedema . 
All the patients were skin test negative to <mark>BPO</mark> ; 49 of 51 ( 96 % ) were also negative to MDM , and 44 of 46 ( 96 % ) to <mark>PG</mark> . 
Skin tests with <mark>AX</mark> were positive in 34 ( 63 % ) patients . 
RAST was positive for <mark>AX</mark> in 22 patients ( 41 % ) and to <mark>BPO</mark> in just 5 ( 9 % ) . 
None of the sera with negative RAST for <mark>AX</mark> were positive to <mark>BPO</mark> . 
Challenge tests with <mark>AX</mark> were performed in 23 subjects ( 43 % ) to establish the diagnosis of immediate allergic reaction to <mark>AX</mark> , and in 15 cases ( 28 % ) both skin test and RAST for <mark>AX</mark> were negative . 
<mark>PG</mark> was well tolerated by all 54 patients . 
We describe the largest group of <mark>AX</mark> - allergic patients who have tolerated <mark>PG</mark> reported so far . 
Diagnosis of these patients can be achieved only if specific <mark>AX</mark> - related reagents are employed . 
Further studies are necessary to determine the exact extent of this problem and to improve the efficacy of diagnostic methods . 
Reversal by <mark>phenylephrine</mark> of the beneficial effects of intravenous <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> in patients with acute myocardial infarction . 
<mark>Nitroglycerin</mark> has been shown to reduce ST - segment elevation during acute myocardial infarction , an effect potentiated in the dog by agents that reverse <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> - induced hypotension . 
Our study was designed to determine the effects of combined <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> and <mark>phenylephrine</mark> therapy . 
Ten patients with acute transmural myocardial infarctions received intravenous <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> , sufficient to reduce mean arterial pressure from 107 + / - 6 to 85 + / - 6 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 001 ) , for 60 minutes . 
Left ventricular filling pressure decreased from 19 + / - 2 to 11 + / - 2 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 001 ) . 
SigmaST , the sum of ST - segment elevations in 16 precordial leads , decreased ( P less than 0 . 02 ) with intravenous <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> . 
Subsequent addition of <mark>phenylephrine</mark> infusion , sufficient to re - elevate mean arterial pressure to 106 + / - 4 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 001 ) for 30 minutes , increased left ventricular filling pressure to 17 + / - 2 mm Hg ( P less than 0 . 05 ) and also significantly increased sigmaST ( P less than 0 . 05 ) . 
Our results suggest that addition of <mark>phenylephrine</mark> to <mark>nitroglycerin</mark> is not beneficial in the treatment of patients with acute myocardial infarction . 
<mark>Acetazolamide</mark> - induced nephrolithiasis : implications for treatment of neuromuscular disorders . 
Carbonic anhydrase inhibitors can cause nephrolithiasis . 
We studied 20 patients receiving long - term carbonic anhydrase inhibitor treatment for periodic paralysis and myotonia . 
Three patients on <mark>acetazolamide</mark> ( 15 % ) developed renal calculi . 
Extracorporeal lithotripsy successfully removed a renal calculus in one patient and surgery removed a staghorn calculus in another , permitting continued treatment . 
Renal function remained normal in all patients . 
Nephrolithiasis is a complication of <mark>acetazolamide</mark> but does not preclude its use . 
Effects of <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers on <mark>bupivacaine</mark> - induced toxicity . 
The purpose of this study was to investigate the influence of <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers on <mark>bupivacaine</mark> - induced acute toxicity . 
For each of the three tested <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers ( <mark>diltiazem</mark> , <mark>verapamil</mark> and <mark>bepridil</mark> ) 6 groups of mice were treated by two different doses , i . e . 2 and 10 mg / kg / i . p . , or an equal volume of saline for the control group ( n = 20 ) ; 15 minutes later , all the animals were injected with a single 50 mg / kg / i . p . dose of <mark>bupivacaine</mark> . 
The convulsant activity , the time of latency to convulse and the mortality rate were assessed in each group . 
The local anesthetic - induced mortality was significantly increased by the three different <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers . 
The convulsant activity of <mark>bupivacaine</mark> was not significantly modified but <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers decreased the time of latency to obtain <mark>bupivacaine</mark> - induced convulsions ; this effect was less pronounced with <mark>bepridil</mark> . 
Epidural blood flow during <mark>prostaglandin E1</mark> or <mark>trimethaphan</mark> induced hypotension . 
To evaluate the effect of <mark>prostaglandin E1</mark> ( <mark>PGE1</mark> ) or <mark>trimethaphan</mark> ( <mark>TMP</mark> ) induced hypotension on epidural blood flow ( EBF ) during spinal surgery , EBF was measured using the heat clearance method in 30 patients who underwent postero - lateral interbody fusion under <mark>isoflurane</mark> anaesthesia . 
An initial dose of 0 . 1 microgram . kg - 1 . min - 1 of <mark>PGE1</mark> ( 15 patients ) , or 10 micrograms . kg - 1 . min - 1 of <mark>TMP</mark> ( 15 patients ) was administered intravenously after the dural opening and the dose was adjusted to maintain the mean arterial blood pressure ( MAP ) at about 60 mmHg . 
The hypotensive drug was discontinued at the completion of the operative procedure . 
After starting <mark>PGE1</mark> or <mark>TMP</mark> , MAP and rate pressure product ( RPP ) decreased significantly compared with preinfusion values ( P < 0 . 01 ) , and the degree of hypotension due to <mark>PGE1</mark> remained constant until 60 min after its discontinuation . 
Heart rate ( HR ) did not change in either group . 
EBFF did not change during <mark>PGE1</mark> infusion whereas in the <mark>TMP</mark> group , EBF decreased significantly at 30 and 60 min after the start of <mark>TMP</mark> ( preinfusion : 45 . 9 + / - 13 . 9 ml / 100g / min . 30 min : 32 . 3 + / - 9 . 9 ml / 100 g / min ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 60 min : 30 + / - 7 . 5 ml / 100 g / min ( P < 0 . 05 ) ) . 
These results suggest that <mark>PGE1</mark> may be preferable to <mark>TMP</mark> for hypotensive anaesthesia in spinal surgery because <mark>TMP</mark> decreased EBF . 
<mark>Dup 753</mark> prevents the development of <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> - induced nephrosis . 
The appearance of nephrotic syndromes such as proteinuria , hypoalbuminemia , hypercholesterolemia and increase in <mark>blood nitrogen urea</mark> , induced in rats by injection of <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> was markedly inhibited by oral administration of <mark>Dup 753</mark> ( <mark>losartan</mark> ) , a novel <mark>angiotensin II</mark> receptor antagonist , at a dose of 1 or 2 mg / kg per day . 
The results suggest a possible involvement of the renin - <mark>angiotensin</mark> system in the development of <mark>puromycin aminonucleoside</mark> - induced nephrosis . 
Neuroplasticity of the adult primate auditory cortex following cochlear hearing loss . 
Tonotopic organization is an essential feature of the primary auditory area ( A1 ) of primate cortex . 
In A1 of macaque monkeys , low frequencies are represented rostrolaterally and high frequencies are represented caudomedially . 
The purpose of this study was to determine if changes occur in this tonotopic organization following cochlear hearing loss . 
Under anesthesia , the superior temporal gyrus of adult macaque monkeys was exposed , and the tonotopic organization of A1 was mapped using conventional microelectrode recording techniques . 
Following recovery , the monkeys were selectively deafened for high frequencies using <mark>kanamycin</mark> and <mark>furosemide</mark> . 
The actual frequencies deafened were determined by the loss of tone - burst elicited auditory brainstem responses . 
Three months after deafening , A1 was remapped . 
Postmortem cytoarchitectural features identifying A1 were correlated with the electrophysiologic data . 
The results indicate that the deprived area of A1 undergoes extensive reorganization and becomes responsive to intact cochlear frequencies . 
The region of cortex that represents the low frequencies was not obviously affected by the cochlear hearing loss . 
<mark>Sodium bicarbonate</mark> alleviates penile pain induced by intracavernous injections for erectile dysfunction . 
In an attempt to determine whether penile pain associated with intracorporeal injections could be due to the acidity of the medication , we performed a randomized study comparing the incidence of penile pain following intracorporeal injections with or without the addition of <mark>sodium bicarbonate</mark> to the intracorporeal medications . 
A total of 38 consecutive patients who presented to our clinic with impotence received 0 . 2 ml . of a combination of 3 drugs : 6 mg . <mark>papaverine</mark> , 100 micrograms . <mark>phentolamine</mark> and 10 micrograms . <mark>prostaglandin E1</mark> with ( pH 7 . 05 ) or without ( pH 4 . 17 ) the addition of <mark>sodium bicarbonate</mark> ( 0 . 03 mEq . ) . 
Of the 19 patients without <mark>sodium bicarbonate</mark> added to the medication 11 ( 58 % ) complained of penile pain due to the medication , while only 1 of the 19 men ( 5 % ) who received <mark>sodium bicarbonate</mark> complained of penile pain . 
From these data we conclude that the penile pain following intracorporeal injections is most likely due to the acidity of the medication , which can be overcome by elevating the pH to a neutral level . 
The use and toxicity of <mark>didanosine</mark> ( <mark>ddI</mark> ) in HIV antibody - positive individuals intolerant to <mark>zidovudine</mark> ( <mark>AZT</mark> ) 
One hundred and fifty - one patients intolerant to <mark>zidovudine</mark> ( <mark>AZT</mark> ) received <mark>didanosine</mark> ( <mark>ddI</mark> ) to a maximum dose of 12 . 5 mg / kg / day . 
Patient response was assessed using changes in CD4 + lymphocyte subset count , HIV p24 antigen , weight , and quality of life . 
Seventy patients developed major opportunistic infections whilst on therapy ; this was the first AIDS diagnosis in 17 . 
Only minor changes in CD4 + lymphocyte subset count were observed in AIDS patients , although a more significant rise occurred in those with earlier stages of disease . 
Of those positive for p24 antigen at the commencement of the study 67 % showed a positive response , and this was most likely in those with CD4 + lymphocyte subset counts above 100 mm3 . 
A positive weight response was seen in 16 % of patients . 
Most patients showed improvement in individual parameters and global score of quality of life . 
Adverse reactions possibly attributable to <mark>didanosine</mark> were common . 
The most common side - effect was diarrhoea , which resulted in cessation of therapy in 19 individuals . 
Peripheral neuropathy occurred in 12 patients and pancreatitis in six . 
Thirteen patients developed a raised serum amylase without abdominal pain . 
Seven patients developed glucose tolerance curves characteristic of diabetes but these were mild , did not require treatment and returned to normal on ceasing <mark>didanosine</mark> . 
Immunohistochemical studies with antibodies to neurofilament proteins on axonal damage in experimental focal lesions in rat . 
Immunohistochemistry with monoclonal antibodies against neurofilament ( NF ) proteins of middle and high molecular weight class , NF - M and NF - H , was used to study axonal injury in the borderzone of focal lesions in rats . 
Focal injury in the cortex was produced by infusion of <mark>lactate</mark> at acid pH or by stab caused by needle insertion . 
Infarcts in substantia nigra pars reticulata were evoked by prolonged <mark>pilocarpine</mark> - induced status epilepticus . 
Immunohistochemical staining for NFs showed characteristic terminal clubs of axons in the borderzone of lesions . 
Differences in the labelling pattern occurred with different antibodies which apparently depended on molecular weight class of NFs and phosphorylation state . 
These immunohistochemical changes of NFs can serve as a marker for axonal damage in various experimental traumatic or ischemic lesions . 
Pharmacokinetic and clinical studies in patients with <mark>cimetidine</mark> - associated mental confusion . 
15 cases of <mark>cimetidine</mark> - associated mental confusion have been reported . 
In order that this syndrome might be investigated changes in mental status ( M . S . ) were correlated with serum concentrations and renal and hepatic function in 36 patients , 30 patients had no M . S . change on <mark>cimetidine</mark> and 6 had moderate to severe changes . 
These 6 patients had both renal and liver dysfunction ( P less than 0 . 05 ) , as well as <mark>cimetidine</mark> trough - concentrations of more than 1 . 25 microgram / ml ( P less than 0 . 05 ) . 
The severity of M . S . changes increased as trough - concentrations rose , 5 patients had lumbar puncture . 
The cerebrospinal fluid : serum ratio of <mark>cimetidine</mark> concentrations was 0 . 24 : 1 and indicates that <mark>cimetidine</mark> passes the blood - brain barrier ; it also raises the possibility that M . S . changes are due to blockade of <mark>histamine</mark> H2 - receptors in the central nervous system . 
Patients likely to have both raised trough - concentrations and mental confusion are those with both severe renal and hepatic dysfunction . 
They should be closely observed and should be given reduced doses of <mark>cimetidine</mark> . 
Prospective study of the long - term effects of somatostatin analog ( <mark>octreotide</mark> ) on gallbladder function and gallstone formation in Chinese acromegalic patients . 
This article reports the changes in gallbladder function examined by ultrasonography in 20 Chinese patients with active acromegaly treated with sc injection of the somatostatin analog <mark>octreotide</mark> in dosages of 300 - 1500 micrograms / day for a mean of 24 . 2 + / - 13 . 9 months . 
During treatment with <mark>octreotide</mark> , 17 patients developed sludge , 10 had gallstones , and 1 developed acute cholecystitis requiring surgery . 
In all of 7 patients examined acutely , gallbladder contractility was inhibited after a single 100 - micrograms injection . 
In 8 patients followed for 24 weeks , gallbladder contractility remained depressed throughout therapy . 
After withdrawal of <mark>octreotide</mark> in 10 patients without gallstones , 8 patients assessed had return of normal gallbladder contractility within 1 month . 
In 8 of the remaining 10 patients who developed gallstones during treatment , gallbladder contractility normalized in 5 patients ( 3 of whom has disappearance of their stones within 3 weeks ) , and remained depressed in 3 ( 2 of whom had stones present at 6 months ) . 
Our results suggest that the suppression of gallbladder contractility is the cause of the successive formation of bile sludge , gallstones , and cholecystitis during <mark>octreotide</mark> therapy in Chinese acromegalic patients . 
It is therefore very important to follow the changes of gallbladder function during long - term <mark>octreotide</mark> therapy of acromegalic patients .

Depression is a major clinical feature of Parkinson ' s disease . 
We report the increased amount of motor disability in four patients with idiopathic Parkinson ' s disease after exposure to the <mark>antidepressant</mark> <mark>fluoxetine</mark> . 
The possibility of a clinically relevant <mark>dopamine</mark> - antagonistic capacity of <mark>fluoxetine</mark> in Parkinson ' s disease patients must be considered . 
Sinus arrest associated with continuous - infusion <mark>cimetidine</mark> . 
The administration of intermittent intravenous infusions of <mark>cimetidine</mark> is infrequently associated with the development of bradyarrhythmias . 
A 40 - year - old man with leukemia and no history of cardiac disease developed recurrent , brief episodes of apparent sinus arrest while receiving continuous - infusion <mark>cimetidine</mark> 50 mg / hour . 
The arrhythmias were temporally related to <mark>cimetidine</mark> administration , disappeared after dechallenge , and did not recur during <mark>ranitidine</mark> treatment . 
This is the first reported case of sinus arrest associated with continuous - infusion <mark>cimetidine</mark> . 
Phase II trial of <mark>vinorelbine</mark> in metastatic squamous cell esophageal carcinoma . 
European Organization for Research and Treatment of Cancer Gastrointestinal Treat Cancer Cooperative Group . 
PURPOSE : To evaluate the response rate and toxic effects of <mark>vinorelbine</mark> ( <mark>VNB</mark> ) administered as a single agent in metastatic squamous cell esophageal carcinoma . 
PATIENTS AND METHODS : Forty - six eligible patients with measurable lesions were included and were stratified according to previous chemotherapy . 
Thirty patients without prior chemotherapy and 16 pretreated with <mark>cisplatin</mark> - based chemotherapy were assessable for toxicity and response . 
<mark>VNB</mark> was administered weekly as a 25 - mg / m2 short intravenous ( i . v . ) infusion . 
RESULTS : Six of 30 patients ( 20 % ) without prior chemotherapy achieved a partial response ( PR ) ( 95 % confidence interval [ CI ] , 8 % to 39 % ) . 
The median duration of response was 21 weeks ( range , 17 to 28 ) . 
One of 16 patients ( 6 % ) with prior chemotherapy had a complete response ( CR ) of 31 weeks ' duration ( 95 % CI , 0 % to 30 % ) . 
The overall response rate ( World Health Organization [ WHO ] criteria ) was 15 % ( CR , 2 % ; PR 13 % ; 95 % CI , 6 % to 29 % ) . 
The median dose - intensity ( DI ) was 20 mg / m2 / wk . 
<mark>VNB</mark> was well tolerated and zero instances of WHO grade 4 nonhematologic toxicity occurred . 
At least one episode of grade 3 or 4 granulocytopenia was seen in 59 % of patients . 
A grade 2 or 3 infection occurred in 16 % of patients , but no toxic deaths occurred . 
Other side effects were rare , and peripheral neurotoxicity has been minor ( 26 % grade 1 ) . 
CONCLUSION : These data indicate that <mark>VNB</mark> is an active agent in metastatic esophageal squamous cell carcinoma . 
Given its excellent tolerance profile and low toxicity , further evaluation of <mark>VNB</mark> in combination therapy is warranted . 
Evaluation of adverse reactions of <mark>aponidine hydrochloride</mark> ophthalmic solution . 
We prospectively evaluated the adverse reactions of <mark>apraclonidine</mark> in 20 normal volunteers by instilling a single drop of 1 % <mark>apraclonidine</mark> in their right eyes . 
Examinations , including blood pressure , pulse rate , conjunctiva and cornea , intraocular pressure ( IOP ) , pupil diameter , basal tear secretion and margin reflex distance of both upper and lower eyelids , were performed prior to entry and at 1 , 3 , 5 and 7 hours after instillation . 
The ocular hypotensive effects were statistically significant for <mark>apraclonidine</mark> - treated eyes throughout the study and also statistically significant for contralateral eyes from three hours after topical administration of 1 % <mark>apraclonidine</mark> . 
Decreases in systolic blood pressure were statistically , but not clinically , significant . 
No significant changes in diastolic blood pressure , pulse rate and basal tear secretion were noted . 
Conjunctival blanching and mydriasis were commonly found . 
Upper lid retraction was frequently noted . 
While the elevations of the upper lid margin in most subjects were not more than 2 mm and did not cause noticeable change in appearance , one subject suffered from mechanical entropion and marked corneal abrasion 3 hours after instillation of the medication . 
This may well be a particularly notable finding in Asian people . 
<mark>Thiopentone</mark> pretreatment for <mark>propofol</mark> injection pain in ambulatory patients . 
This study investigated <mark>propofol</mark> injection pain in patients undergoing ambulatory anaesthesia . 
In a randomized , double - blind trial , 90 women were allocated to receive one of three treatments prior to induction of anaesthesia with <mark>propofol</mark> . 
Patients in Group C received 2 ml normal saline , Group L , 2 ml , <mark>lidocaine</mark> 2 % ( 40 mg ) and Group T , 2 ml <mark>thiopentone</mark> 2 . 5 % ( 50 mg ) . 
Venous discomfort was assessed with a visual analogue scale ( VAS ) 5 - 15 sec after commencing <mark>propofol</mark> administration using an infusion pump ( rate 1000 micrograms . kg - 1 . min - 1 ) . 
Loss of consciousness occurred in 60 - 90 sec . 
Visual analogue scores ( mean + / - SD ) during induction were lower in Groups L ( 3 . 3 + / - 2 . 5 ) and T ( 4 . 1 + / - 2 . 7 ) than in Group C ( 5 . 6 + / - 2 . 3 ) ; P = 0 . 0031 . 
The incidence of venous discomfort was lower in Group L ( 76 . 6 % ; P < 0 . 05 ) than in Group C ( 100 % ) but not different from Group T ( 90 % ) . 
The VAS scores for recall of pain in the recovery room were correlated with the VAS scores during induction ( r = 0 . 7045 ; P < 0 . 0001 ) . 
Recovery room discharge times were similar : C ( 75 . 9 + / - 19 . 4 min ) ; L 73 . 6 + / - 21 . 6 min ) ; T ( 77 . 1 + / - 18 . 9 min ) . 
Assessing their overall satisfaction , 89 . 7 % would choose <mark>propofol</mark> anaesthesia again . 
We conclude that <mark>lidocaine</mark> reduces the incidence and severity of <mark>propofol</mark> injection pain in ambulatory patients whereas <mark>thiopentone</mark> only reduces its severity . 
Persistent paralysis after prolonged use of <mark>atracurium</mark> in the absence of corticosteroids . 
Neuromuscular blocking agents ( NMBAs ) are often used for patients requiring prolonged mechanical ventilation . 
Reports of persistent paralysis after the discontinuance of these drugs have most often involved aminosteroid - based NMBAs such as <mark>vecuronium bromide</mark> , especially when used in conjunction with corticosteroids . 
<mark>Atracurium besylate</mark> , a short - acting <mark>benzylisoquinolinium</mark> NMBA that is eliminated independently of renal or hepatic function , has also been associated with persistent paralysis , but only when used with corticosteroids . 
We report a case of <mark>atracurium</mark> - related paralysis persisting for approximately 50 hours in a patient who was not treated with corticosteroids . 
A phase I / II study of <mark>paclitaxel</mark> plus <mark>cisplatin</mark> as first - line therapy for head and neck cancers : preliminary results . 
Improved outcomes among patients with head and neck carcinomas require investigations of new drugs for induction therapy . 
Preliminary results of an Eastern Cooperative Oncology Group study of single - agent <mark>paclitaxel</mark> ( <mark>Taxol</mark> ; Bristol - Myers Squibb Company , Princeton , NJ ) reported a 37 % response rate in patients with head and neck cancer , and the <mark>paclitaxel</mark> / <mark>cisplatin</mark> combination has been used successfully and has significantly improved median response duration in ovarian cancer patients . 
We initiated a phase I / II trial to determine the response and toxicity of escalating <mark>paclitaxel</mark> doses combined with fixed - dose <mark>cisplatin</mark> with granulocyte colony - stimulating factor support in patients with untreated locally advanced inoperable head and neck carcinoma . 
To date , 23 men with a median age of 50 years and good performance status have entered the trial . 
Primary tumor sites were oropharynx , 10 patients ; hypopharynx , four ; larynx , two ; oral cavity , three ; unknown primary , two ; and nasal cavity and parotid gland , one each . 
Of 20 patients evaluable for toxicity , four had stage III and 16 had stage IV disease . 
Treatment , given every 21 days for a maximum of three cycles , consisted of <mark>paclitaxel</mark> by 3 - hour infusion followed the next day by a fixed dose of <mark>cisplatin</mark> ( 75 mg / m2 ) . 
The dose levels incorporate escalating <mark>paclitaxel</mark> doses , and intrapatient escalations within a given dose level are permitted if toxicity permits . 
At the time of this writing , dose level 4 ( 260 , 270 , and 280 mg / m2 ) is being evaluated ; three patients from this level are evaluable . 
With <mark>paclitaxel</mark> doses of 200 mg / m2 and higher , granulocyte colony - stimulating factor 5 micrograms / kg / d is given ( days 4 through 12 ) . 
Of 18 patients evaluable for response , seven ( 39 % ) achieved a complete response and six ( 33 % ) achieved a partial response . 
Three patients had no change and disease progressed in two . 
The overall response rate is 72 % . 
Eleven responding patients had subsequent surgery / radiotherapy or radical radiotherapy . 
Two pathologic complete responses were observed in patients who had achieved clinical complete responses . 
Alopecia , paresthesias , and arthralgias / myalgias have occurred frequently , but with one exception ( a grade 3 myalgia ) they have been grade 1 or 2 . 
No dose - limiting hematologic toxicity has been seen . 
<mark>Paclitaxel</mark> / <mark>cisplatin</mark> is an effective first - line regimen for locoregionally advanced head and neck cancer and continued study is warranted . 
Results thus far suggest no dose - response effect for <mark>paclitaxel</mark> doses above 200 mg / m2 . 
Improvement of <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced dyskinesia by <mark>propranolol</mark> in Parkinson ' s disease . 
Seven patients suffering from Parkinson ' s disease ( PD ) with severely disabling dyskinesia received low - dose <mark>propranolol</mark> as an adjunct to the currently used medical treatment . 
There was a significant 40 % improvement in the dyskinesia score without increase of parkinsonian motor disability . 
Ballistic and choreic dyskinesia were markedly ameliorated , whereas dystonia was not . 
This study suggests that administration of low doses of beta - blockers may improve <mark>levodopa</mark> - induced ballistic and choreic dyskinesia in PD . 
Habitual use of <mark>acetaminophen</mark> as a risk factor for chronic renal failure : a comparison with <mark>phenacetin</mark> . 
Six epidemiologic studies in the United States and Europe indicate that habitual use of <mark>phenacetin</mark> is associated with the development of chronic renal failure and end - stage renal disease ( ESRD ) , with a relative risk in the range of 4 to 19 . 
As a result of these and other studies , <mark>phenacetin</mark> has now been withdrawn from the market in most countries . 
However , three case control studies , one each in North Carolina , northern Maryland , and West Berlin , Germany , showed that habitual use of <mark>acetaminophen</mark> is also associated with chronic renal failure and ESRD , with a relative risk in the range of 2 to 4 . 
These studies suggest that both <mark>phenacetin</mark> and <mark>acetaminophen</mark> may contribute to the burden of ESRD , with the risk of the latter being somewhat less than that of the former . 
This apparent difference in risk may not be due to differences in nephrotoxic potential of the drugs themselves . 
A lower relative risk would be expected for <mark>acetaminophen</mark> if the risk of both drugs in combination with other analgesics was higher than the risk of either agent alone . 
Thus , <mark>acetaminophen</mark> has been used both as a single agent and in combination with other analgesics , whereas <mark>phenacetin</mark> was available only in combinations . 
The possibility that habitual use of <mark>acetaminophen</mark> alone increases the risk of ESRD has not been clearly demonstrated , but cannot be dismissed . 
<mark>Acetaminophen</mark> - induced hypotension . 
Through 30 years of widespread use , <mark>acetaminophen</mark> has been shown to be a remarkably safe medication in therapeutic dosages . 
The potential for <mark>acetaminophen</mark> to produce cardiovascular toxicities is very low . 
However , <mark>acetaminophen</mark> has been demonstrated to produce symptoms of anaphylaxis , including hypotension , in sensitive individuals . 
This article describes two critically ill patients in whom transient episodes of hypotension reproducibly developed after administration of <mark>acetaminophen</mark> . 
Other symptoms of allergic reactions were not clinically detectable . 
The hypotensive episodes were severe enough to require vasopressor administration . 
The reports illustrate the need for clinicians to consider <mark>acetaminophen</mark> in patients with hypotension of unknown origin . 
Reduction of <mark>heparan sulphate</mark> - associated anionic sites in the glomerular basement membrane of rats with <mark>streptozotocin</mark> - induced diabetic nephropathy . 
<mark>Heparan sulphate</mark> - associated anionic sites in the glomerular basement membrane were studied in rats 8 months after induction of diabetes by <mark>streptozotocin</mark> and in age - adn sex - matched control rats , employing the cationic dye <mark>cuprolinic blue</mark> . 
Morphometric analysis at the ultrastructural level was performed using a computerized image processor . 
The <mark>heparan sulphate</mark> specificity of the <mark>cuprolinic blue</mark> staining was demonstrated by <mark>glycosaminoglycan</mark> - degrading enzymes , showing that pretreatment of the sections with heparitinase abolished all staining , whereas chondroitinase ABC had no effect . 
The majority of anionic sites ( 74 % in diabetic and 81 % in control rats ) were found within the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane . 
A minority of anionic sites were scattered throughout the lamina densa and lamina rara interna , and were significantly smaller than those in the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane ( p < 0 . 001 and p < 0 . 01 for diabetic and control rats , respectively ) . 
Diabetic rats progressively developed albuminuria reaching 40 . 3 ( 32 . 2 - 62 . 0 ) mg / 24 h after 8 months in contrast to the control animals ( 0 . 8 ( 0 . 2 - 0 . 9 ) mg / 24 h , p < 0 . 002 ) . 
At the same time , the number of <mark>heparan sulphate</mark> anionic sites and the total anionic site surface ( number of anionic sites x mean anionic site surface ) in the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane was reduced by 19 % ( p < 0 . 021 ) and by 26 % ( p < 0 . 02 ) , respectively . 
Number and total anionic site surface in the remaining part of the glomerular basement membrane ( lamina densa and lamina rara interna ) were not significantly changed . 
We conclude that in <mark>streptozotocin</mark> - diabetic rats with an increased urinary albumin excretion , a reduced <mark>heparan sulphate</mark> charge barrier / density is found at the lamina rara externa of the glomerular basement membrane . 
Mediation of enhanced reflex vagal bradycardia by <mark>L - dopa</mark> via central <mark>dopamine</mark> formation in dogs . 
<mark>L - Dopa</mark> ( 5 mg / kg i . v . ) decreased blood pressure and heart rate after extracerebral decarboxylase inhibition with <mark>MK - 486</mark> ( 25 mg / kg i . v . ) in anesthetize <mark>MAO</mark> - inhibited dogs . 
In addition , reflex bradycardia caused by injected <mark>norepinephrine</mark> was significantly enhanced by <mark>L - dopa</mark> , <mark>DL - Threo - dihydroxyphenylserine</mark> had no effect on blood pressure , heart rate or reflex responses to <mark>norepinephrine</mark> . 
<mark>FLA - 63</mark> , a <mark>dopamine</mark> - beta - oxidase inhibitor , did not have any effect on the hypotension , bradycardia or reflex - enhancing effect of <mark>L - dopa</mark> . 
<mark>Pimozide</mark> did not affect the actions of <mark>L - dopa</mark> on blood pressure and heart rate but completely blocked the enhancement of reflexes . 
Removal of the carotid sinuses caused an elevation blood pressure and heart rate and abolished the negative chronotropic effect of <mark>norepinephrine</mark> . 
However , <mark>L - dopa</mark> restored the bradycardia caused by <mark>norepinephrine</mark> in addition to decreasing blood pressure and heart rate . 
<mark>5 - HTP</mark> ( 5 mg / kg i . v . ) decreased blood pressure and heart rate and decreased the reflex bradycardia to <mark>norepinephrine</mark> . 
It is concluded that <mark>L - dopa</mark> enhances reflex bradycardia through central alpha - receptor stimulation . 
Furthermore , the effects are mediated through <mark>dopamine</mark> rather than <mark>norepinephrine</mark> and do not require the carotid sinus baroreceptors . 
Microangiopathic hemolytic anemia complicating <mark>FK506</mark> ( <mark>tacrolimus</mark> ) therapy . 
We describe 3 episodes of microangiopathic hemolytic anemia ( MAHA ) in 2 solid organ recipients under <mark>FK506</mark> ( <mark>tacrolimus</mark> ) therapy . 
In both cases , discontinuation of <mark>FK506</mark> and treatment with plasma exchange , fresh frozen plasma replacement , <mark>corticosteroids</mark> , <mark>aspirin</mark> , and <mark>dipyridamole</mark> led to resolution of MAHA . 
In one patient , reintroduction of <mark>FK506</mark> led to rapid recurrence of MAHA . 
<mark>FK506</mark> - associated MAHA is probably rare but physicians must be aware of this severe complication . 
In our experience and according to the literature , <mark>FK506</mark> does not seem to cross - react with <mark>cyclosporin A</mark> ( <mark>CyA</mark> ) , an immuno - suppressive drug already known to induce MAHA . 
Effect of some anticancer drugs and combined chemotherapy on renal toxicity . 
The nephrotoxic action of anticancer drugs such as <mark>nitrogranulogen</mark> ( <mark>NG</mark> ) , <mark>methotrexate</mark> ( <mark>MTX</mark> ) , <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> ( <mark>5 - FU</mark> ) and <mark>cyclophosphamide</mark> ( <mark>CY</mark> ) administered alone or in combination [ <mark>MTX</mark> + <mark>5 - FU</mark> + <mark>CY</mark> ( CMF ) ] was evaluated in experiments on Wistar rats . 
After drug administration , <mark>creatinine</mark> concentrations in the plasma and in the urine of the rats were determined , as well as <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance . 
Histopathologic evaluation of the kidneys was also performed . 
After <mark>MTX</mark> administration a significant increase ( p = 0 . 0228 ) in the plasma <mark>creatinine</mark> concentration and a significant ( p = 0 . 0001 ) decrease in <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance was noted compared to controls . 
After the administration of <mark>NG</mark> , <mark>5 - FU</mark> and <mark>CY</mark> neither a statistically significant increase in <mark>creatinine</mark> concentration nor an increase in <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance was observed compared to the group receiving no cytostatics . 
Following polytherapy according to the CMF regimen , a statistically significant decrease ( p = 0 . 0343 ) in <mark>creatinine</mark> clearance was found , but <mark>creatinine</mark> concentration did not increase significantly compared to controls . 
<mark>CY</mark> caused hemorrhagic cystitis in 40 % of rats , but it did not cause this complication when combined with <mark>5 - FU</mark> and <mark>MTX</mark> . 
Histologic changes were found in rat kidneys after administration of <mark>MTX</mark> , <mark>CY</mark> and <mark>NG</mark> , while no such change was observed after <mark>5 - FU</mark> and joint administration of <mark>MTX</mark> + <mark>5 - FU</mark> + <mark>CY</mark> compared to controls . 
Our studies indicate that nephrotoxicity of <mark>MTX</mark> + <mark>5 - FU</mark> + <mark>CY</mark> administered jointly is lower than in monotherapy . 
The interpeduncular nucleus regulates <mark>nicotine</mark> ' s effects on free - field activity . 
Partial lesions were made with <mark>kainic acid</mark> in the interpeduncular nucleus of the ventral midbrain of the rat . 
Compared with sham - operated controls , lesions significantly ( p < 0 . 25 ) blunted the early ( < 60 min ) free - field locomotor hypoactivity caused by <mark>nicotine</mark> ( 0 . 5 mg kg ( - 1 ) , i . m . ) , enhanced the later ( 60 - 120 min ) <mark>nicotine</mark> - induced hyperactivity , and raised spontaneous nocturnal activity . 
Lesions reduced the extent of immunohistological staining for <mark>choline</mark> acetyltransferase in the interpeduncular nucleus ( p < 0 . 025 ) , but not for <mark>tyrosine</mark> hydroxylase in the surrounding catecholaminergic A10 region . 
We conclude that the interpeduncular nucleus mediates nicotinic depression of locomotor activity and dampens nicotinic arousal mechanisms located elsewhere in the brain . 
<mark>Lithium</mark> - associated cognitive and functional deficits reduced by a switch to <mark>divalproex sodium</mark> : a case series . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Lithium</mark> remains a first - line treatment for the acute and maintenance treatment of bipolar disorder . 
Although much has been written about the management of the more common adverse effects of <mark>lithium</mark> , such as polyuria and tremor , more subtle <mark>lithium</mark> side effects such as cognitive deficits , loss of creativity , and functional impairments remain understudied . 
This report summarizes our experience in switching bipolar patients from <mark>lithium</mark> to <mark>divalproex sodium</mark> to alleviate such cognitive and functional impairments . 
METHOD : Open , case series design . 
RESULTS : We report seven cases where substitution of <mark>lithium</mark> , either fully or partially , with <mark>divalproex sodium</mark> was extremely helpful in reducing the cognitive , motivational , or creative deficits attributed to <mark>lithium</mark> in our bipolar patients . 
CONCLUSION : In this preliminary report , <mark>divalproex sodium</mark> was a superior alternative to <mark>lithium</mark> in bipolar patients experiencing cognitive deficits , loss of creativity , and functional impairments . 
Effect of <mark>nifedipine</mark> on renal function in liver transplant recipients receiving <mark>tacrolimus</mark> . 
The effect of <mark>nifedipine</mark> on renal function in liver transplant recipients who were receiving <mark>tacrolimus</mark> was evaluated between January 1992 and January 1996 . 
Two groups of patients receiving <mark>tacrolimus</mark> were compared over a period of 1 year , one group comprising hypertensive patients who were receiving <mark>nifedipine</mark> , and the other comprising nonhypertensive patients not receiving <mark>nifedipine</mark> . 
The time from transplant to baseline was similar in all patients . 
<mark>Nifedipine</mark> significantly improved kidney function as indicated by a significant lowering of serum <mark>creatinine</mark> levels at 6 and 12 months . 
The observed positive impact of <mark>nifedipine</mark> on reducing the nephrotoxicity associated with <mark>tacrolimus</mark> in liver transplant recipients should be an important factor in selecting an agent to treat hypertension in this population . 
Alpha and beta coma in drug intoxication uncomplicated by cerebral hypoxia . 
Four patients who were rendered comatose or stuporous by drug intoxication , but who were not hypoxic , are described . 
Three patients received high doses of <mark>chlormethiazole</mark> for <mark>alcohol</mark> withdrawal symptoms , and one took a suicidal overdose of <mark>nitrazepam</mark> . 
The patient with <mark>nitrazepam</mark> overdose and two of those with <mark>chlormethiazole</mark> intoxication conformed to the criteria of ' alpha coma ' , showing non - reactive generalized or frontally predominant alpha activity in the EEG . 
The fourth patient who was unconscious after <mark>chlormethiazole</mark> administration exhibite generalized non - reactive activity in the slow beta range . 
All four recovered completely without neurological sequelae following the withdrawal of the offending agents . 
The similarities between the effects of structural lesions and pharmacological depression of the brain stem reticular formation are discussed . 
It is suggested that in both situations disturbed reticulo - thalamic interactions are important in the pathogenesis of alpha coma . 
It is concluded that when this electroencephalographic and behavioural picture is seen in drug intoxication , in the absence of significant hypoxaemia , a favourable outcome may be anticipated . 
Magnetic resonance volumetry of the cerebellum in epileptic patients after <mark>phenytoin</mark> overdosages . 
The aim of this study was to evaluate the relationship between <mark>phenytoin</mark> medication and cerebellar atrophy in patients who had experienced clinical intoxication . 
Five females and 6 males , 21 - 59 years of age , were examined with a 1 . 5 - T whole - body system using a circular polarized head coil . 
Conventional spin echo images were acquired in the sagittal and transverse orientation . 
In addition , we performed a high - resolution 3D gradient echo , T1 - weighted sequences at a 1 - mm slice thickness . 
The images were subsequently processed to obtain volumetric data for the cerebellum . 
Cerebellar volume for the patient group ranged between 67 . 66 and 131 . 08 ml ( mean 108 . 9 ml ) . 
In addition 3D gradient echo data sets from 10 healthy male and 10 healthy female age - matched volunteers were used to compare cerebellar volumes . 
Using linear regression we found that no correlation exists between seizure duration , elevation of <mark>phenytoin</mark> serum levels and cerebellar volume . 
However , multiple regression for the daily dosage , duration of <mark>phenytoin</mark> treatment and cerebellar volume revealed a correlation of these parameters . 
We conclude that <mark>phenytoin</mark> overdosage does not necessarily result in cerebellar atrophy and it is unlikely that <mark>phenytoin</mark> medication was the only cause of cerebellar atrophy in the remaining patients . 
Quantitative morphometric studies of the cerebellum provide valuable insights into the pathogenesis of cerebellar disorders . 
Late recovery of renal function in a woman with the hemolytic uremic syndrome . 
A case is reported of the hemolytic uremic syndrome ( HUS ) in a woman taking <mark>oral contraceptives</mark> . 
She was treated with <mark>heparin</mark> , <mark>dipyridamole</mark> and hemodialysis ; and after more than three months , her urinary output rose above 500 ml ; and six months after the onset of anuria , dialysis treatment was stopped . 
This case emphasizes the possibility that HUS in adults is not invariably irreversible and that , despite prolonged oliguria , recovery of renal function can be obtained . 
Therefore , in adult patients affected by HUS , dialysis should not be discontinued prematurely ; moreover , bilateral nephrectomy , for treatment of severe hypertension and microangiopathic hemolytic anemia , should be performed with caution . 
Morphological features of encephalopathy after chronic administration of the antiepileptic drug <mark>valproate</mark> to rats . 
A transmission electron microscopic study of capillaries in the cerebellar cortex . 
Long - term intragastric application of the antiepileptic drug <mark>sodium valproate</mark> ( Vupral " Polfa " ) at the effective dose of 200 mg / kg b . 
w . once daily to rats for 1 , 3 , 6 , 9 and 12 months revealed neurological disorders indicating cerebellum damage ( " <mark>valproate</mark> encephalopathy " ) . 
The first ultrastructural changes in structural elements of the blood - brain - barrier ( BBB ) in the cerebellar cortex were detectable after 3 months of the experiment . 
They became more severe in the later months of the experiment , and were most severe after 12 months , located mainly in the molecular layer of the cerebellar cortex . 
Lesions of the capillary included necrosis of endothelial cells . 
Organelles of these cells , in particular the mitochondria ( increased number and size , distinct degeneration of their matrix and cristae ) and Golgi apparatus were altered . 
Reduced size of capillary lumen and occlusion were caused by swollen endothelial cells which had <mark>luminal</mark> protrusions and swollen microvilli . 
Pressure on the vessel wall was produced by enlarged perivascular astrocytic processes . 
Fragments of necrotic endothelial cells were in the vascular lumens and in these there was loosening and breaking of tight cellular junctions . 
Damage to the vascular basement lamina was also observed . 
Damage to the capillary was accompanied by marked damage to neuroglial cells , mainly to perivascular processes of astrocytes . 
The proliferation of astrocytes ( Bergmann ' s in particular ) and occasionally of oligodendrocytes was found . 
Alterations in the structural elements of the BBB coexisted with marked lesions of neurons of the cerebellum ( Purkinje cells are earliest ) . 
In electron micrographs both <mark>luminal</mark> and antiluminal sides of the BBB of the cerebellar cortex had similar lesions . 
The possible influence of the hepatic damage , mainly hyperammonemia , upon the development of <mark>valproate</mark> encephalopathy is discussed . 
Fatal intracranial bleeding associated with prehospital use of <mark>epinephrine</mark> . 
We present a case of paramedic misjudgment in the execution of a protocol for the treatment of allergic reaction in a case of pulmonary edema with wheezing . 
The sudden onset of respiratory distress , rash , and a history of a new medicine led the two paramedics on the scene to administer subcutaneous <mark>epinephrine</mark> . 
Subsequently , acute cardiac arrest and fatal subarachnoid hemorrhage occurred . 
<mark>Epinephrine</mark> has a proven role in cardiac arrest in prehospital care ; however , use by paramedics in patients with suspected allergic reaction and severe hypertension should be viewed with caution . 
Role of activation of <mark>bradykinin</mark> B2 receptors in disruption of the blood - brain barrier during acute hypertension . 
Cellular mechanisms which account for disruption the blood - brain barrier during acute hypertension are not clear . 
The goal of this study was to determine the role of synthesis / release of <mark>bradykinin</mark> to activate B2 receptors in disruption of the blood - brain barrier during acute hypertension . 
Permeability of the blood - brain barrier was quantitated by clearance of fluorescent - labeled <mark>dextran</mark> before and during <mark>phenylephrine</mark> - induced acute hypertension in rats treated with vehicle and <mark>Hoe - 140</mark> ( 0 . 1 microM ) . 
<mark>Phenylephrine</mark> infusion increased arterial pressure , arteriolar diameter and clearance of fluorescent <mark>dextran</mark> by a similar magnitude in both groups . 
These findings suggest that disruption of the blood - brain barrier during acute hypertension is not related to the synthesis / release of <mark>bradykinin</mark> to activate B2 receptors . 
Risk factors of sensorineural hearing loss in preterm infants . 
Among 547 preterm infants of < or = 34 weeks gestation born between 1987 and 1991 , 8 children ( 1 . 46 % ) developed severe progressive and bilateral sensorineural hearing loss . 
Perinatal risk factors of infants with hearing loss were compared with those of two control groups matched for gestation and birth weight and for perinatal complications . 
Our observations demonstrated an association of hearing loss with a higher incidence of perinatal complications . 
Ototoxicity appeared closely related to a prolonged administration and higher total dose of ototoxic drugs , particularly <mark>aminoglycosides</mark> and <mark>furosemide</mark> . 
Finally , we strongly recommend to prospectively and regularly perform audiologic assessment in sick preterm children as hearing loss is of delayed onset and in most cases bilateral and severe . 
Seizure resulting from a <mark>venlafaxine</mark> overdose . 
OBJECTIVE : To report a case of <mark>venlafaxine</mark> overdose . 
CASE SUMMARY : A 40 - year - old woman with major depression took an overdose of <mark>venlafaxine</mark> in an apparent suicide attempt . 
After the ingestion of 26 <mark>venlafaxine</mark> 50 - mg tablets , the patient experienced a witnessed generalized seizure . 
She was admitted to the medical intensive care unit , <mark>venlafaxine</mark> was discontinued , and no further sequelae were seen . 
DISCUSSION : To our knowledge , this is the first reported case of <mark>venlafaxine</mark> overdose that resulted in a generalized seizure . 
Based on nonoverdose pharmacokinetics and pharmacodynamics of <mark>venlafaxine</mark> and the potential risks of available interventions , no emergent therapy was instituted . 
CONCLUSIONS : The <mark>venlafaxine</mark> overdose in our patient resulted in a single episode of generalized seizure but elicited no further sequelae . 
Combined effects of prolonged <mark>prostaglandin E1</mark> - induced hypotension and haemodilution on human hepatic function . 
Combined effects of prolonged <mark>prostaglandin E1</mark> ( <mark>PGE1</mark> ) - induced hypotension and haemodilution on hepatic function were studied in 30 patients undergoing hip surgery . 
The patients were randomly allocated to one of three groups ; those in group A ( n = 10 ) were subjected to controlled hypotension alone , those in group B ( n = 10 ) to haemodilution alone and those in group C ( n = 10 ) to both controlled hypotension and haemodilution .
