Haemodilution in groups B and C was produced by withdrawing approximately 1000 mL of blood and replacing it with the same amount of <mark>dextran</mark> solution , and final haematocrit values were 21 or 22 % . 
Controlled hypotension in groups A and C was induced with <mark>PGE1</mark> to maintain mean arterial blood pressure at 55 mmHg for 180 min . 
Measurements included arterial ketone body ratio ( AKBR , <mark>aceto - acetate</mark> / <mark>3 - hydroxybutyrate</mark> ) and clinical hepatic function parameters . 
AKBR and biological hepatic function tests showed no change throughout the time course in groups A and B . 
In group C , AKBR showed a significant decrease at 120 min ( - 40 % ) and at 180 min ( - 49 % ) after the start of hypotension and at 60 min ( - 32 % ) after recovery of normotension , and SGOT , SGPT , LDH and total <mark>bilirubin</mark> showed significant increases after operation . 
The results suggest that a prolonged combination of more than 120 min of <mark>PGE1</mark> - induced hypotension and moderate haemodilution would cause impairment of hepatic function . 
Cardiovascular alterations in rat fetuses exposed to <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers . 
Preclinical toxicologic investigation suggested that a new <mark>calcium</mark> channel blocker , <mark>Ro 40 - 5967</mark> , induced cardiovascular alterations in rat fetuses exposed to this agent during organogenesis . 
The present study was designed to investigate the hypothesis that <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers in general induce cardiovascular malformations indicating a pharmacologic class effect . 
We studied three <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers of different structure , <mark>nifedipine</mark> , <mark>diltiazem</mark> , and <mark>verapamil</mark> , along with the new agent . 
Pregnant rats were administered one of these <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers during the period of cardiac morphogenesis and the offspring examined on day 20 of gestation for cardiovascular malformations . 
A low incidence of cardiovascular malformations was observed after exposure to each of the four <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers , but this incidence was statistically significant only for <mark>verapamil</mark> and <mark>nifedipine</mark> . 
All four agents were associated with aortic arch branching variants , although significantly increased only for <mark>Ro 40 - 5967</mark> and <mark>verapamil</mark> . 
The site of common side effects of <mark>sumatriptan</mark> . 
Atypical sensations following the use of subcutaneous <mark>sumatriptan</mark> are common , but of uncertain origin . 
They are almost always benign , but can be mistaken for a serious adverse event by the patient . 
Two patients are presented with tingling or burning sensations limited to areas of heat exposure or sunburn . 
In these individuals , side effects are most likely generated superficially in the skin . 
Macula toxicity after intravitreal <mark>amikacin</mark> . 
BACKGROUND : Although intravitreal <mark>aminoglycosides</mark> have substantially improved visual prognosis in endophthalmitis , macular infarction may impair full visual recovery . 
METHODS : We present a case of presumed <mark>amikacin</mark> retinal toxicity following treatment with <mark>amikacin</mark> and <mark>vancomycin</mark> for alpha - haemolytic streptococcal endophthalmitis . 
RESULTS : Endophthalmitis resolved with improvement in visual acuity to 6 / 24 at three months . 
Fundus <mark>fluorescein</mark> angiography confirmed macular capillary closure and telangiectasis . 
CONCLUSIONS : Currently accepted intravitreal antibiotic regimens may cause retinal toxicity and macular ischaemia . 
Treatment strategies aimed at avoiding retinal toxicity are discussed . 
The role of <mark>nicotine</mark> in smoking - related cardiovascular disease . 
<mark>Nicotine</mark> activates the sympathetic nervous system and in this way could contribute to cardiovascular disease . 
Animal studies and mechanistic studies indicate that <mark>nicotine</mark> could play a role in accelerating atherosclerosis , but evidence among humans is too inadequate to be definitive about such an effect . 
Almost certainly , <mark>nicotine</mark> via its hemodynamic effects contributes to acute cardiovascular events , although current evidence suggests that the effects of <mark>nicotine</mark> are much less important than are the prothrombotic effects of cigarette smoking or the effects of <mark>carbon monoxide</mark> . 
<mark>Nicotine</mark> does not appear to enhance thrombosis among humans . 
Clinical studies of pipe smokers and people using transdermal <mark>nicotine</mark> support the idea that toxins other than <mark>nicotine</mark> are the most important causes of acute cardiovascular events . 
Finally , the dose response for cardiovascular events of <mark>nicotine</mark> appears to be flat , suggesting that if <mark>nicotine</mark> is involved , adverse effects might be seen with relatively low - level cigarette exposures . 
Iatrogenically induced intractable atrioventricular reentrant tachycardia after <mark>verapamil</mark> and catheter ablation in a patient with Wolff - Parkinson - White syndrome and idiopathic dilated cardiomyopathy . 
In a patient with WPW syndrome and idiopathic dilated cardiomyopathy , intractable atrioventricular reentrant tachycardia ( AVRT ) was iatrogenically induced . 
QRS without preexcitation , caused by junctional escape beats after <mark>verapamil</mark> or unidirectional antegrade block of accessory pathway after catheter ablation , established frequent AVRT attack . 
Epidemic of liver disease caused by <mark>hydrochlorofluorocarbons</mark> used as <mark>ozone</mark> - sparing substitutes of <mark>chlorofluorocarbons</mark> . 
BACKGROUND : <mark>Hydrochlorofluorocarbons</mark> ( <mark>HCFCs</mark> ) are used increasingly in industry as substitutes for <mark>ozone</mark> - depleting <mark>chlorofluorocarbons</mark> ( <mark>CFCs</mark> ) . 
Limited studies in animals indicate potential hepatotoxicity of some of these compounds . 
We investigated an epidemic of liver disease in nine industrial workers who had had repeated accidental exposure to a mixture of <mark>1 , 1 - dichloro - 2 , 2 , 2 - trifluoroethane</mark> ( <mark>HCFC 123</mark> ) and <mark>1 - chloro - 1 , 2 , 2 , 2 - tetrafluoroethane</mark> ( <mark>HCFC 124</mark> ) . 
All nine exposed workers were affected to various degrees . 
Both compounds are metabolised in the same way as <mark>1 - bromo - 1 - chloro - 2 , 2 , 2 - trifluoroethane</mark> ( <mark>halothane</mark> ) to form reactive <mark>trifluoroacetyl</mark> halide intermediates , which have been implicated in the hepatotoxicity of <mark>halothane</mark> . 
We aimed to test whether <mark>HCFCs 123 and 124</mark> can result in serious liver disease . 
METHODS : For one severely affected worker liver biopsy and immunohistochemical stainings for the presence of <mark>trifluoroacetyl</mark> protein adducts were done . 
The serum of six affected workers and five controls was tested for autoantibodies that react with human liver cytochrome - P450 2E1 ( P450 2E1 ) and P58 protein disulphide isomerase isoform ( P58 ) . 
FINDINGS : The liver biopsy sample showed hepatocellular necrosis which was prominent in perivenular zone three and extended focally from portal tracts to portal tracts and centrilobular areas ( bridging necrosis ) . 
<mark>Trifluoroacetyl</mark> - adducted proteins were detected in surviving hepatocytes . 
Autoantibodies against P450 2E1 or P58 , previously associated with halothane hepatitis , were detected in the serum of five affected workers . 
INTERPRETATION : Repeated exposure of human beings to <mark>HCFCs 123 and 124</mark> can result in serious liver injury in a large proportion of the exposed population . 
Although the exact mechanism of hepatotoxicity of these agents is not known , the results suggest that <mark>trifluoroacetyl</mark> - altered liver proteins are involved . 
In view of the potentially widespread use of these compounds , there is an urgent need to develop safer alternatives . 
Bile duct hamartoma occurring in association with long - term treatment with <mark>danazol</mark> . 
We report a case of bile duct hamartoma which developed in a patient who had been on long - term <mark>danazol</mark> treatment . 
Such patients should be under close follow - up , preferably with periodic ultrasound examination of the liver . 
If the patient develops a liver mass , because of non - specific clinical features and imaging appearances , biopsy may be the only way to achieve a definitive diagnosis . 
Endocrine screening in 1 , 022 men with erectile dysfunction : clinical significance and cost - effective strategy . 
PURPOSE : We reviewed the results of serum <mark>testosterone</mark> and prolactin determination in 1 , 022 patients referred because of erectile dysfunction and compared the data with history , results of physical examination , other etiological investigations and effects of endocrine therapy to refine the rules of cost - effective endocrine screening and to pinpoint actual responsibility for hormonal abnormalities . 
MATERIALS AND METHODS : <mark>Testosterone</mark> and prolactin were determined by radioimmunoassay . 
Every patient was screened for <mark>testosterone</mark> and 451 were screened for prolactin on the basis of low sexual desire , gynecomastia or <mark>testosterone</mark> less than 4 ng . / ml . 
Determination was repeated in case of abnormal first results . 
Prolactin results were compared with those of a previous personal cohort of 1 , 340 patients with erectile dysfunction and systematic prolactin determination . 
Main clinical criteria tested regarding efficiency in hormone determination were low sexual desire , small testes and gynecomastia . 
Endocrine therapy consisted of <mark>testosterone heptylate</mark> or human chorionic gonadotropin for hypogonadism and <mark>bromocriptine</mark> for hyperprolactinemia . 
RESULTS : <mark>Testosterone</mark> was less than 3 ng . / ml . in 107 patients but normal in 40 % at repeat determination . 
The prevalence of repeatedly low <mark>testosterone</mark> increased with age ( 4 % before age 50 years and 9 % 50 years or older ) . 
Two pituitary tumors were discovered after <mark>testosterone</mark> determination . 
Most of the other low <mark>testosterone</mark> levels seemed to result from nonorganic hypothalamic dysfunction because of normal serum luteinizing hormone and prolactin and to have only a small role in erectile dysfunction ( definite improvement in only 16 of 44 [ 36 % ] after androgen therapy , normal morning or nocturnal erections in 30 % and definite vasculogenic contributions in 42 % ) . 
Determining <mark>testosterone</mark> only in cases of low sexual desire or abnormal physical examination would have missed 40 % of the cases with low <mark>testosterone</mark> , including 37 % of those subsequently improved by androgen therapy . 
Prolactin exceeded 20 ng . / ml . in 5 men and was normal in 2 at repeat determination . 
Only 1 prolactinoma was discovered . 
These data are lower than those we found during the last 2 decades ( overall prolactin greater than 20 ng . / ml . in 1 . 86 % of 1 , 821 patients , prolactinomas in 7 , 0 . 38 % ) . 
<mark>Bromocriptine</mark> was definitely effective in cases with prolactin greater than 35 ng . / ml . 
( 8 of 12 compared to only 9 of 22 cases with prolactin between 20 and 35 ng . / ml . ) . 
<mark>Testosterone</mark> was low in less than 50 % of cases with prolactin greater than 35 ng . / ml . 
CONCLUSIONS : Low prevalences and effects of low <mark>testosterone</mark> and high prolactin in erectile dysfunction cannot justify their routine determination . 
However , cost - effective screening strategies recommended so far missed 40 to 50 % of cases improved with endocrine therapy and the pituitary tumors . 
We now advocate that before age 50 years <mark>testosterone</mark> be determined only in cases of low sexual desire and abnormal physical examination but that it be measured in all men older than 50 years . 
Prolactin should be determined only in cases of low sexual desire , gynecomastia and / or <mark>testosterone</mark> less than 4 ng . / ml . 
Extrapyramidal side effects with <mark>risperidone</mark> and <mark>haloperidol</mark> at comparable D2 receptor occupancy levels . 
<mark>Risperidone</mark> is an antipsychotic drug with high affinity at <mark>dopamine</mark> D2 and <mark>serotonin 5 - HT2</mark> receptors . 
Previous clinical studies have proposed that <mark>risperidone</mark> ' s pharmacologic profile may produce improved efficacy for negative psychotic symptoms and decreased propensity for extrapyramidal side effects ; features shared by so - called ' atypical ' neuroleptics . 
To determine if routine <mark>risperidone</mark> treatment is associated with a unique degree of D2 receptor occupancy and pattern of clinical effects , we used [ 123I ] IBZM SPECT to determine D2 occupancy in subjects treated with routine clinical doses of <mark>risperidone</mark> ( n = 12 ) or <mark>haloperidol</mark> ( n = 7 ) . 
Both <mark>risperidone</mark> and <mark>haloperidol</mark> produced D2 occupancy levels between approximately 60 and 90 % at standard clinical doses . 
There was no significant difference between occupancy levels obtained with <mark>haloperidol</mark> or <mark>risperidone</mark> . 
Drug - induced parkinsonism was observed in subjects treated with <mark>risperidone</mark> ( 42 % ) and <mark>haloperidol</mark> ( 29 % ) and was observed at occupancy levels above 60 % . 
Based on these observations , it is concluded that 5 - HT2 blockade obtained with <mark>risperidone</mark> at D2 occupancy rates of 60 % and above does not appear to protect against the risk for extrapyramidal side effects . 
Treatment of previously treated metastatic breast cancer by <mark>mitoxantrone</mark> and 48 - hour continuous infusion of high - dose <mark>5 - FU</mark> and <mark>leucovorin</mark> ( <mark>MFL</mark> ) : low palliative benefit and high treatment - related toxicity . 
For previously treated advanced breast cancer , there is no standard second - line therapy . 
Combination chemotherapy with <mark>mitoxantrone</mark> , high - dose <mark>5 - fluorouracil</mark> ( <mark>5 - FU</mark> ) and <mark>leucovorin</mark> ( <mark>MFL regimen</mark> ) had been reported as an effective and well tolerated regimen . 
From October 1993 to November 1995 , we treated 13 patients with previously chemotherapy - treated metastatic breast cancer by <mark>mitoxantrone</mark> , 12 mg / m2 , on day 1 and continuous infusion of <mark>5 - FU</mark> , 3000 mg / m2 , together with <mark>leucovorin</mark> , 300 mg / m2 , for 48 h from day 1 to 2 . 
Each course of chemotherapy was given every 4 weeks . 
Most of these patients had more than two metastatic sites , with lung metastasis predominant . 
Seven patients had been treated with <mark>anthracycline</mark> . 
Seven patients had previously received radiotherapy and seven had received hormone therapy . 
Median number of courses of <mark>MFL regimen</mark> given was six and the median cumulative dose of <mark>mitoxantrone</mark> was 68 . 35 mg / m2 . 
One patient had complete response , seven had stable disease , none had partial response and five had progressive disease . 
The overall objective response rate was 7 . 6 % . 
The median follow - up period was 14 months . 
Median survival was 16 months . 
Median progression - free survival was 5 months . 
A complete responder had relapse - free survival up to 17 months . 
Major toxicities were cardiotoxicity and leukopenia . 
Eight patients were dead in the last follow - up ; two of them died of treatment - related toxicity . 
The <mark>MFL regimen</mark> achieves little palliative benefit and induces severe toxicity at a fairly high rate . 
Administration of this regimen to breast cancer patients who have been treated by chemotherapy and those with impaired heart function requires careful attention . 
<mark>Ticlopidine</mark> - induced aplastic anemia : report of three Chinese patients and review of the literature . 
In this study , three Chinese patients with <mark>ticlopidine</mark> - induced aplastic anemia were reported and another 13 patients in the English literature were reviewed . 
We attempted to find underlying similarities , evaluate the risk factors , and identify appropriate treatment for this complication . 
All but one of the patients were over 60 years old , and the 6 who died were all older than 65 . 
Therefore , old age may be a risk factor for developing this complication . 
Agranulocytosis occurred 3 - 20 weeks after initiation of <mark>ticlopidine</mark> , so frequent examination of white cell count during treatment is recommended . 
There seemed to be no direct correlation between the dose or duration used and the severity of bone marrow suppression . 
Treatment for <mark>ticlopidine</mark> - induced aplastic anemia with colony - stimulating factors seemed to have little effect . 
The fact that 5 of the 6 patients who received concurrent <mark>calcium</mark> channel blockers died , should alert clinicians to be more cautious when using these two drugs simultaneously . 
Upregulation of the expression of <mark>vasopressin</mark> gene in the paraventricular and supraoptic nuclei of the <mark>lithium</mark> - induced diabetes insipidus rat . 
The expression of <mark>arginine vasopressin</mark> ( <mark>AVP</mark> ) gene in the paraventricular ( PVN ) and supraoptic nuclei ( SON ) was investigated in rats with <mark>lithium</mark> ( <mark>Li</mark> ) - induced polyuria , using in situ hybridization histochemistry and radioimmunoassay . 
The male Wistar rats consuming a diet that contained <mark>LiCl</mark> ( 60 mmol / kg ) for 4 weeks developed marked polyuria . 
The <mark>Li</mark> - treated rats produced a large volume of hypotonic urine with low ionic concentrations . 
Plasma <mark>sodium</mark> concentrations were found to be slightly increased in the <mark>Li</mark> - treated rats compared with those in controls . 
Plasma concentration of <mark>AVP</mark> and transcripts of <mark>AVP</mark> gene in the PVN and SON were significantly increased in the <mark>Li</mark> - treated rats compared with controls . 
These results suggest that dehydration and / or the activation of visceral afferent inputs may contribute to the elevation of plasma <mark>AVP</mark> and the upregulation of <mark>AVP</mark> gene expression in the PVN and the SON of the <mark>Li</mark> - induced diabetes insipidus rat . 
Antinociceptive and antiamnesic properties of the presynaptic cholinergic amplifier <mark>PG - 9</mark> . 
The antinociceptive effect of <mark>3 alpha - tropyl 2 - ( p - bromophenyl ) propionate</mark> [ ( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> ] ( 10 - 40 mg kg - 1 s . c . ; 30 - 60 mg kg - 1 p . o . ; 10 - 30 mg kg - 1 i . v . ; 10 - 30 micrograms / mouse i . c . v . ) was examined in mice , rats and guinea pigs by use of the hot - plate , abdominal - constriction , tail - flick and paw - pressure tests . 
( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> antinociception peaked 15 min after injection and then slowly diminished . 
The antinociception produced by ( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> was prevented by the unselective muscarinic antagonist <mark>atropine</mark> , the M1 - selective antagonists <mark>pirenzepine</mark> and <mark>dicyclomine</mark> and the <mark>acetylcholine</mark> depletor <mark>hemicholinium - 3</mark> , but not by the opioid antagonist <mark>naloxone</mark> , the <mark>gamma - aminobutyric acidB</mark> antagonist <mark>3 - aminopropyl - diethoxy - methyl - phosphinic acid</mark> , the H3 agonist <mark>R - ( alpha ) - methylhistamine</mark> , the D2 antagonist <mark>quinpirole</mark> , the <mark>5 - hydroxytryptamine4</mark> antagonist <mark>2 - methoxy - 4 - amino - 5 - chlorobenzoic acid 2 - ( diethylamino ) ethyl ester</mark> hydrochloride , the <mark>5 - hydroxytryptamin1A</mark> antagonist <mark>1 - ( 2 - methoxyphenyl ) - 4 - [ 4 - ( 2 - phthalimido ) butyl ] piperazine</mark> hydrobromide and the polyamines depletor <mark>reserpine</mark> . 
Based on these data , it can be postulated that ( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> exerted an antinociceptive effect mediated by a central potentiation of cholinergic transmission . 
( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> ( 10 - 40 mg kg - 1 i . p . ) was able to prevent amnesia induced by <mark>scopolamine</mark> ( 1 mg kg - 1 i . p . ) and <mark>dicyclomine</mark> ( 2 mg kg - 1 i . p . ) in the mouse passive - avoidance test . 
Affinity profiles of ( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> for muscarinic receptor subtypes , determined by functional studies ( rabbit vas deferens for M1 , guinea pig atrium for M2 , guinea pig ileum for M3 and immature guinea pig uterus for putative M4 ) , have shown an M4 / M1 selectivity ratio of 10 . 2 that might be responsible for the antinociception and the anti - amnesic effect induced by ( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> through an increase in <mark>acetylcholine</mark> extracellular levels . 
In the antinociceptive and antiamnesic dose range , ( + / - ) - <mark>PG - 9</mark> did not impair mouse performance evaluated by the rota - rod test and Animex apparatus . 
The effect of different anaesthetic agents in hearing loss following spinal anaesthesia . 
The cause of hearing loss after spinal anaesthesia is unknown . 
Up until now , the only factor studied has been the effect of the diameter of the spinal needle on post - operative sensorineural hearing loss . 
The aim of this study was to describe this hearing loss and to investigate other factors influencing the degree of hearing loss . 
Two groups of 22 similar patients were studied : one group received 6 mL <mark>prilocaine</mark> 2 % ; and the other received 3 mL <mark>bupivacaine</mark> 0 . 5 % . 
Patients given <mark>prilocaine</mark> were more likely to develop hearing loss ( 10 out of 22 ) than those given <mark>bupivacaine</mark> ( 4 out of 22 ) ( P < 0 . 05 ) . 
The average hearing loss for speech frequencies was about 10 dB after <mark>prilocaine</mark> and 15 dB after <mark>bupivacaine</mark> . 
None of the patients complained of subjective hearing loss . 
Long - term follow - up of the patients was not possible . 
A transient neurological deficit following intrathecal injection of 1 % hyperbaric <mark>bupivacaine</mark> for unilateral spinal anaesthesia . 
We describe a case of transient neurological deficit that occurred after unilateral spinal anaesthesia with 8 mg of 1 % hyperbaric <mark>bupivacaine</mark> slowly injected through a 25 - gauge pencil - point spinal needle . 
The surgery and anaesthesia were uneventful , but 3 days after surgery , the patient reported an area of hypoaesthesia over L3 - L4 dermatomes of the leg which had been operated on ( loss of pinprick sensation ) without reduction in muscular strength . 
Sensation in this area returned to normal over the following 2 weeks . 
Prospective multicentre studies with a large population and a long follow - up should be performed in order to evaluate the incidence of this unusual side effect . 
However , we suggest that a low solution concentration should be preferred for unilateral spinal anaesthesia with a hyperbaric anaesthetic solution ( if pencil - point needle and slow injection rate are employed ) , in order to minimize the risk of a localized high peak anaesthetic concentration , which might lead to a transient neurological deficit . 
Transient neurologic symptoms after spinal anesthesia : a lower incidence with <mark>prilocaine</mark> and <mark>bupivacaine</mark> than with <mark>lidocaine</mark> . 
BACKGROUND : Recent evidence suggests that transient neurologic symptoms ( TNSs ) frequently follow <mark>lidocaine</mark> spinal anesthesia but are infrequent with <mark>bupivacaine</mark> . 
However , identification of a short - acting local anesthetic to substitute for <mark>lidocaine</mark> for brief surgical procedures remains an important goal . 
<mark>Prilocaine</mark> is an amide local anesthetic with a duration of action similar to that of <mark>lidocaine</mark> . 
Accordingly , the present , prospective double - blind study compares <mark>prilocaine</mark> with <mark>lidocaine</mark> and <mark>bupivacaine</mark> with respect to duration of action and relative risk of TNSs . 
METHODS : Ninety patients classified as American Society of Anesthesiologists physical status I or II who were scheduled for short gynecologic procedures under spinal anesthesia were randomly allocated to receive 2 . 5 ml 2 % <mark>lidocaine</mark> in 7 . 5 % <mark>glucose</mark> , 2 % <mark>prilocaine</mark> in 7 . 5 % <mark>glucose</mark> , or 0 . 5 % <mark>bupivacaine</mark> in 7 . 5 % <mark>glucose</mark> . 
All solutions were provided in blinded vials by the hospital pharmacy . 
Details of spinal puncture , extension and regression of spinal block , and the times to reach discharge criteria were noted . 
In the evening of postoperative day 1 , patients were evaluated for TNSs by a physician unaware of the drug administered and the details of the anesthetic procedure . 
RESULTS : Nine of 30 patients receiving <mark>lidocaine</mark> experienced TNSs , 1 of 30 patients receiving <mark>prilocaine</mark> ( P = 0 . 03 ) had them , and none of 30 patients receiving <mark>bupivacaine</mark> had TNSs . 
Times to ambulate and to void were similar after <mark>lidocaine</mark> and <mark>prilocaine</mark> ( 150 vs . 165 min and 238 vs . 253 min , respectively ) but prolonged after <mark>bupivacaine</mark> ( 200 and 299 min , respectively ; P < 0 . 05 ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : <mark>Prilocaine</mark> may be preferable to <mark>lidocaine</mark> for short surgical procedures because it has a similar duration of action but a lower incidence of TNSs . 
<mark>Suxamethonium</mark> - induced cardiac arrest and death following 5 days of immobilization . 
The present report describes a case of cardiac arrest and subsequent death as a result of hyperkalaemia following the use of <mark>suxamethonium</mark> in a 23 - year - old Malawian woman . 
Five days after the onset of the symptoms of meningitis , the patient aspirated stomach contents and needed endotracheal intubation . 
Forty seconds after injection of <mark>suxamethonium</mark> , bradycardia and cardiac arrest occurred . 
Attempts to resuscitate the patient were not successful . 
The serum level of <mark>potassium</mark> was observed to be 8 . 4 mequiv L - 1 . 
Apart from the reduction in the patient ' s level of consciousness , there were no signs of motor neurone damage or of any of the other known predisposing conditions for hyperkalaemia following the administration of <mark>suxamethonium</mark> . 
It is postulated that her death was caused by hypersensitivity to <mark>suxamethonium</mark> , associated with her 5 - day immobilization . 
Acute hepatitis , autoimmune hemolytic anemia , and erythroblastocytopenia induced by <mark>ceftriaxone</mark> . 
An 80 - yr - old man developed acute hepatitis shortly after ingesting oral <mark>ceftriaxone</mark> . 
Although the transaminases gradually returned to baseline after withholding the <mark>beta lactam</mark> antibiotic , there was a gradual increase in serum <mark>bilirubin</mark> and a decrease in hemoglobin concentration caused by an autoimmune hemolytic anemia and erythroblastocytopenia . 
These responded to systemic <mark>steroids</mark> and immunoglobulins . 
Despite the widespread use of these agents this triad of side effects has not previously been reported in connection with <mark>beta lactam</mark> antibiotics . 
<mark>Thyroxine</mark> abuse : an unusual case of thyrotoxicosis in pregnancy . 
Eating disorders and the associated behavioural problems and drug abuse are uncommon in pregnancy . 
When they do occur they are often unrecognized because of denial but when significant may pose a risk to both the mother and her fetus . 
This case illustrates a number of problems that may be encountered in women with eating disorders in pregnancy , including prolonged and recurrent metabolic disturbances and diuretic abuse . 
In particular it illustrates the derangements of thyroid function seen in pregnant women with eating disorders and reminds us that when a cause for thyrotoxicosis remains obscure , <mark>thyroxine</mark> abuse should be considered and explored . 
Repeated <mark>trimipramine</mark> induces <mark>dopamine</mark> D2 / D3 and alpha1 - adrenergic up - regulation . 
<mark>Trimipramine</mark> ( <mark>TRI</mark> ) , which shows a clinical <mark>antidepressant</mark> activity , is chemically related to <mark>imipramine</mark> but does not inhibit the reuptake of <mark>noradrenaline</mark> and <mark>5 - hydroxytryptamine</mark> , nor does it induce beta - adrenergic down - regulation . 
The mechanism of its <mark>antidepressant</mark> activity is still unknown . 
The aim of the present study was to find out whether <mark>TRI</mark> given repeatedly was able to induce adaptive changes in the dopaminergic and alpha1 - adrenergic systems , demonstrated by us previously for various <mark>antidepressants</mark> . 
<mark>TRI</mark> was given to male Wistar rats and male Albino Swiss mice perorally twice daily for 14 days . 
In the acute experiment <mark>TRI</mark> ( given i . p . ) does not antagonize the <mark>reserpine</mark> hypothermia in mice and does not potentiate the <mark>5 - hydroxytryptophan</mark> head twitches in rats . 
<mark>TRI</mark> given repeatedly to rats increases the locomotor hyperactivity induced by <mark>d - amphetamine</mark> , <mark>quinpirole</mark> and ( + ) - 7 - hydroxy - dipropyloaminotetralin ( <mark>dopamine</mark> D2 and D3 effects ) . 
The stereotypies induced by <mark>d - amphetamine</mark> or <mark>apomorphine</mark> are not potentiated by <mark>TRI</mark> . 
It increases the behaviour stimulation evoked by <mark>phenylephrine</mark> ( given intraventricularly ) in rats , evaluated in the open field test as well as the aggressiveness evoked by <mark>clonidine</mark> in mice , both these effects being mediated by an alpha1 - adrenergic receptor . 
It may be concluded that , like other tricyclic <mark>antidepressants</mark> studied previously , <mark>TRI</mark> given repeatedly increases the responsiveness of brain <mark>dopamine</mark> D2 and D3 ( locomotor activity but not stereotypy ) as well as alpha1 - adrenergic receptors to their agonists . 
A question arises whether the reuptake inhibition is of any importance to the adaptive changes induced by repeated <mark>antidepressants</mark> , suggested to be responsible for the <mark>antidepressant</mark> activity . 
<mark>Pethidine</mark> - associated seizure in a healthy adolescent receiving <mark>pethidine</mark> for postoperative pain control . 
A healthy 17 - year - old male received standard intermittent doses of <mark>pethidine</mark> via a patient - controlled analgesia ( PCA ) pump for management of postoperative pain control . 
Twenty - three h postoperatively he developed a brief self - limited seizure . 
Both plasma <mark>pethidine</mark> and <mark>norpethidine</mark> were elevated in the range associated with clinical manifestations of central nervous system excitation . 
No other risk factors for CNS toxicity were identified . 
This method allowed frequent self - dosing of <mark>pethidine</mark> at short time intervals and rapid accumulation of <mark>pethidine</mark> and <mark>norpethidine</mark> . 
The routine use of <mark>pethidine</mark> via PCA even for a brief postoperative analgesia should be reconsidered . 
An unusual toxic reaction to axillary block by <mark>mepivacaine</mark> with <mark>adrenaline</mark> . 
An increase in blood pressure , accompanied by atrial fibrillation , agitation , incomprehensible shouts and loss of consciousness , was observed in an elderly , ASA classification group II , cardiovascularly medicated male , 12 min after performance of axillary block with <mark>mepivacaine</mark> 850 mg containing <mark>adrenaline</mark> 0 . 225 mg , for correction of Dupuytren ' s contracture . 
After intravenous administration of <mark>labetalol</mark> , <mark>metoprolol</mark> and <mark>midazolam</mark> the patient ' s condition improved , and 15 min later he woke up . 
The block was successful and surgery was conducted as scheduled despite persisting atrial fibrillation . 
Postoperatively , the patient refused DC cardioversion and was treated medically . 
Both the temporal relationship of events and the response to treatment suggest that a rapid systemic absorption of <mark>mepivacaine</mark> with <mark>adrenaline</mark> and / or interaction of these drugs with the patient ' s cardiovascular medications were responsible for the perioperative complications . 
Drug - associated acute - onset vanishing bile duct and Stevens - Johnson syndromes in a child . 
Acute vanishing bile duct syndrome is a rare but established cause of progressive cholestasis in adults , is most often drug or toxin related , and is of unknown pathogenesis . 
It has not been reported previously in children . 
Stevens - Johnson syndrome is a well - recognized immune complex - mediated hypersensitivity reaction that affects all age groups , is drug or infection induced , and has classic systemic , mucosal , and dermatologic manifestations . 
A previously healthy child who developed acute , severe , rapidly progressive vanishing bile duct syndrome shortly after Stevens - Johnson syndrome is described ; this was temporally associated with <mark>ibuprofen</mark> use . 
Despite therapy with <mark>ursodeoxycholic acid</mark> , <mark>prednisone</mark> , and then <mark>tacrolimus</mark> , her cholestatic disease was unrelenting , with cirrhosis shown by biopsy 6 months after presentation . 
This case documents acute drug - related vanishing bile duct syndrome in the pediatric age group and suggests shared immune mechanisms in the pathogenesis of both Stevens - Johnson syndrome and vanishing bile duct syndrome . 
High incidence of primary pulmonary hypertension associated with <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> in Belgium . 
Primary pulmonary hypertension is a rare , progressive and incurable disease , which has been associated with the intake of <mark>appetite suppressant</mark> drugs . 
The importance of this association was evaluated in Belgium while this country still had no restriction on the prescription of <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> . 
Thirty - five patients with primary pulmonary hypertension and 85 matched controls were recruited over 32 months ( 1992 - 1994 ) in Belgium . 
Exposure to <mark>appetite - suppressants</mark> was assessed on the basis of hospital records and standardized interview . 
Twenty - three of the patients had previously taken <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> , mainly <mark>fenfluramines</mark> , as compared with only 5 of the controls ( 66 versus 6 % , p < 0 . 0001 ) . 
Five patients died before the interview , all of them had taken <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> . 
In 8 patients the diagnosis of primary pulmonary hypertension was uncertain , 5 of them had taken <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> . 
The patients who had been exposed to <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> tended to be on average more severely ill , and to have a shorter median delay between onset of symptoms and diagnosis . 
A policy of unrestricted prescription of <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> may lead to a high incidence of associated primary pulmonary hypertension . 
Intake of <mark>appetite suppressants</mark> may accelerate the progression of the disease . 
Inappropriate use of <mark>carbamazepine</mark> and <mark>vigabatrin</mark> in typical absence seizures . 
<mark>Carbamazepine</mark> and <mark>vigabatrin</mark> are contraindicated in typical absence seizures . 
Of 18 consecutive referrals of children with resistant typical absences only , eight were erroneously treated with <mark>carbamazepine</mark> either as monotherapy or as an add - on . 
<mark>Vigabatrin</mark> was also used in the treatment of two children . 
Frequency of absences increased in four children treated with <mark>carbamazepine</mark> and two of these developed myoclonic jerks , which resolved on withdrawal of <mark>carbamazepine</mark> . 
Absences were aggravated in both cases where <mark>vigabatrin</mark> was added on to concurrent treatment . 
Optimal control of the absences was achieved with <mark>sodium valproate</mark> , <mark>lamotrigine</mark> , or <mark>ethosuximide</mark> alone or in combination . 
Choreoathetoid movements associated with rapid adjustment to <mark>methadone</mark> . 
Choreatiform hyperkinesias are known to be occasional movement abnormalities during intoxications with <mark>cocaine</mark> but not opiates . 
This is a case report of euphoria and choreoathetoid movements both transiently induced by rapid adjustment to the selective mu - opioid receptor agonist <mark>methadone</mark> in an inpatient previously abusing <mark>heroine</mark> and <mark>cocaine</mark> . 
In addition , minor EEG abnormalities occurred . 
Possible underlying neurobiological phenomena are discussed . 
Adverse effects of the atypical antipsychotics . 
Collaborative Working Group on Clinical Trial Evaluations . 
Adverse effects of antipsychotics often lead to noncompliance . 
Thus , clinicians should address patients ' concerns about adverse effects and attempt to choose medications that will improve their patients ' quality of life as well as overall health . 
The side effect profiles of the atypical antipsychotics are more advantageous than those of the conventional neuroleptics . 
Conventional agents are associated with unwanted central nervous system effects , including extrapyramidal symptoms ( EPS ) , tardive dyskinesia , sedation , and possible impairment of some cognitive measures , as well as cardiac effects , orthostatic hypotension , hepatic changes , anticholinergic side effects , sexual dysfunction , and weight gain . 
The newer atypical agents have a lower risk of EPS , but are associated in varying degrees with sedation , cardiovascular effects , anticholinergic effects , weight gain , sexual dysfunction , hepatic effects , lowered seizure threshold ( primarily <mark>clozapine</mark> ) , and agranulocytosis ( <mark>clozapine</mark> only ) . 
Since the incidence and severity of specific adverse effects differ among the various atypicals , the clinician should carefully consider which side effects are most likely to lead to the individual ' s dissatisfaction and noncompliance before choosing an antipsychotic for a particular patient . 
A randomized , placebo - controlled dose - comparison trial of <mark>haloperidol</mark> for psychosis and disruptive behaviors in Alzheimer ' s disease . 
OBJECTIVE : The goal of this study was to compare the efficacy and side effects of two doses of <mark>haloperidol</mark> and placebo in the treatment of psychosis and disruptive behaviors in patients with Alzheimer ' s disease . 
METHOD : In a 6 - week random - assignment , double - blind , placebo - controlled trial ( phase A ) , <mark>haloperidol</mark> , 2 - 3 mg / day ( standard dose ) , and <mark>haloperidol</mark> , 0 . 50 - 0 . 75 mg / day ( low dose ) , were compared in 71 outpatients with Alzheimer ' s disease . 
For the subsequent 6 - week double - blind crossover phase ( phase B ) , patients taking standard - or low - dose <mark>haloperidol</mark> were switched to placebo , and patients taking placebo were randomly assigned to standard - or low - dose <mark>haloperidol</mark> . 
RESULTS : For the 60 patients who completed phase A , standard - dose <mark>haloperidol</mark> was efficacious and superior to both low - dose <mark>haloperidol</mark> and placebo for scores on the Brief Psychiatric Rating Scale psychosis factor and on psychomotor agitation . 
Response rates according to three sets of criteria were greater with the standard dose ( 55 % - 60 % ) than the low dose ( 25 % - 35 % ) and placebo ( 25 % - 30 % ) . 
The advantage of standard dose over low dose was replicated in phase B . 
In phase A , extrapyramidal signs tended to be greater with the standard dose than in the other two conditions , primarily because of a subgroup ( 20 % ) who developed moderate to severe signs . 
Low - dose <mark>haloperidol</mark> did not differ from placebo on any measure of efficacy or side effects . 
CONCLUSIONS : The results indicated a favorable therapeutic profile for <mark>haloperidol</mark> in doses of 2 - 3 mg / day , although a subgroup developed moderate to severe extrapyramidal signs . 
A starting dose of 1 mg / day with gradual , upward dose titration is recommended . 
The narrow therapeutic window observed with <mark>haloperidol</mark> may also apply to other neuroleptics used in Alzheimer ' s disease patients with psychosis and disruptive behaviors . 
Effects of <mark>acetylsalicylic acid</mark> , <mark>dipyridamole</mark> , and <mark>hydrocortisone</mark> on <mark>epinephrine</mark> - induced myocardial injury in dogs . 
A reproducible model for producing diffuse myocardial injury ( <mark>epinephrine</mark> infusion ) has been developed to study the cardioprotective effects of agents or maneuvers which might alter the evolution of acute myocardial infarction . 
Infusions of <mark>epinephrine</mark> ( 4 mug per kilogram per minute for 6 hours ) increased <mark>radiocalcium</mark> uptakes into intact myocardium and each of its subcellular components with the mitochondrial fraction showing the most consistent changes when compared to saline - infused control animals ( 4 , 957 vs . 827 counts per minute per gram of dried tissue or fraction ) . 
Myocardial concentrations of <mark>calcium</mark> also increased significantly ( 12 . 0 vs . 5 . 0 mg . per 100 Gm . of fat - free dry weight ) . 
Infusions of <mark><mark>calcium</mark> chloride</mark> sufficient to raise serum <mark>calcium</mark> concentrations 2 mEq . per liter failed to increase calcium influx into the myocardial cell . 
Mitochondrial <mark>radiocalcium</mark> uptakes were significantly decreased in animals pretreated with <mark>acetylsalicylic acid</mark> or <mark>dipyridamole</mark> or when <mark>hydrocortisone</mark> was added to the <mark>epinephrine</mark> infusion ( 2 , 682 , 2 , 803 , and 3 , 424 counts per minute per gram of dried fraction , respectively ) . 
Myocardial <mark>calcium</mark> concentrations also were decreased ( 11 . 2 , 8 . 3 , and 8 . 9 mg . per 100 Gm . of fat - free dry weight , respectively ) in the three treatment groups , being significantly decreased only in the last two . 
Evidence of microscopic damage was graded as less severe in the three treatment groups . 
<mark>Acetylsalicylic acid</mark> , <mark>dipyridamole</mark> , and <mark>hydrocortisone</mark> all appear to have cardioprotective effects when tested in this model . 
Clinical and histopathologic examination of renal allografts treated with <mark>tacrolimus</mark> ( <mark>FK506</mark> ) for at least one year . 
BACKGROUND : We clinically and pathologically analyzed renal allografts from 1 9 renal transplant patients treated with <mark>tacrolimus</mark> ( <mark>FK506</mark> ) for more than 1 year . 
METHODS : Twenty - six renal allograft biopsy specimens from 1 9 renal transplant patients who underwent transplantations between 1991 and 1993 were evaluated . 
Thirteen biopsies were performed from stable functioning renal allografts with informed consent ( nonepisode biopsy ) and the other 13 were from dysfunctional renal allografts with a clinical indication for biopsy ( episode biopsy ) . 
RESULTS : The main pathologic diagnoses ( some overlap ) were acute rejection ( AR ; n = 4 ) , chronic rejection ( CR ; n = 5 ) , AR + CR ( n = 4 ) , recurrent IgA nephropathy ( n = 5 ) , normal findings ( n = 2 ) , minimal - type chronic <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy ( n = 9 ) , and mild - type <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy ( n = 11 ) . 
Of the nonepisode biopsies , 7 and 4 biopsies showed minimal - type and mild - type chronic <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy , respectively . 
Chronic <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy consisted of rough and foamy tubular vacuolization ( 5 biopsies ) , arteriolopathy ( angiodegeneration of the arteriolar wall ; 20 biopsies ) , focal segmental glomerulosclerosis ( 4 biopsies ) and the striped form of interstitial fibrosis ( 11 biopsies ) . 
The serum <mark>creatinine</mark> levels of patients in the mild - type chronic <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy group , which included 7 episode biopsies , were statistically higher than those in the minimum - type chronic <mark>FK506</mark> - nephropathy group ( P < 0 . 001 ) . 
CONCLUSIONS : This study demonstrates that chronic <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy consists primarily of arteriolopathy manifesting as insudative hyalinosis of the arteriolar wall , and suggests that mild - type chronic <mark>FK506</mark> nephropathy is a condition which may lead to deterioration of renal allograft function . 
Different lobular distributions of altered hepatocyte tight junctions in rat models of intrahepatic and extrahepatic cholestasis . 
Hepatocyte tight junctions ( TJs ) , the only intercellular barrier between the sinusoidal and the canalicular spaces , play a key role in bile formation . 
Although hepatocyte TJs are impaired in cholestasis , attempts to localize the precise site of hepatocyte TJ damage by freeze - fracture electron microscopy have produced limited information . 
Recently , several TJ - associated proteins like ZO - 1 and 7H6 have been identified and characterized . 
Immunolocalization of 7H6 appears to closely correlate with paracellular permeability . 
We used rat models of intrahepatic cholestasis by <mark>ethinyl estradiol</mark> ( <mark>EE</mark> ) treatment and extrahepatic cholestasis by bile duct ligation ( BDL ) to precisely determine the site of TJ damage . 
Alterations in hepatocyte TJs were assessed by double - immunolabeling for 7H6 and ZO - 1 using a confocal laser scanning microscope . 
In control rats , immunostaining for 7H6 and ZO - 1 colocalized to outline bile canaliculi in a continuous fashion . 
In contrast , 7H6 and ZO - 1 immunostaining was more discontinuous , outlining the bile canaliculi after BDL . 
Immunostaining for 7H6 , not ZO - 1 , decreased and predominantly appeared as discrete signals in the submembranous cytoplasm of periportal hepatocytes after BDL . 
After <mark>EE</mark> treatment , changes in immunostaining for 7H6 and ZO - 1 were similar to those seen in periportal hepatocytes after BDL , but distributed more diffusely throughout the lobule . 
This study is the first to demonstrate that impairment of hepatocyte TJs occurs heterogenously in the liver lobule after BDL and suggests that BDL and <mark>EE</mark> treatments produce different lobular distributions of increased paracellular permeability . 
Memory facilitation and stimulation of endogenous nerve growth factor synthesis by the <mark>acetylcholine</mark> releaser <mark>PG - 9</mark> . 
The effects of <mark>PG - 9</mark> ( <mark>3alpha - tropyl 2 - ( p - bromophenyl ) propionate</mark> ) , the <mark>acetylcholine</mark> releaser , on memory processes and nerve growth factor ( NGF ) synthesis were evaluated . 
In the mouse passive - avoidance test , <mark>PG - 9</mark> ( 10 - 30 mg / kg , i . p . ) , administered 20 min before the training session , prevented amnesia induced by both the non selective antimuscarinic drug <mark>scopolamine</mark> and the M1 - selective antagonist <mark>S - ( - ) - ET - 126</mark> . 
In the same experimental conditions , <mark>PG - 9</mark> ( 5 - 20 microg per mouse , i . c . v . ) was also able to prevent antimuscarine - induced amnesia , demonstrating a central localization of the activity . 
At the highest effective doses , <mark>PG - 9</mark> did not produce any collateral symptoms as revealed by the Irwin test , and it did not modify spontaneous motility and inspection activity , as revealed by the hole - board test . 
<mark>PG - 9</mark> was also able to increase the amount of NGF secreted in vitro by astrocytes in a dose - dependent manner . 
The maximal NGF contents obtained by <mark>PG - 9</mark> were 17 . 6 - fold of the control value . 
During culture , no morphological changes were found at effective concentrations of <mark>PG - 9</mark> . 
The current work indicates the ability of <mark>PG - 9</mark> to induce beneficial effects on cognitive processes and stimulate activity of NGF synthesis in astroglial cells . 
Therefore , <mark>PG - 9</mark> could represent a potential useful drug able to improve the function of impaired cognitive processes . 
Mechanisms of <mark>FK 506</mark> - induced hypertension in the rat . 
- <mark>Tacrolimus</mark> ( <mark>FK 506</mark> ) is a powerful , widely used immunosuppressant . 
The clinical utility of <mark>FK 506</mark> is complicated by substantial hypertension and nephrotoxicity . 
To clarify the mechanisms of <mark>FK 506</mark> - induced hypertension , we studied the chronic effects of <mark>FK 506</mark> on the synthesis of endothelin - 1 ( ET - 1 ) , the expression of mRNA of ET - 1 and endothelin - converting enzyme - 1 ( ECE - 1 ) , the endothelial <mark>nitric oxide</mark> synthase ( eNOS ) activity , and the expression of mRNA of eNOS and C - type natriuretic peptide ( CNP ) in rat blood vessels . 
In addition , the effect of the specific endothelin type A receptor antagonist <mark>FR 139317</mark> on <mark>FK 506</mark> - induced hypertension in rats was studied . 
<mark>FK 506</mark> , 5 mg . 
kg - 1 . 
d - 1 given for 4 weeks , elevated blood pressure from 102 + / - 13 to 152 + / - 15 mm Hg and increased the synthesis of ET - 1 and the levels of ET - 1 mRNA in the mesenteric artery ( 240 % and 230 % , respectively ) . 
Little change was observed in the expression of ECE - 1 mRNA and CNP mRNA . 
<mark>FK 506</mark> decreased eNOS activity and the levels of eNOS mRNA in the aorta ( 48 % and 55 % , respectively ) . 
The administration of <mark>FR 139317</mark> ( 10 mg . kg - 1 . d - 1 ) prevented <mark>FK 506</mark> - induced hypertension in rats . 
These results indicate that <mark>FK 506</mark> may increase blood pressure not only by increasing ET - 1 production but also by decreasing <mark>NO</mark> synthesis in the vasculature .
